O vos, tres chiers filz, je vos ai acomplit cest livre qui est li derriens de la science de medicine ensamble l’emplissement de lui, et ai fait la fin per ses expositions et par ses declarations.	O you, very dear son, I have completed this book which is the last of the science of medicine along with its fulfillment, and I have made an end through its explanations and through its declarations.
Et m’est venu en vision que je le vos acomplisse avec cest traitier, qui est partie de l’uevre de mains, c’est a savoir «cyrurgie».	And it came to me in a vision that I should complete it with this treatise, which is part of the work of the hand, namely surgery.
Et por ceu que l’uevre de mains est fortraite en nostre region et est etraingie dou tout en tout, si est perie li science et decopee, et n’est riens demorez de li fuers que les petites descriptions en livres des anciens que les mains ont muees.	And because the work of the hand is very little treated in our region and is unknown everywhere, the knowledge of it has been lost and only small descriptions in books by the ancients remain, written from the hands themselves.Et si li fuers et la science de cest uvre ne demore pas en nostre region, il demore en l’autre parti de le monde, car il ne peut diez ne poer ne paitre que de ceus qui conssent li science de li corps et de li mebrues.
Et de ceu est venue li error et li vanitez, et sont closes les ententions et est aloignie li science.	And because the strength and science of this work do not remain in our region, they remain in the other parts of the world, for it cannot exist without those who possess the knowledge of the body and its functions.
Or me semble que je la vuel vivifier ensamble l’ordination de cest traitier selonc la voie d’exposition et de declaration et de l’abreviation;	I think I want to animate it together with the arrangement of this treatise according to the way of exposition, declaration, and abbreviation;
et venrai ensamble les formes des ferremens de cautere, et des autres estrumens de l’uevre avec l’ajostement de la declaration et de preparation de li, sicom il est mestier.	and will come together with the forms of the instruments of cautery, and other tools of the work with the adjustment of its declaration and preparation as it is necessary.
Et por la raison de ceu que nuls boins maistres de mains n’est trovez en nostre tens, est li ars de medicine eslongié.	And because no good masters of hands are found in our time, the art of medicine is neglected.
Et covient celui qui s’en entremet sormonter en la science d’anathomie, si com Galiens dit, tant qu’il saiche la juement des menbres, et les formes et les conjunctions et les separations d’aus, et aient connissance des osses et des nerf et des brais et le nombre d’ous, et le demenement et des voines movans et des reposans, et dou leu de lor issue.	And one who undertakes this must excel in the science of anatomy, as Galen says, as long as he knows the judgment of the members, and forms and conjunctions, and separations of bones, and have knowledge of bones and nerves and veins, and the number of ears, and the movement and of their blood vessels.
Et por ceu dist Ypocras que li nons avec le non est mout, et avec l’uevre est poc;	And because Hypocras says that the name with the name is much, and with the work is little;
et meismement en l’art de main.	and especially in the art of hand.
Nos vos disons en l’introite de cest livre que qui n’est conissans des choses devant dites, si se gart qu’il ne chiece en error et qu’il n’ocie les homes;	We tell you at the entrance to this book that whoever is not knowledgeable about the things already said, be careful that he does not fall into error and that he does not harm people;
ensi que j’ai veut maintes fois plusors de ces qui s’entremettent de ceste science et si s’abandonent sen science et sens experiment.	so I have many times more of those who interfere with this knowledge and abandon themselves without knowledge or experience.
Car je vis un fol mire qui copa I apostume de scrophules ou col d’une femme, et copa les arteres dou col;	For I saw a foolish physician who cupped the scrofula on a woman's neck, and cupped the arteries in her neck;
por coi tant de sanc issit hors que li femme cheit morte entre ses mains.	where so much blood flows out that the woman dies in his arms.
Et vis I autre mire qui traït une piere d’un home d’eaige, et li piere estoit grans;	And I saw another surgeon who was treating a stone in a man's testicles, and the stone was large;
si emporta avec li une piece de la vessie, et fut mors li hons dedens III jors.	he took with him a piece of the bladder, and the man died within three days.
Et je i avoie ja esteit apelez por lou traire, et vis la disposition dou malaide et la grandor de la piere, et soi bien s’on lou tailloit il en morroit.	And I had already been called to treat him, and I saw the condition of the patient and the size of the stone, and if they cut it out he would surely die.
Et vis I autre mire qui prist en cure I duc de nostre terre qui avoit la jambe brisie, et avec la briseure ot plaie;	And I saw another surgeon who was treating the Duke of our land who had a broken leg, and with the break there was a wound;
et li mires plains d’ignorance estraint la brisure sus la plaie as esteles par fort lieure, et ne lassa a la plaie point de xalain, et le lassa ensi I termine;	and the ignorant surgeons bound the break above the wound with strong ligatures, and left the wound uncovered, and left it in that state;
et li comanda qu’il ne la desliast mie;	and he commanded that he must not loosen it;
et demora ensi que li jambe fut toute enflee et li piez et vint a perdition.	and it stayed like that until the leg became swollen and the foot, and it came to ruin.
Je fuis apelez por venir a lui, et me hastai por venir deslier la jambe;	I was called to come to him, and I hurried to loosen the leg;
et quant je l’oi desloie si fut em pais et ne sentit point de dolor.	and when I dislocated it, he was relieved of pain and felt no discomfort.
Mais toute voie li corruptions estoit ja confermee ou membre, et ne la poi saner;	However, the corruption had already settled in the limb and could not be healed;
et ne cessa li corrution d’aler par le membre tant que li membres fut dou tout perdus.	and the corruption did not cease from spreading throughout the limb until the limb was completely dead.
Et vis .i. autre mire qui effondra .i. apostume enchancreit, et puis enflama per le malice de sa signorie.	And I saw another patient who had a wound, and then it became inflamed due to the wickedness of his lord.
Car chancre, quant il est purs d’umor melancolique, ne covient mie qu’on i(l) touche de fer s’il n’est en teil leu c’on puisse toute oster ce que est corrumpus.	For a ulcer, when it is clear of melancholy humor, one should not touch it with iron unless it is in such a place that one can completely remove all that is corrupted.
Et por ceu, treschier filz, vos est besoig que vos sachiez que oevre de mains est devisee en II divisions:	And for this reason, dear son, you must know that manual medicine is divided into two parts:
c’est asavoir, huevre ou il a peril en plusors dispositions;	that is, where there is danger in various conditions;
et je mostrerai en chescun leu de cest livre ou il a paour et peril.	and I will demonstrate in each section of this book where there is doubt and fear.
Por coi il est besoig que vos vos en gardez, si que li fol mire ne puissent mal parler de vos.	Therefore, you must be cautious so that the foolish man cannot speak ill of you.Et je mostrerai les perils et les doubtes et les maux qui sont as savans et a ceux qui n’ont point de science en medicine, si com il
Si prenez vos armes en cusenson, et entreprenez vos malaides legierement et fermement, et usez de la millor voie si que per la graice de Deu vos venez a salut et soiez loez;	Take up your weapons with caution, and approach your illnesses gently and firmly, using the best methods, so that through the grace of God you may achieve salvation and be praised.
et lassiez les maladies espoantables de grief saniteit;	and let the terrible diseases of deep sorrow
et ostez vos armes de ceu que vos fait douter, et aiez foit en vos si que vos puissiez venir de cestui monde a l’autre de gloire.	remove your weapons from that which makes you doubt, and have faith in yourselves so that you may pass from this world to the other of glory.
Galiens dist en aucuns de ses amonestemens:	Galen says in one of his warnings:
«Ne prenez mie en cure male maladie, que vos ne soiez apelez fol mire.	Do not take on a difficult disease unless you are called a foolish doctor.
» J’ai deviseit cest traitier selonc III chapitres.	I have arranged this treatise according to three chapters.
Li premiers chapitres est des cauteres de feu et dé cauteres de medicine ague, et est li chapitres ordenez de lou chief jusques as piez;	The first chapter is about fire cauteries and hot iron cauteries, and it is ordered from the head to the feet.
et des formes des estrumens, et des ferremens de cautere, et de tout ceu qui est necessaire en l’ueuvre.	and of the forms of instruments, and of the use of cautery, and of all that is necessary in the craft.
Li secons chapitres si est de taillier et de percier, et des ventouses et des plaies, et des estractions des saiettes, et des semblans choses;	The second chapter is about cutting and piercing, and of leeches and wounds, and the extraction of arrows, and similar things;
et est li chapitres ordenez et les formes des estrumens.	and it includes the forms of instruments.
Li tiers chapitres est de restorer les dislocations et des torcions, et des semblans choses;	The third chapter is about restoring dislocations and twists, and similar things;
et est ordeneiz des lou chief jusc’as piez, et des formes des estrumens.	and it is ordered from the head to the feet, and includes the forms of instruments.
Ainsois que nos nos remembriens de l’uevre, il covient que je die la qualiteit de l’aide et dou nuisement de chescune complexion.	So that we may remember the work, I must describe the nature of each humor and its harmful qualities.
Je dis que li qualiteis de l’aide, et dou nuisement, est li plus longe parole et subtilz science et li secrez reponus;	I say that the qualities of help, and harm, are the longest words and most subtle sciences, and the secret responses;
et de ceu parlerent li plusors des saiges, et s’acorderent a ceu;	and on this point many of the sages spoke, and they agreed with him.
et me soffisent poc lor paroles, car je redous la longesce.	I need little of their words, for I fear lengthiness.
Je dis que cautere aide universement a toute complexion ou il a matiere, fuer que II complexions:	I say that cautery helps universally in every complexion where it has material, except in two complexions:
c’est a savoir complexion chaude sens matere, et complexion seche sens matere.	that is to say, hot complexion without matter, and dry complexion without matter.Et l’un de ceus deux ne doit estre cauteriz, car la cauterie ne le peut supporter; ains li autres
En complexion chaude et seche ensamble matiere, deviserent aucun et dirent que cautere i est grans aide;	In hot and dry complexion together with matter, some people said that cautery is of great help. But others said:
et li autre dirent le contraire:	and the others said the opposite:
que cautere ne vaut a maladie que vient de chalor et de sechour.	that cautery is of no use in illness that comes from heat and dryness.Et quant a complexion frieure et humure ensamble matiere, tous convienent qu’elle
Car li nature dou feu si est chaude, et ne doit mie estre cureiz de chaude maladie par chalor, ne per sechour;	Because the nature of fire is hot, and it should not be cured with heat nor dryness;
et dist cil qui dist lou contraire que cautere fait grant aide a maladie chaude et seche que vient en cors des homes.	and says one who says the opposite that cautery does great good for hot and dry diseases that come upon men's bodies.
Car quant tu comperes le cors de l’ome et sa moistor a la complexion dou feu, tu trueves le cors froit.	For when you compare the body of man and its moisture to the nature of fire, you find the body to be cold.
Et je m’acorde a ceste parole.	And I agree with this statement.
Car je l’ai troveit aucune fois per experiment.	For I have found this to be true through experimentation.
Et toute voie, ne s’en entremette mie fuers que cil qui l’a esproveit, et qui conoit par lonc usaige le chapistre des cauteres, et la diversiteit des complexions des homes, et les dispositions et les causes de lor maladies, et les sorvenues et l’espaice dou tens;	And nevertheless, one should not meddle with it except those who have experienced it and who know through long usage the treatment of cauteries, and the diversity of men's complexions, and their dispositions and the causes of their diseases, and their outcomes and the season of the year;
des autres complexions n’avons nos mie paour, meismement em maladies froides et moistes.	we have no fear of other complexions, especially in cold and moist diseases.
Et tuit li mire s’asemblerent et s’acorderent au cautere.	And all the doctors agreed and concurred with the cautery treatment.
Et sachiez, filz, que cautere ensamble feu si est des secrez des cures, et de plus grant bonteit que cautere de medicine ardant.	And know, my son, that cautery brings fire together with the secrets of healing, and is of greater goodness than burning cautery of medicine.
Car li feus est simples, et ne vient mie fuers que au membre qui est cuis, et ne nuit a autre membre se poc nom.	For fire is simple, and does not spread beyond the cooked member, nor harm any other part if only slightly applied.
Les medicines ardans vienent de membre a autre en aloignant, et font venir au membre maladies de grief sanation;	Burning medicines pass from one member to another by moving away, and bring sickly diseases to the members;
et par aventure ocit lou malaide.	and perchance they kill the disease.
Li feus por sa hautece et por la bonteit de sa substance ne fait mie ceu, s’il n’i a superfluiteit.	Fire does not do harm by its heat and for the goodness of its substance if there is no excess.
Et ceu vos ai je troveit par experiment et par la longesce dou servise et de l’estude que j’ai mis en l’art, et esteit sus la verteit des choses;	And this I have found by experiment and through the length of my service and study that I have devoted to the art, and been placed upon the truth of things;
et por ceu je m’escuse de la longesce de la parole, car il ne me plait mie que je vos oste le secreit qui est reponus ou feu, et la qualiteit de l’uevre, coment il deboute les maladies des cors, si com li philosophe le dit en demostrant;	and because of this I excuse the length of my speech, for it does not please me to take from you the secret that is contained in fire, and the quality of its work, how it cures the diseases of the body, as the philosopher says in his demonstration;
or le recevez en vos pensees.	receive it in your thoughts.
Et sachiez, fil, que il s’acorderent en quel tens doient estre faites les cauteres, et eslirent prientens.	And know, son, that they agreed upon what time the cauteries should be performed, and chose a propitious moment.
Et je dis que cautere est covenable en tous tens, por ceu que li nuisemens sorvenans est desoz mis par l’aide dou cautere;	And I say that cautery is suitable at all times, because the harmful humors are driven out by the help of cautery;
et meismement se li cauteres est por dolors necessaires fors et hastans que ne puent atendre le tens que plus grans malice ne veigne au membre.	and especially when the cautery is for necessary pains that are urgent and cannot wait until greater harm comes to the limb.
Et n’i pensez onques, chier fil, si com font li fol mire;	And never think, dear son, as fools do;
car a la maladie qui est sanee par cautere n’a point de revenue;	for the disease that is cured by cautery does not return;
et il le dient ensi;	and they say it like this:
mais il n’est mie si com il cuident, por ce que cauteres nen est que medicine qui mue la complexion, et seche les humors que sont cause de la dolor, et vaut mues que medicine por le hastement de sa valor, et por la vertut de son oevre et de sa signorie.	but it is not as they believe, because cautery is a medicine that moves the complexions and dries up the humors that are the cause of pain; and it is worth more than other medicines for its swiftness, its strength, and the virtue of its work and its lordship.
Et possans chose est que li maladie viegne aucune fois selonc la complexion dou malaide et lou leu de la maladie et sa vertut;	And it is possible that the disease comes sometimes according to the complexion of the illness and the place of the disease and its strength.
et sont assemblees en lui les superfluitez par l’aquisition des viandes et des semblans choses, se ce n’est cauteres administrez em leu ou il ait poc de superfluitez et de moistor, si com cauteres de dens por la dolor, et les semblans choses, et teil dolor ne revient mie;	and the excesses are gathered in it due to the consumption of food and similar things, unless cauterization is administered in the place where there is little excess and moisture, as with tooth cauterization for pain, and similar things, and such pain does not return.
mais ce avient poc.	but this rarely happens.
Et mout de gens n’entendent mie por coi cauteres est apelez li derriens de medecine, et c’est voir;	And many people do not understand why cauterization is called the last resort of medicine, and that is because:
mais il ne croient mie que cauteres vaille aprés medicine, mais lor ententions est fause, et est cauteres li derriens de medicine por ceu que quant nos aministrons manieres de cures en aucune maladie et elles ne valent, adonc administrons nos le cautere, et il vaut.	but they do not believe that cauterization comes after medicine; their understanding is false, and cauterization is the last resort of medicine because when we administer methods of treatment in any disease and they are ineffective, then we turn to cauterization, and it works.
Adonques apert bien que cauteres est li derriens de medicine, ne mie selonc l’entention des folz mires.	Therefore, it is clear that cauterization is the last resort of medicine, not according to the opinion of foolish people.
Li ancien dirent que cauteres d’estrument d’or est muedres que de fer, et ne dirent ceu fuers que por la qualiteit de l’or et por la hautece de sa substance;	The ancients said that cauteries with instruments of gold are gentler than those of iron, and they said this because of the quality of gold and its lofty essence.
et dirent que li leus de cautere ne fait mie porriture, mais ceu n’est mie voir car je l’ai esprovei, et ai troveit que c’est voir en aucuns homes;	and they said that the site of a cautery does not cause swelling, but this is not true because I have tried it and found that it is true in some people.
et cauteres d’or vaut mues que de fer, si com il lou dirent.	and cauteries with gold are better than those with iron, as they said.
Et toutevoie quant tu chaufes estrument d’or, tu ne seis mie quant il est chaus par la color de l’or, et s’est tantost refroidiez;	And yet, when you heat an instrument of gold, you do not know when it is hot by the color of the gold, and it cools quickly.
et s’on le chaufe trop;	and if it's heated too much;
si font au feu;	if they are heated in the fire;
et ensi i a assez d’empechement.	and so there is enough hindrance.
Et por ce usons nos de cautere de feir que nos l’avons mues apparilliet a nostre oevre.	And for this, we use a fire cautery, which we have made appropriate for our work.
Or vos ai ordeneit cest chapitre des lou chief jusc’a piez, por ceu que li voie soit plus legiere a trover.	Now I have arranged this chapter from the head to the feet, so that the road is easier to find.
dou cautere olivaire	of the olive-oil cautery
Cist cauteres vaut a moistor et a froidor sus lou cerveil, et en i a dous c’on fait par la cause d’une maladie qui est apelee «soda», et par la cause de maintes humors qui dessendent dou chief as eulz, et as oreilles, et por multitude de songes et dolor de dens et dolor de gorge, et meismement a toutes maladies qui vienent de froidor si com paralisie et sode et apoplexie et semblans maladies.	This cautery is useful for moisture and coldness in the head, and there are two reasons for its use: one is because of a disease called "soda", and the other is due to many humors descending from the head to the eyes and ears, as well as for numerous ailments such as pain in the teeth and throat, and especially for diseases caused by coldness, such as paralysis, soda (a type of stroke), and similar conditions.
Li forme de cest cautere si est que li malaides soit espurgiez par medicine solutive mondifiant le chief III nuis ou IIII, selonc ceu que li vertus et li eaige et li acostumance dou malaide le puet soffrir;	The form of this cautery is that the patient be purged by a purifying medicine for three or four nights, depending on what the strength, age, and condition of the patient can endure.
et puis fai rere lou chief dou malaide.	then have the patient's head examined.
Et puis le fai seoir croisiet entre tes mains, et mettre ses mains sor som peis;	Then have the patient sit cross-legged in your lap, and place his hands on his thighs;
aprés met la racine de ta palme sus la racine de son neis entre ses II eulz;	After, place the palm of your hand between the roots of his nose, between his eyes;
et lai ou venra tes dois moiens, si saigne d’enche puis eschaufe le cautere qui est apelé «olivare», de coi ci est li forme:	And there you will place two fingers, then it will bleed; then heat the cautery called 'olive', of which this is the shape:
Et le met sor le leu signiet d’encre, et fai en dessendant et en estraignant ta main poc et poc en trestornant;	And place it on the spot marked with ink, and as you are lowering your hand gently, move it around in small circles;
puis lieve ta main isnelement, et rewarde le leu se tu vois l’os I sol petit;	Then raise your hand gently, and examine the spot again to see if the bone is still protruding;
et se tu ne lou vois, si rencomence le cautere tant que tu voies l’os si com je lou t’ai dit;	And if you do not see it, then reapply the cautery until you see the bone as I have told you;
aprés pren I poc de seil, et met en awe et molle coton dedens, et met sor le leu, et li laisse III jors;	After, take a piece of silk and place some soft cotton inside it, then tie it around the spot and leave it for three days;
aprés met sus cotun moilliet en burre;	after soaking cotton in lard;
et laisse sus tant que li eschaudure soit ostee;	and leave it until the scorch is removed;
aprés cure la plaie de l’oignement qui est apelez «tetrafarmaçon», tant qu’il soit sanez.	afterwards, treat the wound with ointment called 'tetrafarmaçon' until it heals.
Et se dirent li ancien, que quant plus demoure overte li plaie, plus s’espurge;	And the elders say that the more the wound is left open, the more it drains;
et por ce si aide mues.	and so helps scabs to form.
Et dirent aucun de ces que on doit tant lassier le cautere que partie de l’os soit arse, et puis rese on ceu qui est ars de l’os, et soit curez.	And some say that one must let the cautery burn until part of the bone is scorched, and then one should scrape off what is burned from the bone, and it will be cured.
Et dient li autre c’on doit le cautere tant lassier sus, et bouter si fort c’on abaite de l’os ausi large comme I vertoil que les femmes mettent en lor fusez por ceu que les humors issent mues hors;	And some say that you should leave the cautery on for so long, and press down so hard that it breaks the bone as widely as the ring that women put in their navels to draw out humours;
et doit on lassier la plaie longement overte;	and one must leave the wound open for a long time;
aprés le doit on curer et sodeir.	afterwards, one should clean and stitch it up.
Et ces II manieres de cauteres ne me semblent mie estre bones dou tout en tout, fuers qu’en aucuns homes ou il ait voie de paor;	And I do not think that these two methods of cautery are good at all, except in some people where there is a fear;
et mues me semble que je lou doie laissier;	and I think I should let it go;
car li chiés li est afoiblis par les solutions continuees de nature, si com nos le tesmoignons ens autres membres;	because the head is weakened by continuous solutions of nature, as we testify in other members;
et meisme quant li chiés dou malaide est foibles par nature, et li premiere semblance de cautere est plus salve et muedre por moi, et de celi use je oevre en donques emsamble salut.	and the same when the head of the sick person is weakened by nature, and the first appearance of cautery is more gentle and beneficial for me, and from this I perform the operation together with safety.
de l’anciainne dolor dou chief	from the old pain in the head
Quant en tout le chief vient dolor croniques, et dure longement, si doit user li malaides yeris et pilules qui sont apelees «cochie», et d’espurgement de chief et d’oiles et d’emplastres;	When a chronic headache comes and lasts a long time, one must use the herbs and pills that are called 'concoctions', as well as poultices, oils, and plasters for the head;
et s’on li fait le cautere que nos avons devant dit, et il ne vaut.	and if one performs the cautery that we have previously mentioned, and it does not work.
Pren warde se li chiés dou malade est de fort nature, et qu’il ne soit trop froit;	Take care if the head of the patient is of a strong nature, and it is not too cold;
adonques le cauterize desoz celui cautere un poc que nos avons dit desus.	then cauterize him under that cautery, a little bit that we have mentioned above.
Aprés fai cautere sus chescune corne dou chief jusc’a l’os, si com devant avons dit, et fai I cautere ou leu qui est apelez «vasselz»;	After cauterizing each horn of the head to the bone, as we have said before, and making the cautery in the place called "vessel",
et est I leus en coi on met ventouses;	and it is the places where one applies cupping glasses.
et alige ta main si que tu ne voises mie jusc’a l’os:	And lighten your hand so that you do not go to the bone:
li malaides sent trop plus grant dolor en cest cautere que as autres, et je em parlerai aillors;	The patient feels much more pain in this cautery than in others, and I will speak of it elsewhere;
et covient que li cauteres des cornes soient plus subtis que cil dont on cautere la moieneteit dou chief, et c’est li forme:	And the cauteries on the horns must be more delicate than those with which one cauterizes the middle of the head, and this is the form:
dou cautere dou chief	of the cautery on the head
Quant en une partie dou chief vient dolor sodaine, et est estendue li maladie jusc’a l’oil, et li chiés est espurgiez par medicines mondifians, et on a fait les autres cures que j’ai dit en la division des maladies, et tout ceu ne profite mie:	When sudden pain comes in a part of the head and the illness extends to the eye, and the shoulder is purged with purifying medicines, and one has done the other remedies that I have said in the division of illnesses, and all this does not help:
adonques li fai cauteres selonc II manieres, c’est a savoir de medicine ague et de feir.	then you must perform cauterizations according to two methods, namely with hot iron and with fire.
Li cauteres de medicine ague si est que tu preignes une doce d’alz, et oste l’escorce et le recope I poc as II chiés, et puis fent la temple ou li dolor tient en teil maniere que tu puisses reponre la doce d’alz desoz le cuir;	The cautery with hot iron is done by taking a piece of alder wood, removing the bark and heating it until it smokes. Then you make the cauterization at the site of the pain in such a way that you can place the alder wood under the skin.
et quant elle sera reponuee si le lie et l’estraint bien et le laisse ensi XII houres;	And when it is applied, tie it tightly and leave it for twelve hours.
et puis le deslie et trait fuers la doce d’ail, et laisse la plaie ensi II jors ou III;	Then loosen it and treat it with garlic, leaving the wound open for two or three days.
puis met sus cotun plongiet en burre tant que porreture en isse.	Then cover it with a linen cloth soaked in butter until the swelling goes down.
Aprés le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez;	After the wound has healed, treat it with ointment until it is completely healed.
et se tu vues si fai ceu d’aucunes medicines comburans que j’ai escrites ou dozime traitier des medicines comburans.	And if you wish, you can also use some burning medicines which I have written about in the twelfth treatment of burning medicines.
Li cautere de fer si est selonc ceste meniere.	The cautery with iron is as follows.
Chaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	Heat the cautery, of which there is the shape.
Et est apelez «clos» por ceu que li chief est fait a la forme d’un clo ou il ait I poc de corbeure, et em mileu a une petite apparance;	And it is called "clos" because the head is formed in the shape of a cloak with a slight curve, and in the middle has a small appearance;
et le met sor le leu dolorous, et tien ta main et trestorne le feir un poc legierement, tant que li moitiez de l’espés dou keur soit arse;	and he puts it over the painful area, and holds his hand and twists it slightly so that half of the thickness of the heart is burned;
et lieve ta main que li artere n’arde, que est defuers, et decorre habundance de sanc.	and then release your hand so that the artery burns, which is hot, and an abundance of blood flows.
Aprés met coton en awe de seil, et met sor le leu par III jors;	After, put cotton in the wound, and hold it there for three days;
puis i met coton moilliet em burre, et puis cure le leu d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez;	then he applies wet cotton soaked in butter, and then he treats the area with ointment until it heals;
et se tu vuelz cauterize ceste emigraine avec le cautere qui est apelez «cultellare», a tout la pointe, et te garde de coper l’artere en ceste emigraine qui n’est mie anciaine.	and if you want to cauterize this hemorrhoid with the cautery called "cultellare", at the tip only, and be careful not to touch the artery in this hemorrhoid which is not old.
de emigraine	of veins
Quant tu cures emigraine si com nos avons devant dit en divisions des maladies, et ne profite mie, et vois que li cauteres devant dis de la medicine et dou fer ne li soffit mie, adonques covient il que tu eschaufes le cautere qui est apelez «cultellare» tant qu’il soit blans;	When you treat a headache as we have previously described in the divisions of illnesses, and it does not help, and you see that the cauteries before mentioned in medicine, neither with fire nor with iron, benefit him, then you must heat the cautery which is called 'cultellare' until it turns white.
et seigne ainsois sor le leu doillant une ligne de demi doi de lonc, et oste ta main une fois, et l’estrain que tu ne coper l’artere et que ne viegnes jusc’a l’os;	And sign thus on the temple a line of half an inch long, and remove your hand once, and press it so that you do not touch the artery and go no deeper than the bone;
et te warde de la mandibule que muet quant on menjut, et li ners n’ait regart que la muet et que spasmus ne veigne a malaide, et te warde de decorrement de sanc de l’artere quant elle sera copee, ou copement ait grant paour et meismement a celui que ne s’i conoit, et qui n’est estudians et esprovez;	And beware of the mandible that mutates when one chews, and the nerve has no reaction, and that spasms do not come to illness, and beware of blood flow from the artery when it is cut, for this cutting brings great fear especially to those who are unaccustomed and inexperienced.
et laisse l’uevre em mi voie;	and leaves the work halfway;
mais je vos dirai coment on restainche sanc quant li artere est copee, et je vos mostrerai a leu ou il afiert en cest livre.	but I will tell you how to stanch blood when an artery is cut, and I will show you where it opens in this book.
Et se tu vois que cist cauteres ne soffise mie a la maladie, et li malaides est soffrans, cauterize le enmi le chief ausi com nos avons dit, et cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit sanee;	And if you see that this cautery is not sufficient for the disease and the patient is suffering, cauterize him in the head as we have said, and treat the wound until it heals.
et se tu vues, aministre le cautere que nos avons dit ou chapistre de l’estraction de l’artere, avec le cautere qui ait II coutelz;	And if you see, administer the cautery that we have said in the chapter on the extraction of an artery, with the cautery that has two knives;
et est cist cauteres millors de celui et plus aidans.	and this cautery is better and more effective than the other one.
de la dolor des oreilles de part froidor	from pain in the ears due to cold
Quant en l’oreille vient dolor de froit, et on i a ovreit de medicines solutives et des autres cures que nos avons dit en la division, et li dolors ne se muet, adonques eschaufe cest cautere qui est apelez «poins», de coi ci est li forme:	When pain in the ear persists despite treatment with solutive medicines and other remedies that we have described in the previous chapter, and the pain does not go away, then heat this cautery called «poins», which has the following shape:
Aprés pointoie tout entor l’oreille malaide, ou entor les II se la dolor tient en ambedous, et t’esloigne un poc ensus de la racine de l’oreille puis que tu as signiet le leu d’enche;	Afterwards, prick all around the ear where the pain is located in both ears if it occurs in both, and move slightly upwards from the root of the ear after you have marked the place to be cauterized;
et ait X poins entor chescune oreille;	and has X points around each ear;
aprés cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	then treat the area until it is healed.
de la torture de la bouche	of the mouth's torture
Torture qui doit estre curee par cautere nen est fuers que de celles que muevent de fleume, si com nos avons dit en divisions des maladie;	Wounds that should be treated with cautery are only those that cause bleeding, as we have said in the divisions of diseases;
et ne faire point de cautere as semblances que vienent de sechor et de spame de ners.	and do not apply cautery to appearances that come from dryness and nerve pain.
Quant tu cures ceste semblance de torture qui muet de fleume d’ydres et d’espurgemens de chief et de gargarisme, et ceu ne vaut, adonc covient que tu cauterizes le malaide de III cauteres:	When you treat this appearance of a wound that bleeds from fluids and discharges from the head and from gargling, and it does not improve, then you must cauterize the patient with three cauteries:
l’une en la racine de l’oreille, et l’autre un poc defuers la temple, et le tier en l’ajostement des II levres;	one at the root of the ear, another slightly further from the temple, and the third in the junction between the two lips;
et met le cautere en la partie qui apert saine, et li fai cautere endroit le chief de l’oreille desus un poc desoz la corne dou chief, et un autre en la temple ausi longe com uns poce;	and apply the cautery to the part that appears healthy, and cauterize above the tip of the ear at the horn of the head, and another one on the temple as long as a finger;
et laisse le cautere tant sus que li moitiez dou keur soit arse;	and leave the cautery on until the middle of the heart is burned.
et c’est li forme dou cautere:	and this is the shape of the cautery:
Et est li semblance dou cutellaire que nos avons mise devant, mais il est un poc plus subtilz et covient que li coutelz soit un poc plus gros;	And it has the appearance of the scalpel that we placed earlier, but it is a little more slender and the blade should be a little thicker.
aprés cure lou leu si com j’ai devant dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Afterward, dress the wound as I have said before, until it is healed.
Quant apoplexie est ancieinne et tu la cures ensi com nos avons dit, et il ne profite mie, et li malaides n’ait fievre, adonques li fai IIII cauteres:	When the apoplexy is old and you treat it thus as we have said, but it does not help, and the patient has a fever, then make him three cauteries:
II sus les II cornes dou chief, et I emmi le chief, et I ou leu qui est apelez «vasselz» si com nos avons devant dit, et lou derrien cautere sus la bouche de l’estomac;	two on the two horns of the head, and one in the middle of the head, and one at the place called 'vessel' as we have said before, and the last cautery on the mouth of the stomach;
et soit curez si com nos avons dit devant.	and dress them as we have said before.And if he has an old wound and you dress it thus as we have said,
de litargie	of quicksilver
A cest maladie covient doner au malaide yeres grans et pilules mondifians le cerveil;	For this illness, give the patient large pills to cleanse the brain;
aprés reis lou chief dou malaide tout, et li met sus l’occipite l’emplaustre de sinapi qui est escrit ou traitier des emplastres;	then completely shave the head of the sick person and place on the back of the neck the mustard plaster that is written about in the treatise on plasters;
et c’est li maniere dou cautere:	and this is how to do the cautery:
si lou fai si com j’ai dit.	if he does it as I have said.
S’il est sanez ensi, boin est;	If he is cured in this way, that is good;s’il ne fuet, querre li un embaumeur ou un med
et s’il ne l’est, se li fai III cauteres des emmi le chief en dessendant jusc’a col, et ait d’espaice entre chescun cautere I doi de gros;	if not, get an embalmer or a doctor[who will] cauterize the scalp from the top of the head down to the neck, and have two inches between each cautery;and if he is not cured, he should be given three cauteries on the scalp, going down from the top of the head to the neck, with two inches between each cautery;s’il ne fut sanz dolor et sanz saingne, querre li un embaumeur ou
et le cure si com les autres, et se tu i vues ajoster, et li malaides est soffrans, se li fai I cautere en mileu;	if there is no pain and no bleeding, get an embalmer or a doctor[who will] cauterize it as the others, and if you see any hair coming out, and the patient is enduring it, do one cautery in the middle;et si tu vels ajouter encores plus de cauteres, querre li un embaumeur ou
et se mestiers est, II autres sus les II cornes, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez;	and if necessary, two others on the two horns, and treat it until it is healed.
et soit li cauteres qui est apelez «olivare», si com j’ai devant dit.	and use the cautery called "olive tree", as I have already said.
de la froidor dou chief	from the coldness of the head
Il covient que li chief soit mundifiez de yeres et de ceu que nos avons devant dit;	The head must be cleansed of hair and of what we have already mentioned;
aprés reis le chief dou malaide, puis li fai cautere emmi le chief et sus chescune corne, et I derrier et III sus l’espinee dou col;	After shaving the head of the patient, then do cauterization all over the head and on each horn, and once behind and three times on the spine of the neck;
et se tu en as plus mestier, et li cors est moiste et li malaides est soffrans, et li maladie est fors, se li fai IIII cauteres sus l’espinee dou dos;	and if you need more, and the body is moist and the patient is suffering, and the disease is strong, then do four cauterizations on the spine of the back;
et li laisse tant que li plus dou keur soit ars, et lieve ta main;	and let it be until the hottest part burns, then lift your hand;
aprés le cure tant qu’il soit sanez, et soit li cauteres qui est apelez «olivare» que nos avons devant dit.	After healing, use the cautery called "olive tree" which we have mentioned earlier.
de l’epilempsie	of epilepsy
Li epilentiques ne doit useir de cautere fuers que cil qui est fleumatique, et covient premier mondifier le cerveil de yeres et d’autres cures que nos avons dites en la division quant li malaides est grans et soffrans de penre medicine.	Epileptics should not use cautery except for those who are phlegmatic; it is first necessary to cleanse the brain of hair and other things that we mentioned in the division when the illness is great and suffering, taking medicine.
Et se c’est uns enfes qui ne lou puisse soffrir, se li fai gargarisme et mastication mondifiant le cerveil sovent avec bones viandes;	And if it is a child who cannot bear it, make him a gargle and chew, purifying the brain often with good meat.
aprés li reis lou chief em mileu, et i fai I cautere selonc ce que nos avons dit devant, et I cautere sus lou vassel, et sus chescune corne;	after the king the head in the middle, and make the cautery according to what we have said before, and the cautery on the vessel, and on each horn.
et se li malaides est fors et soffrans, se li fai cauteres si com j’ai dit a celui qui ait paralisie et mollification de cors, sus l’espinee dou dos et dou col, et soit li cauteres olivier selonc la maniere que j’ai dit.	and if the ailment is external and tolerable, make him cauteries as I have said for those who have paralysis and softening of the body, on the spine of the back and neck, and let the cautery be olive according to the manner that I have described.
Se li malaides est enfes, se li fai .i. cautere subtil selonc ceste maniere:	If the disease is in an infant, make to him 1 subtle cautery according to this manner:
Quant par la cause de melancolie sunt les superfluitez ou les moistors corrumpues et fleume grosse, adonques lou cauterize de teils cauteres com nos avons dit a celui qui ait paralisie.	When through the cause of melancholy there are corrupted humours and thick phlegm, then cauterize it with mild cauteries as we have said for one who has paralysis.
Et se par la cause de melancolie est li superfluitez declinans a melancolie, et est li cors dou malaide moistes, adonc li done a boivre chose par coi li cervelz soit mundifiez, selonc ceu qu’il est devant en la division.	And if through the cause of melancholy there is the surplus declining to melancholy, and the body of the patient is moist, then give him something to drink by which the brain is cleansed, according to what it says before in the division.
Aprés reis lou chief dou malaide;	After the king the head of the ailment;
aprés fai I torteil de lin bien fait, ausi com I cercle, si le met emmi le chief;	After that, make a well-made linen bandage, as a circle, and put it around the head.
et li malaides sié croisiez, et soit bien tenus de toutes pars;	and the ailment tied up, and held firmly on all sides.
aprés presente le linement, et vaut mues de burre de berbis ancien;	After that, present the linen, and apply the plasters of old beaver fur;
et lou chaufe a feu tempreement, si que li dois s’on li boute le puisse soffrir;	and heat the fire gently so that he can bear it when you apply it to him.
aprés vuide le cercle par dedens emmi le chief, et lou laisse refroidier;	after emptying the circle within the head, and letting it cool.
et fai ce a malaide chescune semaine une fois avec autre governement boin, tant qu’il soit sanez.	and do this to the patient once every week with other good treatment until he is healed.
Ou se tu vues cauterize lou en faisant poins plusors a tot le cautere.	Or if you want to cauterize it all over by making multiple points on the whole cautery.
Ceste maniere de cautere amoistit le cerveil igaument;	This cautery moistens the brain greatly;
et puis met sus coton moilliet en burre et en graisse de geline.	and then put on cotton wetted in butter and grease of goose fat.
de l’awe des eulz	of their eyes
Quant awe vient premierement as eulz par les signes que j’ai dit en la division, adonques encomence et done boivre au malaide chose mundifiant le chief, et le warde de toutes moistors, et lou fai suer ou bain plusors fois a jeun.	When eye disease first appears in the eyes through the signs that I have described in the division, then begin and give the patient drink that cleanses the head, and guard it from all moisture, and make him sweat in the bath several times while fasting.
Aprés li comande a rere son chief, et li fai cautere emmi le chief, et li fai II cauteres sus les II temples se li dessendemens de l’awe est as II eulz ensamble, ou en I se li dessendemens est en I;	Afterwards he orders him to turn his head and cauterizes the scalp, doing 2 cauteries on the 2 temples if the headache is in both eyes together, or one if it is in one eye;
et cope a tout le cautere toutes les voines et les arteres que sont desoz le keur, et soient li cautere lonc selon lou large de la temple;	and cut all the veins and arteries that are beneath the head with the cautery, and make the cauteries long according to the width of the temples;
et te warde de decorrement de sanc, et se tu vois trop de sanc issir, si li estainche de teil pooir com tu as.	and guard against bleeding, and if you see too much blood coming out, then stop it with as much power as you have.
Et je t’enseignerai en l’estraction des arteres et a l’incision la cautele coment tu l’estencheras;	And I will teach you in the extraction of arteries and in the incision, the cautery how to stop it;
et aucune fois fait on cautere ou hatereil desoz les II os derrier.	and sometimes a cautery or hot iron is placed beneath the two bones at the back.
dou cors des larmes	where tears come from the body
Quant les larmes des eulz sont ancienes et acostumees et sont sus les voines, ou delez les arteres que sont en l’aparance dou chief defors;	When tears are old and accustomed to being on veins, or beneath arteries that are on the outside of the head;
et on voit que c’est des superfluitez froides fleumatiques, adonques li fai le cautere que j’ai dit en l’encomencement de l’awe dessendant as eulz:	and it is seen that this is from cold phlegmatic excesses, then he should do the cautery which I have mentioned earlier in the downward breath to the eyes:
I cautere emmi le chief, et II cauteres sus les II temples, et II cauteres ou haiterel desoz les II os;	I cautery on the head, and two cauteries on the two temples, and two cauteries or hot irons beneath the two bones;
et s’il i a besoigne plus, si le cauterize saigement desus le sorcil a tout I petit cautere.	and if more is needed, then he should cauterize bleeding above the eyebrow with a small cautery.
dou cors des larmes par dedens les eulz	through which the body cries inside them
Quant tu le medicines selonc ceu que nos avons dit en la division, et il ne profite mie, adonques done a boivre a malaide III nuis cochies;	When you treat him according to what we have said in the previous section, and he does not improve, then give the patient three nights of drinking through a tube.
aprés li reis le chief, et li fai cautere ou mileu dou cautere olivaire;	After the king, take the head, and cauterize it with olive oil in the middle of the cautery.
et fai II cauteres dou cautere qui est apelez «clavilis» sus les II sorcis, un poc desoz les chevous;	And make two cauteries with a cautery called 'clavicle' above the two joints, a little under the hairline;
et te warde de l’artere que tu ne la coper.	and be careful of the artery that you do not pierce it.
Et c’est li forme dou cautere qui est apelez «clavilis»:	And this is the form of the cautery which is called "clavilis":
Quant li papiere de l’oil est mollifie de maladie et de moistor, adonques la cautarize de cest cautere qui est apelez «olivare».	When the paper of the eye is softened by disease and moisture, then cauterize it with this cautery, which is called "olive".
de coi ci est li forme:	of which there is the shape:
Et se tu vues si fai II cauteres sus les II sorcis ausi lons com li sorcilz sont;	And if you see, make two cauteries on the joints as long as the joints are;
et n’i lassiez mie la main fors que tant que li tierce partie de la papiere soit arse, selonc la maniere que j’ai dit.	and do not leave the hand except that the third part of the paper is burned, according to the manner I have described.And if you see, make two cauteries on the joints as long as the joints are; and do not leave the hand except that the third part of the paper is burned, according to the manner I have described.
dou poil qui point l’oil	the hair that points the eye
Aucune fois avient que li poil des oilz sont convertit au pardedens, et poignent l’oil, et i fait on cauteres selonc II manieres:	Sometimes the hair of the eyelids turns towards the inside, and prick the eye, and they make cauteries according to two methods:
c’est a savoir de feu, ou de medicine ardant.	it is known from fire, or burning medicine.
Ou cautere de feu comande au malaide qu’il laisse les poilz tant qu’il soient lons et igals;	The patient should be instructed to let the hairs grow long and even by using a fire cautery;
et s’il le poignent a lor nassance, se li estraint les eulz qu’il ne se muevent tant qu’il naissent.	and if they prick at their base, hold them steady so they do not move until they grow out.
Quant il naissent et i sont igalz, adonques met le malaide en ton sain;	When they have grown and are even, then put the patient in a warm bath;
aprés seigne sus la papiere des eulz une figure que soit ausi com li fuelle dou mirte, et soit li comencemens dou signe delez les poilz;	afterwards, draw on paper a figure that is similar to the hollow of a myrtle berry, and let the beginning of the sign be among the hairs;
puis i met coton moilliet en glaire d’uef et muscillaige de persillion sus l’oil, puis eschaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	then place wet cotton soaked in egg white and musk of periwinkle over the eye, then heat the cautery so that it matches the shape;
Aprés cauterize sus la figure que tu as signiet poc et poc mout de fois, que li keurs soit ars lai endroit;	Afterwards, cauterize little by little according to the figure you have drawn, so that the heat reaches the area;Car en l’ovraige de cest chapistre avient maintes fois evacuation de sanc a l’ovrir la voinne, et a l’incision sus aposteme,
et li signes de la santeit de l’uevre est que tu voies la papiere retraite, et les poilz levez a la pointure de l’oil;	and the sign of health is when you see the gums recede, and the hair stands up on the tip of the nose;
adonques lieve ta main, et laisse ensi III jors, puis i met coton moilliet en burre tant que li eschaudure soit ostee;	then release your hand, and leave it for three days, then apply wet cotton in butter until the blister is healed;
aprés le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	after cleaning the wound until it is healed.
Et se aprés ceu vienent li poilz, et li papiere est mollifie adonques rencomence le cautere sus cel leu meisme, si com tu as fait premiers;	And if afterwards hair comes and the gums are soft then restart the cautery on the same spot, just as you did before;
et se li poil sont defuer, si le cauterize tant que li papiere soit levee a son leu natureil, et soit igals, et ne poignent mie li poil l’oil.	and if the hair has fallen out, then cauterize until the gums are raised to their natural level, and are even, and do not prick the eye.
Li cauteres de medicine ardant est que tu comandes au malaide qu’il laisse les poilz tant qu’il soient grans et igalz, puis fai de parchemin la forme de la foille de mirte;	The hot cautery of medicine is that you instruct the patient to let the hair grow long and even, then make a parchment in the shape of a myrtle leaf;
puis pren de savon fransois et de vive chalz, de chescun une .З., et broie ensamble bien;	then take French soap and live lye, of each one-third, and grind them well together;
et le fai hastanment, si qu’il ne refroide, puis en espant sus la forme que tu es fait sicom la foille dou mirte, et met sus la papiere des eulz;	and make it quickly so that it does not cool down, then spread it on the mold that you have made like the myrtle leaf, and put them on paper.
et se li maladie tient en I oil soulement, si doit on ovrer en I, et se en ambedous ausi;	and if the illness is only in one eye, then it should be treated there, and if in both, then in both;
et met desoz l’oil coton moilliet en abin d’uef;	and put underneath the eye cotton moistened with egg white;
et li chiés dou malaide soit en ton sain et met ton doi mostrant sus la medicine, et presse I poc et lou muef toutes les fois que li malaide sent mordication de la medicine, car il sent mordication ausi com de feu.	and the head of the patient should be in a healthy position, and put your hand showing under the medicine, and press it gently and move it around every time the patient feels a stinging sensation from the medicine, for it stings as if it were fire.
Quant tu as ceu fait longement, si oste la medicine a ton doit.	When you have done this for a long time, then remove the medicine from your finger.
Et quant li mordication sera passee, si leve le leu d’awe, et rewarde se tu vois la papiere levee ausi com s’ele estoit levee par constraignement de feu ou par incision;	And when the stinging has passed, lift up the eye, and check if you see the paper lifted as it was lifted by the constraint of fire or by incision;
et s’il est ensi, si est bien.	and if it is like that, then it is good.
Se ceu non, si remet encor de la medicine sus lou leu ou li medicine n’ait ovreit, tant que tes ovraiges soit igalz, et tes eulz mis a point;	If not, then apply more medicine to the area until the work is equalized and the eyes are set in their proper position.
puis met sus coton moilliet en burre tant que li keurs ars soit cheus, aprés cure le leu de l’oignement qui est apelez «dyafenis» et d’autre, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then place wet cotton wool on the wound until it heals, after cleaning the area of the ointment that is called "diafenes" and others, so that it is clean.
Et se t’est mestier que tu te warde bien a ton ovraige par grant warde qu’il ne chiece point de la medicine as eulz.	And if you need to take care of your work well with great care that it does not leak medicine into the eyes.
Et se li papiere devient mole aprés, et li poil poignent en l’oil, si recomence la medicine sus celui leu qui est mollifiez de la papiere proprement, ensi com tu as fait devant;	And if the skin becomes soft afterwards, and the hairs prick in the eye, then recommence the medicine on the area that has softened of the paper properly, just as you did before;
aprés le cure tant qu’il soit sanez;	After cleaning it until it is healed;and li poils soient lons, et li oculi ne se muevent en lor nass
et c’est li forme de la fuelle dou mirte:	and the hairs are long, and the eyes do not move in their growth: and this is the shape of the fire-shackle:se li fuelles
Et saichés que li eul des homes sont divers en grandor et en petitece, et selonc ceu soit tes constraignemens;	And know that the eyes of men are diverse in size, and according to this is your constraint;et s’il adonsent les poils qui sont sur la fuellie, il se doit mettre le cautere en lor nassance et le tenir tant qu’il ardisse, si com tu as dit;
et ne soit mie reponue li droite voie a celui cui est li estude de cest art.	and is not returned to the right path by one who has studied this art.
de la cure de fistule par cautere	on the treatment of fistulas by cautery
Quant tu cures fistule si com nos avons dit en divisions des maladies, et tes cures ne profitent mie, adonques covient il que tu li fais cautere selonc ceste maniere.	When you are treating a fistula as we have described in the divisions of diseases, and your treatments are not helping, then you should use cautery according to this method.
Comande au malaide qu’il mette son chief en ton sain;	Instruct the patient to place his head in your lap;
et teigne li menistres son chief entre tes mains en teil maniere qu’il ne se mueve, ne ne demoinne son chief;	and have the assistant hold the patient's head between his hands in such a way that it does not move or nod;
aprés met coton moilliet en abin d’uef ou en jus de persillion sus l’oil;	then soak cotton in vinegar or pigeon droppings and place it over the eye;
aprés chaufe le cautere qui est teilz:	next, heat the cautery iron to a medium temperature;
et est chevez au chief si com li forme d’une penne de vouteul, ensamble la queil soit li cautere;	and hold it to the head in the shape of an arch over the eye;
se tu vues, si soit apointé des l’un chief dusc’a l’autre, et se tu vues, si soit ausi com une tente;	if you see it pointing from one side to the other, and if you see, it is also like a tent;
mais toutevoie, cist qui est chevez vaut mues por ton ovraige.	but all the same, this is how it should be held for your work.
Aprés presse la fistule s’ele est overte, et en trai la porriture, et la seche;	After opening the fistula, press and drain it, and then dry it;
et s’ele est close, si la oevre, et trai fuers la bowe;	and if it is closed, she works on it and draws out the bowstring;
aprés met sus le cautere chaut forment, et tien ta main au cautere a la partie dou neif ensus de l’oil, que ta mains ne faice folie;	afterwards, put on the hot cautery quickly, and hold your hand on the cautery at the place under the eye, so that your hand does not make a mistake;
et met le cautere en la graisse de l’oil, et la corromp.	and put the cautery in the fat of the eye, and corrupt it.
Se tu viens au comencement dou cautere jusc’a l’os, si serait bien.	If you come to the beginning of cautery as far as the bone, that would be good.
Se ceu non, si rencomence le cautere encor une fois, et autre se tu en as mestier, et le laisse III jors;	If not, then repeat the cautery again once more, and another time if you need to, and leave it for three days;
aprés i met sus coton moilliet en burre, et lou cure de l’oignement desiccatif tant qu’il soit sanez, et se XL jors passent qu’il ne soit sanez, si met sus medicine ague corrosive tant que li os soit descovers;	afterwards, put on wet cotton in butter, and let it heal with the ointment until it is healed, and if 40 days pass and it is not healed, then put on corrosive medicine until the bone is exposed;
et lou reis selonc ceu que il venrait en son chapistre.	and let the king do as he wishes in his kingdom.
Et i a une maniere de cautere de fistule que aucun des anciens dirent.	And there is a way of cauterizing a fistula which some of the ancients spoke of.
Entens a fistule, et fens le leu;	Understand about a fistula, and probe the area;si li fistule a III entres, si ne fuige pas le cautere, et
aprés met en la fendure I camahan subtil de coi ci est li forme:	after placing it in the split , apply a subtle chamois which has the form :
et i font a la quantiteit d’une .З. de plonc;	and they make to the amount of an egg;
et tien ta main ou camahan fermement, et ne se mueve li malaides nes point, que li plons fondus ne corre a son oil;	and hold your hand on the chamois firmly so that the patient does not move at all, so that the molten lead does not run into his eye;
et covient c’on mette sus l’oil a malaide coton moilliet en abin d’uefz ou en awe:	and it is necessary to place on the patient's eye wet cotton soaked in vinegar or in water:
li plonc si art lou leu de fistule, et lou saine per mervillouse saniteit.	the lead will heal the fistula, and the healthy eye will be miraculously healed.
Et se li fistule est sanee per le cautere que nos avons dit, c’est boin.	And if the fistula is healed by the cauterization we have described, that is good.
Se ce non, si covient aministrer pertus au neif, et ramener la fistule au cors dou neif selonc ceu qu’il covient en som propre leu.	If not, then one must open the vein and draw the fistula back into the body of the vein according to what is appropriate in its own place.Et si li fistule sont en la main, ou en la pie, ou en autrui membrez del corps, si covient aministrer pertus au neif qui sont approchiez de li fistule:
des crevaices en levres	cracks in the lips
Mout de fois avienent crevaices en levres que sont apelees «poil», et meismement en levres des enfans.	Many times cracks occur in the lips that are called "hair," especially in children's lips.
Quant tu cures ces crevaices de ceu que nos avons dit en divisions, et li cure ne profite, adonques eschaufe .i. petit cautere cultellaire selonc ceste forme:	When you treat these cracks as we have described in the sections above, and the treatment does not help, then heat a small scalpel according to this shape:
Et le met hastanment en celles crevaices tant qu’il viegne jusc’a font;	And they place it in these holes until it reaches the bottom;
aprés cure le leu de cerote tant qu’il soit sanez.	afterwards, clean the area of ointment until it is healed.
de l’aposteme de la goule	of the abscess of the throat
Quant apostume vient en la racine de la goule ou en l’uve, ou ou palais, ou as racines des dens, aprés fait porriture et ront et est enveillis et devient fistule;	When an abscess forms at the root of the gum or in the eye, or on the palate, or at the roots of the teeth, afterwards it becomes suppurant and rot, and is lanced and becomes a fistula;
et tu le cures si com nos avons dit en divisions, et il ne profite mie:	and you treat it as we have said in sections, and it does not help at all:
adonques covient il que tu aies I cautere selonc la quantiteit de la fistule;	therefore, you must have the cautery according to the quantity of the fistula;
aprés le bote ou pertus de la fistule, et tien ta main tant que li fer chaus viegne au font de li, et ou derrien leu;	after the opening of the fistula, and hold your hand so that the hot iron comes to the bottom of it, and at the back also;
et fai ensi une fois ou II, aprés le cure de ce que nos avons dit en cures, tant qu’il soit sanez;	and do this once or twice after treating it as we have said in treatments, until it is healed;
et s’il est curez ensi, c’est boin;	and if it is treated thus, that is good;
et se ceu non, si covient descovrir le leu et oster l’os corrumput, selonc ceu que vos le troverez en son chapistre.	and if not, then one must expose the area and remove the corrupted bone according to what you find in his shoulder joint.
dou movement des dens	of the movement of the teeth
Quant les gencives sont mollifies par moistor et les dens muevent, et tu le cures per medicines et ceu ne vaut, adonc met le chief dou malaide en ton sain;	When the gums are softened by moisture and the teeth move, and you treat it with medicine but it doesn't help, then put the head of the patient in your lap;
aprés eschaufe le cautere dont li forme venra ci aprés en teil maniere que tu mettes une cainne sor le dent;	After heating the cautery of which the form will come below in such a way that you put a cane on the tooth;
et met dedens le cautere chaut hastanment, et tien tant ta main que li malaides sente la chalor venant a la racine dou dent;	and put the hot cautery inside, and hold your hand so that the patient feels the heat coming to the root of the tooth;
aprés lieve ta main et rencomence le cautere selonc ta volenteit;	then lift your hand and reapply the cautery according to your will;
aprés emplisse li malaides sa bouche d’awe salee, et la teigne une houre et raiche fuers.	then fill the patient's mouth with salt water, and let him gargle for an hour and spit it out.
Et en teil maniere li dens qui estoit movans si est confermez, et li gencive mollifie restrainte, et li moistors corrumpue sechie.	And in this way, a tooth that was loose is made firm, and the gums are made soft and moist, and the corrupted moisture is dried up.
de la dolor des dens	of toothache
Quant dolor de dens vient por froidor, ou il i a froidor ou veir, et les cures de medicine ne valent, adonc i ait mestier de cautere selonc II manieres:	When toothache comes from coldness, or there is coldness or whiteness, and the remedies of medicine do not work, then cautery is needed in two ways:Ou cautere de feu comande au malaide qu’il laisse les poilz tant qu’il soient lons et igals; et s’il le poignent a lor nassance, se li estraint les eulz qu’
et cautere de burre et cautere de feu.	and fire cautery, instruct the patient to let the hairs grow long and even; and if they prick at their base, hold the eyes
Cautere de burre si est telz que tu preignes burre de vaiche, et le bout en une cuillier de fer ou d’arain;	Butter cautery is such that you take butter from a cow, and put it on the end of a spoon made of iron or copper.
aprés pren coton et envolope sus la pointe d’une tente, et la moille en burre bulit, et met sus le dent dolant hastanment et tien tant qu’il soit refroidiez;	Take cotton and wrap it around the tip of a skewer, then dip it in hot butter and apply it to the aching tooth until it cools.
et ensi fai sovent tant que sa vertus viegne a la racine de la dent, et se tu vues si moille laine et coton en burre froit, et met sus le dent doillant, et met sus I fer chaut tant que li feus viegne au chevement dou dent.	And so do this often until its virtue reaches the root of the tooth; and if you see moisture in wool and cotton, dip it in cold butter and apply to the aching tooth, and place hot iron on top until the fire reaches the gum of the tooth.
Li cauteres ensamble feu si est telz que tu preignes uns cainne de fer ou d’arain, et soit grosse si que li feus ne viegne a la bouche dou malaide;	Fire cauteries are performed with an iron or copper rod that is thick enough that the fire does not reach the patient's mouth.
aprés chaufe le cautere, de coi li forme venra ci aprés, et le met sus le dent et tien ta main tant que li cauteres soit refroidiez;	After you heat the cautery, in the shape that follows, apply it to the tooth and hold your hand there until the cautery cools.
fai ceu sovent, car li dolor sera ostee celui jor meisme ou l’endemain.	do so often, because the pain will go away that day or the next.
Et covient que li malaides emplisse sa bouche de boin burre en l’empressement de cel cautere, et puis le raiche fuer;	And it is necessary for the patient to fill his mouth with good butter quickly before this cautery, and then he can bear the heat;
et c’est li forme dou cautere:	and this is the form of the cautery:
Et fai cautere dou queil chief que tu voudras, et selonc ceu que tu as pooir;	And make a cautery of whatever size you want, according to what you are able;
et c’est li forme de la caine:	and this is the form of the tongs:
des scrophules	of scrofula
Quant les scrophules sont de fleume et de moistors froides, et ne sont obeissans a digestion par medicines, adonques eschaufe le cautere cheveit de coi ci aprés vient li forme, et ait II aovertures por les fumees a issir au cautere de l’autre partie;	When scrofula is caused by cold moisture and is unresponsive to medicine, then heat the cautery so that this form comes next, and it has two openings for the smoke to exit from the other side of the cautery;
et met le cautere chaut sus l’apostume une fois, ou II se mestier est, tant qu’il viegne au font de l’apostume;	and place the hot cautery on the abscess once, or as many times as necessary, until it reaches the bottom of the abscess;
et se li apostume est petis si met cautere selonc la quantiteit de l’apostume, et le laisse ensi III jors;	and if the abscess is small, apply the cautery according to the size of the abscess, and leave it for three days.
et met sus coton moilliet em burre tant que li arsure soit ostee;	and apply wet cotton on the burn until the scorching is healed;
aprés cure le leu d’oignemens et de tentes tant qu’il soit sanez.	afterwards, treat the area with ointments and poultices until it is healed.
Li forme de la cainne:	The form of the cane:
Quant les moistors vainquent sus les chenals dou pormon, et meismement quant ce vient de froide complexion, adonc covient que li malaides soit voidiez premiers par medicines solutives;	When moisture prevails upon the channels of the lungs, and especially when it comes from a cold complexion, then the patient must first be purged by solubilizing remedies;
aprés li fai cautere a la racine de la gorge, et te garde que tu ne venir mie jusc’a la gorge, et n’ardre dou keur mais c’un poc.	afterwards, apply the cautery to the root of the throat, and be careful not to go too far into the throat, and do not burn the heart but just a little.
Aprés li fai I autre cautere a la jointure dou col au chief de l’espinee, et soit li cauteres qui est apelez «clavile» de coi nos avons la forme devant;	Afterwards, apply another cautery at the junction of the neck and the head, at the top of the spine, and let the cautery be the one called 'clavicle', as we have described it earlier;
et cure le leu si com nos avons devant dit tant qu’il soit sanez.	and treat the area as we have said before, until it is healed.
de la toust	of the tongue
Quant tous et maladie de pormon sont de moistors froides, et li malaides nen ait fievre ne sechor, et est li maladie anciaine, se li fai .II cauteres sus la forcele en leus vuis;	When all illnesses of the stomach are due to cold moisture, and the patient has no fever or dryness, and the illness is chronic, then perform fire cauterization on the navel in the affected areas.

Et se tu vues, fai cautere en poignant a tot le cautere qui est apelez «poins» de coi li forme est ci devant en la maladie des oreilles;	And if you see it, perform a cauterization by piercing the entire cautery that is called "pin", according to the form described earlier for ear diseases;et si les poils sont lons et laies et ne se puet muevre li mal, fai cautere sus lor nassance de coi li cauteres qui est apelez «aguyl» selonc le
et soient li poins jusc’a XXX, ou enqui entor.	And if the hairs are long and laid back, and the patient cannot move, perform a cauterization at their base with the cautery that is called "needle", according to the following
Aprés cure le leu selonc ceu qui est devant dit, et soit li cauteres a III rains selonc ceste forme:	After curing the wound according to what has been said before, let there be three cauteries according to this form:
Et por ceu sont li cautere plus legier, por ceu que tu en fais .iij. a cop.	And for this reason cauteries are gentler when you do them three times.
de la dislocation de l’ajutoire	of the shoulder dislocation
Quant li chiés de l’ajutoire est desaloiez par cause de moistor, et on le remet a leu, et il n’i puet demorer ains revient adés et desalue par petit movement qui avient, si com nos avons esproveit, adonques covient il que tu ramoinnes la dislocation premierement.	When the head of the shoulder is dislocated due to moisture, and it is reset but cannot stay in place, repeatedly dislocating with slight movement as we have experienced, then you must first reset the dislocation.
Aprés soit sovinez li malaides sus son dos et sus son costeit;	Afterwards, have the patient lie on his back and on his side;
aprés lieve le keur qui est dedens le titillite as dois de ta main senestre;	then gently press his heart with the tip of your left hand;
et se li jointure est desaluee dedens, si eschaufe le cautere qui a II ners douqueil ci est li forme:	and if it is dislocated inside, heat up the cautery which has the shape of the nerve's path;
et cauterize lou keur tant qu’il le perce jusc’a costeit, et venrait li fugure dou cautere ensamble IIII cauteres;	and cauterize the heart until it pierces through to the side, and you will see the shape of the cautery in four places;
et por ceu est faite cautere avec le cautere qui a III ners, por coi li figure de cauterization sunt sis cauteres;	and for this reason, six cauteries are made with the cautery which has three nerves, so that the shape of the cauterizations are six cauteries;
et sont li nerf selonc la subtiliteit d’une tente et c’est li forme dou cautere qui a III ners:	and the nerves are according to the subtlety of a tent, and this is the shape of the cautery which has three nerves;
Et aucune fois est ajostez sus ce .i. nerf por coi il i a .viij. cauteres.	And sometimes it is placed on this one nerve so there are eight cauteries.
Aprés met sus le cautere porrelz broiez avec seil;	Afterwards, put crushed vitriol on the cautery;
aprés fai reposer le malaide, et ne soit meus li membres par lonc tens tant qu’il soit bien confortez.	Afterwards, have the patient rest, and do not move the limb for a long time until it is well healed.
Et s’il est desaloiez desus, liquelz chose avient poc, adonques fait cautere sus l’epaisse dou cautere clavile, ou mout de cauteres en poignant.	And if it is dislocated above, not much happens, therefore make the cautery on the thick part of the cautery clave, or a lot of cauteries in puncturing.
Car li jointure est refermee, et est ostee li moistor et est sanez li malaides.	Because the joint is closed and the moisture is removed and the patient is healed.
Quant en l’estomac vienent froidures et mout de moistors tant qu’il l’estraient a sa complexion, et sont multipliet li catharre a lui, et es manieres de cures acostumees et il ne profite mie, adonc covient que li malaides soit sovinez sus son dos, et estende ses jambes et ses mains.	When there are chills and a lot of moisture in the stomach, drawing it out to his complexion, and many catharres multiply in him, and he is not helped by the usual methods of treatment, then the patient should be placed on his back, extending his legs and arms.
De ceu en aprés li fai III cauteres I desoz la cuillier dou pis per la quantiteit d’un doi, a tout le cautere clavile, et II cauteres defuers les II costez tant que li figure des cauteres soit a III angles, et ait teil espaice entre l’une et l’autre qu’elles ne soient jointes ensamble quant elles giteront porriture;	Of this then after make three cauteries I under the collar bone by the quantity of a bean, at all cautery clave, and two cauteries apart on either side so that the figure of the cauteries is in three angles, and there is such space between them that they do not come together when they bend rot;
et soient li cautere si parfont qu’il porpreignent les II pars dou keur, et soit li figure des cauteres selonc ceste forme sens ajostement:	and be the cauteries so deep that they pustulate both parts of the heart, and be the figure of the cauteries according to this form without adjustment:
Et se tu vues cauterize d’un grant cautere enmi l’estomac selonc ceste forme;	And if you wish to cauterize a large cautery within the stomach according to this form:
et celui qui avra paour de cest cautere, cauterize en poignant et seigne sus l’estomac i. point selonc la quantiteit que tu vues d’enche;	and whoever is afraid of this cautery, cauterize in pointing and sign upon the stomach I. point according to the quantity that you wish to eat;
puis le cauterize a tot le cautere qui est apelez «poins».	then cauterize it at all cautery which is called "points.
Aprés le cure de la cure que nos avons eut devant, tant qu’il soit sanez.	After the cure of the ulcer that we have discussed earlier, until it is healed.
Quant au foie vient dolor de froit et de moistor et de grosse ventositeit, tant qu’il est fuer mis de sa complexion natureil per les superfluitez;	When pain in the liver comes from cold and moisture and excessive windiness, as it is forced out of its natural disposition by excesses.
et li malaides est curez de ceu que nos avons dit en divisions, et il ne li profite mie, si covient que li malaides soit sovinez sus son haitereil;	and the patient is cured of this as we have said in the sections above, but if he does not benefit, then he should be bled over his liver.
et signe d’enche III cauteres selonc ceste forme et ceste figure et ceste quantiteit sus lou foie, defuer les ypocondres, lai ou li coutes de l’ome vient;	and perform three cauteries according to this form and figure and quantity over the liver, avoiding the hypogastric region, where the intestines of man are.
et ait d’espaice entre chaicun cautere la groissece d’un doi;	There should be the thickness of a thumb between each cautery.
et soient li cautere dou lonc dou cors, et ne presser mie mout ta main a tot le cautere;	The cauteries should be held lightly on the body, and your hand should not press down too hard during the entire cautery process.
et soit arse tant soulement li moitiez dou keur, et soit li malaides drois sus ses piez;	Only half of the cautery should be applied at a time, and the patient should be kept upright on his feet.
et s’il ne peut, si soit gisans, et estende ses jambes, et lieve ses brais;	And if he cannot stand, then he should lie down and extend his legs and raise his arms.
et c’est li forme:	and this is the form:
Et se ta volentez est, si cauterize ces cauteres dou cutellaire, se tu es subtilz et saiges en l’art, et te warde que tu n’ardes mie tout le keur, car tu feroies sechier tout le cors;	And if you wish, you may cauterize with the sword, if you are skillful and wise in the art, and be careful not to burn the whole body; you would cause it to wither.
et qu’il ne viegne jusc’a boueil, car li keurs est mout subtilz lai endroit, et lou saiches por voir.	and do not let it come to boiling, for the skin is very delicate in that place, and you can tell by looking.
Quant il a apostume au foie, et tu vues savoir s’il est en la char dou foie ou en la toile:	When there is an abscess on the liver, and you wish to know if it is in the flesh of the liver or in the membrane:
s’il est en la char, se sent li malaides dolor ne mie trop fort;	if it is in the flesh, then the pain is not too severe;
et s’il est en la toile, si sent dolor forsenee.	and if it is in the membrane, then there is violent pain.
Et lors quant ceste cure desoit les mires, si covient que li malaides soit sovinez sus sa teste;	And when this treatment is being applied to the abscesses, the patient should be reclining on his back;
et puis seigne d’enche le leu ou li apostumes est, et puis chaufe le cautere qui est semblans au rais, de coi ci est li forme:	then press down on the spot where the abscess is, and then heat the cautery which is like a rod, and this is how it is done:
Et cauterize I cautere tant que li keurs soit ars, et viegne jusc’a syphac, tant que li porreture soit toute fuers;	And cauterize with the cautery until the skin is burned, and goes as far as the nerve, until all the pus is gone.
aprés la cure selonc la cure des essues tant qu’il soit sanez;	after the wound has healed, according to the treatment of wounds, until it is healed;
et ne covient mie que de cest cautere use nuls fuers que cil qui ait estudieit longement en l’art de medicine, et par cui mains cestes maladies ont corrut aucune fois.	and one must not use this cautery except by someone who has studied medicine for a long time, and by whom these diseases have been corrupted at times.
Adonques puet il hardiement ovrer, et toutevoies il me semble que mues vaut li laissier.	Therefore he can safely operate, and in any case it seems to me that it is better to leave it alone.
dou cautere de pleuresin	of the cautery for pleurisy
Li ancien dirent que on doit faire a pleuresin cauteres de racines d’aristologe, et en teil maniere:	The ancients said that one should make cauteries for pleurisy from the roots of aristologist, and in such a way:
pren une racine d’aristologe longe, la plus grant que tu poras troveir, et soit seche, et soit ausi grosse et ausi longe comme tes dois;	take a root of aristologist that is long, dry, as thick and as long as your two fingers;
