adonques covient il que tu i boutes I fil de lin un poc gros, et soit noez de mains nous, et ait entre chescun nout d’espaice I doit ou moins;	therefore you must insert a thread of linen that is somewhat thick, and let it be tied by the hand, with a knot between each nostril, no more than a finger's width apart;
et mette li malaides lou chiés dou fil en son neif a som pooir, et traie en odorant tant qu’il viegne par lou neif dedens la bouche;	and let the patient hold the thread in his nose to its full extent, and pull it through the nose into the mouth until he feels an odor;
et maintes fois font ensi li enfant as escoles, et c’est legiere chose a celui qui le vuet faire;	and many children do this in school, and it is an easy thing for anyone who wants to do it;
puis tien le chief qui vient par lou neif a une main, et l’autre chief qui vient par la bouche a l’autre main, et saiche l’un aprés l’autre en soiant as nous qui sont ou fil.	then hold the head that comes from the nose in one hand and the head that comes from the mouth in the other, and twist them one after the other while standing as we do when spinning yarn.
Fai ceu tant que tu saiches que li nout ont corrompue celle char, puis trai lou filz, essue le sanc, et moille lou fil en oignement egiptien, et le remet derechief au neis si com devant;	Do this until you know that the thread has corrupted the flesh, then pull the thread, wipe off the blood and soak the thread in Egyptian ointment, and put it back in the nose as before.
fai ceu III jors ou plus, tant que li oignemens corrode tout ceu qui est demorez de char;	do this for three days or more, until the ointment corrodes all that remains of the flesh;
et puis met ou neis une caine de plonc aucuns jors tant qu’il soit sanez, et s’il a mestier de medicines sechans, si en use;	and then put in the nose a plug of cotton wool for several days until it is healed, and if there is need for dry medicine, use it.
et c’est li forme de l’estrument por purgier lou chief, a coi on distille les oiles et les medicines ou neis:	and this is the form of the instrument for cleansing the nose, through which one distills oils and medicines into the nose:
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain, semblant a une lampe overte, si com une cainne, et li conduis ausi;	And it can be of silver or bronze, resembling an open lamp, like a candle, and guide it likewise.
et se tu vues, si fai une cainne close, et soit li estrumens plains por espurgier lou chief;	And if you wish to make a closed candle, then the instrument should be filled for purging the head;
et ait I mainche au chief por lou tenir quant on chaufe l’oile ou aucune liquor.	and hold it to the head to keep it steady when one heats the oil or any other liquid.
de la char sor le neis	of the heart above the diaphragm
Maintes fois naist au chief dou neis une maladie qui est apelee «telul», et croist et devient grans adés, tant qu’il est vis chose au regarder;	Many times a disease arises in the head from the nose, called "telul", which grows and becomes large, so that it is an ugly sight to behold;
et por ceu covient que tu lou copes au comencement, et l’oste tout fuer, puis met sor leu lou cautere ou la medicine ardant;	and for this reason one should cut it at the beginning and remove all of it, then place upon it the cautery or burning medicine;
et s’on le tarde a coper tant qu’il soit grans, si pren warde s’il est durs, de fuxe color, de povre sens:	and if one delays in cutting it until it becomes large, then take care, for if it is hard, of foul colour, and poor in sensation:
si ne lou touchier mie de fer car c’est uns apostemes enchancrez, car quant on le cope aucune fois, si en vient grant malice au malaide;	do not touch it with iron, for it is an encrusted abscess, for when one cuts it, great mischief comes to the patient;
et se li apostemes est de soef touchement, non mie de fuxe color, et tu vois c’on le puisse tout coper, si vuide le malaide et lou cope sens paor, et cure le leu de choses sechans et restraignans.	and if the abscess is from a soft touch, not from a flow of color, and you see that one can completely cover it, then empty the patient and cover without fear, and treat the area with dry and constricting things.
quant li neis est copez et cosus	when the heart is cut and sewn
Saiches que quant solutions de continuation vient en une de ces cartillagines ovraiges, i profite poc, fuer que en aucuns homes.	Know that when the solution of continuity comes in one of these cartilage openings, it is beneficial to some people.
Il covient donques cant ceu avient a aucun, si regarde se li plaie est fresche a tout son sanc;	Therefore, when this happens to someone, one must see if the wound is fresh with all its blood;
et adonques ajoste les II levres a une costure, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez;	and then bring the two lips together with a stitch, and then treat it until it is healed;
et se les levres sont ja desevrees d’une part et d’autre, si covient que tu escorches toutes les parties de lor keur tant qu’elles sainent, puis assemble les II levres a une costure, et l’estraint, et poudre sus poudre de sanc de dragon, et encens broiet;	and if the lips are torn on both sides, one must scrape all the parts of their skin until they heal, then bring the two lips together with a stitch, hold them tight, and powder dragon's blood over powder, and ground incense.
et met sus les poudres une piece d’emplaustre de fort ou d’autre emplaustre soudant, et le laisse tant qu’il chiece par lui, puis le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	and place a piece of strong plaster or other binding plaster over the powders, and let it stay until it comes off on its own, then treat it with ointment until it is healed.
Li maniere de la costure si est que tu assembles la solution:	The manner of the cautery is as follows: assemble the solution.
ou par aguilles, si com nos avons dit en la costure dou ventre;	or with needles, as we have said in the suturing of the belly;
ou par fil, si com je le t’ai fait savoir.	or with thread, as I have already informed you.
des apostemes des levres	of lip abscesses
A mains homes avient dedens les levres aposteme dur, semblans a grains de veces, et menor et plus grant;	Within the lips there occur hard abscesses, resembling peas in size, both smaller and larger;
adonques couvient que tu tornes les levres, et fendes sus chescun nout, et le prent as pinceures et le cope en chescune partie;	therefore you must turn the lips inside out, and slit them on each side, and take them with tweezers and squeeze in every part;
puis emple lou leu aprés l’incision de vitriole broiet, tant que li sans soit estainchiez;	then apply vitriol powder to the wound, until the bleeding stops;
et puis lou leive d’aisil, et cure lou leu de choses seches tant qu’il soit sanez.	and then leave it with garlic, and treat the area with dry substances until it is healed.
de la char des gencives	of gum swelling
Maintes fois naist sus les gencives char ajostee, que li ancien apelent «albulus»;	Many times there grow on the gums a swelling called by the ancients 'albus'.;
si covient que tu la sostienes as tenailles, et la cope a sa racine, et laisse corre la bowe ou le sanc;	You should hold it with tweezers and squeeze it at its root, letting the pus or blood run out;
puis met sor le leu vitriole broiet, ou autres poudres restraignans et desiccatives;	then put on vitriol powder, or other restraining and drying powders;
et se celle char revient aprés l’incision, et maintes fois avient, si la cope la seconde fois, et la cauterize:	and if the vein bleeds again after the incision, and it happens many times, then cauterize it a second time:
si ne revient mie aprés le cautere;	if it does not bleed after cautery;
et ce sont les formes des estrumens por coper.	and these are the forms of fistulas to cover.
des sordens	of the eyes, and to the
Aucunes fois sont assemblees au chief des dens, dedens la bouche entre les gencives, escorces qui sont laides et aspres;	Sometimes they are gathered at the top of teeth, inside the mouth between the gums, ugly and rough scabs;s’il est en l’un et l’autre chief de la dent, si le chef prend la couleur du fer:
et aucune fois sont li dent noir et citrin et vers, tant que li corruption vient a la gencive, et sont li dent puant;	and if it is at both ends of the tooth, its tip takes on the color of iron: and sometimes teeth are black, yellow, and green, as far as the corruption reaches the gums, and the teeth stink;si le coruption vient entre la gencive et li dent si que la gencive
si covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains, et ses chiés soit en ton saint, et reis les dens ou les escorces aperent, tant qu’il n’i demore rien;	if the corruption comes between the gum and the tooth so that the patient sits in your hands, and his jaw is in your holy hand, examine the teeth or scabs until nothing remains;et si la corruption est entre li dent et la gencive si que la gencive soit eschaude, et la dent froide:
et ensi fai de la noiror et de la verdor, et de la jaunice et des autres taiches, tant qu’elles soient mondees;	and so it is with darkness and greenness, and yellowing and other discolourations, until they have healed.
et s’on oste ceu que i est a la premiere rasion, c’est boin;	And if one removes what is at the root of it, that is good.
se ceu non, si rencomence a rere le secont jor et lou tier, tant que tu aies tout reis;	If not, then one should begin again on the second and third day, until everything has healed.
et saiches que li dent ont mestier de diverses formes d’estrumens por reire, selonc ceu que li oevre lou demoustre, por ceu que li raseur dont on reit defuer les dens ont autres formes que cil dont on reit entre les dens;	And know that teeth require various instruments to reset, according to what the work demonstrates to you, for the forceps with which one resets the teeth have a different shape from those used to reset teeth inside.
et cestes formes et autres soient avec toi appareillies.	You should have these shapes and others among your tools.
Il covient quant tu cures lou dent de sa dolor que tu tardes dou traire tant com tu pues, car ce ne doit om mie faire;	When you treat a tooth for its pain, you should take as long as you can, for one must not hurry this.Et se li dent sont si apaisiez et la dolour si desraiz que li dent n’ont plus grant dolor, s’il sunt entre les dens, adonc leve li dent
car c’est une substance mout haute jusc’a donc c’on n’ait point d’excusation dou raier.	because it is a very high substance just until one has no excuse to pull.
Adonques quant li malaides est constrains dou traire, si covient que tu soies certains dou dent doillant.	Then, when the patient is compelled to pull, you must be certain of your teeth.
Maintes fois desoit li dolor lou malaide, et cuide qu’elle soit ou dent saint, et fait traire le boin dent;	Many times the pain deceives the patient and he thinks it is in the tooth of Saint, and pulls out the good tooth;
et toutevoie ne se depart mie li dolor per ceu, tant que li malvais estrais, car nos l’avons ja veut faire a ces sainors;	and yet the pain does not leave him because of this, as long as the bad teeth remain, because we have already tried to do it with those healers;
et quant tu es bien certains dou dent doillant, si covient que tu escorches entor lou dent a tout i. spatumile fort por warder la gencive de toutes pars;	and when you are quite sure of the tooth that hurts, then you should scrape around the tooth all around with a strong spatulum to push back the gums from all sides;
puis le mues a tes dois ou as tenailles subtilz au premier poc et poc, tant qu’il soit bien eslochiés, puis i afferme bien les tenailles;	then pull it with your fingers or with fine tweezers gently and gently until it is well loosened, then grip the tweezers tightly;
et soit li chiés dou malaide en ton saint entre tes genous, et lou tien bien si qu’il ne se mueve.	and let the patient be in a seated position between your knees, holding him so he doesn't move.
Aprés estrai lou dent droitement sens brisier, et s’il ne saut fuer, si prent aucun de ces estrumens et le boute dedens de chescune part legierement, et lou remuef si com tu as fait premier.	Then extract the tooth firmly without breaking it, and if it does not come out, take one of these instruments and insert it into each side gently, and move it as you did before.
Et se li dens est perciez et mengiez, si covient que tu l’emplisses de drapelz, lai ou li pertus sont;	And if the teeth are broken and eaten away, then you must fill the holes with linen.
et si l’estraint subtilment as tenailles, que il ne brise a l’estraindre;	and if you hold it tightly with tweezers so that it does not break while being held.
et covient mout saigement ovrer entor la gencive por deschaucier lou dent.	and one must work around the gum to loosen the tooth.
Et te done bien en warde que tu ne le brises, et en remaigne une partie, et reveigne au malaide par la malice de la racine plus grans dolors de la premiere.	And be careful that you don't break it, or part of it remains, and the pain returns worse than before because of the root's sharp edge.
Et te warde que tu ne faices mie ensi com font li ignorant sainor, qui par lor haste et par lor hardiesce brisent aucune fois le charreit, et n’i amenistrent mie ceu que nos avons conteit;	And be wary that you do not act like the ignorant healers who, in their haste and boldness, sometimes break the jaw, and do not follow what we have described:
mais font venir aucune fois par l’oquison de ceu grant maladie por les racines que i demorent, ou por lou charreit qu’il brisent, si com nos avons sovent veut;	but sometimes bring about great illness through the roots that remain, or break the jaw, as we have often seen;
et quant li dens est trais, si lavez lou leu de vin ou d’aisil et de seil;	and when the tooth is drawn, wash the socket with wine or garlic and salt;
et se decorremens de sanc i vient, que sovent avient, si emple lou leu de vitriole broiet;	and if bleeding occurs, which often happens, apply crushed vitriol to the socket;
et se ceu ne vaut, si le cauterize.	and if this does not work, then cauterize it.
Les formes des estrumens, a coi om muet les dens premier, soient a longes pointes et a gros mainches, qu’il ne doublent mie quant tu trairas le dent;	The forms of instruments, with which one pulls out teeth, should have long points and thick handles so that they do not break when you pull the tooth.
et ce sont les formes:	and these are the forms:
Et soient de gros membres si qu’il ne ploient mie au traire, et soient de fer inde bien fait, et soient dentez por mues tenir.	And be made of large pieces so that they don't bend during pulling, and be made of good iron, and be serrated to hold the gums.
de la racine des dens	from the root of teeth
Quant li racine demoure au traire, si covient que tu mettes sor le leu coton moilliet em burre I jor ou II, tant que li leus soit amolis, pues i boute les tenailles qui sont apelees «algefri», de coi li chiés semblet bec de soigne;	When the root remains in the socket, one should put wet cotton on it for a day or two until the socket softens, and then one uses tweezers called "algefri" which look like a pair of tongs, to pull out the tooth.
et soient dedens faites ausi com une lime et c’est li forme:	and they should be made like a file inside, and this is the form:
Et se les racines ne vuellent issir a tout ces tenailles, si covient que tu descuevre la char tot entor la racine, et i met l’estrument qui est apelez «althali», c’est a savoir palainche, de coi ci est li forme:	And if the roots will not come out with all these tweezers, then you must uncover the flesh all around the root and insert the instrument called 'althali', that is, forceps, of which this is the form:
Et soit fors et gros si qu’il ne brise mie, et se li racine saut par ceu, c’est boin;	And it should be strong and thick so that it doesn't break, and if the root comes out with it, all the better.
se ceu non, si t’aide de toz les estrumens, de coi les formes vienent ci aprés:	if not, then use all the instruments, whose forms are described below:
Et si s’aide on de cest estrument qui ait .ij. rains, de coi ci est li forme:	And let one assist with this instrument which has .ij. tips, of which this is the form:
et d’autres ferremens qui sont devant en la rasion des dens, et de cest estrument qui semble unes grans tenailles, dont ci est li forme:	and other tools which are before in the reason of the teeth, and of this instrument which resembles large tweezers, of which this is the form:
Et soit cist estrumens fors qu’il ne puisse brisier, et saiches que mout d’estrumens de dens sont;	And let this instrument be outside so that it does not break, and know that many dental instruments are;
et ausi d’autres estrumens, qui ne sont mie contez;	and also other instruments, which are not counted;
et li saiges maistres subtilz trueve par soi meisme son estrument, selonc ceu que ses ovraiges et li maladie li demoustre, car il i a de teilz maladies ou li ancien n’enseignerent point d’estrument por la diversiteit d’au;s et s’om brise point dou charreit ou des autres os, ou il porrit, si i cerche as estrumens qu’il i covient, que je t’ai dit, et t’aide des gestes, de coi ci est li forme:	and the skilled master craftsman finds by himself his instrument, according to what his work and the disease demonstrates, for there are many diverse diseases where the ancients did not teach about an instrument; if it doesn't break through the jaw or other bones, but protrudes, then he seeks the instruments that he needs, which I have told you, and helps with gestures, so here is the form:
Et soient gros et bien tenant por tenir l’os, qu’il n’eschaipe, mais le puisse tenir et oster;	And let them be thick and strong to hold the bone, so that it doesn't slip away, but he can hold and remove it;
et puis restoure lou leu de medicines convenant a ceu, et s’il ait en l’os porriture, et elle est petite, si la reis a tout cest estrument:	and then restore the place with appropriate medicines, and if there is protuberance in the bone, and it is small, then he should use this instrument:
Quant li dent apperent ne mie selonc lou cors natureil, et li forme est laide, et meismement en femmes puceles, si covient que tu saiches se li dens est neis aprés lou dent, et n’est mie en droit leu, et on ne lou puet soier ne limer:	When the tooth appears not according to nature's course, and its shape is ugly, especially in young women, you must know whether the tooth is growing correctly, and is not in its proper place, and cannot be pushed or filed:
adonques lou raie;	then pull it out;
et s’il est aers avec lou dent, si prent cest estrument dont ci est li forme, et est semblans a I petit bec, et soit de fer inde agut en som:	and if it is growing with the tooth, then take this instrument, whose shape is like a small beak, and made of iron sharpened at its point;
Et lou cope poc et poc em mains jors por la duresce dou dent, et por ceu que tu ne mueves les autres, et s’il est apparans c’on le puisse limer, si lou lime d’une teil lime com ci est li forme:	And the gum recedes little by little day by day because of the hardness of the tooth and so that you do not move the others; and if it is apparent that one can be filed down, then file it with a file such as this, according to its shape:
et est ausi com li lime de coi on fait les aguilles;	it is as sharp as the file used to make needles;
et en lime lou dent poc et poc em mains jors legierement, si qu’il ne se mueve tant qu’il chiece;	and gently file the tooth a little bit at a time, so that it does not move until it breaks;
puis la plaine en la fin a tout aucun raseur, et se li dens est trop trenchans et il blece la lengue, si covient limer l’aspreteit tant qu’il soit igalz, si qu’il ne blece la lengue ne ne corrompe la parole.	then smooth it at the end with a rasp until it is even, so that it does not cut the tongue or impede speech.
quant li dent lochent	When the tooth is loose:
Quant li dent devant lochent, ou par percussion ou par cheoir, et li malaides ne puet presser sus ceu qu’il menjue qu’il ne chient, et tu les as curez de medicines restrignans, et ceu ne vaut;	When the tooth in front loosen, either by percussion or by falling, and the patient cannot bite down on what he eats without defecating, and you have treated them with constricting medicines, but it does not help.
si les covient restraindre d’un fil d’or, car li filz d’argent devient vert et porrit, mais li ors ne se mue onques;	if they should be restrained by a gold wire, for silver wires turn green and rot, but gold never moves.
et soit li filz moiens ne trop gros ne trop menus, selonc la quantiteit de l’espaice entre les dens;	and the wire should not be too thin or too thick, according to the amount of space between the teeth;
et se tu vues adrecier les dens, si pren lou fil et lou boute double entre les II dens sains, puis met les chiés entre les dens meus, s’il en i a I ou plusors, tant que tu veignes saigement jusc’au dent sain d’autre part;	and if you want to straighten the teeth, take the wire and tie it double between two healthy teeth, then place the ends between the loose teeth, whether there is one or more of them, until you reach the healthy tooth on the other side;
puis rencomence la coverture jusc’a la partie ou tu encomensas, et estrains ta main subtilment et saigement, tant qu’il ne se mueve point;	then start the binding again from where you began, and tighten your hand gently but firmly until it does not move.
et soit ta lieeure a la racine dou dent si qu’il ne puist eschaper.	and hold your fire cautery to the root of the tooth so it cannot escape.
Puis cope les chiés dou fil a unes tenailles, et les assemble, et les repont entre le dent sain, et le met ensi qu’il ne blece la lengue;	Then cut the teeth of the file with tongs, and assemble them, and bind them between the healthy tooth and the tooth that is not, and put it in so it does not bite the tongue;
et puis le laisse ensi estroit tant com il puet demorer, et s’il deslie, ou li filz ront, si l’estraint d’un autre fil;	and then leave it tight as long as it can stay, and if it comes undone, or the file breaks, then hold it with another file;
si demorrait et servira ensi tout son tens, et c’est li forme des dens et li figure de l’adrecement des II dens sains, et des II meus, si com tu vois:	if it stays and serves throughout its time, and this is the form of the teeth and the alignment of the II healthy teeth, and the II rotten ones, as you can see;
Et quant li dent chiet, si lou remet on en son leu, de fres en fres, si com nos avons dit;	And when the tooth falls out, one replaces it in its place, little by little, as we have said;
et ne s’en entremette mie qui n’est saiges et soffrans, et aucune fois fait on la forme d’un dent d’os de vaiche, et lou met on au leu ou li defaute est, et l’estraint on si com nos avons dit, et demore et sert ensi lonc tens.	and one who is not wise and suffering should not meddle in this; sometimes one makes the form of a tooth from a calf's bone, and puts it in the place where there is a defect, and holds it as we have said, and it stays and serves for a long time.
de coper lou liien de la lengue	to cover the wound in the tongue
Aucune fois est cist liiens qui vient desoz la lengue ou naturez, que on naist ensi;	Sometimes this vein, which comes from under the tongue, where nature places it, causes one to be born like that.
ou par accident de plaie soudee;	or through an accidental wound;
et li ovraiges est telz que tu oevre la bouche dou malaide, et ait sa teste en ton sain, et li lieve la lengue;	and the treatment is such that you open the mouth of the sick person, and place his head in your lap, and lift up his tongue;
puis cope lou liien nervous dou large, tant que li lengue soit desloie de son tenement, et se il i a duresce ou nout, et c’est de soudement de plaie, si i boute l’uncine et cope dou large celui liement;	then grab the nerved vein firmly, as widely as you can, so that the tongue is loosened from its place, and if there is a lump or wound there, and it is from a sudden injury, then cut the vein with your fingernail;
et garde que li fendure ne soit mie trop em parfont, por l’artere qui est desoz;	and be careful that the cut is not too deep, so as not to reach the artery underneath;
et quant tu as fait, si leve le leu d’aigue rose et d’aisil, ou d’aigue froide, puis met desoz la lengue une tente de lin;	and when you are done, raise the level of the sick person's head with rose water and garlic, or with cold water, then place a tent made of linen underneath the tongue;
et la teigne li malaides chescune nuit, que li leus ne puisse soder.	and the patient's scabies every night, so that the sores cannot heal.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si met sor le leu vitriole broiet;	And if there is bleeding, apply powdered vitriol to the site.
et se li sans te vaint, si le cauterize au cautere lentiginout, qui est boin a ceu;	and if the blood stops, then cauterize with a slow cautery, which is good for this purpose.
puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez,	then treat it further until it is healed.
et se tu lou vois de fusse color ou noir ou dur, si que li malaides ne lou sent, si n’i touchier point, car c’est chancre;	and if you see that it has turned red or black or hard, and the patient does not feel anything, do not touch it, for it is a ulcer.
et s’il est declinans a blenchor, et il i a moistor, si i giete l’oncine, et lou fent d’un spatumile subtil, et lou delivre d’une part et d’autre;	and if it is inclining towards a pustule, and there is moisture in it, then open it with a needle, and drain it from both sides;
et se li sans te vaint a ton ovraige, si met sus vitriole broiet tant qu’il soit estainchiez, puis revien a ton ovraige tant que tu traies tout fuer;	and if the bleeding stops with your treatment, apply powdered vitriol until it is stanched, then return to your treatment until you have removed everything.
puis leve lou leu d’aisil et de seil, et le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	then raise him up from bed and chair, and treat him with other treatments until he is healed.
des apostemes de la gorge	of abscesses in the throat
Aucune fois vient dedens la gorge boces qui sont apelees «godath», et les apele on proprement les II amandres, et quant tu les cures, si com nos avons dit en la division, et elles ne sont sanees, si pren garde:	Sometimes there come into the throat warts which are called 'godath', and they are properly called the tonsils, and when you treat them, as we have said in the division, and they are not healed, then take heed:
se c’est apostemes dur de petit sens et de fusse color, si ne lou touchier mie de fer.	if it is a hard abscess of small size and dark color, do not touch it with iron.si le gosier est delicat et li tros, si la remede de vinger adonques il faillet; s’il est grant, si
Et s’il est rouges et li racine est grosse, si ne lou touchier mie de fer, ausi por lou decorrement de sanc;	And if the throat is delicate and sore, then it needs the remedy of the finger; if it is large, then it must not be touched with iron, also for fear of bleeding.if it is red and the root is swollen, then do not touch it with iron either:
mais lou laisse tant qu’il soit meur, et adonques tu lou partiras, ou il rompirait par soi;	but let it be until it bursts, and then you will part it, or else it will break on its own;et li sang qui vieni de la root a l’esguier, si tu le remuieras, et il fuit adés et se rompre
et s’il est de blainche color reont, et li racine est subtilz, si aies apareilliet l’estrument por coper, mais regarde premierement se li apostemes chalz repose et est apaisiez.	and if they are of a white color, and the roots are fine, then have your instrument ready to cut, but first check that the abscess is cool and calmed.
Adonques fai seoir lou malaide devant lou soleil, et ses chiés soit en ton sain, et li oevre la bouche et lou preigne li serjans entre ses mains, et presse la lengue desoz a tout l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme;	Then have the patient sit facing the sun, and let his head be in your shade, and let him open his mouth and the assistant grip his jaw between their hands, and press the tongue down from under so that this is the shape:
et soit d’argent ou d’arain subtil ausi com uns coutelz:	and it should be made of silver or thin bronze like a little knife:
Cant tu presses la lengue a tout cest estrument, et tu vois l’aposteme, si pren l’oncine et lou fiche en l’amandre, et la trai fuer au desus plus que tu pues;	Then you press the tongue against this instrument and see the abscess, then take the needle and insert it into the pistachio nut, and pull it out above as far as you can;
et trai aucune chose des toiles avec, puis la cope a l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme, que semble unes forces;	and draw something from the threads with it, then cut the instrument into the shape that resembles a scythe;
et toutevoie li chief sont corbé, et l’un endroit l’autre, et sont molt agut, et est fait de fer inde ou d’andainne:	but their heads are curved and hooked, and they are very sharp, and are made of iron or steel.
Et se tu n’as cest estrument present, si lou cope as tenailles, de coi ci est li forme:	And if you do not have this instrument present, cover it with tongs, of which the shape is like this:
Et soit trenchans d’une part, et d’autre part nom;	And some are serrated on one side, and smooth on the other;
et quant tu as copeit l’une des amandres, si cope l’autre selonc cele meisme maniere, et aprés l’incision gargarize li malaides aigue chaude, et aigue et aisil, et se decorremens de sanc avient, si gargarize li malaides aigue, ou escorces de pomes grenates soient cuites, ou fuelles de mirte, et semblans choses, tant que li sans soit estainchiez;	And when you have cut one of the testicles, then cut the other in the same way, and after the incision gargle the patient with hot water, and water and garlic, and if there is bleeding, gargle the patient with water, or with the bark of pomegranates that have been cooked, or with myrtle leaves, and similar things, until the bleeding stops;
puis lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez;	then bandage him until he is healed;
et aucune fois naissent en la gorge autres apostemes que les II amandres, si les cope donques ensi com les II amandres igament.	sometimes other abscesses appear in the throat besides the two testicles, so cut them out just like the two testicles.
Et je medicinai une femme d’un aposteme que li estoit neis dedens la gorge, c’est a savoir I aposteme de petit sens;	I once treated a woman for an abscess that had formed inside her throat; it was a small one,
et avoit jai bien pres close toute la gorge, si que li femme ne pooit expirer por le conduit qui estoit estoupez, et ne pooit ne mengier ne boivre, et fust morte s’elle demorast ensi I jor ou II.	and the throat was almost completely closed, so that the woman could not breathe through the blocked passage, nor eat or drink, and she would have died if it continued for another day or two.
Et li apostemes estoit jai si montez qu’il avoit fuer mis II rains par les II pertuis dou neis.	And the abscess had become so swollen that it had forced out two hairs from the nose holes.
Je hastai donques tantost, et fichai en l’un I oncine, puis lou traï fuers, et en traï grant porcion de bowe;	So I immediately inserted a hook into one nostril, then pulled the worm out, along with a large amount of phlegm;
puis refis autreteil en l’autre pertus dou neis, et li ovrai la bouche et li pressai la lengue;	then I did the same in the other nostril, opened her mouth and pressed her tongue;
aprés fichai l’oncine en ces apostemes, et en copai une partie, et n’en issit fuers que un poc de sanc;	after that, I inserted a hook into these abscesses and scraped out some of the pus, and only a little blood came out;
et ensi fut destoupez li conduis de la gorge la femme, et comensa maintenant a boivre aigue et puis vin, et ne cessai de taillier de cel aposteme par lonc tens;	and so the passage in the woman's throat was cleared, and she began to drink water and then wine, and I continued to cut this abscess for a long time;
et li apostemes recroissoit adés, et remplissoit lou leu que je avoie vuidiet, tant qu’il refut mout gros;	and the abscess re-formed and filled up the space that I had emptied, until it became very large again;
adonques je l’engignai et lou cauterizai dedens la gorge:	then I taught him and cauterized it inside his throat:
ensi demora sens croistre;	so that it will not grow;
et me partis de ces parties, et ne soi que Deus fist de li aprés moi.	and I left those parts, and God did what He would with him after me.
de l’uve	of the grape
Quant reume dessent a l’uve, et elle est enflee et elle est longe, si est apelee «perpendiculaire»;	When the tear sac descends towards the eye, and it is swollen and it is long, then it is called «perpendicular»;
et s’elle est desoz grosse et reonde, si est apelee «uve».	and if it is fat and round, then it is called «eye».;
Quant elle est curee si com nos avons dit en la division, et li cure ne profite mie, et tu vois que li chaus apostemes est apaisiez, et elle est subtilz, si covient que tu la copes;	When it is cured as we have said in the division, and the cure does not help, and you see that the eye's abscess is pacified, and it is thin, then you must cut it;
et celle qui est reonde assemblee et n’est mie longe;	and if it is round and not long;
et elle est sanguine ou de fusse color ou noire, si covient que tu eschues l’incision de li.	and if it is blood red or light brown or black, then you must avoid cutting it.
Car il i a grant peril sus lou malaide.	For there is great danger in doing so.
Il covient donques, quant tu la vois, selonc la maniere que j’ai dit, de sa blenchor et de sa longesce, que tu faices seoir le malaide devant lou soleil, et li presse la lengue a l’estrument dont nos avons fait la remembrance ci devant;	Therefore, when you see it according to the way that I have described, its whiteness and length, you must make the patient sit facing the sun, and press his tongue with the instrument which we mentioned earlier;Adonques je l’engignai et lou cauterizai dedens la gorge:
puis fiche l’oncine en l’uve, et la trai desoz, et la cope a I des II estrumens que j’ai dit en l’incision des II amandres.	then insert the needle into the vein, and pull it through, and cut off one of the two instruments that I mentioned in the incision of the two testicles.
Et covient que tu ne coper mie fuer que la superfluiteit qui est outre le termine natureil;	And you must not cut anything further than the natural limit;
car se tu en copes plus, si grieves a la voix, et a la parolle;	because if you cut too much, it will harm the voice and speech;
et aprés l’incision, use de ceu que nos avons dit en l’incision des II amandres, et le cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	and after the incision, follow what we said in the incision of the two testicles, and treat it until it is healed.
Et se li malaides a paor dou coper, si covient que tu i use d’engien a la cauterization de li sens paor.	And if the patient has fear from covering, then you should use the cautery of the sense of fear.
Et li maniere dou cautere si est aigue ague.	And the manner of the cautery is for acute fever.
Et est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, et puis li presse la lengue a l’estrument que nos avons dit ou chapistre de cautere, et confis avec aigue vive chaus, si qu’elle ne soit mie trop espesse ne trop clere;	And let the patient put his head into your lap, and then press his tongue against the instrument that we mentioned in the chapter on cautery, and mix it with warm vinegar, neither too thick nor too clear;
et en emple le chevement de cest estrument, de coi ci est li forme:	and use this tool to create a mold of the shape:
Et ait ou chief une cheveure ou om met la medecine, si com li chevemens d’une cuillier, et met l’estrument a tout la medicine sus l’uve;	And it has a hair on its head where the medicine is placed, like the handle of a spoon, and put the instrument with all the medicine into the vein;
et li malaides soit gisans sus son costeit, si que li salive et li muscillaige corre de sa bouche de la medicine dedens, si qu’ele ne dessende a la gorge, et lou blece;	and let the patient lie on his side so that saliva and mucus run from his mouth due to the medication inside, so that it does not descend into his throat and lungs;
puis tien ta main a tout la medicine et la presse sus l’uve, la quantiteit de la moitiet d’une houre, tant que tu la vois nercie et li mordications de la medicine soit apaisie;	then hold your hand over the medicine and press it onto the ulcer for about half an hour, until you see it softening and the bites of the medication calming down;
et se tu vues, pren coton et l’envoloupe sus aucun estrument, et moille lou coton en la medicine, et boute l’estrument a tout le couton en la cainne desus, tant que li coton s’aerde sus l’uve;	and if you see it, take cotton and wrap it around any instrument, and wet the cotton in the medicine, and insert the instrument completely with the cotton on top into the ulcer;
et fai ceu sovent, tant que li cauteres soit parfais, puis la laisse elle seche, et chiet aprés IIII jors ou V.	and do this often until the cautery is complete, then let it dry and fall off after 4 or 5 days.
Et se tu as mestier de rencomencier lou cautere de la medicine, si le rencomence, et aprés le cautere l’essue entor l’uve, de couton embut em burre, et mundifie ceu qui est entor de la medicine;	And if you need to renew the cautery of the medicine, then renew it, and after the cautery wipe around the ulcer with cotton dipped in butter, and cleanse what is around the medicine.Et se li mordications sont trop grans et qu’ilz ne puent apier, si le mets a tout la medicine sus l’uve, et le presse tant que tu le vois nercie;
et soit arosez d’aigue froide, et soit curez de gargarismes tant qu’il soit sanez.	and let him drink cold water, and let him gargle until he is healed.
Ceste cure est plus save de l’incision, ne que li cautere;	This treatment is safer than incision or cautery.
s’elle est curee de fumigation selonc ceste maniere, pren calament et ysope et origanum et rue et camomille et avronne et semblans herbes, et les assemble toutes ou aucunes d’eles en I pot, et i met aisil, et fai bullir;	If it is treated with fumigation according to this method, take calaminth and hyssop and origanum and rue and camomile and avens and similar herbs, and combine all or some of them in a pot, and add garlic, and let them boil.
et li potz soit bien gluez de fort terre, et enmi le pot ait I estrument cheveit selonc ceste maniere:	and the pot should be well glazed with strong clay, and once the pot is made he should spread the mixture on it according to this method.
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain, et soit li uns des chiés boutez en la bouche dou malaide tant que li vapor monte a l’uve par la caine, tant que li uve soit mortifie;	And let one of the lips be placed in the mouth of the patient so that the vapor rises to the eye through the nose, until the eye is deadened.
aprés lou rencomence sovent, tant que li uve seche, et garde que tu ne faices ceu au comencement de l’avenement de l’aposteme chaut, car plusors choses i avienent;	Afterwards he should repeat this often until the eye dries up, and be careful not to do this at the beginning of the appearance of the hot abscess, for various things can happen.
et ne faire mie ceu fuer que a la declination d’aposteme chaut.	and do not make it too hot when treating an abscess.
Et se cist estrument n’est presens, si pren une caine et met dedens lou chief une craiffe d’uef, si que li bouche au malaide n’ait mie trop chaut;	And if this instrument is not available, take a cane and place within the handle an egg-yolk, so that the mouth of the instrument is not too hot for the patient;
car li craiffe d’uef ne lait mie la vapor grever la bouche, et c’est bone cure ensamble salut.	for the yolk will not let the vapors overwhelm the patient's mouth, and it is a beneficial treatment all around.
Maintes fois s’aert a la gorge os ou espinee de poisson, ou aucune chose;	Often there is a fishbone or some other object stuck in the throat;
si covient donc que tu traies ceu que tu pues veoir, et li presse la lengue au soleil a tout l’estrument, si que tu voies mues la chose;	so you should try to remove what you can see, and press the tongue against the instrument in sunlight until you dislodge the object.
et ceu que ne t’apert mie et est reponus en la gorge, covient que tu faices vomir le malaide ainsois que li viande soit cuite en l’estomac;	For what you cannot remove and remains stuck in the throat, you must make the patient vomit so that the meat is cooked in the stomach;
par aventure si istra li chose aerse par le vomissement;	perhaps the object will come out with the vomiting.Si li viande ne s’est mie cuite as en la gorge, covient que tu le faices
ou li malaides englutisse une piece d’esponge, ou une piece de navel, ou une racine de laitue, ou I morceil de pain sec;	or the patient should swallow a piece of sponge, or a piece of bread, or a lettuce root, or a piece of dry bread;
et lie a l’esponge I fil, et puis la transglutisse;	and attach a thread to the sponge and then swallow it;
et quant elle venra au leu, si s’aerdra, et puis trairas fuer;	and when it reaches the spot, it will stick, and then you can pull it out;
et s’elle ne vient fuer de ceu que nos avons dit, si pren I estrument de plonc selonc ceste forme:	and if it doesn't come out as we have said, take a piece of salt plaster according to this form:
Et soit li estrumens corbés au chief si qu’il puist plus legierement entrer en la gorge, et ait le chief en haut leveit;	And the instrument should be bent at the tip so that it can more easily enter the throat, and the head should be held up;
et warde que tu ne touchier l’epiglote, que li tous ne li viegne, ne ne bouter mie l’os dedens;	and be careful not to touch the epiglottis, or it will choke, nor push anything into the bone inside;
et mues vaut que li malaides i boute l’estrument, por ceu qu’il seit mues ou li chose est aerse;	And you must make sure that the patient swallows the instrument so that it reaches the spot where the object is lodged;
si la boute aval, ou il la traie fuer a tout l’estrument igalment, tant qu’elle soit fuer.	if the bowels move downward, or he pulls them outward equally with all his strength, until they are forced out.
de la sansue de la gorge	of the blood from the throat
Aucune fois est medicinee li sansue, si com j’ai dit en la division, par la cure de medicines;	Sometimes medicine is given to the patient, as I have said in the section on remedies, to treat the disease.
et quant ceu ne profite mie, adonques regarde en la gorge dou malaide au soleil, puis que tu li presses la lengue a l’estrument que je t’ai dit.	And if that does not help, then examine the throat of the patient in the sun, and then press his tongue with the instrument I have described to you.
Et se tu vois la sansue, si la trai a tout I petit uncine, ou as tenailles subtilz que valent a ceu.	And if you see the blood, draw it out with a small hook or fine tweezers suitable for this purpose.
Et se ceu ne vaut, si pren une caine chevee, et la boute en la gorge dou malaide, puis boute ou chevement de la caine I fer chaut, et fai ce sovent.	And if this does not work, take a curved cane and insert it into the throat of the patient, then heat the tip of the cane, and do this frequently.
Et se teigne li malaides d’aigue toute jor.	And if the patient has a fever all day.
puis pren plein I voirre d’aigue froide, et oevre la bouche, et la giete ens sens englutir, et la mueve a sa main sovent;	Then take some cold water in a glass, open his mouth and pour it in without swallowing, moving his jaw often with your hand.
et si tost com li sansue sent l’aigue, si chiet.	And as soon as he feels the water, let him vomit.
Et s’elle ne chiet si com nos avons dit, si subfumige lou malaide d’asefetide, a l’estrument que j’ai dit en la fumigation de l’uve;	And if it does not come out as we have said, then smoke the patient with assafetida, using the instrument I have described for smoking out the throat.
fai ceu maintes fois, car elle cherra sens targier.	Do this many times, for he will vomit without hurting himself.
Et li maniere de la fumigation si est que tu preignes I pot ou il ait charbons vis, et soit li pos covert d’un coverseil perciet en mileu, et en celui pertus soit li chiés de l’estrument;	And the manner of the fume is that you put burning charcoal in a container with a perforated lid, and the instrument's head goes through the hole.
puis i giete ta fumigation, et li malaides mette lou chief de la cainne en sa bouche, et cloie la bouche, si que li fumee n’en isse mie, mais viegne jusc’a la sansue;	Then you blow the smoke into it, and the patient places the instrument's head in his mouth, closing it so that no smoke escapes but goes to the blood vessels.
et la sansue cherra maintenant, et s’elle ne chiet, si rencomence la fumigation par maintes fois;	And the blood will drop immediately, and if it doesn't, repeat the fume treatment many times.
et soffre li malaides soif, et menjuce choses salees et als, et ne boive point d’aigue;	Let the patient be thirsty, eat salted and dry foods, and drink no water.
et adonques li iert mestier qu’elle isse fuer par cest governement.	Then it will be necessary for it to go out through this method of treatment.
Et li forme de l’estrument a coi on trait la sansue, si est, quant on la puet veoir, semblans a tenailles corbés por mues entrer en la gorge;	And the instrument used to treat the blood vessels is similar in shape, when one can see it, to bent tongs designed to go into the throat.
et ait semblance au bec de soigne, et i ait asperiteit de lime, si que ceu qu’elle prent, elle ne puet lassier;	and resembles a sow's mouth, and has the roughness of sandpaper, so that whatever it grasps, it cannot let go.
et vez ci la forme:	And see the form:
li chapistres des apostemes	the chapters on abscesses
Mout de semblances d’aposteme sont, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient ci aprés d’un et d’autre en cest livre, et sont diver en perforation et en taille;	Mouths of similar abscesses are, according to the recollections that come hereafter from one and another in this book, and they are diverse in penetration and size;
et c’est en II manieres dont l’une est en sa semblance meisme, et de ceu qu’il tient moistor.	and there are two ways in which the first is in its own appearance, and that of what it contains moisture.
Et li seconde maniere si est por les leus ou il sont au cors.	And the second way is for the places where they are in the body.
car li apostemes dou chief est autres que cil dou fondement, et li apostemes dou leu charnut est autres que cil qui vient en jointures, et chescuns ait son jugement en l’uevre.	For the abscesses of the head are different from those of the fundament, and the abscesses of fleshy places are different from those that come in joints, and each has its own judgment in action.
Et si a apostemes c’on ne doit mie percier, tant que li bowe est meure selonc son acomplissement;	And if one must not pierce abscesses until the bowels are dead according to their completion;
et si a de telz qu’il covient percier quant il sont crut, et ne meurent mie selonc lor acomplissement, si com aposteme qui sont delez jointures.	and some which one must pierce when they are crusty, and do not die according to their completion, like abscesses near joints.Et c’est ains qu’on dist que les apostemes son meures quan il sont creuzes et vides; car quan il son creuzes selonc lor acomplissement, si doivent ilz mouoir et ne puet mie rien plus demourer en lor
Car quant apostemes vient delez jointures, et on le laisse tant qu’il est porris entor, par aventure si sont corrumput li liien et li nerf de la jointure, par coi ce est cause de contraction en celui membre.	Because when abscesses develop near the joints and are left untreated until they are pus-filled, it is likely that the ligaments and nerves of the joint will become damaged, causing contraction in that limb.
Ou li aposteme est delez lou membre principel, et se tu tardes la perforation tant qu’il soit meurez, si nuira au membre principeil;	Where the abscess is near a main limb, and if you delay the piercing until it is mature, it will harm the main limb.
ou il est delez lou fondement, si le perce on ainsois qu’il soit meurs;	or where it is near the fundament, then one must pierce it in such a way that it drains completely.
et ne covient mie que tu perces aposteme crut sens digestion acomplie, fuers que celui qui est delez lou fondement, qu’il ne porrisse em parfont, et soit alongiez dedens, et i viegne fistule;	And one should not pierce an abscess without its digestion being completed, except for the one that is by the fundament, which can be allowed to drain a little and extend inwardly, so that a fistula may result.
et ne puisse saner en grant termine.	and not heal in a long time.
Et covient que tu saiches l’oure de la perforation de l’aposteme qui est meur selonc l’acomplissement, et c’est quant li dolor est apaisie, et li departemens de la fievre, et l’amenuisement de la dolor et de la roujor, et dou debatement et de l’aguisement dou chief de l’aposteme, et les autres signes;	And one should know the hour of piercing an abscess that is mature according to its accomplishment, and that is when the pain has subsided, and the departure of fever, and the lessening of the pain and redness, and the softening and hardening of the head of the abscess, and the other signs;
et covient que tu faices seoir la perforation ou plus dependant leu de l’aposteme, et la ou il apert mues;	and you must pierce the vein where it depends most on the abscess, and where there is movement.
et soit li perforation dou lonc dou cors, et se li apostemes est as mains ou as piez, ou en jointures et au ners et as arteres, et en toz leus igalz ou il n’a point de ploieure.	Let the piercing be in the longest part of the body, and if the abscess is on the hands or feet, or in joints, and on nerves and arteries, and in all places where there is no fold.
En ces que ploient, par selonc celui membre.	For those who bend, depending on the limb involved.
Et quant apostemes est en leu charnut, si vaut mues que tu laisses la perforation tant qu’il soit confermez en digestion acomplie, si com nos avons dit.	And when abscesses are in fleshy places, it is better to wait until after digestion is complete before piercing them, as we have said.Et quant il est delez lou membre principal, et tu ne veillies le perforer tant qu’il soit confermez en digestion acomplie, fuers que il soit meurez entor, si nuira au membre principel; et est grant dolur a celui qui le por; et li maux est plusors foiz perilluz.
Car se tu lou perces devant ceu, si iert alongiez li cors dou venim de lui, et est plains de mout d’ordure;	For if you pierce it before this, the venom will flow through the body, and it will be filled with much filth;
et par aventure endurcissent les levres et li parfondetez de lui.	and perhaps harden its lips and depths.
Et si a aucun aposteme que sont perciet selonc le large dou cors, selonc ceu que li membres en ait mestier.	And if there is an abscess that should be punctured according to the width of the body, according to what the member needs.
Et covient que tu amenistres em petis apostemes, petis pertus;	And you must treat small abscesses with small incisions;
et en grans apostemes, grans pertus, et maintes fendures selonc la semblance de la grandor de l’aposteme;	and in large abscesses, large incisions, and many cuts according to the appearance of the size of the abscess;
et si a de tels apostemes ou il covient chever lou keur, et coper;	and if there are such abscesses where one should cut the skin, and cover;
quant il est jai devenus ausi com I drapelz, et est amortis, si covient faire ausi com on fait as bubes:	when he has become as soft as a cloth, and is lifeless, one should then do what one does to blisters.
et si a de telz que sont fendut en III angles, et si a de telz dont on cope ausi com la fuelle de mirte, si com apostemes des angres;	and if they have split into three angles and are like the blister on the miter tree, as with abscesses on the fingers:
et si a de telz ou on fait une reonde taille, et autres tailles et semblant copeure.	and if there are others where one makes a round incision, and other incisions and similar cuts.
Cil qui n’ont point de chief, si com aposteme souef superficial, il covient que tu lou perces plainnement;	Those without a head, like a superficial sweat blister, you should pierce directly through;
et covient quant li apostemes est gros, et il a coillit grant bowe, et tu lou perces, si ne traire mie toute la bowe en celle houre, mais en trai une partie;	and when the abscess is large and has drawn a lot of pus, and you pierce it, then do not draw all the pus in that hour, but only a portion. ;
puis estoupe l’aposteme jusc’a l’autre jor, puis en trai aucune chose derechief;	Then stop up the abscess until the next day and then draw some more out the next day;
fai ceu par maintes fois de greit en greit, tant que li bowe isse toute;	Do this many times until all of the pus is drawn out.
meismement se li malaides est de foible vertut, ou femme portans, ou petis enfes, ou viez hons decrepites.	If the patient is of weak constitution, or a woman carrying child, or a small child, or an old man enfeebled by age.
Car li esperis tressaut aucune fois avec l’issue de la bowe, que par aventure muert li malaides, et tu ne t’en persois.	For the pus sometimes jumps out with the release of the blister, and the patient might die without your realizing it.
Eschuez donques cest chapistre par grant cautele, et quant tu as perciet ton aposteme, si essue la plaie, et regarde se li plaie de l’aposteme est petite;	Therefore, handle this chapter with great caution, and when you have pierced the abscess, wash the wound, and check if the wound of the abscess is small.
et se c’est une tailleure plainne, si amenistre tentes de lin ou de viez coton;	And if it's a clean cut, apply bandages made of linen or old cotton.
et se c’est uns grans apostemes, et il i a mout de pertus, si covient que tu boutes en chescun une tente si qu’ele viegne l’une contre l’autre;	And if it's a large abscess and there are many openings, you should place a tent in each one so that they touch each other.
et se tu as copeit en l’aposteme une partie dou cuir, et tu l’as cheveit entor, si covient que tu l’emplisses de viel couton ou de rasure de dras de lin sens moistor, et le lie jusc’au tier jor;	And if you have cut into the skin of the abscess and it has bled, you should fill it with dry cotton or linen cloth shavings without moisture, and let it be for a third of the day;
puis l’oste, et le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	then the bone, and treat with ointment until it is healed.
Et se decorremens de sanc avient a ton ovraige, si amenistre aigue froide et aisil, et moille I drapeil, et met sor le leu decorrant par maintes fois.	And if bleeding occurs in your work, bring cold water and ease, and wet the cloth, and place it over the bleeding area many times.
Et se li decorremens de sanc persevere, se i amenistre governement et cure, et les poudres que j’ai dit em mains leus en cest livre, et se c’est ou tens d’iver, et li leus ou li apostemes est est mout nervous, si couvient que tu mettes sus tentes et drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile chaut;	And if the bleeding persists, if it is administered control and treatment, and the powders that I have described in this book with my own hands, and if it is in the winter season, and the abscesses are very nervous, then you should put wet tents and cloths soaked in warm wine and oil;
et se c’est en esteit, et li leus est charnus, si covient que tu mes sus drapelz moilliez en aigue et en oile, ou en vin et en oile froit, jusc’au tier jor, si com nos avons dit;	and if it is in the spring, and the abscesses are fleshy, then you should place wet cloths soaked in water and oil, or in cold wine and oil, for a third of a day, as we have said;
et puis deslie l’aposteme et l’essue et le cure, si com il covient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	and then open the abscess, wash it out and treat it as it should be until it is healed.
Et ceu covient il conoistre universement en cures des apostemes:	And this is what one must know generally about the treatment of abscesses:
or vos ai dit coment on doit aler avant as cures des apostemes, et vez ci le chapistre.	Or I have told you how one must go before the treatment of abscesses, and see this chapter.
des soros	of sores
Ou keur dou chief vienent petis apostemes, et sont manieres de nous que sont en toiles, ausi com li josier d’une geline, et mout en i a de semblances.	From the head come small abscesses, and they are caused by people who wear hats, just as the ears of a chicken are, and there are many variations of this type.
Il en i a de gras et de telz ou il a moistor ausi com poulz;	There are some with fat and such that also have moisture as well as pus;
et si a de telz qui sont dur et pierous au taillier, et n’i a point de doutance se li artere n’i fait contraire.	And there are some which are hard and stony in texture, and there is no doubt if the artery does not act contrary to them.
Et li ovraiges de la taille si est que tu esprueve a tout I estrument qui est apelez «entromissoire», de coi li forme vient ci aprés, quel chose il contient.	And the work of the body is that you should test with every instrument called "trocar", whose form comes afterwards, what it contains.
Car s’il contient moistor, si lou fent par desus dou lonc.	For if it contains moisture, they open it from above and draw out the long one.
Et quant li moistor est vuidie, si escorche sens rien laissier la peil qui contient celle moistor, car il revient adés quant on i laisse rien;	And when the moisture has been drained, one should scorch it without leaving anything behind that contains the moisture, for it will return again if nothing is left behind.
puis plonge coton en oignement egiptien, s’il est presens;	Then plunge cotton in Egyptian ointment, if it is present;
se ceu non, en aigue et en seil, et en emple la plaie, et la laisse jusc’a l’autre jor;	if not, in water and salt, and apply it to the wound, and leave it until the next day;
et ceu corront ceu qui est demorez dou nit.	and then cleanse again what is remaining from the night.
Et pues rencomence lou coton, si com devant, le second jor, et lou tier, tant que tu saiches bien qu’il ne demoure point dou nit;	And then begin again with the cotton, as before, the second and third day, until you know well that nothing remains overnight;
puis cure la plaie d’oignement a ceu convenauble, tant qu’il soit sanez.	then heal the wound with an appropriate ointment until it is healed.
Et se li apostemes tient I nout gras, si le cope selonc ceste forme, dou lonc;	And if the abscess contains pus, then open it according to this form, lengthwise:
et i giete tes oncines, et l’escorche de toutes pars, et met toute ta cure de traire fuer la cotte ou il gist;	and he will pour out his bile, and cut away all around it, and use all his skill to draw the poison out from under the skin where it lies;
et se li artere te fait contraire, si fai ceu que je t’ai dit aprés.	and if the artery acts contrary, then do as I have told you above.Et demourera en celi lieu i jus de ceste incision, si laisera li sang couler tant qu’il soit sanz venin;
Et ausi fai de l’aposteme s’il est pierous, et dou taillier et dou curer si com je t’ai dit.	And also do this for a stone-abscess, cutting and treating it as I have said.
Et li taille sus l’aposteme pierous et le moiste, si est plus legiere, car il sont de poc de sanc.	And the incision on the stone-abscess is lighter, because they are full of blood.Et si li artere ne fuit pas, si mettés li chié sus li berlingot, et li muesche a li costez, et li sienge au bout de la verge, et li vachez a l’autre cap; et prendes une fiole d’or et une de verre, et le piez ou il gist, et mettes li cief sus li berlingot, et le corps sus li piez, et les piés sus li sienge, et li col sus li vachez.
Et si a aucuns de ces apostemes ou chief ou il n’a point de moistor, et de ces fut I apostemes que je copai ou chief d’une vielle femme;	And if some of these abscesses have no moisture in them, and the chief of them was on an old woman's head:Et li chiés et les costes et les fesses, et le col et la gueute: si fai I chié par incision sus lor nassance;
et trovai l’aposteme ausi com une piere xourde, aspre et blainche, et ne pooit brisier;	and the shoulders and ribs and buttocks and neck and face: in these cases make an incision over their source;I found the abscess just like a hard, rough, white stone, and it could not be broken;Et le corps qui tenoit la piere, et li artere et li veines, et li nervaus,
et s’on en eust ferut aucun, on li eust ausi bien fait plaie com d’une piere.	and if anyone were struck by it, they would be injured just as by a stone.
En autres apostemes venans ou chief, fuer que ces qui vienent as chief des enfans et as racines des oreilles, li overture si soit toz jors au plus dependant leu, por mues issir la bowe;	For other abscesses coming from the head, especially those that come to the heads of children and to the roots of the ears, the opening should be kept in the most dependent place so that the pus can flow out;
et les cure si com il covient.	and treat them as they should be.
des scrophules	of scrofula
Maintes fois avienent cist aposteme au col, et desoz les asseles, et ens angres, et aucune fois vienent autre part ou cors, et sont mout, et sont enjanrees l’une avec l’autre.	Many times abscesses come on the neck, and under the armpits, and in the groin, and sometimes elsewhere in the body, and they are large, and some are connected to each other.And these that come on the head, and those that come on children, if they have no moisture, and are not broken open, then they are called 'stone-abscesses'. And they cause great pain, and often kill the patient, and sometimes they can be found in the neck, armpit, groin, or elsewhere in the body. They are large and hard like a stone, and if cut open they will bleed profusely just like a wound from a stone.
Et chescune scrophule est proprement dedens sa cote, si com li nout et li aposteme dou chief, si com nos avons dit;	And each scrofula is properly within its coat, like the node and abscess of the head, as we have said;
et les semblances de ces scrophules sont maintes.	and there are many similarities among these scrofulas.
Il i a de teles que contienent moistor, et si a de malignes qui ne vuellent obeir a santeit.	There are some that contain moisture, and there are some that are malignant and will not respond to treatment.
en celle donques que tu vois de bone disposition au tochier, et est semblans a la color dou cors, et muet de chescune part et n’est mie aerse as ners dou col ne a l’artere ne au conduit, et n’est mie parfonde;	So in the one that you see has a good disposition to touch, and is similar in color to the body, and is not swollen on either side, nor pressing on the nerves of the neck or artery or duct, and is not deep;
si covient que tu la copes par desus, et l’escorche de chescune partie, et estent les II levres dou keur as oncines, se tu en as mestier, si com nos avons dit en apostemes dou chief;	you should cover it from above, and scrape each part, and the two lips of the wound should be stitched together, if necessary, as we have said for abscesses of the head;
et la trai poc et poc, et soies seur que tu ne coper lou nerf ne la voine, et ne soit mie li spatumile agus ne trenchans, que li mains n’eschaipe, et ne voise trop avant, que tu ne coper mie ceu que tu ne dois.	And pull it gently, little by little, and be sure not to cover the nerve or the vein, and do not use the spatulum or forceps so that the hand does not slip, and do not look too far forward, so that you do not cover what you should not.
Et se tu copes la voinne ou l’artere, et ceu ne te laisse ovrer, si met en la plaie vitriole broiet, ou aucunes poudres que restainchent sanc, et estraint la plaie;	And if you cover the vein or artery, and it does not let you work, then put crushed vitriol or some powder that stops bleeding into the wound, and bind it tight.
et la laisse tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez, et soit amollie li plaie, et encomence a porrir.	And leave it until the abscess is quieted and the wound softens and begins to fester.
Et quant li sans est estainchiez, si revien a ton ovraige, tant que tu l’acomplisses;	And when the blood is stopped, return to your work, continuing until it is finished.
puis quier a ton doit indice s’il i demoure nules petites scrophules, si les cope et les munde.	Then examine with your finger if any small scrophules remain; cut them out and clean the wound.Et li chiés de l’ajutoire est desaloiez par cause de moistor, et on le remet a leu, et il n’i puet demorer ains revient ad
Et s’il a en la racine de la scrophule voinne grant, si ne covient mie que tu copes celle scrophule en sa racine, mais la lie d’un fil double fort, et la laisse cheoir par li, sens nuisement;	And if there is a large vein in the root of the scrofula, you should not cut into that scrofula at its root, but tie it with a strong double thread and let it fall from it without harm.
puis emple la plaie de viel coton plongiet en oignement egiptien, puis la cure.	Then treat the wound with old cotton soaked in Egyptian ointment, then dress the wound.
Et se tu copes toute la scrophule, si covient que tu assembles les II levres de la plaie, et les cout maintenant, puis qu’il n’i a point demoreit de superfluiteit por la grandor de la scrophule.	And if you cut the whole ulcer, you should bring together the two lips of the wound and sew them now, so that no excess remains due to the size of the ulcer.Et si tu troves en la plaie grant quantite de sangue qu’il ne se peut estaincher a ton ovraige, si covient que tu metes li sur la plaie un panne, et le tiens fort; puis emporte li sang, et laisse li panne adessuz tant qu’il soit estanchié.
si covient que tu entendes a coper la racine de li, et traire fuer, et la cout si com nos avons dit.	then you must understand how to cover the root of it, and pull it out, and cut it as we have said.
Celles scrophules que tienent superfluiteit, perce lai ou il apert meure;	For those scrofulae that are superficial, pierce where there is an exit for pus;
et la perce ensi com celle devant dite, en dependant, puis i amenistre tentes avec oignement et semblans choses, si qu’elle corrompe ceu qui est demorez de la corruption;	and pierce it in the same way as the one described above, and then treat it with poultices and ointments and similar things, so that it corrupts what is left of the corruption;
et quant li plaie est bien mundee, si la cure d’oignement enjanrant char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	and when the wound is clean, then dress it with ointment that promotes scabs, until it heals.
de squinance	from squint
Li ancien dirent et parlerent de la tailleure de la gorge;	The ancients spoke of incisions in the throat;
mais je ne vis onques en nostre terre qui la feist, et c’est li escripture de lor parole.	but I have never seen it done in our land, and this is their written word.
A ces qui ont squinance, il covient que li fendure de la gorge qui est apelee «epiglote» soit eschuee;	For those with squint, it is necessary to cauterize the opening of the throat called the "epiglottis".
et c’on ne faice aide par ceu, por ceu que toutes les voines et li pormon dou malaide sont a ces qui ont aposteme chaut en la bouche, ou en la gorge ou en II amandres.	and this must be done by a professional, because all the veins and the lungs of the sick person are affected by heat in the mouth, or in the throat or in the armpits.
Quant li maladie est en la chenal dou pormon, il covient coper l’epiglote por fuir la perdition qui vient de l’estranglement.	When the illness is in the channel of the pormon, one must cover the epiglottis to avoid loss of life due to strangulation.
Il covient donques, quant nos volons fendre l’epiglote, que nos le fendons desoz III cercles ou IIII une petite fendure dou travers, entre les II cercles ou par la quantiteit de la fendure dou syfac, ne mie en la cartillaige;	Therefore, when we want to cut the epiglottis, we must make a small cut across it between two circles or four, not in the cartilage but in the amount of the cut through the soft palate.
et cil leus si est covenaubles a la section de l’epiglote qu’il n’i a point de char, et li vasseil sont lonc d’enqui.	and those places are suitable for the cutting of the epiglottis where there is no cartilage, and the blood vessels are long underneath.
Et se li maistres est paourous, si covient qu’il estende le cuir de la gorge a tout l’oncine, puis fende lou keur tant qu’il viegne a la cheneil;	And if the master is fearful, he must stretch the skin of the throat to the very end, then cut the skin until it reaches the bone;
et eschue les vasselz de sanc, se tu vois aucune chose, et puis cope lou syfac, si com nos avons dit;	and avoid the blood vessels, if you see anything, and then cauterize with the hot iron, as we have said.
et est demostrez par la section dou fleume de la cheneil ki saut fuer par le leu qui est rompus, et par la defaute de la voix;	and it is demonstrated by the section of the artery in the neck that blood flows out through the opening where it is broken, and by the deficiency of voice.
et laisse la plaie overte une piece.	and leave the wound open for a while.
Et quant li houre est passee de coi on doute l’estranglement, assemble les II levres de la plaie dou keur, et la cout toute soule sens la cartillaige;	And when the time has passed that we fear strangulation, bring together the two lips of the wound in the heart, and sew it up entirely without the cartilage;
puis aministre medicines qui font naistre char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	then administer remedies which promote flesh growth until it is healed.Et s’il advint que la plaie soit trop grande por leuee, si covient ades couper la chair du costé
Albucasim dist c’on ne faice ce jusc’a tant que li gorge est toute estoupee, et li malaides est jugiez a mort, et li defaut li alaine.	Albucasis says that one should not do this until the throat is completely swollen, and the patient is judged to be near death, and the deficiency of blood has been restored.
Adonques cope on l’epiglote por ceu que li malaides ne puet alener, et il respire par la plaie, et ensi est gardez de mort;	Therefore cut away some of the meat from the side [of the wound] if it is too large to be sutured closed. Then cut open the epiglottis so that the patient can breathe and not suffocate, and he will thus be saved from death;
et por ce commanderent li anciain a laissier la plaie overte tant que li malice de la maladie soit passee, et elle est passee en III jors ou en IIII Et adonques il comanderent a coudre la plaie et curer, tant qu’elle fut curee;	and for this reason, the ancients commanded to leave the wound open until the maliciousness of the disease had passed, and it passed in three or four days. And then they commanded to sew up the wound and treat it, until it was healed.
et je vos dirai ceu que je vis.	and I will tell you what I saw.
Je vis que une damoisele prist I coutel, et le ficha en sa gorge, et copa partie des chenelz dou pormon;	I saw a young lady take a knife and stick it into her throat and cut part of the windpipe;
et je fui apelez por li curer, et la trovai ausi com morte.	and I was called to heal her, and found her as good as dead.
Je descovris la plaie, et trovai le sanc qui en estoit issus, et soi bien qu’elle n’avoit mie copeit voine ne conduit fuer que la gorge, et li vens issoit fuer par la plaie.	I discovered the wound and found that blood had come out of it, and that she had not coughed up any phlegm or spittle except what came out through her throat, and the wind was coming out through the wound.
Je me hastai, et cousi la plaie, et la curai tant qu’elle fut sanee;	I hurried, and sewed up the wound, and treated it until it healed;
et n’avint a la damoisele fuer qu’elle fut roge de voix, et revint aprés a sa disposition;	and the young lady had no more than a hoarseness in her voice, and then she returned to her usual state;
por ceu di je que en la tailleure de l’epiglote n’ait mie paour.	therefore I say that one should not fear cutting the epiglottis.
de la grosse gorge	of the large throat
Cist apostemes est apelez «hernie de gorge», et est uns grans apostemes en color d’une jaisse, et est molt en femmes;	This hernia is called "hernia of the throat", and it is a large hernia in the color of a grape, and it is found mostly in women;
et est selonc II manieres:	and it occurs in two ways:
naturez, et accidens;	natural and accidental;
ou natureil n’a point d’engien.	nor does nature help.
Et li accidens est selonc II manieres, de coi l’une est semblans a gras nous, et li autre maniere est semblans a aposteme qui vient de nous d’artere;	And the accidents are of two kinds: one resembles fat growths, and the other kind resembles an abscess that comes from an artery;
et il i ait paour, et ne covient mie ovrer de feir fuers que en celi qui est petite, et le prueve et cerche a tout l’intromissoire:	and there is fear, and one must not use fire that is too hot but only moderate heat, and test and probe throughout the entire opening:
se tu le trueves ausi com I nout gras, et ne pent a nulle voine, si le cope, si com on cope les nous, et le trai a tout sa coife, s’il en i a point;	if you find it as smooth as fat, and it cannot be opened with any effort, then cut it, just as one cuts a nut, and slice it all the way to its core, if there is none;
et encerche bien tot, et le cure si com il covient, tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	and probe carefully throughout, and treat it as it should be, until it is perfectly healed.And if you find it as smooth as fat, and it cannot be opened with any effort, then cut it, just as one cuts a nut, and slice it
des nous	from us
Maintes manieres de nous sont, dont je dirai toutes les semblances;	There are many types of growths, and I will describe all their appearances:
et or covient que je die toute la difference qui est entre nout et issue.	and now I must explain the difference between a dislocation and a joint disorder.
Je dis que issue est chalors et fievre tenans, tant que li ebulicions est passee, et est acomplie li porriture;	I say that a joint disorder is a continuing fever until the swelling has subsided and the pustules have burst.
adonques repose li fievre et li chalor.	then the fever and heat will cease.
Avec lou nout n’a ne chalor ne fievre ne dolor, et contient I syfac, qui est ses propres sac et est selonc la color dou cors, et encomence ausi com une jaisse, et devient gros;	With a dislocation there is no fever, heat, or pain, and it contains pus, which is its own sac and is according to the color of the body, and begins like a pimple, and becomes large;
et sont selonc II semblances, ou grais, ou moiste, et mout de color sont si com j’ai dit en la division.	and they are according to two appearances, either dry or moist, and their colors are as I have said in the division.
Il covient, quant tu viens a la cure dou nout, que tu esprueves et l’enquier premierement a tout l’estrument qui est apelez «entromissoire», selonc ce que sa forme venra ou chapistre qui est aprés.	You should, when you come to the treatment of the nose, test and examine it first with all the instruments called "endoscopic", according to what its shape will allow in the chapter that follows.
Et li maniere de l’inquisicion des apostemes des nous est que tu preignes ou plus moiste leu que tu trueves en l’aposteme, et torne tes dois poc et poc, tant que tu saiches que li estrumens ait perciet le keur, puis que ce soit selonc la grandor de l’aposteme;	And the method of inquiring into abscesses on the head is to squeeze in the most moist place that you find in the abscess, and then press your fingers gently, gently, until you feel that the pus has broken through the skin, and this should be according to the size of the abscess.Et se tu ne le veois pas percer, retreine ta main et li estrumens, et comence a la parfaicte incision sus l’aposteme, et retreigne ainsii tant qu’il soit bien inciz, puis que tu le traies, puis que il soit si espans comme un poing.
puis estrai l’entromissoire, et pren garde en ceu que saut fuer.	then remove the speculum, and take care not to jump out.
Se moistor corrans cort, queil color elle ait, si le fent si com j’ai dit des autres apostemes;	If moisture runs short, whatever its color, they should treat it as I have said for other abscesses:
et se aprés l’entromissoire nen vient moistor, saiches qu’il est gras, si le fent donques en croix, et le prent as pinceures, et l’escorche legierement de chescune part et warde la cotte ou il gist que tu la traies saine avec le nout;	and if after the speculum no moisture comes out, know that it is fat, so they should make a cross in it, and take it with tweezers, and lightly scrape each side and guard the skin where it lies so that you draw it out healthy with the nail;
et se tu ne la pues traire saine, si la trai par pieces si qu’il n’i demoure rien.	and if you cannot draw it out healthy, then draw it out in pieces so that nothing remains.
Car s’il i demoure rien, si revient li nous par maintes fois;	For if anything remains, it will return to the body many times;
et s’il en demore un poc, et li sans te grieve, si emple la plaie d’aucunes poudres corrosives agues, et estraint la plaie, et met sus choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez;	and if a little remains and the pain is not grave, then employ the wound with some corrosive powders, and press the wound, and put warm healing poultices on it, and treat it with other treatments until it is healed;
et se li nous est grans, si cout les II levres de la plaie, et le cure de ceu qui enjanre char.	and if it is large, then cut both lips of the wound, and the cure of that which clogs it.
et se li voine batans t’est contraire ou autre si te haste et emple le leu de vitriole broiet, et lou laisse liiet II jors ou III, tant que li plaie porrisse, et repose li ebulicion dou sanc;	and if the pulsation is contrary or else you hasten and employ the place of ground vitriol, and leave it lightly for two or three days until the wound suppurates, and calm the ebullition of blood;
puis revien au coper ceu que i est demoreit dou nout.	then return to cover what has been left for a day.
Vez ci les formes des estrumens entromissoires, et sont de III manieres:	Here are the forms of instruments that pierce, and they are threefold:
grans et moien et petit;	large, medium, and small;
et s’en i a III quarrez qui sont apelez «albaret», et I qui est apelez «breb», et s’en i a de III manieres:	and there are three edges which are called "albaret", and one which is called "breb", and there are three kinds:
grant, moien, et petit, por encerchier les apostemes de fistule;	large, medium, and small, to surround abscesses of fistulas;
