et puis le laisse tant qu’il chiecent, et quant il seront cheut, si les cure d’oignement et d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez.	then let him defecate, and when he has, treat the wound with ointment and other remedies until it is healed.
dou sechement dou fiens ou fondement	from dryness of the anus or rectum
Maintes fois avient sechement de fiens en l’intestine, et par constrignement de nature, et quant li maladie est vielle et medicine n’i vaut.	Many times there is dryness of the bowels within the intestines, caused by natural constriction, and when the disease is old and medicine does not help.
Si covient que tu reses a la point d’un spatumile ou a ton ungle l’escorce desus, qui ne le laisse a moistir;	You should also cut off any scabs that form on the wound with a spatula or your fingernail, so that moisture does not get trapped underneath.
puis le cure tant qu’il soit sodez si com il covient;	then treat the wound until it is clean and healing as it should be.
et s’il ne puet soder, si rencomence la rasure plus fort que devant, tant qu’il saine mout, et soit escorchiez;	if it cannot heal, then restart the process of scraping off any dead tissue until the wound is clean and healing well, even if this means causing some pain.
puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	then treat the wound until it is fully healed.
dou fremit	when it trembles
Formice est une petite apparance fautree antor le cors, et va mout em parfont;	A furuncle is a small boil-like growth that forms under the skin and can grow quite large;
et aucune fois la trueve li frois, et le sent on ausi comme mort de fremit, et vient en tout le cors, et plus as mains que autre part.	and sometimes the shivering chills him, and he feels it throughout his body, more in his hands than anywhere else.
Et li cure si est que tu pren une cainne d’une penne d’oie, ou une penne de vultul fort, et met celle caine sus le fremit, tant que li cercles porpreigne le fremit tot entor;	And the treatment is that you take a candle made of goose fat, or fat from a wild boar, and hold it to the shivering until the purple circle around the shivering goes away.
puis torne ta main a tout la cainne tant que tu copes tout entor le fremit, et le met em parfont, et esraiche le fremit de ses racines.	Then return your hand to the candle and rub it all around the shivering until you've covered the whole area; this will pull out the shivering by its roots.
Et se tu vues, si fai ceu d’une caine d’arain ou de fer selonc ceste forme, et soit subtilz desoz et traians desus:	And if you see fit to make a candle of bronze or iron according to this shape, let it be thin beneath and drawn out on top.
ne mie perciet, por mues tenir au doi, et mues presser.	Do not pierce it, lest it stick to the candle, and do not press on it too hard.
Et se tu vues, si cauterize lou fremit, si com il est devant ou chapistre de cautere.	And if you wish, you can cauterize the shivering as described in the chapter on cautery.
de la forme dou clistere	of the form of the enema
Aucune fois fait on clistere d’argent ou d’archaut, ou d’arain fondut ou mailliet;	Sometimes they make a clyster of silver, or brass, or molten bronze or copper:
et aucune fois fait on de ces estrumens petis et grans, selonc ces a cui il sont amenistrez.	and sometimes these instruments are made small and large, depending on those to whom they are administered.
Cil donques c’on amenistre en la cure des enfans et qui sont foible et dolorous, sont petis.	Those who are administered for the treatment of children, and who are weak and painful, are small.
Li forme dou clistere petit et grant si est desus large, ou li ventres est liiez selonc ceste maniere:	The form of the small and large enema is above wide, or the belly is bound according to this manner:
et i ait une desevrance ou li ventres soit liiez, si com tu vois, et li chiez soit dedens perciez;	and there is a disconnect in the abdomen, as you can see, and the bowels are pierced inside;
et ait a l’un des costez II pertus, et en l’autre I;	and on one side there is an opening, and on the other there is none;
et soit li ventres ou om met les medicines d’une vessie de beste ou de parchemin, et soit perciez tout entor de menus pertus, et ait entre chescun pertus I doit d’espaice, puis boute en ces pertus I fil fort de fil crut tort en X ou enqui entor, et assemble le ventre si com est une chievre;	and the abdomen is where one puts the medicine, in a bladder made of animal hide or parchment, and it is pierced all around with small holes, and there should be an inch of space between each hole, then insert into these holes a strong thread wound in a spiral, and assemble the abdomen as if it were a goat;
et quant li medicine est dedens, si la lie a l’estrument devant d’un fil fort, puis clisterize;	and when the medicine is inside, tie it to the instrument with a strong thread in front, then climsterize;
et c’est li forme dou cercle:	and this is the shape of the circle:
Et soit li medicine ne trop chaude ne trop froide, et oint le chief dou clistere d’oile ou d’aubun d’uef, ou de semblant chose, puis le boute ens legierement;	And let the medicine not be too hot or too cold, and anoint the head of the catheter with oil or egg yolk, or similar things, then insert it gently;
puis l’espreigne li ministres a ses II mains ensamble, tant qu’il soit toz vuis, puis estrai lou clistere, et lieve li malaides ses jambes a la paroit, et se li medicine vuet issir, si la teigne tant com il puet;	Then the minister squeezes his two hands together, until it is completely empty, then removes the enema, and helps the patient to his feet, and if the medicine wants to come out, he holds it in as much as he can.
et s’il dort une nuit atot, si est plus grans aide.	and if he sleeps a night at once, it is greater help.
Et se tu le clisterizes em maladie de decorrement de ventre, et li medicine se haste d’issir, si le rencomence tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if you treat him with a syringe for dysentery, and the medicine rushes out quickly, then repeat it until he is healed.
Et se li emorroide sont ou fondement, ou aposteme, si soit li clistere ausi subtilz com por I enfant;	And if the hemorrhoids are in the anus or rectum, then the enema should be as gentle as for a child.
et c’est li forme dou clistere subtil sus coi li cuir soit estraint:	and this is how to make the gentle enema that will not hurt the skin:
des plaies	of wounds
Nos avons jai dit en la division la cure des plaies;	We have already said in the section on wound treatment:
or vos dirons les cures de mains et de medicine, selonc l’acomplissement.	now we will tell of the cures for hands and medicine, according to completion.
Je dis que les plaies sont diverses selonc ceu qu’elles sont faites, et selonc les leus ou les plaies sont faites, et de coi elles sont faites.	I say that wounds are diverse according to how they are made, and according to the places where the wounds are made, and according to what makes them.
Les choses par coi plaies sont faites sont par gitement de piere, et taille d’espee et de couteil, ou de lance ou de fust ou de siette, ou de semblans choses;	The things by which wounds are made are by the impact of stones, and cuts from sword and knife, or lance, club, spear, or similar objects;
ou que sont faites selonc les leus dou cors, si com plaie que chiet sus le col, ou sus le chief, ou le peis, ou le ventre, ou le foie, et semblans membres;	where they are made according to the places of the body, as a wound that falls on the neck, or the head, or the leg, or the belly, or the liver, and similar members;
et je vos dirai la cure de chescune plaie, et encomencerai as plaies dou chief simples, car li remenbrance venra en son chapistre.	and I will tell you the cure for each wound, and I will begin with simple head wounds, because the memory will come in its chapter.
Je dis que quant simple plaie vient ou chief, et li os n’est brisiez, si pren garde se c’est de gitement de piere ou de semblans choses, et li cuir est toutevoie rompus et est li plaie grans, et tu doutes levement d’aposteme chaut:	I say that when a simple wound comes to the head and the bone is not broken, then take care if it is a stone or similar object, and the skin is still broken and the wound is large, and you fear quickly of a hot abscess:
si le fai tantost sainier de la cephalique meismement s’il vient poc de sanc de la plaie, et soit li sainie au contraire de la partie navree;	then let him bleed at once from the head itself if it comes from a little blood from the wound, and let the bleeding be in the opposite direction of the wounded part;
et eschuisse li malaides repletion de vin et de viandes grosses.	and dry out the patient's fullness from wine and rich foods.
Et s’il ne vuet sainier, si soit amenuisie sa viande, et ne boive point de vin, ne ne menjuce point de char;	If he does not want to fast, then his diet should be reduced, and he should drink no wine or eat no meat.
et met sor la plaie, se apostemes chaus i vient, coton moilliet en oile roset soulement, ou en vin stiptice;	and put a poultice on the wound, if hot abscesses form, only moistened cotton in rose oil or wine with styptic properties;
et s’il n’i a aposteme chaut, si met sus la plaie, s’elle est fresche a tout son sanc, et elle n’est muee par l’air, poudre, que je dirai un poc ci aprés;	and if there is no hot abscess, then put on the wound, if it is still bleeding and not moved by air, powder which I will describe shortly;
et se li ars l’ait muee, si met sus aucuns oignemens, tant qu’il soit sanez.	and if the wound has been moved by air, then put on some ointments until it is healed.
Et se li plaie est grans si com de tailleure d’espee et de semblans, et les levres ne se pueent assembler par tentes, si les assemble par cousture, si com je dirai as plaies dou ventre, de la costure.	And if the wound is large, such as from a sword cut and similar, and the lips cannot be brought together with stitches, then bring them together with sutures, as I will describe for wounds of the abdomen, of the chest.
Se li plaie est descoverte de l’os, et pent, et ne tient mais que a un poc, si le cope;	If the wound is exposed to the bone and can be closed and only holds by a small amount, then stitch it;
puis cure la plaie de medicine, et restoure char dure en leu de cuir, et comande au malaide a mengier grosses viandes, si com testes et froment cuit, ausi com poulz, et semblans choses.	then treat the wound with medicine, and restore hard food in place of skin, and instruct the patient to eat coarse foods such as eggs and cooked wheat, as well as pulses, and similar things.
Et se tu trueves ou cuir porriture, et il n’aert a l’os, si cope lou porrit tot, et giete fuer, puis le cure;	And if you find a skin boil, and it is not on the bone, then cut off the boil completely, and squeeze it out, then treat it.
et se il ait artere en la plaie ou voine, dont sans cort, et il ne puet estainchier par medicines, si quier l’artere, et se tu la trueves desloie, si la lie d’un fil;	And if there is an artery in the wound or vein, causing blood loss, and it cannot be stopped by medicine, then cut and tie off the artery, and if you open it, then ligate it with a thread.
et se ceu ne profite mie, si la cauterize.	And if that does not help, then cauterize it.
Et se ces plaies sont petites et simples, si est li cure legiere:	And if these wounds are small and simple, then the treatment is light:Car les maladies de la chair sont legierement curables, se on le cueille promptement; mais en
et est que tu mettes ens ceste poudre qui soude ainsois que li ars l’ait muee.	And it is important to apply this powder that draws out the pus as soon as the wound has healed over.
Et li maniere de la poudre si est:	And the way to make the powder is:Prends fin amont de sal armonie, et de vitriol blanc
pren encens une partie;	Take equal parts of harmoneal salt and white vitriol;take one part of incense
sanc de dragon II parties;	blood of a dragon two parts
chalz vive III parties, et le poudre subtilment, et emple la plaie, et l’estraint forment, tant qu’elle s’aerse bien et se joigne a tout son sanc;	white vitriol three parts, and the powder subtly, and apply to the wound, and hold it firmly, until it is well healed and joined with all its blood;
et puis la lie bien, et la laisse sens desliier, s’elle n’enfle;	and then dress it well, and leave it bound, if it does not swell;
car on n’oste la madicine tant qu’ele soit sanee.	for one does not remove the medicine until it is healed.
Et aucune fois fait on ceu de chalz soulement, quant on n’ait l’encens ne lou sanc de dragon, mais que li ars n’ait muee la plaie.	And sometimes one makes it only with chalk, when one doesn't have incense or dragon's blood, but so long as the wound is moved by fire.
Et se li ars ait mueit la plaie, meismement en esteit, si n’i met om mie ceste poudre;	And if the fire has moved the wound, the same way it was, put on some of this powder;
mais met sus aucuns oignemens digestis, ou poulz de farine d’orge faites d’aigue et de miel, tant qu’ele giete bowe;	but put on some digestive poultices, or barley flour made with water and honey, until it becomes soft;
puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	then treat it with other treatments until it is healed.Et se li est aisi granz maux et grant mortur, il doit estre traittes d’aic
Et se li brisure d’os vient avec la plaie, et elle est petite, si l’estrai as pinceures subtilz;	And if the fracture of the bone comes with the wound, and it is small, then draw it out with fine pincers;
et je vos dirai ci aprés les brisures dou chief.	and I will tell you about fractures of the head afterwards.
de la plaie dou col	wounds to the neck
Se plaie vient ou col et elle est simple, si n’a point de difference entre li et celi dou chief, mais se li ners dou col ou li artere est copee.	If the wound is on the neck and it is simple, there is no difference between it and that of the head, but if the nerves of the neck or the artery are cut.
Se c’est li ners, si n’i a autre engien que laissier la cure, et n’i mettre nulle chose restraignant, car il nuit as ners et les fait retraire;	If it is a nerve, there should be nothing done but to leave the wound alone and not put anything restraining on it, because it hurts the nerves and makes them withdraw;
et ne mettre sus la plaie rien froit, car li substance des ners est froide, et li continuation d’aus si est avec le cerveil, qui est li plus haus membres;	and nothing cold should be put on the wound, because the substance of the nerves is cold, and their continuation is with the brain, which is the highest member;
mais soit li medicine souez, si com chalz lavee en aigue douce, et mellee avec oile roset, et cucie lavee ausi en aigue douce, et autres pieres de mine selonc ceste maniere, et oignemens moistes.	but the medicine should be warm, like hot water washed in soft water and mixed with rose oil, and cooked washed also in soft water, and other stones of similar type, and moist ointments.
Et se li plaie est grans, si la cout et lie de bendes, puis la cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the wound is large, then cut and ligate the vessels, then treat it until it heals.
Et se les plaies sont parfondes et ele est chevee et pleinne de bowe, si la perce ou plus bas leu;	And if the wounds are deep, and she is pregnant and full of fetus, then it should be pierced higher up;
et se li artere est copee, et decorremens de sanc en vient, si la desoivre, et la loie, et la cauterize se mestier est;	and if the artery is cut, and blood comes out, then open it, and ligature it, and cauterize it if necessary;
et se li espinee de la gorge est copee, ou li keurs, et li conduiz est gardez, par coi la viande va, si cout le keur sus la cainne de la gorge, et ne touchier la gorge mais la remet selonc sa figure naturel;	and if the spine of the throat is cut, or the neck, and the conduit is kept, through which the meat goes, then cut the neck over the spine of the throat, and do not touch the throat but reset it according to its natural shape.
et puis l’estraint avenanment, et le laisse aucuns jors, puis le cure d’oignemens desechans tant qu’il soit sanez;	and then he tightens it gently, and leaves it for a few days, then cleans the wound with herbs until it is healed.
et se li plaie a fait empression en l’os, si la quier;	and if the wound has made an impression on the bone, then cut it out.
et s’il i a pieces d’os, si les trai fuers toz se tu pues, et ces que tu ne pues avoir, si laisse tant que li plaie porrisse, et soit desevree et aligie li issue;	and if there are bone fragments, then remove all those you can, and the ones you cannot reach, leave until the wound pus, and is drained and healed.
et se li plaie est fresche, si poudre sus la poudre que j’ai dit.	and if the wound is fresh, then powder it with the powder I described earlier.
Et s’il a en la plaie os et il i a fistule, si la cure ensi com j’ai dit en son chapistre.	And if there is bone in the wound and there is a fistula, treat it as I have described in its chapter.
de la plaie de lance ou de coutel	of a wound from a spear or knife
Se c’est cop de lance ou de coutel, et li plaie est parfonde, si regarde se de la plaie saut ventositez cant li malaides alainne:	If it is a stab or cut wound, and the wound is deep, then examine if from the wound, winds blow through the body:
saiches adonques que li plaie est mortelz;	you know therefore that the wound is mortal;
et s’elle n’est parfonde, et elle est fresche a tout son sanc, si n’i mettre mie a la premiere houre la poudre, ne ne la liier mie por le sanc que ne demorse em parfont, et reviegne au cuer, et ocie lou malaide;	and if it is not deep, and it is fresh with all its blood, do not put the powder in it at first, nor ligature it because of the blood which will flow out, piercing through, and return to the heart, and heal the patient.
mais i met oignement atractif, et le lie II fois le jor;	but apply an attractive ointment, and tie it twice a day;
et se tu n’as oignement, si met en la plaie viel coton por succier fuers la moistor, et fai dormir le malaide sus la plaie III jors, ou IIII, ou plusors;	and if you do not have an ointment, then put old cotton in the wound to draw out moisture, and let the patient sleep on the wound for 3, or 4, or more days;
si n’i venra mie spasme, ne tremor male de cuer n’estraingnemens d’alainne;	and if no spasms, nor tremors, nor pain in the limbs come;
et quant tu vois les bones dispositions, si saiches que li plaie est sauve.	and when you see these good signs, then you know that the wound is saved.
Cure la donques de tentes et d’autres cures, tant qu’il soit sanez;	Then cure it with poultices and other remedies until it is healed;
et s’elle ne puet saner, et oevre, adés saiches que il i a fistule;	and if it cannot heal, and works, then know that there is a fistula.
si la cure si com on doit.	treat the wound as one should.
Et se li plaie est d’incision d’espee ou de coutel, et elle est simple, ou pis ou au dos, si la cure de ceu qui est devant;	And if the wound is from a sword or knife, and it is superficial, in front or on the back, then treat it as follows:
s’elle est grans, de cousture;	if it is large, with stitches;
et s’elle est petite, de poudre, et s’elle est empressee en l’os, et en a copeit pieces, si quier la plaie, et les trai fuers s’il sont desevrez;	and if it is small, with powder, and if it is deep in the bone, and has chipped pieces, then clean the wound, and pull out the foreign objects if they are loose;
et s’il ne sont desevrez, si laisse porrir la plaie, si aligera li estractions;	and if they are not loose, let the wound fester, and it will ease the extraction.
et des autres plaies as autres membres est li jugemens si com nos avons dit.	and for other wounds in other limbs, the judgment is as we have said.
dou derrompement dou ventre	from rupturing of the belly
Li derompemens dou ventre est grans et moiens et petis;	There are great, medium and small ruptures of the belly;
de la grant plaie saut aucune fois li intestine, ou li ners des intestines, par coi li intromission d’aus;	of the great rupture, sometimes the intestines, or the nerves of the intestines, pass through;
et li costure est plus malaisie, et aucune fois vaut pis li petite plaie que li grans, por ceu c’on remet plus a poinnes les intestines en, s’on ne les i remet de chaut en chaut;	and the sewing is more difficult, and sometimes a small wound is worse than a large one, because the intestines are not sewed in at once but gradually heated.
por ce que li intestine enflent tantost qu’il sentent le froit, si rentrent plus a poinnes, et por ceu vaut mues li moieinne plaie, por ceu c’on ramoine mues l’intestine a son leu que as autres II.	because the intestines swell as soon as they feel cold, they close up more at once, and therefore a wound in the bowels is better than one elsewhere; and so dislocation of the bowels should be reduced to its place before others.
Et saiches que li routure dou ventre est selonc IIII manieres:	And you should know that there are four ways to sew up the belly:
les II costures communes avienent en la costure dou ventre, et li costure des autres plaies dou cors et II autres costures propres sont communes as autres plaies;	The two common sutures happen in the belly, and the sutures of other wounds of the body; and two proper sutures are common to other wounds.
et toutevoie elles sont plus propres avec la costure dou ventre, et je dirai une chescune et declairerai.	Nevertheless, they are more appropriate with the belly, and I will describe each one and clarify:
Je di que quant li plaie est petite, et aucune chose de l’intestine ist fuer, et griés chose est dou remettre, ceu est par l’une des II manieres:	I say that when the wound is small, and some thing of the intestines are outside, and there is little danger of putting it back, this is through one of two ways:
ou por la petitece de la plaie, si com nos avons dit, ou por ce que li intestine est enflez por le froit.	or because of the smallness of the wound, as we have said, or because the intestines are swollen with cold.
Et quant il est frois, eschaufez lou en teil maniere:	And when it is cold, warm it in such a way:
moillie une esponge ou I mol drapeil en aigue tede soulement, ou tu cuis en aigue squinant et cipre et spique, et arose l’intestine tant que li enfleure soit ostee;	moisten a sponge or soft cloth in tepid water only, or cook it in water with squills and cyperaceae and spicery, and wash the intestines until the swelling is gone;
et aucune fois fait ce vins restraingnans, et est muedre que awe soule por desenfler.	and sometimes they make this restraining wine, and it is helped only by being alone to deflate.
Et quant tu vois l’enfleure departir, si amoiste l’intestine d’aigue ou altee et malves soient cuites, car par ceu est aligie li entree a poc de chose;	And when you see the swelling leaving, moisten the intestines with water or with honey and vinegar in which mallows have been cooked, for through this the entrance is slowed to a little thing;
et s’il n’i puet entrer, si fent un poc la plaie a l’estrument de coi on cope les emorroydes;	and if it cannot enter, they make a small wound in the instrument with which one cuts hemorrhoids;
et li premiere cure est muedre que li taille, que nus n’i doit taillier sens grant necessiteit n’i ait;	and the first treatment is moxibustion of the back, which no one should cut into without great need;
et c’est li estrumens por le fendre:	and here are the instruments for splitting it:
si trenche dedens en la corbeure et defuer non, et vez ci la forme:	if it is split within the curve and does not break, see the shape here:
Et quant li plaie est enlargie, et li intestine saut fuer, si le remet arer selonc la forme naturel en son leu propre, se tu en as pooir, car ce vaut mues.	And when the wound is enlarged, and the intestines jump out, then put them back according to their natural shape in their proper place, if you can, because this is worth it.
Quant li plaie est large, et elle est en la partie desoz lou ventre, si covient que tu faices gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et met ses jambes plus haut que son chief;	When the wound is large and it is in the lower part of the abdomen, you should have the patient lie on his back with his legs raised higher than his head:
et s’elle est en la partie desoz le ventre, si met le chief et le pis plus haut que les parties desoz, et ausi se li routure dou ventre est en l’une des II parties si met t’entente en ceu que li partie navree soit plus haute que li autre;	and if it is in the lower abdomen, place the head and feet higher than the lower parts, and also if the wound is in one of the two lower parts, place the injured part higher than the other;
et ensi covient amenistrer ceu que je dis en plaies grans et moienes.	and thus you should manage those things that I say about large and small wounds.
Es plaies petites met ceu que t’est apparilliet, puis aies entre tes mains I ministre pitous ki teigne toute la routure a sa main, et assemble les levres;	For small wounds, take what you are equipped with, then hold between your fingers and thumbs a piece of cloth which covers the entire wound and gathers its lips;
et c’est la maniere commune de costures, et est que tu preignes une aguille ou plusors, selonc la quantiteit de la largesce de la plaie, puis laisse des le chief de la plaie I doi d’espaice, et i fiche une aguille ou il ait I boin fil fort;	and this is the common method of sewing, and it is that you thread a needle or several, according to the width of the wound, then leave two threads' length from the edge of the wound, and insert a needle with strong thread through it;
et perce les II chiés dou cuir avec les II chiés dou siphac, qui est desoz le cuir dedens, tant que tu la faices percier de celle partie, et assemble les II chief dou siphac les IIII ensamble;	and pierce the two ends of the skin with the two ends of the stitch, which is under the skin inside, so that you make it pierce from that part, and bring the two ends of the stitch together;
puis l’estrain d’un fil double entor l’aguille de II pars, puis assemble les II chiés de la plaie avenanment, et puis laisse I doi d’espaice, et i fiche une autre aguille;	then pull the double thread around the needle from both sides, then bring the two edges of the wound together smoothly, and then leave two threads' lengths, and insert another needle;
puis la lie dou fil si com tu as fait la premiere aguille, et ne cesser de ceu faire selonc ceu que tu as mestier des aguilles, tant que toute li plaie soit restrainte;	then tie the thread as you did with the first needle, and do not cease to do this according to what you need of needles, until the whole wound is closed;et quant la plaie est restraine, tu i mets I boin fil de linteaue ou de cotoen par dessuz les aguilles en la plaie, et li raides entor le corps, et puis tire les II chiés dou fil, et li raides s’ad
et soient les aguilles moienes, entre subtilz et grosses, car les aguilles subtilz copent toute la char, et les trop grosses si ne pueent mie bien entrer:	and let the needles be medium-sized, between fine and thick, because fine needles pierce all the flesh, and those that are too thick cannot pierce well:
por ceu covient qu’elles soient moienes;	for this reason they should be medium-sized;
et ne covient mie bouter les aguilles trop au defuer de la char et dou cuir, k’elles ne copent et oevrent la plaie devant la soudure;	and one must not push the needles too deep into the flesh and through the skin, so that they do not pierce and open the wound before it heals;
et puis cope les chiés des aguilles, qu’elles ne blecent lou malaide au dormir, et i met tentes ou drapelz au chiés des aguilles por mues tenir, et les laisse tant que li plaie soit soudee;	then cut the heads of the needles so that they do not blister the patient when sleeping, and place tents or bandages on the heads of the needles to keep them in place, leaving them until the wound is healed;
et ceste maniere de costure as aguilles est plus covenauble en petites plaies, car il i soffist une aguille ou II.	and this method of sewing with needles is most appropriate for small wounds, because it only requires one or two needles.
Li seconde costure si est commune, et est que tu assemble les II chiés dou cuir et les II chiés dou syfac ensamble a une aguille ou il ait I fort fil moien;	The second sewing method is common, and it is where you bring the two edges of the skin and the two edges of the wound together with one needle and a strong medium-sized thread;
et quant tu avras perciez ces chiez toz IIII ensamble, si ramoinne l’aguille a la partie ou tu as encomenciet, en la maniere c’on cout les dras;	and when you have sewn these four together, then return the needle to the place where you started, in the manner that one sews a dress.
et met d’espaice entre chescune costure la grossece d’un menor doi;	and put spacing between each stitch equal to the thickness of a thumb nail;
ceste costure sevent li home, et je cousi une plaie c’uns hons avoit ou ventre, qui estoit navrez d’un coutel, et estoit li plaie plus d’une palme de grant, et issoit des intestines bien II palmes de grant, et estoit li plaie enmi le ventre.	This sewing saved a man whose stomach had been cut open with a knife; the wound was more than a palm wide, and the intestines protruded two palms out of the abdomen.
Je li ramenai l’intestine puis k’il ot esteit XXIIII houres fuer, et fut li plaie soudee jusc’a XV jors, et le curai, et fut sanez.	I brought him back the intestine, which had been outside for 24 hours; I sewed up the wound and it healed in 15 days.
Et li mire l’avoient jugiet qu’il morroit, et ce fut miracle;	And the physicians had judged that he would die, but it was a miracle:
et ne le curai mie d’oignement, car je estoie en I leu ou on n’en trovoit point, ne nule medicines;	and I did not treat him with ointments, for I was in a place where no such things could be found, nor medicines;
et metoie sens plus sus la plaie coton viel II fois le jor, et le lavoie d’aigue de miel tant qu’il fut sanez.	and changed the cotton on the wound twice a day, and washed it with honey water until he healed.
Or vos dirai les II propres manieres de cousture:	Here I will tell you about two proper methods of sewing:
pren l’aguille, et la boute des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens;	take the needle and thread it with the end going into the inside of the wound;
quant elle a perciet le keur de droit en droit, si lai le chief dou siphac ou cousteit ou tu as bouteit l’aguille, et la fai percier d’autre part des la partie dedens jusc’a celi defuer;	once it has pierced the skin straight on, take hold of the needle where you threaded it and pull it through to the other side of the wound, piercing from the inside out;
et li entendemens de ceste costure si est que tu cous ausi com li peletier font les pelz, et que tu laisses une fois le syfac d’une part, et le reprent d’autre, tant que li costure soit toute acomplie.	and the technique of this sewing is that you sew just as a leatherworker sews hides, and that you take hold of the skin on one side and pull it towards you, and then take hold of the skin on the other side and pull it towards you, until the seam is complete.
Li seconde maniere de costure, que Galiens dist proprement, si est si com aucun font, qui assemblent les II parties ensamble naturelment, et apploient l’un des chief dou syfac a l’autre chief, en teil maniere:	The second method of sewing, which Galen describes as proper, is to bring the two sides of the wound together naturally and to apply one side of the skin to the other, in such a way that:
fiche une aguille ou chief dou mirach prochiene, et fai percier celui leu soulement, et laisse les II chiés dou syfac;	stick a needle or tip of the mirror close to it, and just pierce that spot, and leave the two sides of the syringe;
puis torne l’aguille, et la fai percier des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens, as II chiés dou syfac;	then turn the needle, and have it pierce from outside inwards to inside, through the two sides of the syringe;
puis fai percier l’un et l’autre des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens, en II autres chiés dou mirach que sont on l’autre costeit;	then pierce one and then the other from outside inwards to inside, through two other tips of the mirror that are on the other side;
et c’est li muedre maniere de costure et li plus commune.	and this is the main way of sewing and the most common.
Galiens si dist ceste parolle, et aucun le tesmoignent, c’on doit coudre le ventre a II aguilles, ou il ait fil en chescune;	Galen says this word, and some testify to it, that one should sew up the belly with two needles, with thread in each;
et doit on bouter l’une aguille d’une part, et l’autre d’autre, en la maniere de ces qui cousent corroies;	and one must push one needle from one side and the other from the other, in the manner of those who sew hide;
et saiches que quant li routure est enmi lou ventre, si est li cousture plus griez que des autres leus dou ventre.	and know that when the wound is in the middle of the belly, then the sewing is more difficult than in other places on the belly.
Li jugemens de la plaie si est telz com li jugemens des autres plaies:	The judgments of the wound are such as the judgments of other wounds:
et est que quant tu trueves la plaie fresche a tout son sanc, ainsois que li ars l’ait muee, si remet arer l’intestine, et lou cout;	and it is when you find the fresh wound full of blood, so that the fire has moved it, then return the intestines and the bowels;
puis met sus la poudre enjanrant char, et se li ars l’ait muee, si met sus aucun oignement que soit present, tant que li plaie bowe;	then put on the powder, and if the fire has moved it, then put on some ointment that is present until the wound heals;
et chicent li fil, et soient soudez li sifac, et li mirach;	and cut the thread, and sew the sutures, and the bandages;
puis cure la plaie si com les autres, tant qu’il soit sanez;	then treat the wound as the others, until it is healed;
et se tu n’as medicines, si met sus, tantost qu’ele comance a giter bowe, coton viel, et le remue II fois le jor tant k’il soit sanez.	and if you do not have medicine, then put on old cotton as soon as it begins to heal, and change it twice a day until it is healed.
Car tu n’as mestier d’autre medicine en plusors dispositions cant les plaies sont simples;	For you do not need any other medicine in most cases when the wounds are simple;
et se tu doutes que li plaie ne faice communiteit as membres principelz, si covient ke tu moilles lainne legiere en oile de tempree chalor, ou en oile roset, et la met entor les angres, et desoz les asselles;	and if you doubt that the wound will affect the principal limbs, then you should moisten a light woolen cloth in tempered oil, or rose oil, and place it around the edges of the wound, and under the scabs;
et s’il sent dolor ou porriture en bouelz, et maintes fois avient, si les clisterize de vin noir tede, et meismement se li porriture vient jusc’a l’intestine;	and if there is pain or pus in the bowels, and it often occurs, then enema with warm red wine, especially if the pus comes up to the intestines;
et le perce dedens, et saiches que quant c’est li gros intestines, si est plus legier a saner que li petis.	and open it inside, and know that when it is the large intestine, it is easier to cure than the small one.
Li intestine qui est apelez «jeun» ne puet saner quant il est navrez, et c’est por la planteit des voinnes que i sont, et por la subtiliteit de tout le cors, et l’aprochement de sa nature des ners.	The intestines which are called "young" cannot heal when they are damaged, and this is due to the thinness of their walls, and because of the subtlety of the whole body, and the proximity of their nature to nerves.
Et si li zirbe saut de la plaie, si le remet arrier ausi com l’intestine, tandis qu’il est fres;	And if the worm jumps out of the wound, then put it back inside with the intestine while it is still fresh;
et s’il est vielz et devenus vers ou noir, si covient que tu lies le leu qui est noir, que decorremens de sanc n’i viegne, car il i a voinnes et arteres;	and if it is old and has become like worms or black, then you should tie off the black area so that bleeding does not occur there, for there are veins and arteries there;
puis cope ceu qui est entre le liien, et met les II chiés pendans des la partie desoz la plaie jusque defuer por aligier l’estraction quant li zirbes chiet, et li plaie bowe.	then grasp what is between the fingers, and place the two heads pendant from the part below the wound until it is dislocated to ease the extraction when the circles contract, and the wound heals.
de la routure dou boueil	of the rot of boiling water
Quant li intestine est rons, et li plaie est petite, si la puet on restorer en aucuns homes, por ceu que je vis que uns hons fut navrez ou ventre d’une lance;	When the intestines are ruptured and the wound is small, it can sometimes be restored in some people; for I saw a man who was pierced through the belly with a lance;
et estoit li plaie au destre de l’estomac, et fut envillie et devint fistule, et en issoit li egestion et li ventositez;	and the wound was on the right side of the stomach, and it became an abscess, and the excretion and flatulence came out through it;
je i mis cure selonc ceu que je poi, et ne cessai de subtilier tant qu’il fut sanez, et li leus soudez.	I applied treatment according to what I knew, and did not cease to treat him until he was healed and the wound closed.
Et quant je le vis souder, je doutai que li malaides n’eust mal en son ventre;	And when I saw that it had healed, I feared that the patient still had pain in his belly;
et il n’i ot point de mal, mais demora en millors dispositions, et menjans et bevans;	but he remained in good health, eating and drinking;
et dirent aucun experimentors que quant il a petite plaie en l’intestine, qu’il doit estre liiez en teil maniere:	and some experimenters say that when there is a small wound in the intestines, it must be bound in such a way:
pren fremis a grans testes, puis assemble les levres de la plaie, et quant li fremis ait overte la bouche, si la met sus les II levres, si qu’elle estraigne sa bouche sus;	take a large thread, then bring together the lips of the wound, and when the thread has opened its mouth, place it on top of the two lips so that it holds its mouth closed;
et puis li cope la teste, et ce se tient si qu’il ne puet desliier, puis met I autre fremit aprés en celle maniere que devant, tant que li plaie soit toute porprise;	and then tie off the head of the thread, and this will hold so that it cannot come undone, then place another thread afterward in the same way until the wound is completely bound;
et cout la plaie.	and then cut the wound.
Cil chief si s’aerdent en l’intestine, et ne vient nulle nuisance au malaide, et se puet on liier l’intestine d’un fil subtil qui est copez de l’intestine d’une beste, en teil maniere:	If these wounds are in the intestines and there is no harm to the patient, then one can ligature the intestines with a fine thread cut from the intestines of an animal, in such a way:
pren le chief de cest fil d’intestine que soit mout descharnez, et puis lie au chief de cest fil I fil de lin subtil tort, puis boute le fil en l’aguille, et en cout l’intestine, et le ramoinne en la routure;	take the end of this intestinal thread that is very dried out, and then tie to the end of this intestinal thread a thin twisted linen thread, then thread the needle, cut into the intestine, and wind it in the groove;
et ceste maniere de costure de fremis nen est fuers que selonc la voie de fiance et d’esperance;	and this way of sewing bones is not unsuitable, but according to the path of faith and hope.
et se li plaie est grans et large, meismement quant elle est en l’un des grailes intestines, si n’i a engien ne santeit, fuer que subtiliteit.	and if the wound is great and wide, especially when it is in one of the internal bones, there is no healing without subtlety.
de fistule ou qu’ele soit	of a fistula, wherever it may be
Saiches que toute plaie ou aposteme, quant il enveillist, si est apelee universement «fistule», et meismement quant elle est chevee et rent bowe.	Know that any wound or abscess, when it wakes up, is universally called a "fistula", and especially when it is swollen and becomes bow-shaped.
Et fistule est selonc la verteit nodation fautree dure et blainche, ou on ne sent dolor, et est ausi chevee com li penne d’un oiseil;	And a fistula is according to the green, hard, and white nodule, where one does not feel pain, and is as smooth as the feather of a bird;
et aucune fois en saut clere bowe, et autre fois espesse;	and sometimes it is clear and thin, and sometimes thick.
aucune fois poc, et autre fois assez;	sometimes small, and sometimes large enough;
et je en ai jai parleit en la division des plaies, que toute plaie que n’est sanee, et il n’i a char, ce n’est fuers que par une des VIIII causes:	and I have spoken of this in the division of wounds, that every wound that is not healed, and there is no flesh, it is not unsuitable due to one of the nine causes:
c’est a savoir, par la petitece dou sanc ou cors;	that is to say, due to the smallness of blood or body;
ou por sa malice;	or for its wickedness;
ou por ceu qu’il i a char dure dedens, et sus les levres, que n’i laisse naistre char;	or because there is hard flesh within it, and on the lips, which prevents new flesh from growing;
ou il i a trop de bowe;	or because there is too much puss;
ou li leus est porris, et li matiere est de male qualiteit;	or when the wound is rotting and the matter is of poor quality;
ou li medicine n’est mie bone en la cure;	or because the medicine is not good for the treatment;
ou por ceu que li corruption est maniere de pestilence;	or because the rot is like a pestilence;
ou por la proprieteit en la region est tardive li digestion, et tarde li santeit, et enflee par nature;	or because the digestion is slow in that region and so is the recovery which also swells by nature;
ou il i a voinnes ou os:	or there are veins or bones:
et j’ai ja mostreit toutes ces causes, et les signes, et les cures de medicines en la division.	And I have already shown all these causes and their signs and treatments with medicine in the division.
Or covient que je te faice a savoir la cure de fistule qui est faite par oevre de mains.	Now I should let you know about the treatment of fistula which is done by handiwork.
Saiches que fistule avient en tous membres dou cors;	Know that a fistula can occur in any part of the body;
car il i a fistules que vienent as grans voines, et as arteres, et as ners, ou au syfac, ou a l’intestine, ou a la vessie, ou a aucunes des costes, ou a l’espinee dou dos, ou a aucune jointe des mains ou des piez;	For it can occur in large veins, or in arteries and nerves, in the eye socket, intestine, bladder, sides, spine, shoulder, or any joint of hands or feet. ;
et si a teil que vient a la proprieteit dou membre principeil, et as semblans leus.	and if there is swelling that comes to the principal member, and similar swellings.
Et toutes les fistules que sont de ceste maniere sont de grief sanation, et n’i a fors que labour, et ignorance;	And all the fistulas that are in this way, they are of grievous healing, and there is no other than labor and ignorance;
et se il i a aucune fistule que ne veigne mie jusc’a leu que j’ai dit, et tu as fiance de la cure, et tu la vues conoistre, si pren une tente d’arain ou de fer, se li fistule est droite, si la quier;	and if there is any fistula that does not come to the place I have described, and you have confidence in its cure, and you see it known, then take a tent of bronze or iron, if the fistula is straight, then pierce it;
et se li fistule est torte, si la cerche d’une subtil tente de plonc, car li plons se ploie mues entor la tortuositeit;	and if the fistula is crooked, then look for a slender tent of lead, because lead bends with the crookedness;
et se li fistule a mains pertus et tu ne la pues mie bien cerchier par tentes, si la clisterize par l’un des pertus, car la moistors si cort d’un pertus a autre, et la mundifie;	and if the fistula has multiple openings and you cannot pierce it well with tents, then cleanse it by enema through one of the openings, because moisture moves from one opening to another;
puis la quier saigement a ton pooir, que tu conoisses s’il i a os ou nerf, et est chevee em parfont, et demande bien au malaide de la dolor qu’il sent au presser de ta main, et le leu ou il la sent;	then let the patient bleed at your hand, so that you may feel whether there is bone or nerve, and whether it is swollen all over, and ask the patient about the pain he feels when you press with your hand, and where he feels it.
et quant tu savras vraiement le leu ou elle est, et s’elle est loing de jointure, ou de nerf, ou d’artere ou de voine, ou en aucuns des leus que je t’ai dit, si la cope selonc ceu que je t’ai dit, et oste fuer la fautreure et les chars corrumpues que sont dedens;	and when you have learned the exact location and whether it is far from a joint, nerve, artery or vein, or in any of the places I told you about, then cut according to what I instructed, and remove the rotten flesh and matter inside.
et puis la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee, et se li fistule est bien parfonde de droit endroit, si covient que tu copes em parfont, tant com tu pues, puis i met tentes moillies en medicine ague, et les boute jusc’au chief de la fistule, tant que li medicine corrode la superfluiteit qui est demoree au fons;	then treat it until it is healed, and if the fistula is very deep in a straight place, you should cut deeply as much as you can, then put moist bandages in medicinal vinegar, and insert them into the fistula up to its head, so that the medicine corrodes the excess matter remaining at the bottom.
et puis i met oignemens enjanrans sainne char, tant qu’il soit sanez;	and then I put warming poultices on healthy flesh until it is healed;
et s’il n’est sanez par ceu, si le cauterize si com nos avons dit, et se li os est corrompus de la fistule, si le cope.	and if it does not heal by this method, then cauterize it as we have said, and if the bone is corrupted by the fistula, then cut it out.
Se voinne ou ners ne te greve ou membres principelz, si com nos avons dit;	If a vein or nerve causes pain in the principal limbs, as we have said;
et se li os est descovers, et il i a corruption et noiror, si lou reis tant que li corruption soit toute ostee, puis le cure de choses enjanrans char tant qu’il soit sanez;	and if the bone is exposed and there is corruption and darkness, then cut it until the corruption is entirely removed, then treat it with warming poultices until it is healed;
et s’il n’est sanez, et rent bowe si com devant, saiches que tu n’es mie alez jusc’a font:	and if it does not heal, and the wound is closed as before, know that you have not gone to the bottom;
si descuevre et quier tant que tu soies au fons, et oste toute la corruption, puis restore le leu;	if it exposes and pierces until you reach the bottom, and remove all the corruption, then restore the place;
et s’il est ensi sanez, c’est bien.	and if it is thus healed, that is good.
Se ceu non, saiches que la corruption est trop en parfont, que tu n’i pues avenir;	If not, then know that the corruption is too deep for you to reach.
si n’i a autre engien que dou lassier a nature;	if there is no other remedy except to let nature take its course;
et s’il i a i petit os corrumput, et tu le pues traire as tenailles, si l’estrai a I estrument covenauble a ceu, et s’il i a maint os, si les trai trestoz, ne n’en laissier nes un;	and if there is a small bone that is rotten and you can pull it out with tongs, then remove it with the appropriate instrument for this purpose, but if there are many bones, then draw them all out, leaving none behind;
et se li moistor te fait contraire, et il n’i a error ne paour, si cope et moistor et char, et delivre les os.	and if the moisture causes no harm and there is no error or fear, then cut through the flesh and moisture and free the bones.
Et se tu ne les pues oster a une houre, si met sus la plaie chose enjanrant porriture, et laisse tant que li leus soit porris entor les os, et adonc si avront plus legierement les os;	And if you cannot remove them in one hour, then place something over the wound to encourage pus formation, and leave it until the flesh around the bones becomes soft, and then they will come out more easily;
et se c’est uns grans os, si com de jambe ou de cuisse, si reis tant soulement la corruption tant que li noiror soit toute ostee, puis restoure la plaie;	and if it is a large bone, such as from the leg or thigh, then clean out the corruption only until the blackness is gone, and then close the wound;si n’at maint os ne grans, si met li meisme remede et restoure la plaie.
et s’il en i a grant partie dou corrumput, et vient jusc’a mole de l’os;	and if there is a large portion of it that is corrupted, and it comes to the softness of the bone;
si le covient soier et coper tout jusc’a la corruption, et puis le cure tant qu’il soit soudez;	then cut away and cover all the way to the corruption, then treat until it is healed over;
et je te dirai d’une fistule qui avint I home en sa jambe, si que tu i preignes exemple et aide en ton ovraige.	and I will tell you of a fistula that occurred in a man's leg, so that you can take example and help from it in your work.
Il fut I jovencelz entor XXX ans, qui ot une dolor en sa jambe d’une cause que vint dedens le cors, tant que les matieres vinrent a la jambe, et fut enflee d’un gros aposteme, et n’ot point de cause defuer por ovrir;	He was a young man of about 30 years old, who had a pain in his leg from a cause that came from within the body, so that the matter came to the leg, and it was swollen with a large abscess, and had no reason to drain to open;
mais li mire par lor folie ovrerent tant sus que li apostemes ovri, et en corroient mout de matieres, et devint fistule, et i vint mout de pertus que tuit gitoient bowe et moistor dou cors;	but the doctors, through their folly, worked so much on it that the abscess burst, and a great deal of matter came out, and it became a fistula, and there were many openings that all bled and secreted moisture from the body;
et maint mire i mirent cure entor II ans, et n’i ot nul saige en l’art de mains, tant que je i fui apelez, et vi sa jambe et les medicines dont on le curoit, et ceu que corroit par les pertus a grant cors;	and many bled him for two years, and there was no surgeon in the art of medicine, so I was called to see his leg and the remedies with which he was being treated, and the pus that flowed through the holes in great abundance.
et devenoit rouges li cors dou jouvenceil, et avoit color citrine.	and the body of the youth became red and had a yellow color.
Je boutai une tente en l’un de ces pertus, et puis cerchai toz les pertus, et trovai que li uns venoit encontre l’autre de toutes les parties de la jambe.	I placed a tent over one of the holes and then examined all the openings, finding that they connected with each other throughout the leg.
Je me hastai donques, et copai en l’un des pertus tant que je descovri une partie de l’os, et le trovai corrumput et perciet, et venoit li corruption jusc’a l’os dedens;	I therefore hastened and cut one of the holes so that I could see part of the bone, and found it to be rotten and pierced, and the corruption was going right through to the bone inside.
je soiai ceu qui m’aparissoit de l’os corrumput, et cuidai qu’il n’i eust autre corruption, fuer que celi que je ostai;	I removed what appeared to be rotten from the bone, and believed that there was no other corruption except for that which I had taken out;
et comensai a restourer la plaie de medicines sodans par lonc tens, et ne pot souder;	and began to heal the wound with dried medicines over a long time, but it could not be closed;et s’il eust estoit curat des premiers joures qu’il fuist mal curat, quare li pertuis erent trop grans,
et puis rencomensai, et descovri l’os si com devant, et trovai la corruption continuee en l’os, et la soiai, et puis l’ostai, et me penai de souder le leu;	and then I began again and uncovered the bone as before, and found the corruption continued in the bone, and I removed it, and then I tried to solder the place;
mais je ne pou tant que je copai entor une palme de l’os, et le traï fuer a tout son mole, puis le restourai de medicines;	but I could not, so I cut around a palm of the bone, and drove it out with all its molars, then I restored it with medicine;
et il fut sanez et soudez hastanment, et ne covint plus rencomencier l’ovraige fors por la foibleté dou malaide, qui ne pooit soffrir, et por la paour de mort que je avoie de lui.	and it healed and was soldered quickly, and the wound need not be opened again except for the weakness of the disease, which he could not bear, and because of the fear of death that I had of him.
Car por l’evacuation sanglotoit sovent, mais il fut sanez entierement, et nasquit en leu de l’os une char dure, et fut de bone disposition et n’ot point de nuisement ne de contraire dou tout en tout, ne a l’aleir ne a venir.	For often because of the bloodletting he bled a lot, but he was completely healed and in the place of the bone a hard lump formed, and he had a good disposition and did not suffer any harm or ill effects in every way, neither when walking nor when standing.
Et se li os est brisiez en aucun leu dou cors, si le covient soier en ceste maniere:	And if the bone is broken in any part of the body, it should be treated in this way:
pren I liien, et l’estrain au chief de l’os qui apert, et comande aucun k’il l’estende en haut;	take a string, and tie it to the head of the bone which is open, and order someone to pull it upwards;
et met I autre lien de lainne plus gros dou premier liien, et le lie sus la char qui est desor l’os, et estent le chief, si que tu traies la char corrumpue au desoz, et descuevre la char sus le leu ou tu vues soier, que li soie ne blece la char;	and tie another string of linen larger than the first string, and tie it around the flesh which is above the bone, and pull on the head, so that you draw up the rotten flesh from below, and uncover the flesh above the place where you want to solder, so that the soldering does not hurt the flesh;
et met I tison ou une tauble desoz l’os por mues coper la char corrumpue;	and place a fire or a table under the bone to cover the rotten flesh;
et covient tant soier com on puet veoir et sentir la corruption, et soier ancor autre fois.	and one must probe as far as one can see and feel the corruption, and probe again afterwards.
Et se li os est corrumpus, et n’apert mie, et li corruptions est en mileu ou en une partie, si descuevre la char toute;	And if the bone is rotten and does not open, and the corruption is in the middle or in a part, then uncover all the flesh;
puis met I tison desoz, et puis soie des l’une partie a l’autre la corruption, et soit li soieure dou lonc de la corruption I poc, si com nos avons dit;	then place fire under it, and probe from one side of the corruption to the other, probing deeply into the corruption as we have said;
et se li corruptions est en la jointure, si cope la jointure corrumpue, et soie l’os ou elle contient de l’autre part;	and if the corruption is at the joint, then uncover the rotten joint and probe the bone on the other side of it;
et se li corruptions est en la continuation des II jointes, si n’i a autre angien que dou coper;	and if the corruption is in the middle of two joints, there is no need to uncover it all;
et se li corruptions est ou poignil de la main, ou ou poignil dou piet, si est mout fort celle chose, mais toutevoie il covient que tu enquieres celle corrosion, coment elle t’apert;	and if the corruption is at the base of the hand or the foot, then that is a serious matter, but nevertheless you must probe to find out how it opens;
et la mundifie en toutes les manieres que tu pues, mais que li voine ou li nerf ne te faicent contraire;	and cleanse it in every way you can, but be careful not to damage the vein or nerve.
et saiches que li incisoire et les soies por coper ces os sont maintes, selonc l’assise des os et l’aparance d’ous, et lor grossece et lor subtiliteit, et lor grandor et lor petitece, et lor duresce;	and know that the types of knives and needles used for cutting bone are many, depending on the position of the bones, their appearance, their thickness, their thinness, their size, and their strength.
et por ceu covient il apareillier a chescune semblance d’ovraige son estrument;	and because of this, you must prepare a tool for each type of work.
et saiches que l’uevre te moustrera l’estrument dont tu avras mestier, selonc la conissance de cest art, et le tesmoignaige des manieres des maladies;	and know that the work will show you what tool to use, depending on your knowledge of this craft and the nature of the disease.
si porpense l’estrument dont tu as mestier selonc ceu qu’il le covient.	then choose the tool that is appropriate for what is needed.
dou feu	of fire
Li chiés porrissent ou par cause dedens, ou par cause defuer;	The shoulders may dislocate due to internal or external causes;
et quant tu avras medicinee celle corrosion par la cure des medicines, et il ne profitent mie, si covient coper celui membre jusques au leu ou li corrosion vient, si que li malaides eschaipe par ceu de la mort, ou par la malice, qui est plus grans, de la defaute dou membre;	And when you have treated that corrosion with various medicines, but it does not improve, then you must cover that limb up to the place where the corrosion is, so that the patient escapes death or, if it is greater, the evil of the limb.
et li signes si est que li membres devient noir, si qu’il semble qu’il soit ars dou feu, et porrist aprés la noiror, pues va celle corrosions de membre em membre, et prent par tout le cors;	and the signs are that the limb becomes black, so that it seems to be burned by fire, and then the blackness appears, after which the corrosion spreads from one limb to another and throughout the body.
si te haste dou coper, et se c’est par la percussion d’aucunes venimouses bestes, si com scorpion de mer et wivre et semblans, se li corrosion est au chief dou doi, si le cope, et ne li doner mie espaice de venir jusc’a la main.	and if it is caused by poison from certain venomous creatures such as sea scorpions and vipers and the like, if the corrosion is on the head of the arm, then cut it off, and do not give any time for the venom to spread to the hand.
Et s’elle vient jusc’a la main, si la cope a la jointe, si que la corrosion ne viegne jusc’a bras;	And if it reaches the hand, then cut at the joint so that the corrosion does not spread to the arm.Et s’il vient jusc’a bras, si la coupe a la coude, et ne li doner mie espais de venir adé;
et s’elle vient au bras, si le cope au coute;	and if it reaches the arm, cut at the elbow so that the corrosion does not spread further.And if it reaches the elbow, cut at the joint of the wrist
et s’elle passe le coute, c’est li mors, et n’i vaut amenistremens fuers que li quantitez de sa vertut;	and if it passes the wrist, that is death, and there is no remedy but to cut off the affected limb.Et s’il est al chief du bras ou al coudé, si le coupe a la jointe sus la piere, et s’il li viegne par maint ou par auter member, si le cope a l’
et tot ensi fai quant li corrosion vient ou piet:	and do likewise when frostbite occurs on the foot:
s’elle vient en la premiere jointe, si la cope aprés l’autre jointe;	if it occurs in the first joint, then the toe after the other joint;
et s’elle vient ou piet, si cope tout le piet;	and if it occurs on the foot, then all of the foot;
et s’elle monte en la jambe, si cope a la jointure dou genoil;	and if it ascends the leg, then at the knee joint;
et s’elle vient desus le genoil, si n’i a autre engien que dou lassier le malaide a mort;	and if it occurs above the knee, there is no remedy except to cut off the limb and the patient will die;
et li maniere dou coper ou dou soier le membre si est que tu le lie desus et desoz, et estende uns menistres l’un des liiens aval, et uns autres ministres l’autre liien amont, et tu dessevre la char qui est entre les II liiens a I spatumile large, tant que li os soit descovers;	and the method of covering the affected limb is to tie it above and below, and extend one minister below the binding, and another minister above the binding, and you untie the flesh between the two bindings with a one-span wide incision, so that the bone is exposed;
puis le cope ou soie, et met de chescune part I drapeil de lin, si que li soie ne touche le leu sain, et viegne au malaide autre lesion et aposteme chaus.	then cover it with silk, and place a linen cloth on each side so that the silk does not touch the healthy area, and cause other injury and abscesses.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient quant tu oevres, si cauterize le leu hastanment, ou tu met sus aucunes poudres restraignans;	And if bleeding occurs when you operate, then cauterize the area strongly, or apply some restraining powders to it.
puis revien a ta medicine tant qu’elle soit acomplie, puis lie le membre navreit d’un liien covenauble, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez;	Then return to your medicine until it is complete, then bind the wounded member with suitable bandages and treat it until it is healed.
et je te conterai k’il avint a I home en som piet:	And I will tell you what happened to a man one night:
il li avint une noiror qui sembloit arsure de feu, et celle corrosion vint premier en son doi dou piet, tant qu’elle porprist tout le piet;	He had a darkness that looked like a burn from fire, and this corrosion first appeared on his toe of the foot, so much so that it discolored all the way to the foot.
et quant li hons vit la corrosion, si se hasta de coper le piet, et fut sanez;	And when the man saw the corrosion, he started to cover the foot, and it was healed.
et lonc tens aprés li revint li corrosion ou doi de la main, et il vint a moi, et je li mis sus choses repercussives aprés la mundification dou cors, et ne pot cesser li corrosions;	A long time after, the corrosion returned to his finger on the hand, and he came to me, and I applied some powdery substances after cleansing the body, but could not stop the corrosion.
et il vot que je li copasse la main, et je ne vou, que je avoie esperance de repercuter la matiere;	and he wanted me to examine his hand, but I didn't want to because I had no hope of understanding the nature of the matter.
et doutai ausi que se je tailloie sa main, qu’il ne morist, car li vertus de l’ome estoit foible;	and I doubted that if I cut his hand, he would die, for man's strength was weak;
et il se despera toz, et revint en sa terre, et se hasta de coper sa main, et fut sanez;	and they all despaired, and returned to their land, and had their hand bandaged, and were healed;
et je n’ai ceu conteit fuers que por ceu c’on faice autreteil, s’on en a mestier.	and I have not written this tale for anything but that one might learn from it if they need to.
Aucune fois vient aposteme en leu charnut, et demore si longement qu’il fait grant assemblee de bowe;	Sometimes an abscess forms in a fleshy part, and remains so long that it causes great swelling;
et puis ront et perce, et en saut li bowe, et demoure li leus vuis, ausi com uns vasselz;	and then they rupture and discharge, and the flesh remains hollow, just like vessels;
et li cuir qui est desus est ausi subtilz com I drapelz deliiez, et ne corront mie jusc’a l’os, ne jusc’au nerf, et telz maladie si est apelee «sain», et n’est mie apelee «fistule»;	and the skin above is as delicate as a split piece of cloth, and it does not heal up to the bone or nerve, and such a disease is called 'sain', and is not called 'fistula';
mais s’elle est si alongie qu’elle viegne jusc’a l’os em parfont, si est apelee «fistule»;	but if it is so long that it reaches the bone deep inside, then it is called a "fistula".
et li cuire si est que tu cope celui cuir tout entor, et meismement quant il est subtilz, ausi com uns drapelz;	and if it is so superficial that you can cover the whole wound with a single bandage, especially when it is thin, just like a napkin;
et ne s’aert mie por sa corruption.	and do not worry about its decay.
Et se tu as fiance que li cuirs s’aerde, et li corruption n’est mie en parfont, et li cuir est espés de char, si le cure de clistere ensi:	And if you suspect that the skin will die, and the decay is not deep, and the flesh around it is thick, then treat the wound with a blister:
regarde se li seins est grans, et li bowe qui en ist est de puant odor, adonques le clisterize de medicine egiptiaine qui est ensi faite:	examine if the abscess is large and the pus in it has an offensive smell; then blister with Egyptian medicine which is made like this:
prenez aisil, et oile, et litargire, igalment, et metez cuire en I vassel au feu, tant que li medicine soit rouge, et deviegne ausi espesse com miel;	take honey, oil and litharge, in equal amounts, and mix the medicine in a vessel over fire until the medicine turns red and thickens like honey;
et puis pren de ceu selonc ta necessiteit, et le font en aigue et en miel, et en clisterize lou sein, et estraint le pertus;	and then take this according to your need, and make it into water and honey, and inject the breast, and constrict the orifice;
et laisse la medicine ens par II houres, puis l’estrai en espreignant;	and let the medicine remain in for two hours, then remove it by squeezing;
fai ce mout de fois, tant que li seins soit mondefiiez, et soit ostee li puor;	do this as many times as necessary until the breast is deflated and the pus removed;
et aucune fois est clisterizeis d’aigue de cendres, quant ceste medicine n’est presens, et est que tu preignes cendres de fust de vigne, et giete aigue desus, puis la coule, et en clisterize, tant que tu saiches que li seins est bien mondez;	and sometimes they are injected with water of ashes when the other medicine is not available; take vinegar ashes from a grapevine, pour water over it, then strain and inject into the breast until you know that the breast is fully drained;
et se li malaides ne le puet soffrir, ne la medicine egiptiaine ne l’aigue de cendres, si le clisterize d’aigue et de miel ou il ait un poc de litargire broiet;	and if the patient cannot tolerate the Egyptian medicine or the water of ashes, then inject a mixture of water and honey with a little quicklime powdered in it;
ou tu la clistirize de miel et de vin melleit, que li mielz ait proprieteit de mundifiier et de laver, et li vins fait aerdre le sain;	or you can inject a mixture of honey and melted wax, so that the honey has the property of cleaning and washing, and the wax makes the breast perspire;
et quant tu as ce fait, et tu as fiance que li seins est bien mundifiiez, si le clisterize de ceu que fait naistre char en li, et est que tu preignes emplaustre diafinit, et le font avec oile roset et en vin;	and when you have done this, and you are certain that the wound is well cleaned, then cleanse it with something that makes flesh grow in it, and you take a poultice of diafinit, and mix it with rose oil and wine;
ou tu le clisterize d’aucunes medicines et d’oignemens, dont j’ai dit les proprietez ou traitier des oignemens;	or you cleanse it with some medicine and ointments, of which I have spoken about the properties in the section on ointments;
et se li pertus dou sein est petis, et li cainne dou clistere n’i puet entrer, si l’eslarge d’un fer un poc, et met ens une tente de l’oignement egiptiein, ou oignement basilicon, tant k’il soit eslargiez;	and if the wound is small and the tip of the clewing tube cannot enter it, then widen it with a knife a little, and put in it a tent made of egyptian ointment, or basilicon ointment, until it is widened enough;
et se li plaie est trop large, si la cout et i laisse tant soulement I leu ou li clistere puisse entrer, et se li pertus que giete bowe est au desus, si le cope ou plus bas leu que i est.	and if the wound is too large, then cut it and leave only enough space for the clewing tube to enter, and if the opening that weeps is above, then cover it with a cup or something else that is lower down.
Car quant li bowe est en parfont, si n’i laisse enjanrer char;	For when the bow is drawn fully, one should not let the arrow fly;
et se tu ne pues coper lou sein desoz si com tu vues, si appareille en tel maniere que li bowe corre au plus bas leu que i est, car quant li bowe est parfont, si n’i laisse enjanrer char et se tu ne pues coper lou sein desoz si com tu vues, si apareille en teil maniere:	and if you cannot cover the target below as you wish, then adjust so that the bow points to the lowest place it can reach, for when the bow is drawn fully, one should not let the arrow fly; and if you cannot cover the target below as you wish, then adjust in such a way:
que li bowe corre legierement aval, et n’i lassier rien de la bowe;	let the bow point slightly downward, and leave nothing of the bow;
et pren medicines consolidatives por mettre sor le sain, et estent sus I drapeil de lin que cuevre tout le sain;	and take consolidation medicines to place over the wound, and they are on top of the linen cloth that covers the entire wound;
puis cope as forces endroit le pertus dou sein I poc plus large dou premier, pues estent oignement souef sus I autre drapel selonc la quantiteit dou pertus, et le met sus le pertus dou sain por aligier la bowe, et n’oster mie le grant drapeil fuers que aprés maint jor une fois;	then cover the hole of the wound as tightly as possible with the largest opening first, then apply ointment on the other cloth according to the size of the hole, and place it over the wound to loosen the bow, and do not remove the large cloth for several days once;
et celui qui est sor le pertus dou sein, oste sovent por oster la bowe, et saiches ceu que corra de la bowe, se c’est venin ou poc ou assez, ou digeste, ou indigeste;	and that which is above the opening of the breast, often remove in order to take out the bowels, and know what flows from the bowels, whether it is venom or pus or enough, or digested, or undigested;
et pren warde se li patiens sent dolor ou nom, et s’il i a aposteme ou non, et quant ta medicine s’est en teil maniere estendue et tu vois la nature que saut sus le pertus dou sain, si saiches que li seins s’aert ja, et aproche li santez;	and take care if the patient feels pain or not, and if there is an abscess or not, and when your medicine has been applied in such a way and you see the nature that emerges above the opening of the breast, then you know that the milk flows out, and the breasts are empty;
et puis le deslie le matin, ou le tier jor, et quant tu delies la plaie, si chainge I autre drapeil, et renovele l’oignement.	and then loosen it in the morning, or the third day, and when you loosen the wound, change the other dressing, and renew the ointment.
Et se li seins giete bowe indigeste aprés maint jor, saiches que li seins ne s’aert mie.	And if the breast milk flows low and indigestible after many days, know that the breast does not open.
Et se venins subtilz cort aprés lonc tens, si ne te desperer mie de la santeit, car li santez aproche.	And if subtle poisons creep slowly, you must not despair of health, for health draws near.
Car il i a homes cui tarde enjanremens de char en ses plaies, et de ces que font le contraire;	For there are people whose wounds heal slowly, and others who heal quickly;
et se bowe indigeste saut dou sein aprés maint jor, saiches que li seins ne s’aert mie;	and if undigested bowels emerge from the breast after many days, know that the breasts will not empty;
et se li seins tarde d’aerdre, et est porloigniez, si ajoste medicines sechans moistes en substance et seches en vertut, si com oignement diafinit, car il i a grant partie de vitriole, et c’est li derriene medicine;	and if the breast is slow to dry and is swollen, then apply medicines that are moist in substance but dry in effect, like an ointment of diafragma, for it contains a large portion of vitriol, and it is the most effective medicine.
pren oignement dyafinit, et le font avec oile roset, et l’arose de viel vin igal en substance;	take diafragma ointment, and make it with rose oil, and equal amounts of old wine;
puis le confit et en use;	then cook it and use it;
et ceu meisme fait mielz cuit engroissiez, quant oignemens dyafinit n’est presens, ou tu pren mirre et aloen et encens, et le broie, et le poudre sus le miel quant il est sor le feu;	and with the same make honey candy, when diafragma ointment is not available, or take myrrh and aloe and incense, grind them and sprinkle on the honey while it is over the fire;
et puis en glue I drapel, et l’estent sor le sein, et aucune fois i aministre on aristologe longe, et racines de lis celeste, qui est ausi com farine de veces et centoire;	then apply it to a cloth, and place it over the breast, and sometimes also administer aristologus, a long root, and roots of celestial lily, which is like barley grain and centaury;
et en use de simples ou de compostes:	and use simple remedies or compounds:
broie les, et en fai poudre, et met sus le miel que j’ai dit, et en use;	Grind them up into a powder and mix with the honey I mentioned earlier, then use it.
et se li cure est alongie, et n’est curez par ceste cure, adonc saiches que la corruptions est em parfont, et fait empression en l’os, ou as membres durs, ou as liemens;	And if the wound is deep and not healed by this treatment, then you will know that the corruption goes deep, causing impressions in the bones, or hardening of the limbs or organs.
si le cure de la cure de fistule, si com nos avons dit ci devant.	if the wound is a fistula, as we have already said earlier.
de l’aposteme de l’ungle	of the abscess of the nail
Panarice est un aposteme que naist desoz l’ungle dou pouchiet de la main, ou dou piet, ou par aventure naist en autres dois;	Panarice is an abscess that forms underneath the nail of the finger or toe, or occasionally in other places. It may form on the hand, foot, or elsewhere.
et quant il est envielliez, et on n’i prent garde, si i vient I aposteme chaus, et corront et giete bowe tant qu’elle corront la racine de l’ungle, et par aventure la corront toute;	And when it becomes infected and is left untreated, an abscess will form, and it will spread and discharge pus until it reaches the root of the nail, and sometimes it will spread all the way across.
et vient li corrosions jusc’a l’os, tant qu’il i vient dolor puant, et est li chiés dou doi larges, et est li color fuxe.	This will lead to corrosion of the bone, causing a foul-smelling pain, and the finger or toe will become swollen and red in color.
Quant tu le cures si com nos avons dit en la division, et li cure ne profite mie, si covient que tu copes a i. fer toute la superfluiteit qui est demoree de l’ungle, puis cauterize la plaie aprés.	When you treat it as we have described in the previous section, and the treatment is ineffective, then you must cut away all the excess tissue that remains beneath the nail, and then cauterize the wound afterwards.
Li cauteres est mout grans aide se li os est sains, et li ungle est sainne;	Cauteries are of great aid if the bone is healthy, and the nail is healthy.
et se li ungle apresse la char ens, et l’encomence a poindre, et la blece, si covient que tu mettes lou rait desoz l’ungle que point la char, et la boute en haut, et cope celi char subtilment et legierement, et met sus le remenant de la char medicines ardans et corrosives por oster tout;	and if the nail presses into the flesh and starts to grow in, you should place a thread under the nail so that it pulls the nail away from the flesh, and then lift it up, and gently cut away at the flesh underneath, and put medicine on the remaining flesh to burn and corrode it all away.
puis le cure d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then treat it with ointments until it heals.
Et se li corrosion est en l’os, si le cope, et trai fuer, car tant com li os corrumpus i est, si ne puet saner;	And if the corruption is in the bone, cut it away and draw out the pus, for as long as the bone is corrupted it cannot heal.
et se tu vois le doi corrumpre, si le cope en I des nous si com il est devant dit, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez;	And if you see the toe become corrupted, cut it in half as previously described, and then treat it until it heals.
et s’il est ferus, et boutez, et il sent grant dolor, si covient que tu le sainnes premier;	If it is swollen and filled with pus and causing great pain, then it must be treated first;
puis cope l’ungle dou spatumile agut en taillant de travers desus, et warde que li taille ne viegne jusc’a la char qui est desoz l’ungle, car li malaides sentiroit trop grant dolor;	then cut the nail of the big toe with a chisel, cutting diagonally across it, and be careful that the chisel does not go all the way to the bone underneath the nail, for otherwise the patient will feel too much pain.
et s’il avient, si met chose sus qui apaise.	and if it happens, place something on it to soothe it.
la dolor dou sourdoit de la main	the pain of a deafness in the hand
Li dois ajostez qui naist en mains d’aucuns homes par aventure est toz charnus, et par aventure i a teil ou il a osses, et aucune fois i a ungle, et aucun d’aus naissent en la racine de la jointure, ou li naissance est en aucuns nous des dois.	The two toenails that sometimes grow on people's hands by chance are sometimes all flesh, and sometimes they have bones, and sometimes they have nails, and some grow from the root of the joint, or from one of the toes.
Cil qui naist en aucune nout dou doi ne se muet, et cil qui naist a la jointure dou doi, par aventure se muet;	Nails that grow out of the top of the toe do not move, but those that grow from the joint of the toe sometimes move.
la taille de celui qui est charnus si est legiere, en teil maniere:	The incision for one who is fat should be made in this way:
taille le en sa racine d’un large spatumile.	Cut it at its root with a broad chisel.
Cil qui naist en la racine de la jointure si est grief a curer:	That which grows from the root of the joint is difficult to treat:
si te tien dou coper.	if you try to cut it.
En celui qui naist ou doit au derrien nout, si covient que tu copes premier la char reondement jusc’a l’os, puis cope l’os a une soie convenable a ceu, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	For one who is born with an extra tooth in the gum at the back, you should first cut away the round flesh to the bone, then cut the bone with a suitable silk thread, then heal it until it is healed.
Li soudemens que vient as dois ensamble vient par naissance, ou par soudement de plaie, ou par arsure de feu, ou par semblans choses.	The joints that come together come by birth, or by joint wound, or by burn from fire, or by similar things.
Si couvient que tu copes celle soudeure, si que li doit repairent selonc lor formes naturelz;	You should cut this growth so that the toes grow back together according to their natural shape;
puis met entre dous tentes ou drapelz moilliez en oile roset, qu’il ne se soudent;	then place between them two moistened tents or pieces of cloth in rose oil, so that they do not grow together;
