ou tu met entre dous pieces de plonc subtilz, tant que li leus soit soudez, si com il covient.	or you place between two pieces of fine wood, so that the join is smooth, as it should be.
Se soudemens vient a aucun de ses dois avec la paume, si cope celle sodure si com il covient.	If sealing occurs on one of his hands with the palm, then treat that wound as it should be treated.
des vils	of the villainous
Vis sont voinnes grosses envoloupees pleines de superfluitez melancoliouses, que vienent em plusors membres dou cors;	Veins are large enveloping tubes filled with melancholy excesses which come from various parts of the body;
et plus avient en jambes de ces qui vont a piet et qui travaillent et portent, que a autres.	and it happens more often in the legs of those who walk and work and carry things, than in others.
Il covient donques que tu li aministres aucune fois espurgement de cole, et puis le saine de la basilique.	Therefore, you should administer to him a cleansing enema, and then the basilicon ointment.Et li amonestre et la maniere dou saine et dou cautere, et que il doit faire, si te veult dire.
Li cure de fer si est selonc II manieres:	There are two types of iron cautery:
l’une est c’on les cope, et traie on fuer le sanc noir;	one is where they cut the skin and draw out the black blood;
et li autre maniere si est que tu lieves la voinne, et la trai toute fuer.	and the other way is to lift up the vein and draw it all out.
Li taille si est selonc ceste maniere:	The incision is made in this way:Tu prends un fer chaud, et le mets sus li bouton ou sus la
arose li premier la jambe d’aigue chaude mout fort, tant que li gros sans soit subtiliiez, puis estrain la jambe dou malaide des desus la cuixe jusc’a la partie desoz le genoil;	You take a hot iron and place it on the button or on the top of the leg where the pain is worst, until the large veins are made small, then you draw the leg out of the joint from above the thigh down to the part below the knee;Tu laves li bouton et la jambe d’aigue chaude mout fort, si traies le sans noir qui est en li bouton avec un fer chaud de ceste maniere:
puis cope la voinne en I leu, ou en II ou en III, d’une taille large, puis eslieve et trair fuer le sanc noir a ta main, des l’un chief jusc’a l’autre, tant que tant de sans en isse com li vertus dou malaide puet soffrir;	then open the vein in place I, or II, or III, with an incision of a large size, then draw and squeeze out the black blood into your hand, from one end to the other, until as much blood comes out as the patient can endure;
et puis la lie, et li comande qu’il se teigne de viandes enjanrant cole noire;	and then bandage it, and instruct him to bind himself with black woolen cloth;
et recomence l’evacuation et la sainie quant les voinnes sont plainnes, et nuist au malaide.	and repeat the evacuation and bleeding when the veins are full, and help the patient.
Li alevemens de li est selonc ceste maniere:	The remedies for it are as follows:
reis la jambe dou malaide, s’il i a mout de poil, puis le met ou bain, et li arose la jambe d’aigue chaude tant qu’elle deviegne rouge, et enflent les voinnes;	examine the leg of the patient, if there are many hairs on it, then put it in the bath, and pour hot water on the leg until it turns red and opens the veins;
et se tu n’as point de baing, si le chaufe au feu, et puis le cope endroit la voinne dou lonc au chief dou genoil, ou en la partie desoz a la cheville;	and if you do not have a bath, then heat it with fire, and then open the vein from the top of the knee to the bottom of the ankle, or in the part below the ankle;
puis aoevre le cuir a l’oncine, et escorche la voinne de chescune part, tant qu’ele apere quant on la sent;	then open the skin at the knuckle, and scrape the vein from both sides until it appears when one feels it;
et on la voit rouge et noire, et quant elle entre ou cuir si semble ausi com une corde blainche;	and one sees it red and black, and when it enters the skin it looks like a white string;
puis boute le rait desoz, tant qu’ele soit alevee dou cuir, et puis la pent a l’oncine legier, puis le cope en I autre leu ensus III dois;	then tie off the vein underneath, until it is raised from the skin, and then one can feel it at the knuckle lightly, then cut it in another place above in three places;
puis escorche le cuir sus la voinne tant qu’ele apere, puis la lieve au rais, si com tu as fait, et la pent a un autre uncine, si com tu as fait premiers;	then scrape the skin over the vein until it appears, then lift it with the blade, just as you have done, and feel at another knuckle, just as you did before;puis la lieve au rait sus la voinne, et la coupe a III dois, si com tu as fait premiers.
puis cope une autre taille, ou plusors se tu en as mestier, puis la lieve, et la cope au doi dou piet, puis la trai et lieve jusc’a la seconde taille;	then lift it with the blade on top of the vein, and cut it in three places, just as you did before. Then make another incision, or several if you need to, then lift it and cut it at the toe joint, then pull and lift until the second incision;puis la lieve jusques a la premiere taille, et ainsi adons qu’ele soit alevee de tout le cuir, et que ele soit teneue de
puis l’estrai de taille en taille, tant qu’elle isse toute fuer, puis la cope;	then I extracted it bit by bit, until it was all out, then the scabbard;
et se tu ne la pues traire et lever, si i boute une aguille a tout I fil fort double, et la lie et la trai, et i boute desoz I rait, et torne ta main d’une part et d’autre, tant qu’il en isse;	and if you cannot pull and lift it, then thread a strong double needle, tie it and pull it, and insert the needle under the nail, and turn your hand from side to side, until it comes out;
et garde qu’elle ne cope, car s’elle cope, si ne la puet on traire ne lever, et en vient nuisement au malaide;	and be careful that it doesn't split, because if it does, you won't be able to pull and lift it, and the patient will be harmed;
et quant tu l’as toute traite, si met sor le leu de la plaie laine moillie en vin et en oile roset;	and when you have pulled it all out, then place on the wound wool moistened with wine and rose oil;
et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	and treat it until it is healed.
Et se li vis est contraite et torte et envoloupee ensamble, et ele n’est mie droite, si com nos avons dit, si covient que tu la fendes tortement, mais ne la coper mie;	And if the nail is bent and twisted and wrapped around the finger, as we have said, then you must split it crookedly but not split it;
et la trai si com nos avons devant dit.	and treat them as we have already said.
Li forme dou fer dont on cope la vis si est corbes, et ne trenche mie, qu’il ne cope la voinne;	The shape of the knife used to cut the vein is curved, and it does not cut, so that it can pierce the vein.
et est de grosse corbeure, car s’il estoit subtilz, si coperoit la voine, mais soit gros si com nos avons dit, et ci est li forme:	and it is very curved, because if it were thin, it would cut the vein; but it should be thick as we have said, and this is its shape:
de la voinne civile	of the civil vein
Ceste voinne est enjanree en jambes, en chaudes parties ou il ne naist herbes ne arbre, et en terre ou il n’a point de moistor;	This vein is found in the legs, in dry areas where no herbs or trees grow, and in land without moisture;
et par aventure naist autre part qu’en jambes, et ceu avient de la porriture que vient desoz le cuir, si com il vient dedens le cors serpens et vers, enjanrez entre cuir et char.	and sometimes it grows elsewhere, and this happens from the humors that come under the skin, as do snakes and worms, between the skin and flesh.
Et se li signes de l’encomencement de ceste voinne si est qu’il vient en la jambe une tres grans enflammation, puis se chainge li leus, et comence li voinne fors issir, ausi com une racine d’une plante.	And if the signs of the beginning of this wound are that a great inflammation comes in the leg, then the place changes, and the wound begins to come out forcefully, just as the root of a plant.
Quant li chiés apert, si covient que tu envoloupes entor une piece de plonc des une З et demi jusc’a II З., et la noe, et laisse le plonc pendant a la jambe, et totes les fois qu’il en ist point au defuer, si l’envoloupe entor le plonc, et la nowe;	When the shoulder is dislocated, you must wrap it in a piece of cloth four and a half to five and a half feet long, and tie a knot, leaving the cloth hanging down the leg; and every time it slips out of place, wrap it around the cloth again, and tie a knot.
et s’elle est trop longe, si en cope une partie, et envoloupe le remenant, et ne la coper mie en sa racine, tant qu’elle soit toute issue;	and if it is too long, cut off a part of it, and wrap the remainder around, and do not cover it at all at its root, until it is completely healed.
car se tu la copes, si rentre en la char, et fait venir aposteme et porriture ou leu, et male maladie;	for if you cover it, it will enter the flesh and cause an abscess and pus in that place, and great illness.
por la queil chose il covient qu’elle soit traite poc et poc jusc’a chief, et n’en remaigne rien ou cors;	For this reason, it must be treated a little at a time until the very end, and nothing should remain in the body;
et est aucune fois ceste voinne quant elle est traite de V paumes de lonc, ou de X, et uns hons vint ja a moi, a cui elle issit de X paumes de long, et quant tu la copes, si boute I rais ou pertus, et la perce jusc’a fons, si que tout en isse;	and sometimes this vein is as long as two or three palms, and once a man came to me whose vein was as long as ten palms; and when you cover it, it causes pain in the hole, and penetrates to the very bottom, so that everything comes out.
et soit vuidie li matiere qui est dedens, et amenistre au leu medicines enjanrans porriture aucun jor, puis le cure si com les apostemes.	and the matter within is evacuated, and healing medicines are applied to the area for a few days; then it is treated like an abscess.
Et aucune fois a ceste voinne mains rains, et meismement quant elle apert en la jointure dou piet, ou ou piet, et i vient mout de pertus, et dont il saut rains;	And sometimes this vein opens up in the joint of the foot or the leg, and it bleeds profusely and causes swelling;
cure le donques si com nos avons dit devant.	treat it therefore as we have said before.
des vers qui naissent entre cuir et char	from worms that grow between skin and flesh
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «maladie de buef», por ceu qu’elle avient maintes fois as bués, et est un petis vers qui naist entre cuir et char, et va par tout le cors montant et dessendant, et le sent om bien a l’aler de membre en membre, tant qu’il desront le cuir ou il vait, et saut fuer;	This disease is called "cattle disease" in our land, because it often affects oxen. It is a small worm that lives between the skin and the flesh, moving throughout the body, ascending and descending, until it breaks out of the skin where it goes, causing bleeding;
et est enjanrez de porriture d’aucunes humors, si com vienent vers et serpens et lumbris et ascarides ou ventre;	and it is caused by an excess of humor, like worms and serpents and roundworms in the belly;
et doute on de son malice, car quant il va par le cors, et il monte au chief, et il vient a l’oil, par aventure rentre, et destruit l’oil;	and one fears its malice, for when it moves through the body and ascends to the head, it can enter the eye and destroy it;
et ceu avient maintes fois.	and this often happens.
Quant tu le vues curer et traire, si ne puet on fuers que quant il vait:	When you see him being cured and milked, he cannot resist it, but when he sees it, he will resist.
si covient donques que tu lies le leu desus et desoz d’un fort liien bien estroitement, puis cope sus et le trai fuer, et se li vers est em parfont en la char, et tu ne le trueves, si le cauterize de feu sus, tant qu’il muire;	So you should tie the area above and below with a strong string tightly, then squeeze it from above and milk it firmly. If the venom has spread deeply into the flesh, and you cannot draw it out, then cauterize it with fire until it comes out.
et li plus grans nuisemens que il fait, si est qu’il corront l’oil, si com nos avons dit;	And one of the greatest dangers he poses is that he will run to your eye, as we have said;
et se tu le vois venir ou chief pres de l’oil, si estraint desoz lui le sorcil forment, puis cope sus, et le trai fuer;	and if you see him coming near the eye, grab under his chin firmly, then squeeze and milk him firmly.
et covient user le malaide de mundifiement de cors de medicines solutives por les males humors porries, et se warse de viandes enjanrans porriture.	And one should use the wound medicine for cleansing the body of putrid and corrupt humors, and the meat in the intestines must be dried out.
de la dolor qui vient de ventositeit	from the pain that comes from wind
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «vakirir», et est une dolor que vient en aucuns membres, et pues se mue de membre en membre;	This disease is called 'vacirir' in our land, and it is a pain that comes to some members, and then moves from member to member;
et je vis ceu que je vos di.	and I saw what I am telling you.
Je fui apelez a une femme malaide, et me descovrit som bras, et vis une petite enfleure en la voinne dou brais;	I was called to a sick woman and she uncovered her arm, and I saw a small swelling on the vein of her arm;
et I poc aprés, li vis monter ausi com un ver a l’espaule, plus tost que nulle chose, ausi com vif argent quant il cort de leu a autre;	and soon after, I saw it rise up to her shoulder as quickly as a worm, as fast as quicksilver when it moves from one place to another;
li dolor se departit de celui leu, et se ficha en l’espaule, et puis un poc aprés corrut par tout le cors, tant qu’ele vint en l’autre brais;	the pain left that spot and moved to her shoulder, and then a little later ran through her whole body until it reached the other arm;
puis me contait qu’elle tornioit adés entor le cors, si com je la vis.	then she told me that it was circling around her body as I watched.
Je me mervillai mout coment elle se movoit ensi de membre em membre, car je n’avoie onques veut ceste maladie selonc ceste maniere.	I was very surprised how she moved from limb to limb, for I had never seen this disease progress in this way before.
Toutevoie, je avoie veut maint que bien avoient veut movoir dolor de leu a autre, mais je ne l’avoie mie veut, si com je le vis en la femme;	Nevertheless, I have seen many who wanted the pain to move from one place to another, but I have not seen it happen as I did in this woman;
et je me pensai que c’estoit por ceu que li femme avoit sec cors, et les voinnes descovertes, et por ceu apparoit celle ventositez constrainte;	and I thought that perhaps it was because the woman had a dry body and exposed veins, and thus the wind was forced out;
et n’aperent mie selonc ceste raison a ces qui sont delicious, et qui ont moistes cors et voinnes reponues.	and they do not appear according to this rationale for those who are delicate, and who have moist bodies and relaxed veins.
Et quant tu vues curer ceste maladie, et li malaides sent celle dolor, s’elle t’apert si com nos avons dit, si la lie desus et desoz hastanment, et puis cope sus tant que cele ventositez constrainte au leu isse fuer;	And when you see this disease being treated, and the patient feels the pain, if it appears to you as we have said, then release it above and below quickly, and then press on until the windiness forced out of its place.
et cauterize le leu;	and cauterize the spot;
et se tu ne la vois a tes eulz, si le cure de ceu qui deboute les ventositez, si com pilules fetides, et pilules de serapin, et semblans autres.	and if you do not see it yourself, then treat it with the remover of windiness, such as foul-smelling pills, and pills made from saranapin, and similar others.
des saiettes	arrows
Les saiettes sont diverses, selonc lor semblances et selonc les leus dou cors ou elles chient.	Arrows are diverse, according to their appearance and according to the part of the body where they land.
Li diversitez de lor si est qu’il i a de celles qui ont grans pointes, et petites, et chevees, et soudees;	The variety of their points is that some have large ones, and small, and forked, and hollow;
et de celles qui ont II angles, et de celz qui ont lengues, et de celles ou il a pieces;	and some have two angles, and others have tongues, and some have pieces in them;
et celle qui chiet en aucun membre si chiet selonc II manieres:	and those that break a bone do so in two ways:
ou en membre principeil cheveit, si com cerveil, cuer, foie, pormon, rains, intestine, vessie, et semblans membres.	or in a principal member such as brain, heart, liver, lungs, intestines, bladder, and similar members.
Quant elle chiet donques en aucun leu de ces membres, et li signe de mort, que je te dirai ci aprés, t’aperent:	When it therefore occurs in any of these members, and the signs of death that I will tell you about later become apparent:
si covient que tu te warses de l’estraction de ceste saiette, car li mors vient aprés en plusors dispositions;	then you must be cautious about extracting this arrow, for death comes afterwards in many cases;
et quant cist mal signe ne t’aperent mie, et li saiette n’est mie em parfont, si la trai, et cure la plaie.	and if these bad signs do not appear to you, and the arrow is not deeply lodged, then pull it out and treat the wound.
Et li signe dou cerveil quant li saiette i chiet et perce l’os, et saut li syfac fuer qui est sus le cerveil, est quant scotomie et sode et esvertin et roujor ens eulz, et enflammation et roujor de lengue, et spasme et permixtion d’entendement, et vomissemens de cole;	The signs of the brain are when the arrow pierces and breaks through the bone, and the dura mater which is above the brain is punctured, and there is bleeding and swelling of the brain itself, and redness and inflammation of the tongue, and spasms and disturbance of the mind, and vomiting of bile;
et per aventure ist sans fuer des narines, ou des oreilles;	and sometimes they issue from the nostrils, or the ears;
et par aventure pert la parole et la voix;	and sometimes they lose their speech and voice;
et saut de la plaie moistor blanche semblant a poulz, et en saut ausi com bruee de char;	and from the wound issues white moisture resembling pus, and also as black blood;
et se cist signe t’aperent, si te tien de la cure, et trai la saiette s’elle n’est ens.	and if these signs appear to you, then withhold treatment, and draw out the arrow if it is not inside.
Li signe de la siette quant elle chiet ou cuer, sont qu’elle est pres de la mamele senestre, et sent ausi com s’elle estoit fichie en chose dure, ne mie vuide;	The signs of a wound when it falls on the heart are that it is close to the left breast, and feels as if it were stuck in something hard, not soft;
et par aventure li siette se muet ausi com li poulz, et en cort noir sanc, et vient froidor et suor froide, et sincope:	and sometimes the wound also becomes mute like the pulse, and black blood flows from it, and there is chilliness and cold sweat, and syncope:
saiches adonc sens doute ke li mors dessent.	therefore you should know without doubt that death will follow.
Et li signe de la saiette que nevre lou pormon est que sans plains d’escume saut de la plaie, et li gorge enfle, et li malaides mue color, et sospire haut et quiert le froit ar.	And the sign of an arrow wound that affects the lung is spitting foam from the wound, and a swollen throat, and the patient changes color, and breathes heavily and seeks the cold air.
Et se li saiette chiet en la coverture dou pis, si est delez les petites costes;	And if the arrow falls into the fold of the foot, it is near the small bones;
et giete grant alainne et grant dolor et sospire;	and breathes greatly with difficulty and with great pain and sighing;
et li muevent tuit li membre des espaules.	and all his limbs move from his shoulders.
Et se li saiette chiet ou stomac, par aventure si saut de la plaie aucune chose de la viande indigeste.	And if the arrow pierces the stomach, by chance some undigested food may come out through the wound.
Et se li saiette chiet ou ventre, et en saut point de fien par l’intestine rout, si n’a point d’esperance en la cure, ne en l’estraction de la saiette.	And if the arrow pierces the intestines in the abdomen, and no feces escape through the rear end, then there is no hope for a cure or for removing the arrow.
Et se li saiette chiet en la vessie, et li urine en saut et vient defuer, et li malaides sent fort dolor:	And if the arrow pierces into the bladder, and urine flows out in spurts and it escapes, and the patient feels great pain:
saiches que li plaie est mortelz.	you should know that the wound is deadly.
Li autre membre, si com li faice et li colz et li gorge et li espaule et li adjutoire et li espinee dou dos et li forcele et li cuixe et les jambes, et li membre semblant, sont sauf selonc plusors dispositions.	The other members, such as the face, neck, throat, shoulder, armpit, spine of the back, hip, thigh, and leg, and similar limbs, are safe according to various dispositions.
Quant li saiette est en lou nerf ou l’artere, et elle n’est venimouse, si com je vos dirai qu’il m’avint, por ceu que vos faciez autretel.	When the arrow is in a nerve or artery, and it is not venomous, as I will tell you so that you may do likewise.
Il avint a I home c’une saiette li chut ou larmier en la racine dou neis:	It happened to a man that an arrow pierced his armpit at the root of his elbow:
je la tentai, et la traï d’autre part desoz la graisse de l’oreille, et fut sanez sens nusement.	I probed it, and withdrew it from under the fat of the ear, and he was healed without feeling anything.
Et traï a un jeu une saiette que li chut en la graisse de l’oil desoz la papiere desoz, et li saiette estoit reponue, et n’en poi ataindre que la pointe devers lou fust, et estoit li saiette grans d’un arc turcois, a tout I fer legier sens oreilles;	And I extracted from a man's eye an arrow that had pierced under the papilla under the fat of the eyelid, and the arrow was bent, and it could only be touched at its tip towards the shaft, and the arrow was as long as a Turkish bowstring, all in one piece without any notches;
li jeus fut sanez, et ne li vint nulz mavais accidens.	the child was healthy, and no ill accidents came to him.
Et traï une saiette de la gorge a un crestien, et estoit li saiette arabique a oreilles:	And they pulled out an arrow from the throat of a Christian, and the arrowhead was made of Arab metal, and it was in his ears:
je soiai les barbions, et subtiliai tant que je la traï, et fut sanez li crestiens.	I cut off the barbs, and I pulled it out gently until I extracted it, and the Christian was healed.
Et traï une saiette a I home, que li estoit cheue ou ventre, et pensai qu’il moroit;	And they pulled an arrow from inside a man's home that had lodged in his belly, and I thought he would die;
et puis qu’il ot passez XXX jors, si ne mua point sa disposition;	and then after thirty days, he showed no improvement;
je taillai sus la saiette, et l’engignai, et la traï fuer, et n’ot point de mavais accident.	I cut into the arrow and inserted an instrument to pull it out, and it came out without causing any ill effects.
Et si vis I home cui une saiette chut ou dos, et fut li plaie soudee sus;	And if you see a man with an arrow lodged in his back, and the wound is closed over it;
et demora li saiette dedens li, et ne chainja point ses dispositions naturez, ne ne trova nuisement en aucune de ses oevres naturelz.	and the arrow remains inside him, and he shows no change in his natural functions, nor any harm in any of his natural processes.
Et vis I autre homme, cui il chut une saiette en sa faice, et fut soudee li plaie;	And I saw another man, to whom an arrow had hit his face, and the wound was sewn up.
et demora ensi sens soffrir grant dolor;	and stayed thus without suffering great pain.
et mout d’autres semblans.	and many others similar.
Et traï une saiette a I home des princes le roi, que li estoit cheue enmi lou neiz, et estoit un poc declinans a la destre partie;	And I saw an arrow hit the king's nephew in the eye, and he was slightly inclined to the right side;
et estoit li saiette toute reponue.	and the arrow was all the way in.
Je fui apelez a la cure aprés ceu qu’elle fut cheue III jors.	I was called to treat her after she had been hit for three days.
Si trovai la plaie mult estroite.	I found the wound very tight.
Je la quis a tout une subtil tente, et ne la sentis mie;	I examined her with all my skills and found nothing;
et il sentoit pointure et dolor desoz sa destre oreille.	and she felt numbness and pain under her right ear.
Je pensai que c’estoit de la pointe de la saiette Je mis sus lou leu emplaustre atratifet digestif, por ceu que li leus n’enflast;	I thought it was from the tip of the arrow I placed a soothing and digestive ointment on the spot to reduce swelling;
et m’aparut li leus de la saiette.	and I saw the place where the arrow had hit.
Je i mis l’emplaustre mains jors, et resouda li plaie derechief, et demora ensi li malaides lonc tens, tant qu’il sentit la saiette I jor dedens son neis;	I applied the ointment many times, and the wound healed directly, and the patient suffered for a long time until he felt the arrow one day inside his nose;
et il le me dist.	and he told me about it.
Je mis sus la plaie medicine ague corrosive par mains jors, tant qu’elle fut overte, et la tentai, et sentis le chief de la saiette qui s’aerdoit au leu;	I applied medicine with a corrosive agent to the wound many times until it was open, and I probed it and felt the head of the arrow which had pierced through;
puis ajostai en l’overture de la plaie par celle medicine ague, tant que li chiés de la saiette m’aparut visablement;	then I adjusted the opening of the wound with that medicine until the head of the arrow appeared visibly;
et trespassa bien li termines entor IIII mois, et puis eslarja si li plaie que je i boutai les tenailles, et le meus d’une part et d’autre, et ne pot issir;	and it healed well in about 4 months, and then I lanced the wound that I had probed with tweezers, and squeezed it from both sides, but it would not come out;
adonques ne cessai de subtiliier et d’engignier de manieres d’estrumens, tant que je la pris I jor as tenailles bien faites, selonc ceu que sa forme venra en la fin de cest chapistre, tant que je la traï, et restourai la plaie.	so I did not cease to use subtle methods and tools, until one day I took the arrow with well-made tweezers according to what its shape would allow, as described in this chapter, pulling and squeezing the wound.
Et li mire jugent que li cartillaige dou nez ne puet restorer:	And the doctors judge that the cartilage of the nose cannot be restored:
je la restourai adonques, et fut soudee li plaie, et fut sanez li malaides entierement.	I restored it then, and the wound was sewn up and the patient completely healed.
Or t’ai dit la qualiteit de l’estraction d’aucunes saiettes, si que tu mettes ta cure sus ceu que je ne dis mie, car li livres ne puet mie tout porprendre;	Now I have told you about the extraction of certain arrows so that you can apply my instructions to similar cases, for books cannot encompass everything.
mais li saiges maistres compere sus bien poc grant chose, et sus ceu que li est present et defaillant, trueve nueve oevre, et nuef estrument, au dessendement des choses estrainges qui avienent en cest art.	But the wise masters compare based on a few great things and on what is present and lacking; they find new treatments and new instruments in the descent of strange things that occur in this art.
Je dis que les saiettes n’issent des membres ou elles sont fichies fuer que selonc II manieres:	I say that arrows enter the body where they are pierced in two ways:
ou par lou leu ou elles entrent, ou par d’autre part;	either through the place where they entered or through another part;
et celle que saut fuer par lai ou elle entre, c’est saiette entrans en leus charnus, et saut fuer aucune fois maintenant.	and that which enters through where it pierces is called an arrow entering the flesh, and sometimes it has exited now.
Et s’elle ne saut maintenant, si la laisse tant que li chars soit porrie entor, et soit alegie li issue;	And if it does not heal now, leave it until the wound becomes putrid around the edges and the discharge has stopped.
et ausi s’elle est fichie en l’os, et elle ne puet issir, si la laisse ensi aucuns jors, et la muef chescun jor;	and if it is embedded in the bone, and cannot drain, then leave it like that for a few days, stirring it each day;
et adonques elle saut, et s’elle ne saut, si perce entor a tout I foret subtil, tant que li leus entor soit eslargiez, et puis la trai.	and then it will drain. And if it does not, pierce around the edge with a very thin instrument until the edges are widened, and then draw it out.
Et se li saiette est fichie en l’os dou chief, et vait jusc’a l’un des ventres dou cerveil, et aucuns des accidens que j’ai dit apert au malaide:	And if the arrow is lodged in the bone of the head and penetrates to one of the ventricles of the brain, and any of the aforesaid symptoms manifest in the patient:
si ne la traire mie, mais la laisse tant qu’elle soit igalz aprés aucuns jors, car se li saiette vient jusc’a syfac, c’est li mors.	do not extract it, but leave it until it has drained for a few days, for if the arrow has reached the brain, it is fatal.
Et se li saiette n’est fichie fuer qu’en l’os soulement, et ne vient jusc’a syfac, et demoure li malaides aucuns jors sens mavais accident, si l’engigne dou traire.	And if the arrow is lodged only in the bone and does not go to the brain, and the patient remains for several days without any bad symptoms, then prepare an instrument for extraction.
Et s’elle est mout fichie ensi et ne puet issir fuer, si i aministre tareres entor, si com je t’ai dit;	And if it is lodged very deeply and cannot drain outward, then administer cauterizations around the wound as I have instructed;
puis cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	then treat the area until it is healed.
Et se li saiette est reponue en leu dou cors si c’on ne la puisse veoir, si la quier a tout la tente;	And if the arrow is lodged in the body where it cannot be seen, then one wants to know its location throughout the entire body;
et se tu la sens, si la trai a aucun estrument covenauble;	and if you feel it, then draw it out with an appropriate instrument;
et se tu ne pues por l’estrecement de la plaie, et por la parfondesce de la saiette, et il n’i a os ne nerf ne voine, si la fens tant que li plaie soit grans;	and if you cannot due to the tightness of the wound and the depth of the arrow, and there is no bone, nerve, or vein, then cut it out as much as the wound is large;
et trai la saiette se tu pues, et s’il ait en la saiette oreilles a coi elle tient, si oste la char qui est ens fichie de II pars au mues que tu pues, et puis brise ou ploie les oreilles de la saiette, tant que tu la puisses traire;	and pull out the arrow if you can, and if it has barbs that are holding it in place, then cut away the flesh where it is lodged on both sides as much as you can, and then bend or twist the barbs of the arrow until you can pull it out;
et subtilie bien que tu ne brisier la saiette, que tu la trairoies plus griement.	and be careful not to break the arrow as you pull it out more forcefully.
Et se tu ne pues a une fois, si la lai jusque li leus entor soit porris, puis la trai, car li estraction iert alegie.	And if you cannot on one try, then leave it until the wound around it is swollen; then pull it out, for extraction is eased.
Et se li decorremens de sanc te fait contraire, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit de la cure en son chapistre;	And if the bleeding makes it contrary, then administer what we have said about the treatment in its chapter;
et te warde de l’incision dou nerf et de la voinne, et met engien coment tu pues mues traire la saiette sens peril, ou tost ou tart, ou fermement ou belement;	and beware of cutting into the nerve and the vein, and put in a clean way as you can move the arrow without danger, quickly or slowly, firmly or gently;
et met le malaide selonc la forme qu’il estoit quant li saiette li chut ens, car c’est li plus grans aide que i soit, et se tu ne pues, si lou met selonc ceu que li signe lou te mostrent.	and put the patient in the same position as when the arrow struck him, for that is his greatest aid; and if you cannot, then put him according to what the signs show you.
Li saiette que vient fuer d’autre part, ou il apert aucune chose de li, ou li cuir est enflez endroit si c’on le voit ou sent aparamment:	Arrows that come from another direction, or something appears from him, or his skin is swollen in that place where one sees or feels it apparently:
taille donques sus, tant que les tenailles i puissent prendre, et puis l’estrai:	Cut therefore above, as far as the tweezers can reach, and then pull it out;
si saut fuer maintenant.	if it will not come out now.
Et s’elle est retenue en l’os, si tornoie ta main rondement, tant qu’elle entre en l’os, et eslarge l’os, puis la trai.	If it is stuck in the bone, rotate your hand rapidly, forcing it into the bone and widening the opening; then pull it out.
Et s’elle ne puet issir, si la laisse encor, et puis rencomence l’estraction tant qu’elle isse fuer;	And if it cannot be pulled out, then leave it for now, and then try pulling again until it comes out;
et se li fust de la saiette i est, se le boute a tout le fust;	and if there is a shaft of an arrow inside him, then it goes all the way through.
et se li fust chiet, et tu vues aministrer boutement, si i aministre I estrument cheveit, si que li pointe de la saiette entre en la cheveure de l’estrument;	and if there is a broken shaft, and you wish to administer an extraction tool, then the tip of the arrow must enter into the groove of the tool.
et puis boute fuer, et se li saiette est chevee, se i boute I estrument a pointe entrant ens, por alegier l’estraction.	and then pull outward, and if the arrow is hooked, then pull the tool inward with its tip entering in, to aid the extraction.
Et se li saiette est entouchie, si covient que tu copes toute la char entor ou li venins est, se tu pues, puis cure la plaie si com il couvient.	And if the arrow has touched [the wound], then you must cut away all the flesh around where the poison is, if you can; then treat the wound as it should be.
Et se li saiette chiet ou peis ou au ventre ou a la vessie ou au costeit, et elle est prochiene, et tu pues coper sus, se i cope;	And if the arrow is broken in the shoulder or leg or belly or bladder or groin, and it is close to the surface, and you can reach it by pressing, then press it out.
et te garde de coper la voinne et lou nerf, et puis l’estrai, et puis cout la plaie, se mestier est;	And be careful not to press on a vein or nerve, and then pull it out, and then examine the wound, if necessary.
et la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	and treat it until it is healed.
Li forme des tenailles dont on trait les saiettes sont semblans au bec d’oiseil, et vez ci la forme:	The shape of the forceps used to treat arrows is similar to an owl's beak; see the diagram.
Et en sont mout de manieres:	There are many ways to do this:
grans, moienes, et petites, selonc la quantitei de la saiette.	large, medium, and small, depending on the size of the arrow.
Li forme dou boutant cheveit est ausi com li penne d’un oisel, por bouter a la pointe de la saiette, si com ci est li forme:	The shape of the broad-headed arrowhead is also like the feather of a bird, to catch on the tip of the arrow, just as its shape is:
li forme des tenailles por bouter et por sachier si est ci:	the form of tongs for pushing and probing is as follows:
des voinnes dou cors communes	of common body veins
Des voinnes dont on se saine sont XXXI, de coi il a ou chef XVI, c’est a savoir:	There are 31 veins from which one can bleed, and they have 16 branches in total, as follows:
II batans qui sont aprés les oreilles, qui sont apelees les dous «herbech»;	Two veins that are behind the ears, called "the two little cows";
et les II arteres qui sont en II temples apparans;	and the two arteries in the two temples;
et II voines que sont en II larmiers des II eulz, que sont apelees «aspires»;	and two veins that are in the eyelids, which are called "aspirers";
et li voine que est emmi le front;	and the vein that is in the forehead;
et li voinne que est au chief dou neis;	and the vein that is at the top of the nose;
et les II guindeges qui sont ou col;	and the two windpipes which are in the neck;
et les II voinnes que sont en levres desus de la bouche, et ce sont les voines que sont apelees «augeherich»;	and the two veins that are on the upper lip, and they are the veins called "augerich";
et II voinnes que sont desoz la lengue.	and the two veins that are under the tongue.
Les voinnes dont on saine communement sont V en chescun bras:	The veins from which one commonly bleeds are five in each arm:
l’une est li cephalique, et est dou senestre costeit, et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou chief»;	one is the cephalic vein, and it is on the left side of the chest, and common people call it the "vein of the head";
et li moiene est apelee «faste», et est composte de la cephalique et de la basilique, et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou cuer»;	and the middle one is called the "fast" vein, and it is composed of the cephalic and basilic veins, and common people call it the  "vein of the heart";
et li basilique si est ou destre costeit, et l’apelent li laie gent «voinne dou ventre», et est sus le foscile, et est celle dont on saine, qui apert manifestement sus le pouchet.	and the basilic vein is located on the right side, and the common people call it "vein of the belly", and it is situated above the bladder, and it is that vein which is clearly visible above the scrotum.
Et li salvatelle est li voine qui est entre l’auriculaire et l’anulaire, et si a II rains;	And the basilic vein is located between the little finger and the ring finger, and it has two branches:
et en la jambe et ou piet sont III voinnes:	and in the leg and the foot there are three veins;
l’une si est desoz la corbeure dou pochet dou senestre costeit, et li seconde sophene qui est a la cheville dou destre costeit;	one is below the curve of the scrotum on the left side, and the second superficial vein is at the ankle on the right side;
et li voine qui est apelee «nesse», que est en la cheville de l’autre costei;	and the third vein, called "nesse," is at the other ankle.And there are two more veins in the arm: one is above the elbow joint and is called "vein of the elbow" (veine dou coude), and the other is below
et en l’autre jambe sont III voinnes desoz celles.	and in the other leg there are three veins below those mentioned.And in the neck are two veins, one on each side, called  "veins of
Li sainie des voinnes que sont aprés les oreilles si aide as catharres anciens, et a emigraine;	The bleeding of veins which are behind the ears is helped by old cataracts, and by emigration.
et li qualiteis dou sainier, si com je te dis, et est que tu reises lou chief dou malaide, et frote lou leu ou les voinnes sont d’un drap aspre;	and the qualities of the bleeding, as I told you, and it is that you raise the head of the patient, and rub the area where the veins are with a rough cloth;
puis estrigne li malaides son col a une vis, tant que les II voinnes aperent derrier les oreilles en II leus dependens dou chief:	then squeeze the patient's neck with your hand, until the two veins appear behind the ears, coming out of the head in two places.
quier les donques a ton doi, et ou tu sens lou poulz desoz ton doi, si seigne d’enche;	take them therefore to your fingers, and where you feel the pulse under your fingers, stop it there;
puis pren la lancette, et la boute par desoz la voine jusc’a l’os, puis lieve ta main a tout la voinne amont, et cope et lou cuir et la voinne bien II dois dou traver, et fai issir dou sanc tant que tu vues;	then take the lance and thrust it under the vein up to the bone, then lift your hand all along the vein, and cut through both skin and vein thoroughly with two strokes of the lance, and let blood out until you see enough.
puis l’estrain et lie, tant qu’ele soit sanee;	then squeeze it and bind it, until it is healed.
et j’ai ja dit l’incision et le cautere ou premier livre.	and I have already spoken of incisions and cauteries in the first book.
Li sainie des II arteres que sont en II temples, si vaut a emigrainne anciene, et sode, et obtalmie acostumee, et au cors des larmes agues as eulz;	The bleeding of the two arteries in the temples is good for long-standing migraines, and eye sores, and regular tears, and pain in the eyes.
et li qualitez dou sainier si est si com je dis:	and the qualities of the bleeding are as I have said:
et est que li malaides estraigne son col, tant que les II voinnes aperent apertement;	and the patient should stretch his neck so that the two veins are clearly visible;
et sent lou polz desoz ton doi, et puis seigne d’enche;	and feel for the pulse under your finger, and then press inwards;
puis lieve lou keur sus la voinne en haut a ton doi indice, et boute la lancette desoz, et lieve la voine en haut, et la cope, si com tu as fait en II autres voinnes, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit;	then gently press the vein near the top with your thumb, and insert the lance underneath, and release the vein above, and stop the bleeding according to your need; then clean the wound as before and do the same for the other vein.
puis deslie lou malaide, et met ton doi sus la voine une houre, puis met sus coton;	then release the patient, and put your finger on the vein for an hour, then put cotton on it;
et puis la lie forment, et la laisse tant qu’elle soit sanee;	and then forms a scurf, and leaves it until it is healed;
et nos en avons jai parleit et de lor copement et de lor estraction, ou comencement dou livre.	and we have spoken of their appearance and extraction in the beginning of the book.
Li sainie de la voine dou front si vaut autant com li sainie de la cephalique as maladies de la faice ancienes, et a emigraine, et a roujor;	The bleeding from the frontal vein is just as dangerous as the bleeding from the cephalic vein in old facial diseases, and causes emigration and redness;
et li qualitez si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant, tant que li voine apere;	and its quality is such that the patient twists his neck until the vein appears;
puis pren l’estrument qui est apelez «fosseur», dont ci est li forme:	then take the instrument called "borer", of which this is the form:
Et met la pointe sus la voinne, et fier sus de ta main, ou d’autre chose, et laisse dou sanc issir selonc la quantiteit que tu vues;	And place the point on the vein, press firmly with your hand or something else, and let the blood issue according to the amount you see;
puis delie au malaide le col, et lie la voine tant qu’elle soit saneel et aucune fois l’uevre on d’un flaime large.	then loosen the patient's neck, and ligature the vein until it is healed; sometimes the work is done with a wide flame.
Toutevoie, il ne covient mie que li flaimes soit trop agus;	However, the flames must not be too sharp;
et le saine de travers, car li os est pres, et par aventure brise li flaimes quant il est subtilz.	and the vein is crooked, for the bone is close by, and the flame may break when it is thin.
Li sainie des II voines que sont en II larmiers si aide as eulz, et a la tigne, et a la roujor, et a l’oriuel en l’oil, et as maladies de la faice;	The veins of the two arms help each other, and so do those in the legs, and those in the face, and so do the diseases of the eye and the face;
et li qualitez de lor sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant d’aucun liien, si com devant;	and the nature of their veins is such that the patient turns his neck in twisting some ligament, as before;
puis le saine, et soit li sainie dou traver, un poc dou lonc dou flaime un poc large, car il n’i a point de char.	then open the vein, and if the vein is deep, make the flame somewhat long and broad, for there is no flesh there.
Et se li flaimes est subtilz, par aventure si brise;	And if the flame is thin, it may break by accident;
puis fai corre dou sanc, tant com tu en as mestier, et puis lie sus couton, et le lie bien.	then let the blood flow, as much as you need, and then ligature the vein, and tie it well.
Li sainie de la voine dou neis si vaut a ague, et a sode forsenee, et a maladies de faice, si com emigraine et roujor que vient en la faice, et meimement quant elle est anciene;	The bleeding of the vein in the nose is good for the headache, and for a sudden seizure, and for illnesses of the face, such as migraine and redness that comes to the face, and also when it is old.
et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estrigne son col, puis estrain son neis a ta main senestre, et pren lou flaime subtil lonc, et le fiche emmi la levre en l’espaice qui est entre les II narines, car li voinne n’apert mie bien enqui, et li sans comencera maintenant a corre;	and the quality of the bleeding is such that the patient squeezes his neck, then pinches his nose with his left hand, and takes a long, thin flame, and inserts it into the lip in the space between the two nostrils, for the vein does not open well there, and the blood will now begin to flow.
et n’aler mie trop em parfont, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit, puis la lie une nuit, car elle est mout tost restoree;	and do not go too deep, and let the blood flow according to your need, then ligate it for a night, for it is soon restored.
et c’est li forme dou flaime:	And this is the form of the flame:
Li sainie des II guindeges si aide a l’estrecement de l’alainne, et a l’encomencement de meselerie, et a mout de maladies, et a empetigine, et a corrodens, et a herpes, et estiomenes;	The bleeding of the two veins helps with strangury, and with the beginning of mensuration, and with many illnesses, and with impetigo, and with corrosives, and with herpes, and with stomach-aches;
et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col desoz l’une et l’autre, si com nos avons dit;	and the quality of the healing is such that the patient stretches his neck back and forth, as we have said.
et soit li maistres estans sus lou chief dou malaide, et li malaides siece sus I siege, puis saine la voine dou lonc un poc largement, puis trai dou sanc tempreement, ou tant com mestier est;	and the master standing above the patient's head, and the patient seated, then open the vein of the long arm widely, then draw out blood temperately, as much as is needed.
puis refai autreteil en l’autre voinne, puis deslie lou liien, et estraint andous les voines moienement, que li malaides n’estrangle;	then do the same in the other vein, then loosen the bandage, and gently constrict the veins so that the patient does not choke.
et le laisse jusc’au matin, que li plaie soit sanee.	and leave it until the morning, for the wound to heal.
de la sainie des leivres	of bleeding gums
Li sainie des voinnes des levres desus si aident a cole en la bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et fendures de levres, et dou neis et entor.	Here is the translation: The bleeding of the veins in the lips above helps with sores in the mouth, and gum corruption, and splits in the lips, and the pain of teeth and gums.
Et li qualitez de la sainie si est de faire seoir lou malaide devant toi, et estraint son col si com j’ai dit;	And the quality of the healing is such that you have the patient sit in front of you and stretch his neck as I have said.
puis torne la levre, et regarde as II voinnes, dont l’une est a la destre levre et li autre a la senestre, et les conoist on par ceu qu’elles sont noires, et par ceu que entor elles a voines menues noires:	Then turn the lip and examine the two veins, one on the right and the other on the left. You can identify them because they are black and because there are tiny black veins around them:
cope donques l’une et l’autre, et se tu ne les conois, et tu en es en doutance, si cope la plus grosse de chescune part, et tout ausi fai des II voinnes que sont desus et desoz, car c’est une meisme maniere.	therefore take one and the other, and if you do not know them, and you are in doubt, then take the thickest of each side, and likewise do to the two veins that are above and below, for it is the same manner.
de la sainie desoz la lengue	of bleeding under the tongue
Li sainie des voinnes que sont desoz la lengue si aide aprés la sainie de la cephalique, et c’est a l’estrecement de la gorge, et as maladies de l’uve, et as maladies de la bouche;	The bleeding of the veins that are under the tongue helps after the bleeding of the cephalic vein, and it is for the constriction of the throat, and for diseases of the liver, and for diseases of the mouth;
et li qualitez dou sainier si est que li malaides siece entre tes mains devant lou soleil, et li lieve la lengue, et regarde desoz en chescun costeit une voinne noire:	and the qualities of the bleeder are such that the patient sits between your hands in front of the sun, and he sticks out his tongue, and looks under each armpit for a black vein:
saine donques l’une et l’autre, et n’aler mie trop em parfont, car desoz sont les arteres.	therefore bleed one and the other, and do not go too deep, for under them are the arteries.
Les voinnes dou coute dont on saine communement sont sainies selonc II manieres:	The veins of the neck from which one commonly bleeds are bled according to two manners:car il y a l’une qui est desus la veine qui va sus la gorge, et l’auter qui est desouz
ou em poignant a tout I flaime mirtin large, ou olivaire subtil si com coutez trenchans, et est apelez «anesil»;	or with a pointed flame of a large myrtle twig, or an olive tree sprig as thin as you can get it, and it is called "anesil".
et sont large et subtil selonc la largesce et l’estrecement des voinnes.	and they are wide and thin according to the width and tightness of the veins.
Li forme dou flaime mirtin si est mout renommee, et est large si com tu vois:	The shape of the candle flame is very important, and it should be as wide as you see:
Et ait mestier por ovrir les voinnes chevees plaines de gros sanc apparent, et que contienent gros sanc et trouble;	And it is necessary to open the flat, veiny veins that hold large amounts of visible blood;
et c’est li forme dou flaime olivaire:	and this is the shape of the olive flame:
et est plus subtilz apointé, et est por sainier les voinnes subtilz, ou il a subtil sanc citrin.	and it is more pointed and suitable for bleeding the subtle veins where there is thin, yellow blood.
Li sainie de la basilique, qui est une de ces voinnes, si aide as maladies que sont desoz la gorge, et ou col, et ou peis, et ou ventre;	The basil vein, which is one of these veins, helps with illnesses under the throat, and in the neck, chest, and abdomen;
et covient au sainor qu’il saine saigement, et qu’il se warse de l’artere qui est desoz.	and the surgeon should bleed it, and then compress the artery underneath.
Et s’il cope l’arterre, et decorremens de sanc vient, si le covient estainchier, si com j’ai dit;	And if he pierces the artery, and bleeding occurs, he must then stanch it as I have said;
et ne doit mie estre poignans li flaime, mais taillans si com anesil.	and the flame should not be piercing, but cutting like an "anesil".
Et se li basilique n’apert manifestement, si covient que tu l’estrainges, et chainge une autre;	And if the basil does not open clearly, then you must extract it and replace it with another;
ou tu quieres aucun rain de li, ou tu saine en leu de li la voinne emmi le bras:	or you can tie some thread to it, or you can ligate the vein in the arm in its place:
elle apert manifestement;	it opens clearly;
et la cope au flaime anesil, si com nos avons dit.	and apply the cup to the flame, as we have said.
Et se tu vues conoistre le leu de la sainie, si covient ainsois que tu estraignes lou bras, que tu touches le leu tant que tu conoisses le poulz;	And if you want to find the place for bleeding, then you must stretch out the arm and touch the spot until you feel the pulse;et la sainie se fait en ce leu qui le poulz est le plus fort; et la sainie se doit faire sus le piez de costé li bras;
puis signe le leu d’enche, et puis lie lou bras, et cope la voine dou flaime anesil;	then sign the place for bleeding, and then tie the arm, and apply the cup to the flame with the heat lessened;et si tu voulues saine a l'autre piez de li bras, si covient que tu liasse le piez en bas, et la vo
et warde que tu ne ferir en l’artere quant tu vois le leu enfleit, car c’est de l’artere:	And if you want to bleed at the other side of the arm, then you must let the foot hang down, and keep your hand steady so that you do not pierce an artery when you see the spot swollen, for it is an artery;
eschui la donques.	Avoid it therefore.
Et se tu vois saillir en haut ausi com l’urine d’un enfant, et li sans est rouges et subtilz, saiches que c’est sans de l’artere:	And if you see it emerging upwards like a child's urine, and the blood is red and thin, know that this is blood from an artery:
haste toi donques, et met ton doi sus longement, puis oste ton doi se li sans estainche, que maintes fois avient;	Therefore hurry, and place your finger over it for a long time, then remove your finger if the flow stops, which often happens.
se lie lou bras, et laisse ensi, et ne lou mueve li malaides;	Bind the arm and leave it thus, and do not move it:
et soit sus paour, et ne lou mueve tant qu’il soit sanez.	and be careful not to move it until it is healed.
Et se li sans n’est estainchiez, et il te vaint, et li medicine ne t’est presens, si cope l’artere s’elle apert, car li chief de li retraient;	And if the flow does not stop and the medicine is not present, then cut open the artery, for its source is within.
et estainche li sans.	Stop the bleeding.Et si tu vois sortir li sang a l’envers, si
Et pren une escorce de fistice, et la fent, et pren l’une des moitiez et lie sus bien jusc’a l’autre jor;	And if you see the blood flowing backwards, then take an oak twig, split it, and take one half and bind it on tightly until the next day;
se li sans estainche, c’est bien;	if it closes the wound, that is good;
se ce non, si le cure, si com nos avons dit, des poudres qui estainchent sanc;	if not, then treat it with the powders that stop bleeding, as we have said;
et li estainchemens n’est mie griés em plusors dispositions por le petit leu de la plaie, et la possance dou liien dou bras.	and the wound is not cauterized in many ways due to the small size of the wound and the strength of the arm.
Li sainie de la voinne em mileu si aide qu’elle trait sanc dou chief desus, et dou cors desoz, por ceu qu’elle est composte de la basilique et de la cephalique, si com nos avons dit;	The bleeding from the vein in the middle, if it draws blood from above and below, because it is made up of basil and skullcap, as we have said;
et covient au sainor qu’il se warse por lou nerf qui est desoz, et s’il point trop em parfont, et il trueve lou nerf, et il enfle et li santez soit griés, et par aventure ne puet saner;	and the surgeon must be careful not to go too deep and to find the nerve underneath, and if it pricks too much and the nerve is inflamed and the wound is cauterized, and perhaps cannot heal;
et cist nerf apert mult de fois, et s’il n’apert en aucuns homes por sa subtiliteit, si covient que tu lou saines de l’estrument anesil;	and this nerve often opens up, and if it does not open in some people due to its subtlety, then you must treat it with the instrument called 'anesil';et li sainie de la voinne de la man si fait que li santez ne soit pas griés en aucun maniere, et ne trieve li nerf por quoy il soit enfle, car en ceste maniere est granz paors.
et eschui lou nerf a ton pooir.	and avoid the nerve with your touch.
Et se il a voinne entre les .ij. ners, si la fent dou lonc.	And if there is a vein between the two nerves, they cut it deeply.
Li sainie de la cephalique si aide, qu’ele atrait sanc dou chief, et aide as eulz;	The headache if it helps, that it draws blood from the head, and helps the eyes;
et covient sainier em poignant au flaime olivaire ou au flaime mirtin, car c’est li plus sauve de toutes les voinnes, car il n’a desoz li ne nerf ne artere.	and it is necessary to bleed them with an olive-oil flame or a myrtle flame, for it is the safest of all veins, for there are no nerves or arteries underneath it.
Toutevoie, covient querir lou plus legier leu, et ne grieve rien s’on faut la premiere fois, et on rencomence;	Nevertheless, one should seek the lightest place, and not harm anything if one needs to do it a second time;
et par aventure enfle li leus a aucuns homes, cant on faut la premiere fois, mais il ne grieve rien.	and by chance, it swells in some people, where one needs to do it the first time, but it does not harm anything.
La qualitez de la sainie si est selonc ta pensee.	The quality of the bleeding is according to your thoughts.
Li premiere chose que tu dois savoir de sainier, si est que sainie n’est amenistree fuer que por garder santeit, et por eschuir les maladies a venir;	The first thing you should know about bleeding is that bleeding is not done simply to maintain health and prevent diseases;
et soit li sainie faite en l’une des III voinnes que sont ou coute:	and the bleeding is done in one of the three veins that are in the arm:
c’est a savoir, cephalique, faste, et basilique;	Here is to know, cephalic, fast, and basilic;
et se doit on sainier en l’encomencement de prientens a geun, et en autompne et en yver aprés mengier, quant li signe de repletion aperent;	and one should bleed in the beginning of spring, autumn, and winter after eating, when the signs of repletion are apparent;
et se doit on sainier le premier jor ou le tier, aprés II houres ou III dou jor.	and one should bleed the first day or the third, after two hours or three of the day.
Li sainie qui est aministree as maladies n’a point d’oure determinee, mais que quant besoing est de jor ou de nut, en toutes houres et en toz tens;	The bleeding administered for diseases does not have a set time, but when the need arises, day or night, at all times and in all seasons;
et ne covient mie sainier les enfans jusc’a XIIII ans, ne femme portant fuer que des lou quart mois jusc’a septime.	and one must not bleed children until they are 14 years old, nor a woman carrying a child before the fourth month until the seventh month.Li sainie qui est aministree as maladies n'a point d'oure determinee, mais que quant besoing est de jor ou de nut, en toutes houres et en toz tens;
Ne ne se doient mie sainier li viel qui ont passez .lx. ans.	Nor should the very old who have passed 60 years be bled.
Et quant aucuns se vuet sainier, en quel maniere que ce soit, si covient k’il mondefie les intestines d’un clistere legier, s’il a mout de fiens retenut, si que les voines n’atraient des intestines les superfluitez porries nuisans as membres principelz;	And when one wishes to bleed, in whatever manner, one should first cleanse the intestines with a gentle enema if one has retained much feces, so that the veins do not draw in harmful excess fluids from the intestines, which harm the principal members.Et quant aucuns se vuet sainier, en quel maniere que ce soit, si covient k’il mondefie les intestines d’un clistere legier, s’il a mout de fiens retenut, si que les voines n’atraient des intestines les superfluitez porries nuisans as membres principelz;
ne ne se saine mie cil qui est trop saolez de viandes, ne qui est yvres, tant k’il en soit fuer, ne ydropiques;	one does not heal at all those who are too full of meat, nor the drunk, however long they may be, nor the dropsical.
et se warse on de sainier aprés colique passion, et vomissement, et decorrement de ventre, et multipliement d’abiter a femme, et de traval, de veiller et de juner, et ceu que tot la vertu, ou par chose de l’arme ou dou cors;	and if one wishes to heal after colic, vomiting, and diarrhea, and excessive sexual intercourse, and exertion, from waking and fasting, and all that weakens the body, whether through injury or illness.
puis subtilie les humors, se li sans est gros, par viandes et par bevraiges et par medicines, se tu en as lou poir;	then gently draw out the humors, if the body is swollen, through meat and drink and medicine, if you have the skill.
puis entre ou bain, s’aucune chose ne lou deffent, por subtiliier lou sanc, et te saine de la voinne dou pis entor la tierce, si com nos avons dit;	then enter the bath, if nothing else harms them, to draw out the blood, and heal the wound around the navel, as we have said.
et te garde celui jor de travail, et de poinne, et de luxure, et de semblans choses;	and avoid that day exertion, pain, and lust, and similar things.
et soies liez et joians, et soit li sainieres plus haut que cil cui on saine, et li frote lou bras II fois ou III, puis estraigne lou liien desus moienement, car quant il est trop estrois ou poc, si ne puet corre li sans;	and be relaxed and cheerful, and let the healer sit higher than the one being healed, and rub the arm two or three times, then tighten the ligature above the wound, for if it is too loose or too tight, it cannot heal the wound.
et puis le frote le leu as mains, tant que les voines enflent, et les sente on;	and then rub the area with the hands, until the veins swell, and you feel them;
puis moille li sainieres le flaime d’un poc d’oile viel, puis mette son doit de sa main senestre sus celle voinne desoz lou leu un poc ou il vuet sainier, que li voinne ne fue et faille au ferir.	then moisten the wound with a little old oil, then place his left hand’s index finger on that vein below the area he wants to bleed, so that the blood flows and doesn’t stop at the cut.
Car il i a voinnes que fuient ausi com cordes au sainier, et si a de telz que sont plainnes de ventositeit, si que quant on met sus le flaime, si retrait a flaime, et ne puet ovrir li voinne, et ensi est on de ceus;	For there are veins that flow like strings when bled, and some are filled with windiness, so that when one applies the flame, it retreats, and the wound cannot be opened, and thus it is with some.
et s’il aoevre la voinne, si est li plaie trop estroite, por ceu si covient que li sainieres soit avisez en ces choses.	And if he opens the vein, the wound is too narrow, so the bleeder must be skilled in these things.
Et se li voine oevre la premiere fois, c’est boin;	And if the vein opens the first time, that is good;et s’il ne peut ovrir au premier coup de flaime, si covient que il fuige les voinne
se ceu non, si rencomence ancor un poc desoz celui leu ou sus hastanment, se li leus n’est enflez.	if not, then restart a little lower down that area or above the hospital, if the area isn't swollen.
Et se li leus est enflez, et li malaides s’espoante, se li laisse I jor ou II, et ne liier mie le bras:	And if the area is swollen and the patient is in fear, let him for a day or two, and don't bind his arm.
par aventure i venra apostemes chaus;	perhaps hot abscesses will arise;
ne n’entre ou bain, puis rencomence la sainie s’elle li plait;	don't enter the bath, then restart the bleeding if she wishes;
et se li pertuis est petis, ou li sans cort subtilment et tu doutes qu’il n’isse mie tant de sanc com tu vues, si fier en celui pertuis meisme a tout le flaime droitement;	and if the vein is small, cut it short and carefully, and you doubt that not as much blood will flow as you wish, then pierce in that vein directly;
et l’uevre un poc hastanment, ainsois que li leus soit enflez;	and work a little on the hospital, until the area is swollen;
car ceu avient maintes fois, quant li plaie est petite.	for this happens many times, when the wound is small.
Se tu vois le leu enfleit, si ne rencomencier mie la sainie, et met sus un poc de lie d’oile, car elle alige lou cors dou sanc, et est muedre en cest leu li lie que li oile;	If you see the area swollen, then don't restart the bleeding, and put on a little lamb's wool, for it lightens the body of blood, and is medicine in this place where the oil is.
et ensi aministre la lie de oile en chescune sainie que tu saines les voines, por estanchier lou cours dou sanc;	and likewise apply oil to each wound that you treat veins to stop the flow of blood;
et ceu meisme fait triaicle et bowe d’eus, quant on le met sus le leu;	and with this one does cauterize and brand, when it is placed on the area;
si subtilie li sans et s’espart quant il est trop gros.	so skillfully he splits and separates them when they are too large.
Et s’il i vient uns apostemes gros, qui avient maintes fois, meismement quant il n’est sainiez fuer que a celi fois ou li overture de la voinne est petite, si te haste, et met sus le leu esponge moillie en aigue et en seil un poc chaut, et l’estraint une houre;	And if there comes a large abscess, which happens often, especially when it is not treated before the opening of the vein is small, you should act quickly and place a sponge moistened in warm water on the area, and hold it for an hour;
et covient que tu faices ceu aprés l’issue dou sanc de la voinne, et s’il demoure au leu aprés aucuns jors aucune noiror ou verdor, si ne li nuist mie;	and you should do this after the flow of blood from the vein has stopped, and if it remains in place for several days, it will do no harm;
et se tu vues, met sus aucune chose de aloes ou de mirre remise en jus de calament, monstastre, ou semblant.	and if you see any swelling, apply a poultice of aloe or myrrh made into a paste with rosewater, or something similar.
Et maintes fois avient aposteme et aparance a la sainie de la basilique:	And many times there is an abscess and appearance at the exit of the basilic vein:
met donques ta main sus, et se tu trueves le leu mol a la compression de la main, si est celle aparance male.	so put your hand above it, and if you find the area soft to the pressure of your hand, then that appearance is bad.
Eschui donques que tu ne mettes sus aucune chose de ceu que nos avons dit, car par aventure en cort sans de l’artere;	So avoid putting anything on it of what we have said, for it may go into the artery;
mais li fai I emplaustre sec por endurcir le leu, puis le cure d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez.	but make a dry poultice to harden the area, then treat it with other treatments until it is healed.
Et trai a chescun dou sanc selonc la quantiteit de sa vertu, et de la color dou sanc.	And treat each wound according to its blood flow and the color of the blood.
Car se li sans est noir, si en laisse issir tant qu’il soit rouges;	For if the blood is black, let it out until it runs red;
et se tu lou vois gros, si lou laisse tant qu’il soit subtiliiez;	and if you see it thick, let it out until it becomes thin;
et s’il est trop chaus, si le laisse refroidier.	and if it is too hot, let it cool down.And so the blood must be let out of the basilic vein, in order to heal an abscess or wound
Et covient a celui qui est plains et fors, et ait mestier d’estraction de sanc, c’on li faice plus large plaie, et soit li flaimes larges;	And it is fitting for one who is full and swollen, and needs bloodletting, that they make him a larger wound, and let the flames be wide;
et a celui qui est foibles, fai le contraire, et le covient sainier poc et sovent, et le doit on sainier en taillant de travers, ne mie en poignant;	and for the weak, do the opposite, and one should bleed them a little often, and they must be bled by cutting across, not piercing.
et ceste maniere de sainie est sauve de decorrement de sanc et de copement de nerf, et vaut mues que li sainie dou lonc ne dou large.	and this bleeding method is safe from bloodletting and nerve damage, and it is better than the long or wide incisions.
Et a celui cui li cors faut a la sainie, covient doner pain moilliet en jus de pomes grenates;	And for the one whose body needs bleeding, give moist bread in pomegranate juice;
s’il est eschaufez, si trai dou sanc III fois ou IIII Et s’il est de froide complexion, si menjuce devant la sainie pain moilliet en sirop muzé, ou en sirop de miel aromatique avec espices, si com poivre, canelle, gingibre, et chiches, et sirop bien odorant.	If he is hot-tempered, eat some pomegranate juice three or four times before bleeding. And if of a cold temperament, eat moist bread in rosewater syrup, or in aromatic honey syrup with spices like pepper, cinnamon, ginger, and chickpeas, and well-scented syrup.
Et s’il paume a la sainie, aprés l’issue de mout de sanc, si covient qu’il hume brouet de char, et sirop odorant subtil, et use des autres choses que nos avons dit en la division ou chapistre de sincope, por l’evacuation de voinne.	And if he faints after losing a lot of blood, then he should drink a broth made from meat, and a subtle scented syrup, and use the other things we mentioned in the section on syncope, for the opening of a vein.
Et s’il vuet esventer som bras, et sainier autre fois, si covient, quant il est afoiblis par grant sainie, k’il se saine poc et poc, selonc la quantiteit de sa vertu continueement.	And if he wants to open his arm and bleed again, he should do so little by little according to the amount of his continuing strength.
Et qui vuet esventer som bras aprés la premiere sainie, et il a cors fort, si se saine .vij. houres aprés la premiere sainie, ou aprés la nuevime houre.	And those who want to open their arms after the first bleeding, and they have a strong body, should bleed .7 hours after the first bleeding, or after the ninth hour.
Et qui se vuet sainier d’autre part, si se doit sainier lou secont jor ou le tier.	And whoever wants to bleed elsewhere, they should bleed on the second or third day.
Car il a mout de sanc dedens le cors qui est ja eschaufez, et fait venir fievre;	For he has a lot of blood inside his body that is hot, which brings on fever;
si en covient traire grant quantiteit, et eslargir le pertus tant qu’il chiece em pameson;	if one must draw a great quantity, and widen the opening as much as possible.
puis que tu rewardes toutes les conditions de sainie, et met ta main sus som poulz quant il saine, que li mors ne viegne en leu de pameson, et ceu avient maintes fois, quant li sainieres est negligens;	then you examine all the conditions of healing, and put your hand over the patient's pulse when he is healing, so that death does not come to the site of the wound, and this happens many times when the surgeon is negligent.
et ne covient mie quant tu vues desliier lou bras, et faire issir sanc la seconde fois, et li pertus est clos, que tu presses forment sus;	And one must not, when you see to release the arm and make blood come out a second time, and the opening is closed, press hard upon it;
ne s’il est corbes, qu’il estende lou bras hastanment, car ce seroit malz;	nor if it is crooked that he extends the arm suddenly, for this would be bad;
mais le laisse tant qu’il saine la seconde fois;	but let him keep still until it heals a second time.
ou tu i point a la pointe dou flaime, tant que li sans qui est congelez a pertus de la voinne isse fuer, et met sus I poc de seil remis en aigue, et presse sus legierement.	Or you put the cautery to the tip of the flame, until the blood which is congealed at the opening of the vein flows out, and put on it a little salt dissolved in water, and press gently upon it.
Et se li voine est enflee, si la laisse et ne l’estreindre mie, tant que li aposteme soit apaisiez.	And if the vein is swollen, let it be and do not bind it, until the abscess is soothed.
Et se necessitez est dou traire dou sanc la seconde fois, si le saine en celui leu meisme, ou en un autre voinne, ou en l’autre bras.	And if it is necessary to draw blood a second time, let it be in the same place, or in another vein, or in the other arm.
Li voinne emmi le bras est sainie en leu de la voine dou chief por ceu qu’elle est composte.	The veins in the arms are healthy in the area of the vein in the head because it is composite.
Et li maniere de la sainie si est que li malaides boute sa main en aigue chaude, tant que li foscile soit rouges;	And the manner of healing is for the patient to place his hand in hot water until the wound turns red.
puis soit liiéz moienement, si que li voinne apere bien, puis le saine maintenant dou travers, ne mie dou large ne dou lonc;	then let it be left to heal slowly, so that the vein appears well, then heal it now from the inside, not from the wide or long end.
et soit li pertus larges, et soit sainiez bien pres de la jointe de la main, et se sans n’en puet issir, si remet la main en aigue chaude, et laisse corre lou sanc en l’aigue, tant que tu en aies assez;	and let the hole be wide, and let it be healed near the joint of the hand, and if blood cannot issue from it, then put the hand back in hot water, and let the blood flow into the water until you have enough.
et se c’est en esteit, si ne rebouter mie la main en aigue chaude, car on l’i met plus en yver que en esteit;	and if it is swollen, do not put the hand back in hot water, because it is put in more during winter than when swollen.
et li sainie de ceste voine est plus sauve de toutes autres voinnes, qu’il n’i a ne artere ne nerf.	and the healing of this vein is safer than all other veins, that there is no artery or nerve in it.
Li sainie de la salvatele de la main destre si vaut a toutes les maladies dou foie, et c’est li maniere:	The healing of the right hand's little finger is useful for all diseases of the liver, and here is how:
estrain la main, et boute en aigue chaude, tant que li voinne soit enflee, si c’on la voie;	Hold the hand steady, and pour in hot water until the vein swells, as one can see it.
et se la saine de travers, et se tu la copes dou tout en tout, si ne grieve rien;	and if the vein is healthy but crossing it, and you press on it from all sides, it will not hurt at all;
et n’aler mie trop em parfont, car li nerf sont desoz toz desnuez de char, et puis remet la main en aigue chaude, se li sans est congelez en la plaie, et n’en puet issir.	and do not go too deep because the nerves are completely stripped of flesh underneath; then put the hand back in hot water if the blood has congealed in the wound and it cannot come out.
Et quant tu avras trait dou sanc tant com mestier t’est, si met sus la voinne oile et seil por souder hastanment, et ensi fai de chescun rain.	And when you have finished treating the blood as necessary, put oil and silk on the vein to seal it temporarily, and do the same for each vein.
Li sainie de li en la main senestre si vaut a la maladie de la mice, et fai tout ausi com je t’ai dit devers destre.	The bleeding in the left hand is beneficial for the disease of the mouse, and do everything as I have told you about the right.
Li sainie de la sophene si vaut a toutes les maladies que sont desoz le cors, si com maladies de la marris, et retenement de flors, et maladie des rains, et des cuixes et des jambes ancienes, et semblans maladies.	The salve of the soporific plant is good for all diseases beneath the body, such as diseases of the brain, and retention of fluids, and diseases of the kidneys, and of the hips and legs, and similar diseases.
Et li qualitez de sa sainie si est que li malaides boute som piet en aigue chaude, et frote sus la voinne tant qu’elle pere, et lie desus la jointure dou piet;	And the quality of this treatment is that the patient should put his foot in hot water and rub the vein until it breaks, and then press on the joint of the foot;
et li voinne si est a la cheville, et par desus lou piet en vont mout de rains;	and if the vein is at the ankle, and going up the foot there are many veins;
saine la donques ou plus large rain, ou a la cheville, que mues vaut.	then treat the largest vein, either at the ankle or on the foot, whichever is easier to access.
Et se tu la saines sus lou piet, si te warde des ners qui sont desoz, et la saine de traver ausi com en copant;	And if you heal it on the foot, then guard against the nerves that are underneath, and heal it across as well as up and down.
et soit li flaimes anesil.	Let the flames be anesthetized.
Et se li sans n’en puet issir, si remet lou piet en l’aigue, et laisse bien vuidier la voine.	And if the blood cannot flow out, then immerse the foot in water and let the vein drain well.
Et se li sainieres faut la premiere fois, si rencomence la seconde au desus un poc, car li leus est salz;	And if the healing doesn't work the first time, then try again a second time from above a little bit, because the place is salty.
ne ne douter de nerf, si com nos avons dit, et ensi fai de la sophene de l’autre piet igalment.	Do not doubt the nerve, as we have said, and similarly do the same for the other foot equally.
Li leus de la voinne sciatique est a la cheville de fuer, et sa sainie vaut a la dolor de la hainche, quant c’est por sanc chaut.	The location of the sciatic vein is at the ankle, and its pulsation relates to the pain in the hip when there is hot blood.
Et li qualitez de sa sainie si est que li malaides entre ou bain, et estraigne desus la cheville IIII dois en tordant, car autrement n’apert li voinne;	And the nature of its healing is that the patient enters into the bath, and twists above the ankle three times in twisting, for otherwise the vein will not open;
et s’elle apert, si le saine en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et en traversant;	and if it opens, then heal it in all ways that you can, and by crossing over;
et vaut mues que tu la copes, car li leus est saus, et elle est mout reponue a mains homes.	and it is better that you cup her, for the place is safe, and she is very susceptible to many people.
Et se tu ne la trueves, si saine aucun rain de li qui apert ou dos dou piet, et vers lou petit doi, et te warde des ners;	And if you do not believe me, heal a vein on his back or front towards the small intestine, and be careful of the nerves.
et fai tant corre dou sanc que tu vues, et puis deslie lou lien, et met sus coton et l’estraint;	and let blood flow until you see it, then loosen the ligature and put cotton on it and compress it.
ele est maintenant sanee.	It is now healed.
des sainies de ventouse	from cupping marks
Ventouses sont fait de cornes, ou d’arain, ou de voirre;	Cupping glasses are made from horns, or brass, or glass;
et ventosation si est faite selonc II manieres:	and cupping is done in two ways:
ou par ferir et atraire sanc, ou sens ferir.	either by cutting and drawing blood, or without cutting.
Et ceste ventosation qui est sens ferir si est selonc II manieres:	And this cupping without cutting is done in two ways:l’une est par le feu et l’autra par la main.
ou elle est a tout feu, ou sens feu;	one is with fire and the other without fire;
et ventosation qui est faite par ferir et par estraction de sanc si est faite en XIIII leus dou cors, de coi li uns est tout en som le chief;	and cupping which is done by cutting and drawing blood is done in 14 places on the body, of which one is on the head;
et li autres est emmi le col;	and the others are in the neck;
et II autres en II costeis dou col;	and two more on either side of the neck;
et li ventouse desoz lou menton;	and a cupping glass under the chin;
