et li ventouse des II espaules;	and a cupping glass on both shoulders;
et li ventouse sus les crupies;	and a cupping glass above the hips;
et les ventouses emmi les II bras;	and the cupping glasses in between the two arms;
et les ventouses des II jambes;	and the cupping glasses on both legs;
et les ventouses des II chevilles;	and the cupping glasses at the ankles;
et li ventosation ne trait point de sanc, fuer que des menues voinnes que sont esparses en la char, et por ceu n’en afoiblist om mie, si com on fait de sainie de voinne;	and bloodletting does not treat blood, unless it is from small veins that are scattered throughout the body, and because of this it does not weaken at all, as is done with bloodletting;
et ne covient mie qu’elle soit aministree, ne a tout feu ne sens feu, en aucune maladie qui vient de repletion, tant que toz li cors soit vuidiez.	and it should not be administered, nor with all heat or without heat, in any disease that comes from fullness, until the whole body is emptied.
Et se par necessiteit de maladies covient ventoser, ou por acostumances, si l’amenistrons chescune houre en l’encomencement dou mois, ou en la fin, et emmi et en chescun tens;	And if, due to necessity or habit, one must bloodlet, then we should do so every hour at the beginning and end of the month, and in between and at all times;
car il i a de telz qui, quant il ont mestier de ventoser, si ont pesant chief;	for there are some who, when they need to belch, have a heavy head;
et si a telz qui truevent repletion et roujor en lor faice, et en lor chief, et au col, et tenebrour as eulz;	and some who experience bloating and redness in their face, head, and neck, and darkness in their eyes;
et telz qui truevent une goute de sanc en lor bouche, et ont enflee la lengue, et raichent sanc;	and some who spit up a drop of blood in their mouth, and have swollen tongues, and bleed;
et si i a de telz qui songent, et voient par nut sanc et navrez et mors et semblans choses.	and there are those who dream, and see through blood and pain and death and similar things.
Et quant nos voions ces signes, et meismement quant c’est emmi lou mois, nos lou commandons a ventoser aprés .iij. houres dou jor.	And when we see these signs, especially if it is during the month, we command them to fast after the third hour of the day.
Li sainie de la muze si aide a la grieteit dou chief … que vient as eulz, et ne covient mie que ce soit aprés l’evacuation de tout lou cors;	The bleeding from the nose helps with headaches ... that comes to the eyes, and should not happen after evacuating the whole body;
et ceste ventosation si est en leu de la sainie de la cephalique, et ne covient mie que cil qui est de froide complexion en use, ou qui ait chatharre, car ce lor fait mout grant nuisement;	and this venting is in the place of bleeding from the head, and should not be used by those who are of a cold complexion, or who have catarrh, for it does them great harm;et si i a de telz qui truevent une goute de sanc en lor bouche, et ont enflee la lengue, et raichent sanc;
et por ceu ne covient mie que li veillart en usent, ne qui ont ou chief froides maladies.	and for this reason the elderly should not use it, nor those with serious illnesses.
Et cil qui s’en saine sovent, si devient oblious, et por ce covient mettre la ventouse un poc plus aval par la doutance d’obliance.	And those who heal themselves frequently, become oblate, and because of this, one should place the leech lower down for fear of oblate.
Li ventosation emmi le col est en leu de la sainie dou chief et de la basilique, et por ceu vaut elle a l’estrecement dou pis, et a fendure de la chenal dou pormon, et a toust, et a repletion;	The wind-treatment on the neck is located where the sinus of the head and the basilic vein are, and for this reason it is good for constriction of the feet, and fissures in the canal of the lungs, and for puffiness and distension;
et la covient poc bouter, car s’elle tient trop fermement, si enjanre obliance ou stomac et ou cuer.	and one should not push it too hard, because if it is held too tightly, it injures the oesophagus or stomach and heart.
Li ventosations as II costelz dou col si vaut as dolors dou chief, et obtalmie et emigrainne, et a l’estranglement, et a la dolor as racines des dens, et est en leu de la sainie de la basilique;	The wind-treatments at the side of the neck are good for headaches, and eye pain and migraine, and strangulation, and toothache, and are located where the sinus of the basilic vein is;
et covient que tu comandes au sainor qu’il espresse sa main au mettre, qu’il ne cope l’artere, et ne veigne decorremens de sanc.	and you should instruct the patient to express his hand when putting it on so that he does not compress the artery and cause blood to flow.
Li ventosations desoz lou menton si vaut a maladie de bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et semblans maladies qui sont en la bouche;	The venting below the chin is good for mouth diseases, and gum decay, and similar illnesses that are in the mouth;
et est en leu des sainies des II levres.	and is where there are sores on the two lips.
Li ventosations des espaules vaut a maladie que vient de chalor et de remplissement.	The windings on the shoulders are good for diseases that come from heat and fullness.
Li ventosations des coutes si vaut autant com des III voinnes dou bras, car elle atrait sanc de ces grosses voinnes;	The venting of the armpits is just as good as three veins in the arm, because it draws blood from these large veins;
et comande au sainor qu’il ne fiere mie trop em parfont, car li leus est nus de char, et sait desoz ners et arteres.	Instruct the bloodletter to not cut too deeply, because the area is bare of flesh and contains nerves and arteries underneath;
Li ventouse qui est sus la croupe si vaut as emoroydes dou fondement, et as maladies desoz, et covient que li ventouse soit grans, et soit d’arain, qu’elle a mestier de bien traire;	The cupping glass placed on the buttocks is good for hemorrhoids in the anus, and for illnesses underneath, and it should be a large cupping glass made of iron, which needs to be well applied;
et par aventure, s’elle estoit subtilz, si briseroit;	And if they are thin, they will break;Li ventosations desoz les cotés si vaut aux maladies de l’estomach et de la mesentere, et a les maux dou fond
et i fai grans plaies.	and cause great wounds.
Les ventouses des jambes si sainent apertement, car elles atraient sanc de tout le cors, et valent as dolors ancienes des rains, et de la marris, et de la vessie, et ramoinnent les flors;	Leg cupping heals quickly and openly, because it draws blood from the entire body, and is effective for old pains in the kidneys, and the bladder, and restores the flow;
et sont en leu des II sophenes, et des II chevilles, et toutevoie elles afoiblissent lou cors aprés lonc us, et font venir paumison em plusors dispositions.	They are located at the two ankles and knees, and they weaken the entire body after long use, and bring on paralysis in many cases.
Li maniere de mettre la ventouse si est que tu la mettes premier vuide, et succe tempreement, et la met hastanment, et remue igalment, et ne cesser de ceu faire, tant que tu voies lou leu rouge et enfleit, et apere li roujor dou sanc;	The way to apply the cupping is to first place it empty, and suck gently, and then press firmly, and move evenly, and not cease doing this until you see the area red and swollen, and the blood flows.
puis fier, et remet les ventouses, et pren warde en la disposition des cors, car il i a telz qui ont tanre char, et clers porez:	Then wait, and replace the cupping, and take heed of the condition of the body, for there are some who have such thin skin, and clear pores:
si covient ferir une fois soulement, et covient faire larges plaies, et un poc parfondes;	it is necessary to cut only once, and it must be a wide wound, and not too deep.li dolors de la piere se traittent as l’autrier fu dit, si avient plusors fois que li membres son defformez
et suce legierement.	and suck gently.
Et se li sans est gros, si couvient ferir II fois:	And if the vein is thick, it is necessary to pierce twice:
la premiere fois por subtiliier la voie dou sanc gros.	the first time to make the way for the thick blood.
Et se li sans est tres espés, si covient ferir la tierce fois;	And if the vein is very thick, it must be pierced a third time;
et quant nos volons traire dou sanc poc et poc, si nos soffist soulement une fois.	and when we want to draw blood little by little, we only need to pierce once.
Et se nos volons mout de sanc, si rencomensons sovent;	And if we want a lot of blood, we should do it frequently;
et se li sans est espés, si fier em parfont, et li termines si est que li keurs soit perciez soudement, et couvient a celui qui a gros cuir et dur, et qui ont estrois porelz, que tu oignes les leus des ventouses d’oile aperitif et dissolutif:	and if the vein is thick, pierce it deeply, and let the ends be such that the skin is pierced suddenly, and it is necessary to anoint the places of the cupping-glasses with an opening and dissolving oil for those who have tough and hard skin, and who have narrow pores:
se c’est en esteit, d’oile violet, ou d’oile d’amandres douces, ou d’oile de semence de cucurbite;	if it is on the head, use violet oil, or sweet almond oil, or squash seed oil;
et se c’est en yveir, d’oile de cresson, ou de lis, ou de camomille, ou autre semblant.	and if it is on an eye, use oil of watercress, or lily, or chamomile, or something similar.
Et se li superfluitez est grosse et froide, si pren oile amaratin, ou de balsamite, ou oile d’anet, et les semblans.	And if the excess is thick and cold, take oil of amarant, or of balsam, or dill oil, and the like.
Et se cil cui on saine a tendre char et larges porelz, se n’i covient mettre point d’oile, mais le covient laver aprés la ventosation d’aigue rose, ou d’aigue froide, ou d’aigue de morelle, ou d’aigue de cucurbite, ou d’aigue de porcelainne, ou autre semblant.	And if the one we heal has tender flesh and wide pores, no oil should be applied, but it must be washed after cupping with rosewater, or cold water, or mulberry water, or pumpkin water, or porcelain water, or similar.
Et cil qui a mout de moistor, si se leve d’aisil, ou d’aigue de mirte, et de sumac, et de semblans choses.	And those who have a lot of moisture, if they rise from parsley, or myrtle water, and sumac, and similar things.
Et cil qui ont grosses superfluitez se levent de vin viel, ou d’aigue de seuc, ou de decoction d’anet ou de camomile, ou d’autres semblans;	And those with large growths are cured by old wine, or dried water, or a potion of fennel or chamomile, or similar things;
et ne se covient mie sainier de ventouse devant le bain ne em bain, mais aprés lou bain une houre ou II;	and it is not good to bleed with a cupping glass before the bath or in the bath, but an hour or two after the bath;
et ne dorme mie aprés la ventosacion, et covient k’il se warse, quant il se doit ventoser et quant il est ventosez.	and he should not sleep after cupping, and it is necessary that he should stay awake when he is being bled and after he has been bled.
Et warde se cil qui se saine est coleriques, et se li sans est trop agus et enflamez;	And watch if the person being bled is choleric, and if the blood is too thin and inflamed;
si covient qu’il preigne choses froides, si com pomes grenates et endives et laitues a l’aisil, et semblans choses;	if he should eat cool things, such as pomegranates, endive, lettuce with garlic, and similar things;
et menjuce pucins, et char de chastron, et viandes moistes.	and eat little, and charcoal from a brazier, and moist meat.
Et cil qui a froide complexion, si preigne syrop de miel, et vin odorant moien, qui est entre viel et noveil, et menjuce poc, et menjuce pucins et petis oiselz et pijons;	And those of a cold complexion should drink syrup of honey and moderate-aged fragrant wine, and eat little, and charcoal from a brazier, and moist meat;
et lou jor qu’il se ventousera, si doit plus boivre que mengier;	and on the day that he vomits, he should drink more than he eats;
et covient doner a aucuns homes aucune fois triaicle ou muscate devant la ventosacion, ou aprés, por conforter les membres principalz;	and it is necessary to give some men teliakle or musk before or after vomiting, to comfort the principal members;
et soit subtiliiez li sans, mais il ne covient mie que cil qui sont chaut le boivent.	and dilute the wine, but those who are hot-tempered should not drink it.
Les ventouses que sont mises sens ferir sont celles que sont mises sus lou foie, et sus la mice, et podagre, et sus lou ventre et la boude et les rains et la hainche, car cil membre ne soffrent mie ferir sus oulz, et ne le fait on fuer que por atraire sanc de membre em membre, si com nos mettons sus les mameles quant li neis sainne;	The leeches that are placed without bleeding are those placed on the liver, and on the mouse, and podagra, and on the belly and the throat and the rains and the hip, because these members do not bear bleeding on their own, and it is only done to draw blood from one member to another, as we put them on breasts when nipples are sore.
por oster la viscositeit qui est au membre, si com nos metons ventouses sus le ventre et sus la boude por amenuisier le membre;	to reduce the viscosity in the limb, as we place cupping glasses on the belly and buttocks to make the limb smaller
et oste la dolor, quant il i a opilation ou piere, si oste par sa vertu atractive par aventure l’opilation, ou desaert la piere de son leu;	and removes pain; when there is obstruction or stone, it removes the obstruction by its attractive power, or drives out the stone from its place;
et ensi fait ele quant on le met sus lou foie et sus la mice quant il i a ventositeit retenue, et ces ventouses sont aministrees vuides por sucier tant soulement;	and it does the same when placed on the liver and on the abdomen when there is retained wind; these cupping glasses are administered empty in order to suck only slightly;
et aucune fois sont aministrees ensamble feu, et aucunes fois plainnes d’aigue tede, si com em maladies dou pleuresin, et en tel maniere c’on emplisse la ventouse d’aigue chaude soule, ou d’aigue ou il ait cuit herbes covenaubles a ceu.	and sometimes they are administered with fire, and sometimes filled with warm water, as in diseases of the pleurisy; and in such a way one fills the cupping glass with warm water, or water in which suitable herbs have been boiled.
Li forme de la ventouse aministré a feu si est ci:	The form of the fire cupping is as follows:
Et ait II dois de large et demi palme de parfont, et ait ou costeit entor lou mileu I petit pertus, ausi com por bouter une aguille, et soit d’arain, souef devant si qu’ele ne blece lou malaide au mettre sus lou membre;	And it has a diameter of two digits and a half palm in depth, and on the side around the middle there is a small hole, as large as to pass a needle, and it is made of brass, smooth in front so that it does not hurt the patient when placed on the limb;
et ait em mileu une verge de travers d’arain ou de fer, por mettre une chandoile emprise, et en soient et grans et petites selonc les maladies et l’eaige de ces qui les prenent;	and has in the middle a crossbar of iron or steel, to hold a candle, and they are both large and small according to the illnesses and age of those who take them;
car les ventouses des enfans sont autres que des vielz, et des maigres que des gras.	for the cupping glasses of children are different from those of the elderly, and of the thin from the fat.
Et doit on ensi mettre ceste ventouse sus lou membre:	And one must thus place this cupping glass upon the limb:
empren la chandoile de cire ou I linement, et le met emmi la ventouse au traver de la verge qui est emmi la ventouse, si que li clartez soit au fons de la ventouse qu’elle ne brule le malaide;	take the candle of wax or tallow, and place it inside the cupping glass at the crossbar in the middle of the cupping glass, so that the flame is at the bottom of the cupping glass and does not burn the patient;
et puis la met sus lou membre, et tes dois soit sus lou pertus que nos avons dit, si que quant on vuet, si en va li vapor, et oste on la ventouse;	and then place it upon the limb, and your fingers must be over the hole that we have described, so that when one wishes, the vapors go out, and one removes the cupping glass;
et emprent on le linement si com devant, et le rencomence sovent, se tu as mestier.	and they take the tallow as before, and repeat it often if necessary.
En la ventouse donques qui est aministree em maladie de pleuresin, a tout aigue, n’a point de verge ne de pertus, et n’est amenistree fuer que quant ele est plaine d’aigue, et est mise sus lou membre tant soulement;	In the cupping glass therefore which is administered for disease of pleurisy, with all acute illnesses, has no tube or opening, and is not removed until it is full of fluid, and is placed on the limb only by itself.
et c’est li forme:	and this is its form:
Sansues ne sont amenistrees fuer que en membres ou on ne puet mettre ventouses por lour petitece, si com levres et gencives, et semblans leus;	Leeches are not removed until in members where one cannot place cupping glasses due to their smallness, such as lips and gums, and similar places;
et en leus desnuez de char, si com doi ou neis, et autres semblans;	and in bare flesh, such as breast or nose, and others similar;
et li qualitez de l’user si est que quant tu trueves sansues que sont en aigues douces nettes sens porreture, si les pren;	and the quality of its use is such that when you find leeches that are in clean, sweet water without mud, then take them;
et les met une nut en aigue douce, tant qu’elles soient famillouses, et n’aient rien en ventres;	and put one into clean, sweet water, until they become familiar and have nothing in their bellies;
et puis soit sainiez de voinne et de ventouse, puis frote le membre tant k’il soit rouges, et met sus les sansues;	and then cleanse with a vein opening and cupping, then rub the limb until it is red, and put on the leeches;
et quant elles seront plainnes, et cherront, se c’est leu ou on puisse mettre ventouse, se li met, car ce vaut mout aprés.	and when they are flat and swelling, if it is possible to put a cupping glass on them, then one should do so, for this is much better.
Se ceu non, si leve le leu d’aisil, et puis d’aigue, mout bien, et puis l’espreint;	If not, then raise the area with a pillow, and then with water, very well, and then squeeze it out.
et se li leus saine trop aprés lou cors des sansues, si moille I drapel de lin en aigue froide, et met sus, tant que li sans soit estenchiés;	and if the bite is too far from the body of the snake, then wet a linen cloth in cold water and place it over the bite until the swelling goes down;
et se li sans est multipliez, si met sus vitriole broié, ou gales, et semblans choses, tant qu’il soit estenchiez;	and if there are many bites, then apply ground vitriol or gall, and similar things, until the swelling goes down;
ou tu met sor le leu moitiez de feves pelees, et les laisse tant qu’elles s’aerdent au leu, si estanchera maintenant;	or you can place half a handful of peeled peas over the bite and leave them until they warm the area, which will stop the bleeding immediately;
et se tu en as de plus mestier, si pren autres sansues.	and if you need more, then catch other snakes.
Et se les sansues ne se vuellent prendre, si frote le leu de sanc fres, ou tu i fiche une aguille tant que li sans en isse, et puis les met sus, et tantost com elles sentent lou sanc, si s’aerdent;	And if the snakes do not want to be caught, then rub the bite with fresh blood or stab it with a needle so that the snake's venom comes out, and then place them over the bite, and as soon as they smell the blood, they will warm up.
et quant tu vues qu’elles chieent, si poudre sus un poc d’aloen et de seil broiet, ou de cendre, si cherront maintenant.	and when you see them defecating, then powder on a little aloe and ash, or charcoal, they will stop immediately.
Ci comence li livre des brisures	Here begins the book of fractures.
Cist chapistres est maintes fois necessaires en l’art de medicine, et est restorement de brisure et de desaluement.	This chapter is often necessary in the art of medicine, and it is a remedy for fractures and dislocations.
Saichiez, chier fil, que li fol mire se gietent de cest chapistre, qu’il ne virent onques nul des anciens livres, ne lettre n’en lurent;	Know, dear reader, that the fools mock this chapter, which they have never seen in any ancient book nor read any letter of it;
et por ceste cause est estraingie li science en nostre terre, car je n’en trovai onques nul boin;	and for this reason knowledge is strange in our land, for I have never found any good ones;
et n’en sai nient, fuer que par la science des anciens livres, ou j’ai tant estudiiet que je en ai traite la science, et par experiment, et par l’acostumance de ma vie;	and I know nothing about it except through the knowledge of ancient books, from which I have studied so much that I have attained to its science, and through experimentation, and through the habit of my life;
et je vos ai jai descrit en cest chapistre ceu qui est contenut, et l’ai abregié en la fin, et ai mostreit clerement les formes des estrumens que sont amenistrez, si com j’ai fait en ces II chapistres ci devant.	and I have described to you in this chapter what is contained therein, and abbreviated at the end, and clearly shown the forms of the instruments that are used, just as I have done in these two chapters above.
Il covient donques que nos disons ou prologue de cest livre les sommes de la parole et les chapistres ou li saiges met son entendement, et demore sus la verteit, si que cil qui sont esproveit saichent et aprenent cest art noble, et l’aprenent a autrui.	Therefore, we should say in the prologue of this book the sums of the matter and the chapters in which the sage places his understanding, and dwells upon their truth, so that those who have experience know and learn this noble art, and teach it to others.
Je dis que quant brisure ou dislocation ou torsions ou quasseure vient a aucun, si covient que tu te hastes de sainier lou malaide d’une part et d’autre, s’aucune chose ne lou te tot, si com foiblece de cors, ou enfes, ou viellars;	I say that when a fracture or dislocation or twisting or bruising befalls someone, you must hurry to heal the patient from one side and the other, if any part does not heal him completely, as in weakness of the body, or children, or the elderly.
ou se li tens n’est tres chaus, ou trop frois;	or if the weather is very hot, or too cold;
et menjuce cholz frois, c’est a savoir froides joutes, et char d’oiseil et de chevril, et ne boive point de vin, ne menjuce nules grasses chars, et ne s’emplisse mie trop de viandes qui remplissent les voinnes de sanc, tant que tu n’aies doute d’aposteme chaut, ne d’espandement de matiere au membre;	and eat cold foods, namely cold meats and meat from young animals, and drink no wine, nor eat any fatty foods, and do not eat too much meat that fills the veins with blood, until you have reason to suspect a hot abscess or inflammation in the limb;
si reviegne li malaides a som premerain governement k’il a useit.	if the illness returns under its first treatment.
Et quant li os brisiés comence a restourer, si covient que on norrisse le malaide de viandes que font gros norrissement, ou il ait viscositeit, si com froment cuit en aigue, et ris, et testes, et piez, et pance de vaiche, et oefz, et poissons fres, et gros vin, et semblans chose.	When the broken bone begins to heal, the patient should be nourished with foods that promote swelling or have viscosity, such as cooked wheat in water, rice, testicles, pigs' feet, pig's belly, eggs, fresh fish, and full-bodied wine, and similar things.
Car a teil norrissement se reprent mues et plus tost li brisure.	Because with such nourishing the swelling will subside and the break will heal more quickly.
Et saichiez que li os brisiez des vielz et des decrepites ne se pueent mie bien reprendre ne souder selonc lor nature por la sechor des membres, ne cil ausi qui sont trop tendre, si com os de petis enfans;	And know that broken bones of the old and the weak cannot heal well or knit together according to their nature due to the dryness of the limbs, nor those that are too tender, such as the bones of small children;
mais n’a cure, ramoinne sus l’os brisiet I gros tenrons qui s’aert et joint le membre ensamble, tant qu’il enforce si com il fut devant;	but have no concern, reset on the broken bone The thick tendons that pierce and join the limb together, so that it enforces as it was before;
et ne li tot point de son oevre, et por ceu le covient norrir de grosses viandes, si com nos avons dit.	and do not stop there, but also tend to the surrounding broken bones, and for this one needs to feed thick meats as we have said.
Et saiches que les briseures sont diverses em maintes manieres.	And you should know that fractures are diverse in many ways.
Car li brisure dou chief est autre que li brisure dou pis, ou de la jambe, et je vos dirai en cest chapistre toutes manieres de brisure.	For the fracture of the head is different than the fracture of the foot, or of the leg; and in this chapter I will tell you about all types of fractures.
Car il i a brisure que vait a arvol, et autre en aguisant, si com li taille d’une penne por escrire.	For there is a fracture that goes to the bone, and another that is only skin deep, like the cut of a quill pen for writing.
Et si a brisure avec plaie, et brisure a tout une petite fendure.	And there is a fracture with a wound, and a fracture that is just a small crack.
Et a chescune maniere ait son engien, et son estrument propre en la restauration, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient en son leu;	And in each manner has its own technique, and a unique instrument for restoration, according to the memory that comes to mind;
et est conue li brisure de l’os par ceu que li leus est tors, et apert bien par defuer, et sone au presseir de la main;	and one can tell if the bone is broken by how it feels twisted, and clearly appears deformed when pressed with the hand;
et quant il n’i a tortuositeit ne son au tochier, et li malaides ne sent mie grant dolor, se n’i a point de brisure;	and when there is no twisting or deformity to touch, and the patient does not feel great pain, then there is no break;
mais il puet bien avoir tortuositeit, ou fendure, ou petite brisure.	but it can still have twisting, or fracturing, or a minor break.
Si ne covient mie que tu lou mueves a la main, mais met sus medicines que vienent ci aprés, et puis l’estraint maintenant subtilment.	It is not advisable to move it by hand, but apply remedies that come later, and then hold it firmly but gently now.
Et saiches que li brisure que vait en arvol, et sont les II parties desjointes, il les covient maintenant mettre a point igalment, ainsois que apostemes chaus i viegne;	And know that breaks that occur in the arm, where the two parts are separated, they must now be put back into place evenly so that abscesses will heal;
et se apostemes chaulz i vient, si lou laisse aucun jor, tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez;	and if hot abscesses come, then let them remain for a day, until the abscesses are soothed;
puis le met igal au mues que tu pues legierement et saigement, et saiches que li restauration de li est plus legiere que li restaurations de celi ou il ait pieces;	then set it even with the others as quickly and smoothly as you can, knowing that the restoration of this one is easier than the restoration of those that have pieces;
puis l’estraint, si com il covient ci aprés.	then stretch it, as appropriate afterwards.
Et se en l’os a piéces brisies, si l’estent de II pars, se c’est mains ou piet, ou a ta main se c’est uns petis membres, ou a II cordes, ou a une corde et a ta main;	And if there are broken pieces of bone, if it is in two parts, whether it is an arm or a leg, or to the hand if it is a small member, or to two cords, or to one cord and to the hand;
et met le membre selonc sa figure natureil, si que quant les parties dou membre brisiet sont desevrees, si ramoinne par toz engiens les additions en lor leus au mues que tu pues, et garde que par ton ovraige ne viegne au malaide lesion ne doulor;	and set the member according to its natural shape, so that when the broken parts of the member are brought together, you bring them by all means into their places as smoothly as you can, and be careful that your action does not cause injury or pain to the patient;
et ajoste bien les II chiés des os selonc les millors formes.	and adjust the two heads of the bone according to the best forms.
Et le sent bien a la main s’il te semble k’il ne soit mie bien:	And feel it with your hand if it seems to you that it is not well:
si la dresce bellement, et ne l’estraindre mie trop, ne presser si com font cil qui i font venir par lor ovraige aposteme chaut et contraction au membre, si com nos avons veut maintes fois.	if you set it well, and do not pull too hard, nor press as those who cause hot abscesses and contractions in the limb by their work, as we have seen many times.
Et quant li membres est a point, si chastie bien lou malaide qu’il ne lou mueve, ne en veillant ne en dormant, ne en tornant, ne en autre maniere;	And when the limb is healed, take care that the patient does not move it, whether waking or sleeping, turning or in any other way;
et warde bien que li membres soit si asseurez qu’il ne sente nule dolor.	and be sure that the limb is so secure that he feels no pain.Et s’il y a grant dolor, et ne peut demorer en tel estat, si le covient esprouver par autre maniere
Car quant il sent nulle dolor, si n’est mie a point, et le covient mettre en teil disposition qu’il ne sent nule dolor;	For when he feels no pain, then it is not yet healed, and you should put him in such a position that he feels no pain;Et s’il y a grant dolor, et ne peut demorer en tel estat, si le covient esprouver par autre maniere.
et te garde k’il soit mis droitement, que tortuositez n’i veigne quant il iert restorez;	and make sure it is put back correctly so that no crookedness comes to it when it is restored.
et li qualitez dou membre brisiet est selonc ceu que je te dis.	and the qualities of the broken member are according to what I tell you.
Saiches que li membre brisiet sont divers em petitece et en grandor et en forme.	Know that broken limbs vary in size, shape, and appearance.
Car il i a petis membres, si com brais et dois et semblans:	For there are small members like arms and fingers and similar things:
si covient envoloupeir drapelz de lin molz et subtilz;	then one should wrap them in soft and delicate linen;
et cil qui sont gros, si com cuixe et jambe:	and those that are large, like thighs and legs;
si covient envoloupeir d’un liien large et dur, car li larges liiens embraice tout le grant membre, et l’estraint de toutes pars igalment, si qu’il n’i a nule taiche;	then one should wrap them in a wide and firm bandage, for the wide bandages embrace the whole large member and constrict it evenly all around so that no crookedness remains;
puis lie entor estoupes legieres, III tours ou IIII selonc lou membre, et estraint ta main un poc a tout le liien, puis vai au desus de la brisure et l’estraint moins, que la brisure puis esloigne un poc la brisure;	then tie around it with light sponges, 3 or 4 times depending on the member, and tighten your hand all around the bandage, then go above the dislocation and tighten less so that the dislocation is pushed out a little;
et mollifie lou liien poc et poc, tant que tu preignes grant partie dou leu sain, puis repren I autre liien, et torne entor derechief sus lou leu brisiet;	and soften the ligament little by little, until you grip a large part of the healthy tissue, then take another ligament, and return around the broken area;
puis revai a la partie desoz de la brisure, et l’estraint moienement, ne mie trop fort ne trop molement, si com nos avons dit en la premiere lieure desus;	then go to the part underneath the break, and grip gently, not too hard or too softly, as we have said in the first hour above;
puis met entre les liiens estoupes de lin ou drapelz, tant qu’il soit toz igalz, puis lie tout par desus I bendeil, et puis met tes esteles bien faites sus, s’il n’i a aposteme ou enfleure.	then place between the ligaments, stuffing with linen or cloth until it is all even, then tie it all together above with a bandage, and then place your splints well-fitted above, if there is no abscess or swelling.
Et s’il i a enfleure ou aposteme, si met sus chose apaisant aposteme chaut, et qui oste l’enfleure, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors;	And if there is swelling or an abscess, then place something hot above to reduce the swelling, and leave it thus for a few days;
puis estrain sus tes esteles, et soient de moitiet d’une large cainne rese saigement, ou de fust dont on fait les clives, ou de rains de palme, et soient selonc ceste figure:	then grip above your splints, and let them be of a mid-sized cane split lengthwise, or of wood used for making oars, or of palm branches, and let them be shaped thus:
mais il covient que li estele que om met sus la brisure soit un poc plus grosse et plus large que les autres;	but it is necessary for the star that one puts on the break to be a little bigger and wider than the others;
et soit ausi longe com il covient au membre de petitece ou de grandor;	and also as long as it is convenient for the limb, small or large;
puis estraint sus les esteles ausi com tu as fait a la premiere lieure, puis lie desus un fil avenanment, si com en la premiere lieure sus la briseure;	then bind on the stars as you did at first, then tie a thread properly, just as in the first instance of the dislocation;
plus estroit est ensus, adés moins;	the tighter it is, the better; less so, afterwards;
et covient que li fil soient moien, ne trop gros ne trop menus, et soient de lin mol;	and the thread should be medium thickness, not too thick nor too thin, and made of soft flax;
car se li fil sont gros, si com j’ai veut des oevres des folz qui font lor lieures des cordes de linement tort, et c’est grant error, car li lieure ne puet estre igal s’il est trop subtilz, et ne covient mie qu’il ait entre chescune estele moins dou doi d’espaice.	because if the thread is thick, as I have seen foolish people make their ligatures with twisted cords, and that is a great error, for the ligature cannot be even if it is too thin, and there should not be less than two threads between each star.
Et se li malaides est navrez par les chiés des esteles aprés l’estrignement en leus sains, si met desoz elles estoupes de lin, ou lainne charpie, si qu’il ne se blece.	And if the patient is nervous because of the stars after the pressing in their healthy areas, then put under them flaxen lint or linen rags so that it does not hurt.
Quant li plaie est avec la briseure, et li keurs est rompus, je en dirai la cure ci aprés.	When the wound is accompanied by a fracture, and the bone is broken, I will describe the treatment below.
Et saiches qu’il ne covient mie estraindre d’esteles toz les membres brisiez le premier jor.	And you should know that it is not advisable to manipulate all broken bones on the first day.
Car quant li membres est grans, se n’i covient mie mettre esteles fuer que aprés V jors ou VII, ou plus selonc ta seurteit d’aposteme chaut sorvenant;	For when the member is swollen, it is not advisable to apply a poultice for more than five or seven days, or longer depending on the heat of the abscess.
et vez ci la maniere des emplaustres anciiens por restorer brisure, dislocation, et torsion:	And now here is the manner of ancient poultices to restore fractures, dislocations, and twists:
et est que tu pren de la farine que se tient as parois dou molin, et la confis avec abun d’uef, et met ceste confection, ne trop clere ne trop espesse, et en use, et c’est li commune maniere de l’emplaustre restorant la brisure a plusors dispositions, et meismement as femmes et as petis enfans, car il n’est mie ne trop chas ne trop frois.	And you should take flour from the walls of the mill and mix it with plenty of egg, and apply this mixture, neither too thin nor too thick, and use it. This is the common manner of the poultice that restores fractures in various conditions, especially in women and small children, because it is not too hot or too cold.
Autre maniere d’emplastre restorans la brisure et la dislocation et la torsion:	Another manner of poultice that restores fractures, dislocations, and twists:Prend les veines de lie, et le blanc d’uef, et met la veine de lie et le blanc d’
pren З abareis et ladani et enule et asefetide et gomme arabique et mugat, ana X З.;	Take the veins of bran, and the white of an egg, and put the bran vein and the white, and the adder's tongue and daniel, and myrrh, and assafetida, and gum arabic, each 5 scrip.
mirre et aloes, ana V З.;	myrrh and aloes, each 5 drachms;
alechil VIIII З.;	galangal root 1 ounce;
et en fai poudre, et les melle avec aubun d’uef;	and make into powder, and mix with egg white;
se li complexion de l’ome est chaude, si use de cest emplaustre, car il est de bone composition, et restoure les os brisiés hastanment, et vaut a plusors homes.	if the person's complexion is hot, use this plaster, for it is of good composition and restores broken bones quickly, and benefits many people.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a torsion:	Another recipe for a plaster that helps with twisting injuries:
pren mugat et vismalve, ana X З.;	take mallow leaves and violets, bruised, with oil of roses, apply this three times.
mirre et aloes, ana VIIII З.;	myrrh and aloes, mix together, nine parts.
acaice VI З.;	cinnamomom six parts;
bolic armenic X З., et broie bien, et confit avec aigue ou abun d’uef, et l’aministre.	armenian bole ten parts, and grind well, and cook with egg white or vinegar, and administer it.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre a jointes et as os desevrez de lor leus, et apaise la dolor sorvenant, et le taille usent de l’os, et la briseure:	Another method of plaster for joints and bones separated from their sockets, and it relieves pain, and wears away the bone, and breaks it:pren mirre et zibeth, ana XII З.;
pren lainne novele, et la moille en aisil et en oile cuit, et met sus lou leu.	take new lamb’s wool, moisten it in garlic and oil, and apply it to the affected area.pren saindore, et aloes, ana XII З.;
Cist emplastres ne restoure mie, mais il est boins por apaisier d’aposteme chaut, et oste proprement les dolors.	This plaster does not restore, but it is good for soothing a hot abscess, and it removes pain cleanly.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre qui restoure les os brisiez:	Another method of plaster which restores broken bones: take myrrh and civet, mix together, twelve parts;take mallow leaves, bruised, and violets, and oil of
pren foilles de figuier seches, et foilles de pavol terrestre, et broie ensamble, et fai emplaustre.	take fig leaves dried, and leaves of ground ivy, and grind them together, and make a plaster.pren saindore, et mirre, ana XII З.;
Autre maniere d’emplaustre a la restoration de la brisure de l’os et por amenusier lou remenant de l’aposteme.	Another method of plaster to restore the fracture of the bone, and to reduce the remaining abscess: take new linen, and soak it in vinegar and cooked oil, and apply it to the affected area.
Pren racine de vismalve, camomille, flors de violettes, farine de veces, de chescune une partie;	Take the root of marshmallow, chamomile, violets, and wheat flour, one part each.
et broie, et confis avec vin, et se li membres est eschaufez, se le confis avec aigue de coriandre moiste, ou d’aigue, et en use.	Grind them and make into an ointment with wine, and if the member is burning, make it with moist coriander water, or water, and use it.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre plus fors que li premier, quant aposteme dur vient a la restauration dou membre.	Another stronger method of plaster, when a hard abscess comes to the restoration of the member.Take the juice of leeks and onions, and mix with vinegar, and apply it to the affected area until restored.
Pren racines de vismalve, et semence de lin, balauste, mellilote, et sansuce, et flors de violetes et de camomille, de toutes ana une partie;	Take marshmallow roots, and flax seeds, borage, milkweed, and violet and chamomile flowers, one part each.
et broie, et confit avec aigue de salz, ou aigue douce, ou avec vin, selonc la chalor du membre, et son repos.	Grind them and make into an ointment with salt water, or sweet water, or wine, depending on the heat of the member and its condition.
Ypocras dist en son livre c’on ne mette sus lou membre brisiet por restorer fuer que cerote fait de cire et d’oile, et nulle autre chose plus, et dist qu’il soit entre dous ne trop molz ne trop durs.	Hyposurgeon writes in his book that one should not put anything on a broken limb to heal it except for a cerate made of wax and oil, and nothing else, and that it should be between soft and too hard.Et dist qu’il soit entre dous ne trop molz ne trop durs. Et s’il adveint qu’il soit trop sec, metez y oile; et s’il est trop moli, metez y cire; et si la brisure est grande, qu’on ne puet restorer, qu’on fasse cerote de cire et d’oile, et qu’on le broie tres fins, et qu’on y mette poudres d’armonie et de sante, et de violete, et qu’on le met sus la brisure, et qu’il soit entre dous ne trop molz ne trop durs.
Et il semble galien c’on doit mettre sus lou membre brisiet, por restoreir, choses seches un poc chaudes, si com mirre et aloes et encens et semblans choses, si com nos avons dit.	And it seems that Galen says that one should put on the broken limb, for healing, dry things that are slightly warm, such as myrrh, aloe, incense, and similar things, as we have said.Et dist galien qu’on doit mettre sus lou membre brisiet por restoreir, choses seches un poc chaudes, si com mirre et aloes et encens et semblans choses, si com nos avons dit. Et s’il adveint que la brisure soit granz et profont, dist galien qu’on doit mettre sus la brisure cerote de cire et d’oile, et qu’on le broie tres fins, et qu’on y mette poudres d’armonie et de sante, et de violete, et qu’on le met sus la brisure.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a lesion et a dolor:	Another recipe for an ointment that is good for injury and pain:Pren radice de vismalve, camomille, flors de violetes, farine de vez
pren mugath et chevolz d’omes decopez, ou pennes d’oiseil, et vismalve, et seil igalment, et les broie, et en fai emplaustre et lou lie.	Take mugwort and human hair cut in pieces, or bird feathers, and marshmallow, and mix them together, and grind them and make an ointment from it.
Et puis lou deslie un poc aprés, et pren garde se li malaides ne sent nule dolor, ne ne s’est meus li os de son leu;	Then loosen it a little after, and take care that the patient does not feel any pain, nor move the bone from its place.
si ne lou deslie par mains jors.	if you do not loosen it by hand for several days.
Et se dolor vient au leu, ou prurite, sens repos ou enfleure, si te haste, et le deslie, et oste l’emplaustre maintenant;	And if pain comes to the site, or itching, loss of appetite, or swelling, then hurry and loosen it, and remove the plaster immediately.
et pren drapeil legier, et esponge de mer moiste, et plonge en aigue, et en leve lou leu, tant que li prurite cesse, et soit apaisie li dolor;	and take a light cloth, and a sponge of sea moss soaked in water, and apply it to the site until the itching stops and the pain is relieved.
puis laisse reposer lou membre une houre, puis met sus lainne seche, moillie en aigue ou en oile roset, et lie sus une nut, tant que tu soies seur d’aposteme chaut;	Then let the limb rest for an hour, then apply cool linen, moistened in water or rose oil, and bind it up with a bandage, until you are sure there is no hot abscess.
et repose li enflammation dou membre, et soit ostee li dolor, puis rencomence la lieure subtil, et un poc d’emplaustre, et ne l’estraindre mie si fort com devant;	Let the inflammation of the limb subside, and the pain be relieved, then begin gently again with a little more plaster, and do not hold it as tightly as before.
et subtilie tant qu’il soit sanez.	and gently until it heals.
Et se tu vois que aposteme chaus et roujor et dolor et enfleure sont jai osteit dou tout, et tu as mestier d’emplaustre et de liien, si le rencomence, si com tu a fait premier igalment.	And if you see that the abscess is closed and red and painful and swollen all over, and you need ointment and bandages, then resume it, just as you did at first.
Et s’il ne vient au membre nient de ceu que nos avons dit, si ne le desliier fuer que aprés III jors ou IIII ou V ou VII;	And if nothing of what we have said comes to the member, do not dislocate it until after 3 or 4 or 5 or 7 days.
et aucune fois le laisse XX jors, selonc ce c’on voit, tant que li briseure s’aert, et aproche li ajostement de la char sus;	And sometimes leave it for 20 days, depending on what one sees, until the fracture heals and the flesh comes close to the bone.
adonques lou restraint plus que premier, et li engroisse sa viande, si com j’ai dit devant;	then restrain it more than before, and increase its food intake, as I have said before.
et se tu vois lou leu sechier plus que mestier n’est, saiches que norrissemens n’i puet venir;	And if you see the area drier than necessary, know that infection cannot come.
arose lou donques d’aigue chaude tede, toutes les fois que tu lou deslies, et ce soit chescun tier jor, et eslaiche un poc la lieure;	Then wash it with warm water when you dislocate it, and do so every third day, and loosen the bandage a little.
par cest ovraige donques cort li norrissemens au membre, et esmende hastanment ceu que font li fol mire, que restourent le membre tortement:	Through this process, infection will leave the limb, and it will quickly heal what the foolish do, who twist the limb.
c’est malvais, et si est ovraiges paourous, et je n’i voi autre chose que dou lassier et de l’ovrer droitement.	It is wicked, and so are the works of cowards; I see no other way than to leave it and do it properly.
des diverses manieres de brisure	of the various methods of breaking
Maintes manieres de brisures sont, et diverses figures, et les causes sont destintees;	There are many types of fractures, with various shapes and distinct causes;
car il a brisures que sont faites de percussion d’espee, et li colz oste tout l’os jusc’a syfac qui est desoz l’os, si com fait haiche ou fust;	for there are fractures that are made by the impact of a sword, and the collar bone breaks all the way to the sinfist which is under the bone, just like an ax or a pole;
et por ceu est apelee ceste maniere de briseure «haichure».	and for this reason, this type of fracture is called "haichure".
Ou li espee cope l’os par desus sens percier, et est apelee ceste maniere de brisure «absolue»;	Or the sword cuts through the bone from above without piercing it, and this type of fracture is called "absolute";
et est li plaie de ces II brisures grans ou petite.	and the wound of these two fractures are large or small.Apres doit l’om medecin porver si li os est sanz espas, ou il y a
Et s’il i a percussion emboee, ou fendure ou de colz de piere, ou de cheoir sus piere, ou d’autres semblans.	And if there is a strike with the flat of the sword, or a cut, or from the collar bone, or from falling on stone, or from other similar causes.
Et s’il a brisure persant, qui aproiche jusc’a la toile qui est desoz l’os, ou elle est sus l’os, et est ceste plaie ou grans ou petite.	And if there is a fracture that penetrates, which approaches the membrane beneath the bone, or is on top of the bone; this wound is either large or small.
Et si a plaie qui est reponue en l’os ausi subtil com uns chevous, et est li fendure petite, et por ceu est apelee ceste brisure «capillaire»;	Then the doctor must determine if the bone is without space, or if there is
et si la plaie qui est faite ou par ferir de piere, ou par cheoir, ou par semblant chose, et fait entrer la piece de l’os aval, et est li leus chevez si com font li chaudelier quant il fierent sus les chaudieres;	and if the wound is made by a stone or by falling, or by similar things, and the bone goes in below, and the place is shaved smooth as the blacksmiths do when they work on pots.
si entre li piere dedens.	if the stone goes inside.
Et ceu avient plus a sous qui ont ou chief moistes os, si com chief d’enfant;	And this happens more to those who have soft bone at the top, as in the head of an infant;
et avient a toutes ces manieres de brisure que pieces menues en sont desevrees si com esteles;	and it happens with all these types of fractures where small pieces are dislocated, like tiles;
et je em parlerai en son leu.	and I will speak about this in detail.
Et conoissons toutes manieres de briseures par la detraction sus elles, et l’inquisition a tentes, et par la char corrumpue qui est sus.	And we know all kinds of fractures by their deformity, and by the inquiry into the tent, and by the corruption of the flesh that is above it.
Li semblance capillaire est conue par ceu que quant on a descovert l’os, et on frote enche sus, si apert li brisure noire.	The hairline fracture is known because when the bone is uncovered and rubbed on top, the fracture appears black.
En la cure de la brisure, pren garde as accidens dou malaide, et se tu vois nul malvais accident, si com vomissement de cole, et amission d’entendement, et estension, et paumeson, et fievre ague, et les eulz issir fuer et rougir, et autres semblans em plusors dispositions, si ne puet saner sens doute.	In the treatment of a fracture, pay attention to the accidents of the illness; and if you see no malicious accident, such as vomiting of phlegm, loss of consciousness, extension, paralysis, fever, eyes popping out and turning red, and other similar things in various dispositions, then it can heal without a doubt.
Et se tu ne vois accident espoantauble, et tu esperes salut, si comence la cure.	And if you see no shocking accident, and you expect recovery, then begin the treatment.
Et quant li navrez vient premier a toi, et c’est en yver, si covient oster l’os devant lou quatorzime jor au mues que tu pues.	And when the baby comes to you first, and it is in winter, you should remove the foreskin before the fourteenth day when you can.
Et se c’est en esteit, si te haste d’oster l’os devant lou septime jor, ainsois que li toile desoz l’os soit corrumpue, et vienent li accident que nos avons dit.	And if it is in the summer, you should hasten to remove the foreskin before the seventh day, so that the skin under the foreskin does not become corrupted, and so that the accidents we have mentioned do not occur.
Et se li brisure de l’os vient jusc’a la toile que cuevre lou cerveil, si covient que tu fendes la partie fendue ensi:	And if the fracture of the bone reaches the membrane that covers the brain, then you must split the fractured part thus:
et est que tu preignes lou chief dou malaide navreit, et descuevre sus l’os en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et sus la figure de la plaie plus souef que tu pues, et se decorrement de sanc vient au descovrir l’os, ou aposteme chaus, se li aide de ceu qu’il covient, et est que tu emplisses lou leu de drapelz moilliez en oile roset;	and you must grip the head of the wounded person firmly and expose the bone in every way that you can, and according to the shape of the wound as much as possible, and if blood comes out when you expose the bone, or an abscess forms, then aid him with what is appropriate, and you must fill the area with dampened pieces of cloth in rose oil;
et fai reposer la plaie tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et soies asseurez de decorrement de sanc;	and let the wound rest until the abscess is drained and there is no more bleeding.
puis comence entor l’os a oster, et c’est fait selonc II manieres d’ovraige:	then begin around the bone to remove it, and this can be done in two ways:
l’une manieres si est que tu copes au taillement estroit devant, et c’est li forme:	one way is to cut closely in front, and that is the shape:
Et puis i boute .i. autre taillement plus grant que lou premier.	And then make another cut larger than the first.
Et li seconde maniere si est que tu aies nombre de taillemens divers, les uns estrois et les autres larges, et soient a pointe, et soient de fer inde;	and the other way is to have diverse cuts, some narrow and some wide, pointed, and made of iron:
et en oevre legierement, que tu ne bleces le chief.	and work gently, so that you do not cut the head.
Et se li os est fors et durs, si covient que tu lou perces entor, ainsois que tu i aministres taillemens avec tareres, ne mie parfont qu’il ne percent outre l’os dou test, et doit avoir desus la pointe une marge ou I cercle, que ne laisse passer la pointe outre l’os;	And if the bone is thick and hard, you must pierce around it, so that you apply cuts with chisels, not deep enough to penetrate through the bone, and it should have a rim or circle on top, preventing the point from going through the bone;
et t’en covient avoir plusors, si que chescuns viegne en son leu de l’espés de l’os, si que tu aies tareres por toz test;	and you should have several of these, so that each one comes in its place in the thickness of the bone, so that you have chisels for all parts of the skull;
et c’est li forme des III manieres de tareres:	and there are three types of cautery:
Li qualitez por percier entor l’os brisiet est que tu mettes I tarere sus l’os, et torne a tes dois tant que tu saiches que li os est perciez;	The qualities for piercing around the broken bone are that you must place the cautery on the bone and move it with your fingers until you feel the bone is pierced;
puis remet lou tarere autre part un poc aprés, et ensi fai tout entor, puis cope as incisoires l’espaice de l’os qui est entre les pertu, et fai ceu plus subtilment que tu pues, et legierement, si com nos avons dit, tant que tu en traies l’os a ta main, ou a aucun des estrumens que tu as si com tenailles, pinceures;	then move the cautery elsewhere a little later, and do this all around, then cut into the space between the bone fragments with the incision, and do this as skillfully and gently as you can, as we have said, until you pull out the bone with your hand or with one of the instruments you have, such as tweezers;
et garde que tu ne touchier au cerveil ne au syfac.	Be careful not to touch the brain or the dura mater.
Et quant tu avras l’os perciet, et trait, si couvient que tu reses l’apreteit qui est demoree de l’os a tout I autre estrument semblant a un incisoire, mais il covient qu’il soit plus tenves et plus subtilz que li autre incisoire;	And when you have pierced and pulled out the bone, it is necessary to remove the membrane that remains attached to the bone with another instrument similar to a scalpel, but it must be more flexible and thinner than the other scalpel;
et s’il demore rien des petis os, ne nulles escailles, si les oste legierement a I des estrumens;	and if it remains stuck in the small bones or any scales, then gently dislodge them with instruments.
puis cure la plaie de tentes et d’oignemens que nos avons dit.	then treat the wound with tenting and poultices as we have described.
Et li autre maniere d’ovraige si est cil que Galiiens dist, qui est plus saus;	And the other method of treatment is that which Galen describes, which is safer:
et le loa molt fort, et c’est sa parole.	and he highly recommends it, and his word is law.
Il covient premier que tu descuevres une partie de l’os, lai ou li brisure apert mues, si que quant tu avras descovert celle partie, si metras desoz lou chief de cest incisoire lenticulaire, de coi ci est li forme:	First, you must uncover a part of the bone where the fracture is open and moving. Once you have uncovered that part, place under it the cutting edge of this lens-shaped instrument, which is its shape:
Et ne trenche mie d’une part, et est li partie ague en II costez, si que li trenchans est devers l’os;	And do not cut from one side only, as the wound will be deeper on the bone side;
puis fier d’un petit maillet sus, si que tu copes legierement l’os tout entor, et te done bien en garde de la toile que est desoz;	then gently strike with a small mallet all around so that you slightly move the bone all around, taking care not to damage the membrane underneath;
s’elle est aerse a l’os, si l’oste legierement, car on l’oste bien sens nuisement, et sens paor.	if it is attached to the bone, then gently move the bone, for it can be moved without harm or fear.
Et se li brisure de l’os ne perce jusc’a la toile, et li os est copez tant soulement par desus, et il i a petites pieces, si couvient rere celle asperiteit, et oster les escailles au raseur subtil dont tu dois avoir diverses quantitez, por amenistrer en chescun leu le plus covenauble, selonc l’ovraige et la figure de la brisure.	And if the fracture does not penetrate through to the membrane, and the bone is cut only slightly from above, with small pieces, then one must remove this roughness, and take away the scales with a very fine rasp of which you should have various sizes, in order to smooth each part according to the work and the shape of the fracture.
Si reis devant de grant raseurs, et aprés de plus subtilz, et ne cesser de ceu faire tant k’il soit bien.	If you use a large razor at first, and then a finer one afterwards, and do not stop doing this until it is done well.
En chescune des autres tailleures capillaires et brisure subtil, covient que tu amenistres cause selonc son adrecement;	For all other hairline and subtle fractures, you must treat according to the specifics of the case;
et c’est chose que n’est mie reponue a celui qui a mis son estude en cest art.	and this is something that has not been answered for one who has dedicated their study to this art.
Et se li syfac est descovers, si covient que tu preignes I drapeil de lin, selonc la quantiteit de la plaie, et le moille en oile roset, et le mete sus la plaie;	And if the wound is exposed, one should press a linen bandage according to the size of the wound, and moisten it in rose oil, and place it over the wound;
puis pren I autre drapeil doublé en II ou en III, et le moille en vin et en oile roset, et le met sus le premier drapeil;	Then take another bandage doubled into two or three, moisten it in wine and rose oil, and place it over the first bandage;
et fai ceu plus legierement que tu pues, que tu ne grever lou syfac, puis aministre par desus I autre liien, et ne l’estraindre mie fuer que tant k’il teigne la plaie soulement;	and do this as gently as you can so that you don't burden the wound, then administer another bandage on top, and don't tighten it more than necessary so that it only presses the wound;
et le laisse ensi I jor ou II, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, puis le deslie, et i aministre medicines si com racines de lis, et farine de veces, et poudre d’encens, et aristologe, et semblans choses;	and let it be like this for one or two days, until the abscess is soothed, then loosen it, and administer remedies such as lily roots, and flour of beans, and incense powder, and aristologus, and similar things;
et de ces choses fai poudre, et met sus la plaie, et i aministre adés medicines mondefians sens mordication;	and from these things make a powder, and apply it to the wound, and then administer other medicine without biting;
et warde que li plaie soit adés nette, que tu n’i laissier mie l’oignement, ne n’i laissier mie assembler bowe, car quant bowe s’asemble sus la toile dou cerveil, si la corront et porrist, et avient au malaide grans malice;	and ensure that the wound is clean, so that you do not leave any oil or allow any pus to gather, for when pus gathers on the brain's membrane, it will corrupt and cause great harm to the patient;
car quant on met sus lou syfac chose mordant, si nercist par desus.	for when one applies something biting to a wound, it numbs from above.
Pren warde donques, se nulz mavais accidens vient au malaide, si com nos avons dit, si est doutable sens doute.	Take care therefore, if any bad accident happens to the patient, as we have said, that it is without doubt.
Et se noiror n’i vient fuers que por la medicine c’on a mise sus, que teil vertu ait, si covient que tu preignes une partie de miel, et III parties d’oile roset et en glue I drapel, et lou met sus lou syfac;	And if blackness does not disappear but only becomes worse due to the medicine applied, one should mix a portion of honey with three portions of rose oil and apply this mixture to the wound using a bandage.
puis lou cure de manieres de cures qu’il couvient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then, treat it in the usual ways until it heals.
Saiches que aucune fois sont brisies les II parties dou neis desus, ou li une par li soulement, car ce sont II os;	You should know that sometimes both parts of the nose's bridge are broken, or just one part, because there are two bones there;
et cil desoz est cartillaginous, et ne brise mie, si ne fait fuer k’enbower ou tordre, et puis saine.	and those below are cartilaginous, and do not break, unless they are bent or twisted, and then heal.
Et se l’une des II parties est brisie, si covient que tu boutes ton petit doi ou pertus dou neis, et met igal cele brisure dedens a ton doi indice, et au pouchet par defuer, tant que li neis reveigne selonc sa figure natureil;	And if one of the two parts is broken, you should press your little finger or hole of the nail, and place the break inside your index finger, and hold it in place with your thumb until the nail returns to its natural shape.
et fai ce legierement, et warde que li malaides ne sente dolor par ton ovraige.	And do this gently, and be careful that the patient does not feel pain from your work.
Et se li brisure est en la partie desus lou neis, et ne puet venir li dois au leu, si couvient que tu lou mettes igal au chief d’un rait un poc gros.	If the fracture is above the nose, and the bones cannot be aligned, then you must place it evenly at the end of a rather thick thread.
Et se li brisure est de II pars, si refai autretel, et te haste de restorer lou premier jor, se tu pues;	And if the break is in two parts, do the same, and hurry to restore it on the first day, if you can;for si li malaide demore longuement, li brisure ne velt selonc sa figure natureil, mai est contors a la figure del membre, et aler se contors en
se ce non, aprés lou septime ou le disime, quant li apostemes chaus est apaisiez, puis bouthe au chief dou neis tentes de drapelz de lin, se li brisure est en une partie.	But if the patient lingers long, the break will not return to its natural shape but distort the shape of the limb; and it will remain distorted unless, on the seventh or tenth day, when the abscesses have healed, you press the head of the nail with tent-like pieces of linen cloth, if the break is in one part.
Ou tu boutes I autre d’autre part, se li brisure i est;	Or you sew him up elsewhere, if the wound is there.
et soient les tentes si grosses qu’eles emplissent les pertus dou neis.	and the stitches should be so large that they fill the holes in the nipples.
Et dirent aucun restorour c’on doit moillier les tentes em burre, et muer chescun jor.	And some restorers say that one must moisten the tents with butter, and change them every day.
Il ne me semble mie que ce soit bien, mais covient qu’elles soient moillies en confection d’aubun d’uef, et de poudre de molin;	I do not think this is good, but it is necessary that they be moistened with an egg yolk and flour;
puis laisse la tente, tant que li os soit fers, et li cartilaiges endurcis.	then leave the stitch in place until the bone is healed and the cartilage hardened.
Et aucune fois boute on ou neis pennes d’oie en leu de tentes, et si a I souef drapeil entor, et se tient la briseure, et soffle li malaides parmi;	And sometimes we sew in goose feathers instead of stitches, and wrap it with a thin cloth, and the dislocation is held in place, and the patient breathes among them;
or fai lou kel ke tu vues.	or do what you want.
Et se apostemes chaus vient au neis tandis com tu i oevres, si i met cerote ou coton moilliet en oile roset, ou en .i. poc de dyaquilon.	And if hot abscesses come to the nose while you are working on it, then put cerate or cotton moistened in rose oil, or in a little diaquilon.
Et se apostemes chaus n’i vient, si met emplastre par defuer, de farine de sisament, et de poudre d’encens, confites avec aubun d’uef, puis met sus estoupes legieres, et ne liier mie lou neis;	And if a wound comes to the nipples, put on a poultice, made from flour of vetches, and incense powder, mixed with egg yolk, then put on top light lint, and do not tie it to the nipple;
et se li brisure dou neis est petite, et il est brisiés em menues pieces, si l’estrai as estrumens covenables a ceu, puis cout la fendure, et la cure de choses enjanrans char, et soudant, si com emplastres et oignemens covenables a ceu;	and if the fracture of the nose is small, and it is broken into small pieces, then extract them with instruments suitable for this purpose, then close the wound, and treat things that are out of joint, and mend, as with plasters and ointments suitable for this purpose.
et s’il n’a dedens lou neis nule plaie, si lou cure de tentes, et i met cainnes de plonc, tant qu’il soit sanez.	and if there is no wound inside the nose, then treat it with tenting and put in canes of lead until it is healed.
de la routure de la mandibule	of a broken jaw:
Quant li mandibule est route desoz, et il n’i a point de plaie defuer, et li brisure est defuer tant soulement, et n’est mie brisiez en dous, fuer que corbelz dedens, si le conoist on legierement.	When the jaw is broken underneath and there is no open wound, and the break is only on the surface and not broken in two, one can know it easily.
Il covient, se li brisure est en la destre partie, que tu boutes ton doi indice en la bouche dou malaide;	It is necessary, if the fracture is on the right side, that you put your index finger into the mouth of the patient:
et se li brisure est en la mandibule senestre, si boute ton doi indice de la main destre, et boute la brisure dedens legierement, et l’afaite a l’autre main par defuer, et met igal.	and if the fracture is in the left jaw, then put your index finger of the right hand and put pressure on the fracture gently and pull it with the other hand equally.
Et se li brisure de la mandibule est desevree en .ij., si covient que tu aministres extension de .ij. pars, tant qu’il soit igalz.	And if the fracture of the jaw is displaced in .ii., then you must administer an extension of .i. parts, so that it is equalized.
Et se commovemens des dens avient, ou routure, si les estrain d’un fil d’or ou d’argent ou de soie, puis met sus la mandibule brisie cerote, et met sus I drapel double;	And if there is movement of the teeth, or dislocation, then hold them in place with a thread of gold, silver, or silk, and then put over the broken jaw a cerote, and put over that a double cloth;
et met sus lou drapel une grant estele bien faite, ou une piece de cuir igal, longe et large selonc la mandibule, et la lie sus au mues que tu pues, et comande a malaide qu’il se repose, et menjuce viandes legieres.	and place on top of the wound a well-made bandage, or a piece of leather equal in size, long and wide according to the jaw, and tie it as tightly as possible; and instruct the patient to rest and eat light foods.
Et se tu vois que li figure se chainge, si le deslie au tier jor, et puis remet a point ceu que c’est chaingiet;	And if you see that the jaw is changing shape, then loosen it for three days, and then reset it to its original position.
et met emplaustre sus, de la poudre dou moulin avec abun d’uef ou farine de sisament, aprés ceu que tu as osteit lou cerote;	and apply a poultice on top of that, made from ground powder of egg or flour of millet, after you have removed the kerchief.
et met sus l’emplaustre lainne legiere, et se li emplaustres s’aert, et li disposition dou malaide ne se chainge, laisse le tant k’il soit sanez;	and apply a light bandage on top of the poultice, and if the poultices become soaked through, and the patient's condition does not change, then leave it until it heals.
maintes fois est sanez en III semainnes.	It often heals within three weeks.
Et se apostemes chaus vient, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit maintes fois.	And if a hot abscess comes, then administer what we have said many times before.
Et s’il i a brisure et plaie ensamble, rewarde se nule piece de l’os en est ostee;	And if there is a break and wound together, examine it to see if any bone is missing;
si subtilie de l’oster as estrumens covenaubles a ceu.	So skillfully hide from them the implements needed for this procedure.
Et se li plaie est estroite, si l’eslarge a flaime selonc ta necessiteit.	And if the wound is narrow, dilate it with flame according to your necessity.
Et quant tu avras ostees toutes ces pieces, et il n’i demore nule, si cout la plaie, s’ele est large, et met sus .i. des emplaustres covenaubles a ceu, por enjanrer char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when you have removed all these pieces, and there remains none, then close the wound, if it is wide, and place upon it suitable poultices to promote healing.
de la forcele	of the forceps
Li forcele brise plusors fois devant, devers l’espaule, et li brisure si est selonc III manieres:	The bone is broken in several places in front of the shoulder, and the fracture occurs in three ways:
ou elle est brisie et desevree en II, et i a pieces, et est li plus legiere a restorer;	1. it is broken and separated into two pieces, which is the easiest to heal;
ou il i a brisure avec plaie.	where there is a break with a wound.
Et li ovraiges si est quant li brisure est sens plaie, que tu aies II ministres, si que li uns teigne l’ajutoire que sent la forcele brisie;	And the procedure is the same when the break is without a wound: you must have two assistants so that one can hold the shoulder where the collarbone is broken,
et li autres estende lou col vers la partie;	and the other stretches the neck towards the affected side;
puis met igal la brisure a tes dois, si que li forme soit si com il covient, et n’i ait ne apparance ne chevement.	Then put the broken bone back into place with your fingers, so that it is set correctly and there is no displacement or gap.
Et se tu a mestier de plus estendre, si met desoz l’espaule au malaide une spere reonde de drap, ou de lainne, et soit grosse selonc ta necessiteit;	And if you need to extend it further, place a round pillow of cloth or wool underneath the shoulder, as thick as needed;
et estent et lieve la forcele, et estraint le spere a ta main, si que tu mettes igal la brisure, si com il covient.	and stretch and gently pull on the collarbone, while pushing the pillow away with your hand, so that you reset the bone in its proper place.
Et se tu ne pues traire le chief de la forcele au defuer, por ceu qu’elle vient em parfont, si covient que li malaides gise sovin sus son hatereil, et met desoz l’espaule .i. oreillier moien, et boute li ministres l’espaule aval, tant que li os de la forcele soit levez.	And if you cannot pull out the head of the dislocated shoulder, because it comes up very tightly, then the patient should lie on his back, and put something under the shoulder, an ear, and the assistant pushes the shoulder down while pulling the arm upward, until the bone of the shoulder is dislodged.
Et puis adrece la brisure a tes dois, et se tu lou trueves debrisiet, si covient que tu fendes sus;	Then press the bones together with your fingers, and if you find them loose, then you must split them;
et trai fuer les pieces legierement, et se li os ne puet joindre por aucun sormontement, si le cope a l’un des incisoires que tu as;	and gently pull on the pieces, and if the bone cannot be joined due to any swelling, then cut at one of the incisions that you have made.
mais que tu mettes desoz la forcele cest estrument, por warder lou syfac:	but you must put under pressure this instrument, in order to push out the pus:
et semble une cuiller, et n’est mie chevez, et soit ausi large com il lou covient, selonc la grandor de l’os et la possance de l’uevre;	and it should be shaped like a spoon, and not sharp, and as wide as is necessary, according to the size of the bone and the strength of the action;
et ait II chiés, si com tu vois, et soit li uns larges, et li autres estrois, si com est li routure de la plaie que tu as fait quant tu as trait les os;	and it has two heads, as you can see, and one is wide and the other narrow, according to the nature of the wound that you have made when you pulled on the bones.
et quant tu es asseurez d’aposteme chaut, si cout la plaie, et se li routure est petite, ou tu doutes aposteme chaut, si emple la plaie de drapelz et de tentes, selonc sa quantiteit.	And when you are sure that there is a hot abscess, then cut the wound, and if the opening is small, or if you doubt there is a hot abscess, then dress the wound with bandages and bandages, according to its size.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si moille .i. drapel en oile roset et en aisil et en vin, et met sus.	And if hot abscesses appear, moisten a cloth in rose oil and garlic and wine, and place it on top.
Li estrignement de l’os, quant il est sens plaies et sens tailleure, est que tu mettes sus l’os l’enplaustre de la poudre dou molin et d’aubun d’uef, et met estoupes legieres sus, et met une spere desoz l’assele, se tu en as mestier;	The stretching of the bone, when it is without wounds and without fracturing, is to place on the bone the plaster made from mill dust and egg white, and put light bandages on top, and place a sphere underneath the splint, if you need one.
puis pren une tres grant bende d’une palme de large, puis met I drapeil double sus estoupes, et l’emplaustre;	Then take a very large bandage, one palm wide, then put the double drape on top of the bandages and plaster;
puis pren une estele subtil de III dois de large et de lonc, et l’envoloupe entor celui bendeil, si que li chief dou bendeil soient pendant;	Then take a subtle needle three fingers wide and long, and wrap it around the bandage so that the head of the bandage hangs down.
et met l’estele sus la briseure, et torne le bendeil sus lou col, et desoz l’asselle sainne, et desoz l’asselle malaide;	And place the needle on the fracture, and wrap the bandage around the neck, and under the healthy scapula, and under the injured scapula.
et la ramoinne de chescune partie, et quant tu vois ke li lieure tient la briseure avenanment, et tu vois clerement que li estele ne se muet desus l’os brisiet, si le rewarde chescun jor, et quant li liiens eslaiche, si lou restraint;	And reset it from each part, and when you see that the ligament holds the fracture in place satisfactorily, and you clearly see that the needle does not move over the broken bone, then release it a little, and when the ligature slackens, constrain it again.
et fai gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et li met quant il dort I petit orillier desoz l’assele, por lever l’ajutoire en haut;	and let the patient lie on his back, and put a small pillow under his shoulder to raise the shoulder joint;
si aligera li brisure de la forcele par l’aligement de l’espaule, ou tu li lie lou bras au col, et ne lou desliier se malvais accidens n’i vient, jusc’a XX jors;	if it eases the fracture of the collarbone by aligning the shoulder, then tie his arm to his neck and do not untie it unless an evil accident happens, for up to 20 days;
puis rencomence l’emplaustre, se tu vois qu’il en ait mestier, et l’estraint et le laisse ensi, tant qu’il soit restorez;	then renew the poultice, if you see that he needs it, and keep him so, until he is healed;and let him not wear a garment over the shoulder, but rather have the arm bare, to see how it goes;et s’il li vemme de la pluit ou del puais, et qu’il velt le taster, faiz le coger ou un chas o si
et elle est restoree au plus en XXVIII jors, et en moins a aucuns homes.	and if pus or blood comes out and he wants to taste it, let him catch it on his finger;if the wound is healed within 28 days, it is restored in less time for some people.
de la brisure de l’espaule	of the dislocation of the shoulder
Poc avient que li espaule brise ou large leu ne em mileu, et ne lou seit on fuers que par lou touchement;	It sometimes happens that the shoulder dislocates or breaks, and they do not feel any pain except through touch;and if he feels pain in his shoulder, it is because of a wound made by fire or cold, or a fall, or a blow.And if the wound is deep, it is necessary to open it,
si l’apareille selonc la figure de la brisure, et la ramoinne selonc sa forme natureil, en toutes les manieres que tu pues;	then set it according to the shape of the fracture, and reset it according to its natural form, in every way that you can.
puis met sor le leu poudre dou molin avec abun d’uef, et estoupes legieres, et met sus I drapeil double;	then put on the site powdered flour with egg white, and light dressings, and place over it a doubled-over cloth;
puis met sus une estele large et subtil, un poc plus large de l’espaule, et se desoz l’estele est chevemens en aucun leu de l’espaule, si emple celle cheveure d’estoupes de lin, si que li estele siece igalment;	then place a wide and thin board, slightly wider than the shoulder, on top, and if there is swelling beneath the board at any point on the shoulder, stuff that area with linen dressings so that the board lies flat and even. Then;
et puis l’estraint a tout une grant bende fermement, si que li estele ne se mueve de son leu, et regarde le liien chescun jor;	and then tighten it with a large bandage firmly, so that the board does not move from its place, and check the dressing every day. Then;
et toutes les fois k’il amolist, si l’estraint, et met igal l’estele s’elle est fuer de son leu, et gise li malaides sus son costeit;	and whenever it softens, tighten it again and reset the board if it has moved out of place. Then have the patient lie on his side.
et li espaule est restouree en XX jors ou en XXV.	and the shoulder is restored in 20 days or 25.
Et quant cist nombres est acomplis, si le deslie, et soies seur, car ce n’est mie os qui se mette fuer legierement.	And when this time is completed, he releases it and is sure, because it is not an easy bone to set.
Et se une piece de l’os tent avant, et point desoz lou keur, si fent sus, et l’oste, et fai ceu que nos avons dit en la brisure de la forcele d’apaisier aposteme chaut.	And if a part of the bone protrudes forward, and not beneath the heart, they should push it up, and the bone, and do as we said in the breaking of the forceps to soothe the hot abscess.
de la brisure dou pis	of the breaking of the foot
Li peis est aucune fois brisiez em mileu, mais ce avient poc;	The penis is sometimes broken in the middle, but that rarely happens;
mais il brise sovent au defuer.	but it often breaks at the tip.
Et quant il est brisiez emmi, si decline au desoz, et sent li malaides grant dolor, et faute d’alainne, et toust, et par aventure vomist sanc, et apert li chevemens en l’os brisiés, et lou sent om bien.
