And when it is broken in the middle, it bends downward, and the patient feels great pain and weakness throughout his body, and sometimes vomits blood, and there are open wounds in the broken bone, which he feels with his fingers.
Et li restoracion si est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos, et li met I cussin entre les espaules, puis presse les espaules, et li assemble les costes des II costelz a tes mains, et subtilie dou mettre igal a toutes les manieres que tu pues, tant que li figure de l’os soit si com il covient;	And the restoration is that the patient lies on his back, and he puts a pillow between his shoulders, then presses his shoulders, and brings together the sides of the two ribs with his hands, and carefully ensures they are even in all ways he can, so that the shape of the bone is as it should be;
puis met sus emplaustres et estoupes desus l’estele subtil de salz, ou d’autre fust legier, et l’envoloupe en I drapeil, et la lie sus l’os brisiet, si qu’elle ne se mueve;	then he applies plasters and poultices on top of the splint made from light wood, and wraps it in a cloth, and ties it onto the broken bone so that it does not move;
et torne le liien reondement au dos, et l’estraint avenanment, et rewarde chescune houre la liure, et s’elle ramolist, si l’estraint;	and turn the bandage smoothly to the back, and tighten it skillfully, and check every hour that the wound is not softening, and if it softens, tighten it.
et s’il lou covient desliier, por corrosion ou por prurite que vient au leu, ou dolor ou aposteme, si te haste, et lou deslie, et raie l’emplaustre, et adresce ceu qui i est venus de manieres de cures;	and if it needs to be loosened because of corrosion or itching at the site, or pain or an abscess, then hurry and loosen it, and scrape off the ointment, and address what has come about in various ways.
puis ramoinne l’emplaustre, et l’estraint tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then reset the ointment, and tighten it until it heals.
de la brisure des costes	of the fracture of the ribs
Saiches que li briseure des costes ne vient fuer que en leus gros aprés le dos, et au chief dedens, et ne ploient fuer que por ceu qu’eles sont glairouses;	Know that the fracture of the ribs only occurs above the back, and in the chest, and they only bend because they are slippery.
et le sent om bien a l’inquisition as dois.	and you will feel it well on examination in those places.Et s’il adonques arrive qu’ele soit brisee, il cov
Et li restoremens si est que tu met igal la brisure, si com il covient.	And the treatment is to set the break evenly, as it should be.
Et puis met l’emplaustre, et l’estraint d’une estele, se tu en as mestier.	Then apply the ointment, and bind it with a cloth, if necessary.
Et se li brisure des costes est declinans au dedens, si sent li malaides tres grant dolor, et pointure, ausi com de pleuresin, car li os point la toile;	And if the fracture of the ribs is inward-leaning, then the patient feels great pain and piercing, just as with pleurisy, because the bone punctures the membrane.Et si li brisure des costes est vers le dos, il sent pointure et dolor, car li os deffend la toile;
et alaine a poinnes, et toust et vomist grant planteit de sanc, et c’est de grief santeit, et li ancien i ont mis grant engien.	and has pain in his fingernails, and feels nauseous and vomits a great quantity of blood, this is a serious illness, and the physicians have given him strong medicine.
Et si a de ces qui dient qu’il le covient aministrer viandes qui enflent le ventre, por bouter la briseure au defuer.	And if there are those who say that one should administer foods that swell the belly, to push the fracture out.
Nos ne faisons mie ceu, que apostemes chaulz n’i viegne, s’il n’i est venus.	We do not do this, unless hot abscesses come to it, if they have not come to it already.
Et s’il i est venus, si le saine.	And if it has come to it, then heal it.
Et dirent aucun d’ous c’on met ventouses sor le leu, por sucier forment, et c’est semblant a raison;	And some say that cupping glasses should be placed over the area to draw out the poison, and this is reasonable advice:
toutevoie, doutance i a que li ventouse n’atraie les superfluitez au leu por la disposition de foiblece.	However, there is a doubt that the cupping glass will attract the excess fluids due to the weakness of the patient.
Et dirent aucun d’ous c’on doit covrir le leu de lainne moillie en oile chaut, et met on tentes entre les costes por metre igal la lieure entor, puis soit curez de la cure de pleurisin, de viande et de medicine.	And some say that one should cover the area with soft lamb's wool soaked in hot oil, and place a tent between the ribs to ensure even pressure all around, then it should be bandaged with bandages of pleurisy, meat and medicine.
Et se li malaides sent grant dolor qu’il ne puet soffrir par l’os qui point la toile, et doutance est au malaide, si covient fendre sus lou leu de la coste brisie, et covient mettre desoz I estrument por warder lou syfac;	And if the patient feels great pain that they cannot endure through the bone that punctures the skin, and there is doubt about the patient, then one should split open the ribcage over the site of the broken bone, and place a instrument underneath to push out the infection;
et adonques doit on trenchier l’os, et traire legierement, et puis coudre les II levres de la plaie, s’elle est grans, et le curez d’emplaustres, tant qu’il soit sanez.	and then split the bone, and gently pull it out, and then sew up the two lips of the wound if it is large, and treat it with poultices until it heals.
Et se apostemes chaus vient, si met sus drapelz moilliez en oile roset, et met sus lou leu;	And if swollen abscesses come, then put wet cloths in rose oil, and put them on the affected area;
et cure tandis le leu de ceu qu’il covient a aposteme, et soit gisans sovins sus lou costeit ou il doit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	and treat the area around the abscess as needed, and let the patient lie on his side where it is, until he is healed.
de la brisure dou col	from the fracture of the neck:
Aucune fois vient briseure as os dou col, et poc avient k’il ploie;	Sometimes there is a fracture in the collarbone, and it can be dislocated;
et ausi a l’espinee dou dos.	and also in the spine of the back.
Et quant ce avient a aucun, et tu vues savoir s’il sera sanez ou non, si pren warde se tu vois ses mains mollifiies et enflees et mortes, et ne les puet movoir ne estendre, et quant tu les poins d’une aguille, si ne lou sent.	And when this happens to someone, and you want to know if they will recover or not, take note if their hands are soft and swollen and numb, and they cannot move or straighten them, and when you prick them with a needle, they do not feel it.
Saiches qu’il est mortelz em plusors dispositions, et s’il les muet et sent bien quant on les estraint et point, saiches que li jointure de l’os est sauve, et que li malaides iert curez, s’on i met cure.	Know that it is deadly in many ways, and if they are numb and feel pain when you stretch or pinch them, know that the joint of the bone is saved, and that the illness is healed, if proper care is given.And si li mains ne sont pas mollifiiez ne enflees ne mortes, et les sent bien quant on les estraint, sache que li maux est de la chair ou de la peau et qu’il n’est pas de l’os; et si tu le mets en cure, il sera sain.
Et se semblans chose vient a l’espinee dou dos, et tu vues savoir s’il iert sanez ou non, si pren warde se li piez sont amollis, et se li accident i sont qui sont em mains, et sus lou dos saut ventositeit et egestion sens volonteit;	And if something similar happens to the spine in the back, and you want to know if he is healthy or not, then see if his feet are numb, and if the senses are in his hands, and in his back there are wind and urination without will;
et quant on l’a sovineit sus son ventre, si saut egestion sens volonteit.	and when he lies on his stomach, there is urination without will.
Et quant il est sovinez sus son dos et il vuet asseller, si ne puet.	And when he is placed on his back and he wants to sit up, he cannot.
Saiches qu’il est mortelz:	Know that it is fatal:
si ne laboreir mie en sa cure.	if there is no improvement in the treatment.
Et se cist accident ne li vienent, si est li chose plus legiere.	And if these effects do not occur, then the condition is less severe.
Et li cure si est que tu rewardes s’il i a aposteme chaut, si met sus l’espinee oile roset ou oile de moieuf d’uef, tant qu’il soit apaisiez;	And the cure is that you must examine if there is a hot abscess, and put rosy oil or hen's egg yolk on the spine until it is soothed.
puis met sus un des emplaustres confortans et sechans, et le lie d’un liien, et comande au malaide a reposer;	then apply one of the comforting and drying poultices, and bind it with a bandage, and instruct the patient to rest.
et ne dorme mie sus celle partie ou il sent la dolor, tant k’il soit sanez.	and not to sleep on the painful part until it is healed.
Et se aucuns os se dessevre, si covient coper sus lou keur;	And if any bone is dislocated, it must be put back in place;
et oste l’os, puis assemble les II levres de la plaie, s’elle est grans, a une costure, puis le cure d’oignement enjanrant char, tant qu’il soit sanez;	remove the bone, then bring together the two lips of the wound, if it is large, with one stitch, then the doctor should treat it with ointment and bandages until it is healed;
et se li chiés de l’os est brisiez, ki est apelez li «chiés de la kowe», se i boute ton pouchet de ta main senestre, et le met igal a l’autre main a ton pooir, puis met l’emplaustre et l’estele sus, se tu en a mestier;	and if the head of the bone is broken, which is called the "head of the cow", put your left hand over it and your right hand underneath it, then apply the poultice and bandage it if necessary.
puis l’estraint, et s’il i a os desevreit, si fent sus, et l’oste, et cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit sanee.	then they bind it, and if there is bone exposed, they cover it with skin and then the wound is healed until it is cured.
de la brisure de l’os de la hainche	of the fracture of the hip bone
Poc avient que li os de la hainche soit brisiez, et s’il avient, si n’avient fuer c’un poc d’amenuisement au chief;	It rarely happens that the hip bone is broken, and if it does, there will be little thinning at the head.
et fent dou lonc, et decline au pardedens, et vient au malaide dolor au leu, et pointure, et enfle ceu que brise.	And they make it long, and decline towards the buttocks, and comes to the patient's pain in the area, and piercing, and swelling where it is broken.
Et li restoration si est que tu estendes ta main sus, tant que tu soies sus la briseure;	And its restoration is that you extend your hand over it, as far as you can reach the break;
et saiches quelz est li brisure et li figure de li;	and know which is the break and its shape;
et se li brisure est au chief soulement, si met igal cele brisure, tant qu’ele soit a figure natureil.	and if the break is only at the head, put it in place so that the break is even and the joint is in its natural shape.
Et se li brisure est dou lonc, ou elle decline au dedens, si fai gesir le malaide sus son ventre, tant que li restauration de cele brisure te soit aparillie.	If the fracture is long, or if it slopes downward, have the patient lie on his stomach until the healing of that fracture is prepared for.
Et quant tu l’avras mise igal, si met sus l’emplaustre, puis met sus une estele de fust ou de keur, et estraint la briseure, si qu’ele ne se mueve;	And when you have put it in place, apply the ointment, then put on a splint of wood or horn and bind the break so that it does not move;
et emple le leu desoz les costes, tant que li lieure soit igalz.	and employ the cautery underneath the ribs, until the skin is even.
Et comande au malaide k’il dorme sus son costeit sain, ou sus son dos.	And instruct the patient to sleep on his healthy side, or on his back.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si n’i tochier, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et met sus ceu que nos avons devant dit;	And if a boil comes, do not touch it, until the boil has subsided, and apply what we have mentioned before;
et puis revien a la restauration, et l’estraint si com il covient, s’il n’i a nul mavais accident;	and then return to healing, and restrain it as appropriate, if there is no bad incident;
et c’est li maniere.	and that's the way it is.
de la brisure de l’ajutoire	of the dislocation of the shoulder
Li adjutoires est ceu qui est entre lou coute et lou chief de l’espaule, et s’il est brisiez, si le doit on restorer selonc l’une des II manieres:	The shoulder joint is what is between the elbow and the head of the shoulder, and if it is dislocated, it should be restored according to one of two methods:
dont l’une est que tu pren I fust plain de moiene groissor, selonc ceste forme:	one of which is to take a plain staff of medium thickness, according to this form:
Et lie as II chiés II liens, et les pent en haut, et siece li malaide sus I siege;	And tie the two ends together, and hold them upright, and seat the patient on a bench;
puis li giete som bras brisiet sus le fust, tant qu’il viegne a l’aissele, et ait em mi une corbeure de fust, puis pent sus aucune pesant chose ou li ministres l’estende aval;	then let him swing his broken arm over the staff, until he reaches the bottom, and have a curve in the staff, then lean over some heavy object or have the minister hold it down below;
puis mette li mires la briseure igal a ses mains ensamble, tant que li briseure retorne si com il covient.	then place the splint on the fracture evenly with his hands together, until the fracture returns as it should.
Et li autre maniere si est que on sovine le malaide sus son hatereil, et li lie la main a son col, puis comande a .ij. ministres que li uns teigne ceu qui est sus la briseure a ses mains, et li autres teigne desoz a tout .i. liien, et estende chescuns a sa partie.	And the other method is to have the patient lean on his elbow, and tie his hand to his neck; then have one minister hold what is above the dislocation in their hands, and the other minister hold beneath the dislocation, at each end of the rod, and stretch each end in opposite directions.
Et se tu vues que li estraction soit plus fors, si estraint I liien desoz la briseure, et sus la briseure, et estende chescuns des ministres a sa part.	And if you want the extraction to be more thorough, then tighten the ligature below the fracture, and above it as well, and each assistant must do their part.
Et se li briseure est prochiene au chief de l’espaule, si covient que tu mettes I liien moien desoz l’assele, et I autre vers lou coute, desoz la briseure;	And if the fracture is near the head of the shoulder, you should place one strap underneath the armpit and the other towards the neck, underneath the fracture.
et ausi se li briseure est devers lou coute, si i covient mettre I liien legierement, sens labor, tant que li briseure soit igalz sus lou leu, et sus lou coute;	And if the fracture is towards the neck, then one strap should be placed lightly and gently, without labor, so that the fracture is aligned with its place, and with the neck.
puis met igal la brisure, si com il covient, et l’estraint, se apostemes chaus n’i vient.	Then align the fracture as it should be, and bind it, if no abscess comes of it.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si ne l’estraindre mie jusc’a VII jors, et met sus lainne moillie en aisil et en oile roset, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez;	And if a swollen abscess comes of it, then do not bind it for 7 days, but place soft wool in vinegar and rose oil on the swollen abscess until it is soothed.
puis l’estraint, et li maniere de l’estraindre si est que tu mettes l’emplaustre sus la briseure, puis assemble le bras sus l’ajutoire, et met ta main sus l’espaule ou sus lou sein;	then you must restrain it, and the way to restrain it is to apply the ointment to the fracture, then assemble the arm onto the shoulder, and place your hand on the shoulder or the chest;
et met le drapeil, et estraint sus l’ajutoire, et sus lou bras, si que li bras soit en leu d’esteles, s’aucune chose ne le te deffent, ou se li os n’est muez.	and apply the bandage, and restrain it onto the shoulder and arm, so that the arm is held in place, unless something dislocates it or the bones move.
Et se tu doutes que li os ne se mueve, si use d’esteles, et met sus la brisure une estele plus large et plus fort des autres, et ait entre chescune estele I doi d’espaice, et soit chescune estele si grans qu’elle passe la briseure III dois de chescune part;	And if you fear that the bones will move, use splints, and place a larger and stronger splint over the fracture, and have two inches of space between each splint, and make each splint large enough so that it extends three inches on each side of the fracture;
puis estrain sus les esteles, ensi com j’ai dit au comencement dou chapistre sus la briseure, plus fort et moins en aloignant.	then restrain over the splints, as I said at the beginning of the chapter about the fracture, more strongly and less widely.
Et se tu vois l’assise des esteles, et l’estrignement, si com nos avons dit, en l’oure que tu restoures le membre brisiet, et tu doutes l’aposteme chaut, si le laisse a liier jusc’a septime jor, si com nos avons dit;	And if you see the position of the stars and the constriction, as we have said, in the hour that you restore the broken member, and you doubt the hot abscess, then let it be bound until the seventh day, as we have said.
puis regarde chescuns III jors lou lien, que prurite ne enfleure n’i viegne au leu, ou li norrissemens ne puist venir au membre por ceu k’il est trop estrois.	Then examine the bandages every three days to ensure no itching or swelling occurs, and that no pus can reach the member due to it being too tight.
Si l’adrece, si com nos avons dit.	If the abscess, as we have said.
Et se nulz telz accidens n’i vient, si ne lou desliier fuer que aprés III jors ou plus, et dorme li malaides sus son dos, et ait ses mains sus son stomac;	And if no such accidents occur, then remove the bandages after three days or more, and let the patient sleep on his back, with his hands on his stomach;
et met desoz l’ajutoire I cussin plain de laine igalment, et regarde chescune houre dou jor ou de la nut, que li figure dou membre brisiet ne se mueve, ou ne soit amollis li liiens;	and place underneath the shoulder a plain woolen pillow evenly, and examine every hour of the day or night that the broken member does not move, nor the bandages become soft.
si l’adrece par la vertu de medicine, et li done la viande que nos avons devant mis, en teil maniere que li viande soit au premier subtilz;	if he is treated with medicine, and is given the food we have previously mentioned, in such a way that the food reaches the subtlest parts.
et quant il comance a reprendre, si soit grosse.	and when he begins to recover, then it should be thick.
Et est costume que li ajutoire et li jambe doient estre repris en XL jors dou tout;	And it is customary for the shoulder and leg to take forty days to heal completely;
et adonques lou doit on desliier et aministrer bain et medicines d’oignemens por le leu adrecier.	and then one should loosen and administer baths and medicated oils to help it heal.
Et se li estricture est laide et emboee, si demore a desliier L jors ou II mois.	And if the dislocation is severe and stuck, it remains to be released for 50 days or two months.
de la brisure du bras	of the breaking of the arm
Li bras est compos de II os, qui sont apelez li dui «foscile», de coi li uns est petis, et est cil qui enseut le pouchet;	The arm is composed of two bones, which are called the two "foscile", one of which is small and is the one that follows the armpit;
et li autres est grans, et est cil qui est desoz, devers lou petit doi;	and the other is large, and is the one that is underneath, towards the little finger;
par aventure brise li grans foscile soulement, ou li petis, et par aventure andui ensamble.	by chance, only the large foscile may be broken, or only the small one, or both together.Si li chiés de l’ajutoire est desaloiez par cause de moistor, et on le remet a leu, et il n’i
Quant li petis fosciles est brisiez, li restaurations est legiere, et li sanations;	When the small bones are broken, their restoration is easy, and so is their healing.
et quant li grans est brisiez, si est li sanation male, et plus griés que quant il sont brisiez andui ensamble.	And when the large bones are broken, their healing is difficult, and more painful than when they are broken all at once.
Se c’est li petis foscile qui est brisiez soulement, si le covient poc estendre legierement, et mettre igal.	If it is only a small bone that is broken, then one must extend it slightly and put it in place.And if a large bone is broken, one should not extend it too much, but put it in its place with a little extension.
Et se c’est li grans foscile, si le covient estraindre plus fort;	And if it is a large bone, one must pull harder;
et l’estende sus I cussin, et teigne le pouchet de la main plus haut des autres, et li petis dois plus bas des autres dois, et soit li malaides croisiez sus lui meisme, et I cussin devant lui plus haut, que li malaides ne soffre nule labor;	and stretch him out on a pillow, and raise the pouch of his hand higher than the others, and the little fingers lower than the other fingers, and have the patient cross himself over his chest, and the pillow in front of him higher so that the patient does not suffer any strain;
puis estende li ministres som bras a la partie desoz a sa main, ou a I liien, et uns autres ministres a I autre au desus.	Then extend the minister's right arm to the part below his hand, or to the armpit, and another minister to the other side above.
Et puis le mette li mires igal, selonc sa millor forme.	And then put the bandages on evenly, according to its best form.
Et se en la brisure a pieces, si met chescune en son leu, et s’il en i a nule desevree ke poigne lou keur, et tu ne la pues restorer en son leu, si fent sus et l’oste, si com nos avons dit devant.	And if the bone has broken into pieces, place each one in its proper position; and if any have become dislocated, and you cannot restore them to their places, then cut through the bone, as we have described earlier.
Et se avec la briseure a plaie, je en ai parleit au chapistre singuler;	And if with the break there is a wound, I have spoken about it in a particular chapter;
si pren la cure.	if one takes the remedy.
Et se en l’encomencement dou restorement sorvient apostemes chaus, si glue I drapeil de cerote fait d’oile roset et de cire blainche, que ne soit mie ne trop durs ne trop molz;	And if in the beginning of the restoration, abscesses occur, then apply a plaster made from rosin oil and white wax, not too hard or too soft.
et lie I drapeil par sus subtilment, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez.	and apply the plaster gently, until the abscesses are soothed.
Et puis oste lou cerote, et i met l’emplaustre de la poudre dou molin avec abun d’uef, pues met les esteles, et soit li estele de la briseure adés plus fors, et un poc plus large que les autres;	Then remove the plaster, and apply the ointment made from mill powder with egg white, then put on the bandages, and let the bandage of the fracture be a bit stronger, and a little larger than the others;
et saiches que il doit avoir VI esteles ou bras em plusors dispositions:	and know that he must have six bandages on his arm in various places:
soit que li briseure soit en l’un des os, soit en II;	whether the fracture is in one or two bones;
et estraint plus sus la briseure que autre part, et toz jors moins en aloignant, si com j’ai dit au comencement dou chapistre;	and tighten more over the fracture than elsewhere, and always lessen it as I said at the beginning of the chapter;
et soient li drapelz que sont sus la briseure molz et moistes, et ne soient mie dur ne aspres;	and let the bandages which are on the broken bone be soft and moist, and not hard nor rough;
et soit li filz, dont il est estrains, de lin, ne trop gros ne trop menus, si com nos avons dit.	and let the thread, with which it is bound, be of flax, neither too thick nor too fine, as we have said.
Et rewarde lou membre et lou liien aprés aucuns jors.	And re-examine the limb and the joint after a few days.
Et se aucuns mavais accidens vient au membre, si com prurite ki vient au membre, si covient que tu aroses lou membre d’aigue chaude, tant que cil prurites soit apaisiez;	And if any bad accident comes to the limb, such as itching coming to the limb, then you must moisten the limb with warm water until those itches are relieved;
et laisse le membre ne mie estroit reposer.	and let the limb not be bound tightly so that it can rest.
Et puis rencomence l’estrignement, et se li liiens est amolis et li os desevrez, et semblant chose, si l’adresce.	And then renew the binding, and if the ligaments are relaxed and the bones dislocated, and similar things, then correct it.
Et se pren warde se li norrissemens ne puet venir au membre, por ceu qu’il est trop estrois, si covient que tu l’amollisses .i. poc, et laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant que li norrissemens i corre, et puis l’estraint.	And if one must guard against the nutrients not being able to reach the member because it is too bound up, then one must loosen it a little and leave it thus for some days, until the nutrients flow to it, and then bind it again.
Et se nules de ces choses que nos avons dit ne vient au malaide, si ne lou desliier jusc’a XX jors.	And if none of these things that we have said happens to the patient, then do not loosen it for 20 days.
ou enqui entor, puis li pent les mains a son col, et soit ses cols igalz, et se warde de movement et de degitement, et dorme sus son dos;	or twist around, then he can hold his hands to his neck, and let his neck be straight, and guard against movement and dislocation, and sleep on his back;
et saiches que ceste briseure est restoree en XXX jors ou en XXXV, et par aventure en XX jors, selonc les compositions et les complexions des vertus.	and know that this dislocation is restored in 30 days or 35, and perhaps in 20 days, according to the compositions and complexes of the virtues.
de la brisure de la main	of the fracture of the hand
Saiches que au dos de la main et as nous des dois avient poc de briseures, et n’i vient mais que ploieure maintes fois.	Know that in the back of the hand and on the fingers there are few fractures, and they only come from many foldings.
Et quant li plante de la main est brisie ou ploie, si covient que li malaides siece croisiet, et siet droitement devant lui igalement;	And when the palm of the hand is broken or bent, then the patient should cut a cross in it and sit upright in front of him evenly.
puis met sa main sus la toie estendue, et estende li ministres les os brisiez, et les mete igalz li mires, tant qu’il soient bien joint;	then put his hand on the extended towel, and extend the broken bones, and make them equal with the other bones, so that they are well-joined.
et met l’emplastre et les estoupes, se apostemes n’i vient, puis i met une estele selonc la quantiteit dou leu;	and put on a poultice and bandages, if an abscess does not come, then he puts on a plaster according to the quantity of the wound.
et soit envoloupee en I drapeil de lin.	and it should be wrapped in a linen cloth.
Et se li briseure est au pardedens entor lou ventre de la plante, si fai une spere de drapelz, et comande au malaide qu’il l’estrigne a sa plante brisie;	And if the break is around the palm, towards the belly, then make a ball of cloth, and instruct the patient to press it against the broken palm.
et puis l’estrain d’un lonc drapeil, et soit li estele de keur souef ausi grans com li plante de la main, et l’estraint, si com il covient.	And then he pulls on a long cloth, and the splint should be of cured pig's skin as large as the palm of the hand, and he applies it, as it should be.
Et se li brisure est au defuer, si covient que tu mettes une estele sus, et une autre desoz en la plante, si que li mains soit overte et droite, puis le lie tot entor la main, et estanche lou liien entre les dois.	And if the fracture is in the forearm, you must put a splint on top and another underneath the plant, so that the hand is open and straight, then bind it all around the hand, and stop the bleeding between the two.
Et se li briseure vient a aucun des nous des dois, se c’est li pouchés, si le met igal, si com il covient;	And if the dislocation comes to us on one of our arms, if it is the shoulder, then we set it straight, as it should be.
et l’estraint avec la plante, et se tu vues si met une estele droite petite por lever la briseure, et ne se mueve;	and hold it with your palm, and if you see [it], put a small, straight splint to raise the dislocation, and do not move it;
et se li brisure est as autres dois, si com en l’indice ou l’un des autres, si le met igal, et lou lie avec lou doi sain qui est aprés;	and if the dislocation is in the other arms, such as in the index or one of the others, then we set it straight and bind it with the healthy arm that is next to it;
ou tu les lie toz en I tenant, que mues vaut, ou tu met sus une estele, si com ou pouchet;	or you bind them both in the same way, holding them still, or you put a splint on it, as on the shoulder;
et pren warde en la restauration et en la disposition d’aposteme chaut, et secor ceu qui i vient, si com j’ai dit.	and take care in the restoration and the preparation of a hot abscess, and treat that which comes to it, as I have said.
de la cuixe brisie	of the broken thigh
Li os de la cuixe est maintes fois brisiez, et bien le voit on quant elle torne devant et derrier;	The thigh bone is often broken, and one can easily see this when it turns forward and backward;
et li restauration si est c’on lie I liien desus la briseure, et I autre desoz.	and the restoration is to tie one above the fracture, and the other below.
Et li malaides gise sus sa faice, puis estende chescuns ministres son lien a sa part igalment;	And the patient lies on his face, then each minister stretches their band to their part equally;
et c’est quant li brisure est emmi l’os.	and that is when the fracture is in the bone.
Et se li brisure est prochiene a la racine de la cuixe, si soit li uns des liiens devers lou poignil, et li autres liiens desoz la briseure.	And if the fracture is close to the root of the thigh, let one ligature be towards the armpit, and the other ligatures below the fracture.
Et ausi s’elle est prochiene au genoil, et adonques soit li liens delez lou genoil, et soit li extension aval;	And also if it is close to the knee, then the band should be below the knee, and the extension should be upwards;
puis mette li mires l’os igal a ses II mains, tant qu’il soit selonc sa figure natureil, et puis met l’emplaustre, et lou lie, se apostemes chaz n’i vient.	then put the splint on the bone evenly with his two hands, so that it is in its natural position, and then apply the ointment and the bandage, unless pus comes out.If the fracture is in the arm near the elbow: then put one band above the elbow, and the other below, and extend upwards; then put the splint on the bone evenly with his two hands, so that it is in its natural position, and then apply the ointment and the bandage, unless pus comes out.
Et s’il i a aposteme chaut, si le laisse apaisier puis revien a ton ovraige et a ta cure;	And if there is a hot abscess, let it calm down first, then return to your work and treatment;
li lieure est faite en teil maniere.	It is made in this way.
Il covient que tu envoloupes sus la briseure I bendeil dur doublé en II ou III, et en demoure li superfluitez, puis torne la jambe tant que li talons veigne a la racine de la naige, et boute I fil lonc entre la cuixe et la jambe, delez lou genoil desoz, et veignent li chief dou fil au desus;	You must wrap the broken bone with a long strip of thick linen, and tie it tightly, then bring the leg so that the heel touches the root of the thigh, and push a long needle between the thigh and the leg, below the knee, and let the end of the thread come out at the top;
puis torne sus la jambe et sus la cuixe le bendeil, puis met sus la briseure esteles, et met une estele sus l’os de la jambe;	then wrap the bandage around the leg and thigh, then place splints over the fracture, and put a splint on the shinbone of the leg;
puis emple le leu vuit entre la jambe et la cuixe de drapelz souef por mettre igal l’estrignement, puis comence a liier forment III tors ou IIII sus la briseure;	then fill the space between the leg and thigh with soft cloth to even out the pressure, then begin by tying three or four knots over the fracture;
et quant plus vas en sus de la briseure, et moins l’estraint;	and as you go higher above the fracture, tighten it less;
puis enten as II chiés dou fil que tu as bouteit entre la jambe et la cuixe, et en lie III esteles que sont desus, puis revai au desoz au chief dou fil, tant que tu veignes delez le piet;	then tighten the two ends of the thread that you pushed between the leg and thigh, and tie three splints that are above it, then go back down to the end of the thread, until you reach the foot;
et l’estraint, si qu’il ne se mueve de son leu, puis le laisse ensi, puis k’il n’i vient ne aposteme ne enfleure n’autre semblant.	and hold it so that it does not move from its place, then let it be thus, until no abscess or swelling or similar occurs.
Et s’il i avient, si le deslie, et adresce ceu que i vient, si com nos avons dit maintes fois;	And if something happens, dislocate and address what is happening, as we have said many times;
et se il i a pieces de l’os que poigne, si le covient ewer, s’om puet;	and if there are pieces of bone that prick, they should be removed, if possible;
et s’on ne puet, si covient fendre le leu, et traire fuer;	and if not, the place should be split and the bone pulled out;
et le cure si com nos avons dit, tant k’il soit sanez.	and the wound treated as we have said, until it is healed.
Et aucune fois est brisie li cuixe ensi c’on i met esteles, si com en l’ajutoire et ou bras;	And sometimes the thigh is dislocated thus when a staff is placed against it, as in the shoulder and arm;
toutevoie, en la restauration ensi faite ne cloche mie li malaides.	Nevertheless, this restoration does not help the ailment.Et li remede de cest chapistre est de le deslieer et de le retreire, et de l’estrecier
Et saiches que li cuixe est restoree en .l. jors, ou poc moins ou poc plus, selonc les diversitez des complexions.	And you shall know that the neck is restored in one day, or a little less or more, according to the variety of complexions.
de la ruelle dou genoil	of the fold of the knee
Saiches que en la ruelle dou genoil avient poc brisure, mais elle ploie maintes fois.	Know that in the bend of the knee there is little breaking, but it bends many times.
Et s’elle brise, si n’est mais c’une fendure, ou I pertus, et avient a tout plaie, et sens plaie, et ce sent om bien.	And if it breaks, then there is only a crack or an opening, and it happens to everyone, with or without pain, and it feels good to all.
Et li restauration si est c’on mette igal ceu qui est rons a ses dois, tant qu’il soit assemblez mues c’on puet;	And the restoration is to dislocate and draw it out, and hold it tightly until it is set in place, as one puts fingers together, as far as one can;
puis met l’emplaustre, et i met une estele reonde, se tu en as mestier, et l’estraint si com il covient, puis rewarde toutes les dispositions que nos avons dit ens autres briseures, si com aposteme chaut et autre semblant;	then apply the plaster, and place a round pad on top if necessary, and hold it in place as needed. Then follow all the instructions we have given for other fractures, such as hot abscesses and similar conditions.
si met a chescun accident ceu k’il li covient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	he should use whatever is appropriate for each condition until the patient is healed.
de la brisure de la jambe	of the fracture of the leg
Saiches que en la jambe ait II os, de coi li uns est apelez par droit non «mustelz», et li autres est apelez «foscile»;	Know that in the leg there are two bones, one of which is properly called the "mustel" and the other the "foscile";
et avient tout auteil briseure com il vient au bras, et por ceu est li restauracion si com celle dou bras igalment, et li ovraiges est tout i. Et se li dui os sont brisiet ensamble, si torne li jambe de toutes pars.	and all other fractures occur in the leg as they do in the arm, and the treatment is the same. If both bones are broken at the same time, then the leg turns completely inside out.
Et se li os subtilz est brisiez, si torne devant.	And if only the small bones are broken, it turns forward.
Et se li gros os est brisiez, si sent on grant dolor, et le voit on bien;	And if the large bone is broken, one feels great pain and it can be seen clearly;
et torne desoz.	and it turns inside out.
Adonques amenistre extension, et le met igal, et lie les esteles igalement;	Therefore, apply traction and make it even, and tie the bandages evenly.
mais toutevoie, il covient se li brisure est laide, et il i a plusors pieces, que li extension soit menor et plus legiere;	However, if the fracture is ugly, and there are several pieces, then the traction should be milder and gentler.
et l’alige selonc ta vertu.	and apply it according to your ability.
Et quant tu as tout acomplit ton ovraige, si pren II faixes de fust chevees que porpreignent la jambe d’une part et d’autre, et soient dou lonc de la jambe des le genoil jusque desoz;	And when you have finished your work, take two bundles of wood shavings that reach from one side of the leg to the other, and let them be as long as the leg from the knee down to just below it.
puis envoloupe en II leus I bendeil desus et desoz, et le lie em mileu ausi, et a ceste lieure ne pora li jambe decliner a destre ne a senestre, et ensi est bien;	Then wrap two bands around it above and below, and tie it in the middle as well. At this point, the leg will not be able to decline to the right or left, and thus it is good.
et aucun i aministrent I bers dou lonc de la jambe, et s’est de fust, et i met on la jambe por warder de movement, et proprement fait on ceu en la brisure ou il a plaie;	And some use a bed as long as the leg, and it is made of wood, and they put the leg in it to guard against movement, and they carefully do this at the site of the injury.
et remue chescun jor la jambe, por veoir s’il i a aposteme chaut n’autre accident;	and move the leg each day to see if there is a hot abscess or other incident;
si le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	until it is healed.
de la brisure des os dou piet	of the break of the bones of the foot
A la cheville ne vient point de brisure, mais as os dou piet vient aucune fois brisure et as dois poc, et n’i avient fuer que quassure em plusor dispositions.	At the ankle there is no break, but sometimes there is a break in the bones of the foot and in both feet, and there is only bruising in various ways.
Et s’il avient as os dou piet brisure, et tu vois ces os sormonter l’un l’autre, si mette si malaides som piet sus la terre, ausi com s’il voloit aler, et puis met maintenant ton piet sus lou sien, lai ou li os sont levez, puis le presse tant k’il reveignent en lor leus;	And if it happens that there is a break in the bone of the foot, and you see the bones sticking out, then put the patient's foot on the ground, as if he wanted to walk, and then put your foot on his, where the bones are protruding, and then press until they return to their place;
puis met l’emplaustre et estoupes sus, et met desoz lou ventre dou piet une petite tauble a II chiés plains, puis l’estraint au piet avenanment, puis que tu as envoloupez drapelz entor, et autres choses dont tu as mestier.	then apply the ointment and bandages on top, and place a small wooden board with two flat sides underneath the foot's belly, then tighten it to the foot comfortably, then wrap cloth around it, and other things that you need.
Et quant .iij. jors ou .iiij. seront passez, si deslie lou liien, car tu troveras les os igalz, soient brisiez, soient desaluez.	And after three or four days have passed, loosen the bandage, for you will find that the bones are healed, whether broken or dislocated.
Et s’il i a aucuns des dois brisiez, si les restoure, si com nos avons dit as dois de la main;	And if any of the fingers are broken, restore them as we have said for the fingers of the hand;
puis met au doi brisiet une estele selonc la longesce dou doi, et soit un poc plus large, puis met desoz le piet celle tauble que j’ai dit, et l’estrain avenanment;	then put a splint on the broken bone according to the length of the bone, and make it a little wider, then put under the foot that table which I have said, and tighten it conveniently;
et s’il en i a II ou III, ou plus, brisiez, si met sus chescun doi une estele selonc sa quantiteit, envoloupee en I drapeil de lin, et estraint la tauble desoz lou piet;	and if there are two or three, or more, broken, then put on each bone a splint according to its quantity, wrapped in a linen cloth, and tighten the table under the foot;
et soit estans sus lou chief de la tauble defuer lou ventre dou piet, si qu’il le teigne bien.	and let there be a projection on the top of the table to press against the belly of the foot, so that it holds it well.
Et covient que tu n’oblier mie les autres choses que j’ai dit as autres briseures, des que nos avons dit;	And you must not forget the other things which I have said about other fractures, from what we have already said;
et secor chescun accident si com il covient.	and treat each accident as it should be treated.
de la brisure de l’os dou poignil	of the fracture of the bone of the finger
Quant li os de la nature la femme est brisiez, si la fai seoir enlargie, puis l’encline a la partie dou dos, et soit tenue par derrier;	When the bones of the woman's nature are broken, then make her sit upright, then lean her towards the side of the back, and hold her from behind;
puis emplisse li baile la nature de la malaide de couton, et en i mette ausi gros com I sto;	then fill the ball with the nature of the cotton disease, and put in it as much as a thumb;
puis deboute la femme, et lieve lou dos poc et poc, et adonques saut li coton, tant qu’il vient a l’entree de la nature, et revient li os avec lou sto;	then stand the woman up, and gently poke her back a little bit, and then the cotton will jump, until it comes to the entrance of the nature, and the bone will return with the thumb;
et quant elle vuet pissier, si oste lou coton, et quant elle a pissiet, se li remette, et ensi faice VII jors ou entor:	and when she wants to urinate, take out the cotton, and when she has urinated, put it back in, and do this for 7 days or so;
si sera restoree li brisure, et se tu vues, pren une vessie de berbis, et lie au pertus une cainne, et boute toute la vessie en la nature;	then the fracture will be restored, and if you wish, take a sheep's bladder, and tie it at the opening with a string, and fill the entire bladder into the nature;
puis soffle en la cainne forment, tant que li vessie soit enflee dedens:	then blow into the string until the bladder is inflated inside;
la nature si revenra li brisure;	the nature will then restore the fracture;
puis soit emplie de coton, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant qu’il soit sanez.	then it should be filled with cotton and left like that for a few days until it is healed.
Et quant li os dou poignil de l’ome est brisiez, ou de la femme, si le restoure ensi com nos avons dit en l’os de la hainche;	And when the bone of the man's or woman's elbow is broken, restore it as we have said for the bone of the hip;
et ne sont mie occultees ces briseures prochienes a celui qui i met son estude et son us, et entent mon livre.	and these breaks are not concealed from those who devote themselves to its study and practice, and understand my book.
Car li brisure li signifie em plusors dispositions la droite voie de la restauration:	For the breaks indicate in many ways the correct path to restoration:
enten le donques.	Understand them therefore.
En la verge, quant elle est brisie, pren une gorge d’oie et i boute la verge;	In a bone that is broken, take a goose's throat and insert it into the bone;
puis envoloupe drapelz entor, et le laisse III jors ou enqui entor, et il sera sanez hastanment.	then wrap cloth around it, and leave it for three days or more, and it will be healed quickly.
de brisure avec plaie	of fracture with wound
Il covient a celui qui a brisure avec plaie, meismement s’elle est grans, si com li os de la cuixe ou de l’ajutoire ou semblant, qu’il soit sainiez maintenant, si que les sainies que nos avons dit le tesmoignent.	It is necessary for one who has a fracture with wound, especially if it is large, such as the thigh or shoulder bone or similar, that he be bled immediately, in accordance with the bleeding we have described earlier.
Et se li plaie saine, si la restainche de vitriole, se tu n’as autre chose, puis rencomence a restorer la briseure en cele meisme houre, ou celui jor, se apostemes chaus n’i vient.	And if the wound bleeds, then add vitriol again, if you have nothing else; then reset the fracture in that same hour or day, if no abscesses form.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si laisse la restauration jusc’a nuevime jor, tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez, et n’i touchier ne au tier jor ne au quart, car tu i feroies venir malvais accident.	And if abscesses form, then wait until the third day to reset the fracture, as long as the abscesses are subsiding; do not touch them on the second or fourth day, for you would cause a dangerous accident.
Et se li os brisiez est aparans sus lou keur descovert, si covient que tu lou mettes a point legierement a tes mains, a extension petite.	And if the broken bone is visible beneath the uncovered chest, you should gently place it in its proper position with your hands, with a slight extension.
Et se li extensions ne t’est apareillie por mettre igal a tes mains, si le ramoine a cest estrument qui est de fer, qui a VII dois ou VIII de lonc, et li largesce est selonc la quantiteit de la plaie;	And if the dislocation does not appear to you in order to put it equal to your hands, then reset it with this instrument made of iron, which is seven or eight inches long, and its width depends on the size of the wound;
et por ceu est mestier au mire qu’il empreigne III ou IIII, selonc ceu qu’il en ait mestier en chescune cure de briseure;	and therefore it is necessary for the surgeon to take three or four stitches, depending on what he needs in each case of fracture.
et soit rons et un poc gros, k’il ne ploie mie a la compression sus lou membre a ton ovraige, et soit agus devant, et gros des le mileu en avant, ensi:	Let it be round and slightly thick, so that it does not bend when you press on the limb while doing your work, and let it be sharp at the end, and thick from the middle towards the front, thus:
Et est apelez «palainche», por coi il covient que li chiés corbes soit mis sus lou chief de l’os apparent;	It is called a 'splint', so that it is necessary to put the curved side on top of the protruding bone.
et le boute a une fois, tant k’il reviegne, et soit igalz l’un encontre l’autre.	And when you wrap it once around, do so until it fits tightly, and let one end be even with the other.
Et se li brisure est subtilz, et li estrumens ne puet bien prendre l’os, si covient que tu copes lou chief de l’os, tant que li estrumens en ait possance.	And if the break is small and the instrument cannot well grasp the bone, you must pare the head of the bone so that the instrument can hold it firmly.Et se li os ne vout point demorer a son leu, si convint que tu l’estrenges tant qu’il soit en son leu et en sa possance; car en ce cas ne peuit li membres valer.
Et se tu ne pues ramener l’os, si com nos avons dit, si lou cope d’un estrument covenable a ceu, ou incisoire ou soieure, a ton pooir;	And if you cannot reset the bone as we have said, then use an appropriate tool, either a knife or a saw, at your discretion;
puis reis ceu qui est demorez en l’os d’aspreteit et de menues escorces.	then remove what remains in the bone of splinters and small fragments.Et si li os sont trop fenduers ou trop rompus, si convenable est que tu les brises, et si li estres de l’un et l’autre ne s’entrecongnissent mie
Et quant li os est ramenez, et li malaides sent grant dolor aprés, saiches qu’il n’est mie en son leu natureil.	And when the bone is reset, and the patient feels great pain afterward, know that it is not in its natural place.
Si fai tant qu’il soit en son leu, puis moille I drapeil en vin stiptique noir, et proprement se c’est en esteit;	Do this until it is in its place, then moisten the cloth with black wine vinegar, and cleanse if necessary.
et ne mettre mie sus la plaie cerote ne autre chose ou il ait oile, qu’il n’i faice venir porriture et corruption;	and do not put ointment or anything else on the wound that would cause pus and corruption;
puis aministre esteles quant tu as restoreit l’os, et laisse la plaie descoverte, et cope la coverture tout entor, selonc la quantiteit de la plaie, et te done bien en garde que li plaie ne soit estrainte avec la brisure;	then administer bandages when you have reset the bone, and leave the wound uncovered, and wrap the covering all around according to the size of the wound, and be careful that the wound is not restricted by the dressing;
et maintes fois ont ce fait li fol mire, et ont fait venir sus le malaide ou mort ou corrodent aucune fois;	and many times they have done this with foolishness, causing corruption or death in some cases;
et soit li estrignemens plus molz et plus souef des autres brisures.	and it is the most delicate and soft of all dislocations.
Et se li plaie est male ou grans, et tu doutes que mavais accidens n’i veigne, si com nos avons dit, et tu trueves dolor au leu, si n’i covient mie mettre sus esteles;	And if the wound is large and you doubt that a bad accident may occur as we have said, and you find pain in the area, then you should not put bandages on it;
mais envoloupe entor, en leu d’esteles, drapelz durs, et les lie.	but wrap around, instead of a pillow, hard, folded cloths, and tie them.
Et quant tu vois aprés I jor ou II enjanrer bowe a la plaie, si oste ceu que tu as mis sus a tout vin, et i met oignement sanant plaies, si com oignement tetrafarmaçon et semblans.	And when you see after one or two days that the wound is puffed up, then remove what you have put on it and apply healing ointment, such as tetrapharmacon and similar.
Et covient que tu deslies lou membre .ij. fois le jor, lou matin et au vespre, tant qu’il soit soudez et sanez.	And you should loosen the limb twice a day, in the morning and at evening, until it is healed and closed.
Et covient que li membres soit aparilliez en teil maniere que li bowe corre aval legierement.	And it is necessary for the limb to be prepared in such a way that the bowstring runs downhill easily.
Et se maint jor trespassent, et il ne puet souder mais rent adés bowe, saiches k’il i a petites pieces d’os, por coi il covient que tu quieres la plaie avec tente, et oste toutes ces pieces desevrees que font venir celle dolor.	And if they remain for many days, and it cannot be souded but keeps returning apart, know that there are small pieces of bone causing this, so you should probe the wound with a probe and remove all these displaced pieces that cause the pain.
Et se fistule vient au leu, ou autre maniere de corruption, si covient que tu le cures, selonc ceu qu’il dist en son chapistre ci devant.	And if a fistula comes to the surface, or any other kind of corruption, then you should treat it according to what he said in his chapter above.
Et quant li os est brisiez, et apert sus lou membre, si com li os de la cuixe ou de l’ajutoire, et autres semblans des grans membres, si ne le traire mie, car maintes fois en vient li mors, mais le laisse tant qu’il porrisse;	And when the bone is broken and exposed on the limb, as in the thigh or shoulder, and other similar large limbs, do not draw it out, but leave it alone until it can be pulled out;
par aventure cherra par lui aprés XX jors ou XXX, puis cure la plaie, se tu pues;	perhaps it will fall out after 20 or 30 days, then cure the wound if you can;et s’il ne puet chiere, si trais li os entor qu’il soit apertes, et metes entor
et se tu ne pues, si la laisse.	and if it cannot be pulled out, then cut the bone around so that it is exposed, and put in
des brus qui vienent sor la sodure	of bruises that come after healing:
Nous vienent maintes fois aprés la santeit de la briseure, meismement quant c’est pres de la jointure, et laide chose est a veoir li figure dou membre;	Many times after the healing of the fracture, especially when it is near the joint, and an ugly sight is the shape of the limb;et quant li os traie sus li membre, si metes entor de l’erbe c’est-a-savoir, sanz rime ne mesure, car il est hardi et n’est pas de nature.
et par aventure ne puet faire li membres ses ovraiges naturelz.	and sometimes cannot perform its natural functions.
Pren warde donques se li nous est fres:	So take care then, if we are wise:
si li aministre medicines stiptiques, si com aloes, encens, et mirre, et sarcocolle, acaice, et semblans autres, ensi que tu preignes aucune de ces choses, ou toutes ensamble, et les confit avec vin stiptique ou avec abun d’uef ou avec aisil;	if the minister gives constipating medicines, such as aloes, incense, myrrh, and sarcocolla, acacia, and similar others, so that you can prepare some of these things, or all together, and mix them with stinting wine, or with the yolk of an egg, or with garlic;
et les met sus le nout en estoupes, et l’estraint bien, et ne la desliier en mains jors;	and apply it to the navel as a poultice, and tie it on tightly, and don't untie it for several days;
et puis la desloie, et rencomence une autre, tant que li nodations soit ostee;	and then untie it, and do another one, until the swelling is gone;
ou tu estrain sus une piece de plonc bien faite;	or you can strain it onto a well-made piece of linen;
car li proprietez dou plonc si est qu’il oste toutes les enfleures desus les membres;	because the property of linen is that it removes all swellings from the limbs;
et se li nodation est ja convertie en durteit ausi com piere, et il est besoing de l’oster, si la cope desus, et fent la superfluiteit apparent;	and if the swelling has turned into hardness like stone, and it needs to be removed, then cut it away, and scrape off the excess;
ou tu la reis a aucun raseur, tant qu’ele soit ostee, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee.	or have it removed by a barber, until it is healed.
dou membre qui est foibles aprés la garison	of the limb which is weakened after the healing
Quant li brisure de l’os est restoree, et demoure aprés li membres foibles et subtilz, si avient por mout de causes:	When the fracture of the bone is restored and remains afterwards in the weak and delicate members, this happens for many reasons:
de coi l’une est por ceu qu’il fut liiez trop estroit, et ne fut mie liiez si com il covenoit;	one reason is that it was bound too tightly and not as it should have been;
ou por ceu qu’il i ot trop de liiens, et ne pooit venir li norrissemens au membre;	or because there were too many ligatures, and the member could not receive nourishment;
ou por multitude d’arosement;	or because of too much bandaging;
ou por trop grans movements, ne mie en son houre;	or because of excessive movement, and not at the right time;
ou por ceu qu’il a poc de sanc en son cors, si est foibles.	or because there is little blood in his body, and it is weak.
Et li cure si est que tu faices mengier le malaide, et faire le cors tendre, tant que li sans soit multipliiez en lui;	And the treatment is that you should feed the patient and make the body soft, so that the blood is multiplied within him;
et li aministre bain, et li done joie et liesce;	and give him a bath, and bring him joy and leisure;
puis met poix sus le membre, si que li poix atraie a li grant norrissement, et l’arose sovent d’aigue tede, tant que li norrissement corre au membre;	then apply pitch to the limb so that it draws out the great putrefaction, and often wash with cold water until the putrefaction is gone from the limb;
et reviegne a sa figure natureil.	and returns to its natural shape.
dou membre tort aprés la santeit	until the limb is straightened after recovery
Quant li membres est tors aprés la restauration, et li os brisiez apert, et li forme dou membre est laide, toutevoie ne pert mie son ovraige natureil:	When the limb is twisted after restoration, and the broken bones are open, and the form of the limb is ugly, yet it does not lose its natural function:
si ne croire mie les folz qui dient c’on doit brisier lou membre tout de noveil, et maint fol mire ont ce fait en nostre terre;	if you do not believe the fools who say that one must break the limb completely anew, and many fools have done this in our land;
et cist ovraiges est blamez, et en vient grans malz, et par aventure li mors;	and these practices are blamed, and great harm often comes from them, and sometimes death;
toutevoie, se li nodations et li torture sont fres, si covient k’il soient arosez d’aigue chaude, ou herbes mollifians soient cuites, si com foilles de vismalve, et racines, et mellilote, et semblans choses;	yet if the dislocations and injuries are fresh, then they should be washed with hot water, or herbs that soften should be boiled, such as leaves of marshmallow, and roots, and melilot, and similar things;
et li fai I emplaustre mollificatif, si com dyaquilon bien fait, et tu pren le muscillaige de vismalve, et la confit avec graisse de geline ou oile de sisament, et fai emplaustre sus;	and apply a soothing ointment, such as well-prepared diaquillon, and take the mustard plant's mucilage and confit it with goose fat or sesame oil, and apply it on top.
ou tu pren figues graisses, et les broie avec fien de colon, et semblans medicines que amenuisent le soudement.	or you can take fatty figs and crush them with colon's hay, and similar medicines that soften quickly.
Et aucune fois est ostee li nodacion por froter continuelment et longement a mains moistes.	And sometimes the joint is dislocated by constantly rubbing with moist hands.
Et soit amenistrez movement au membre chescune houre.	And movement must be applied to the limb every hour.
Et se li tortuositez est enveillie et endurcie, ausi com piere, et besoins est de l’oster au fer, si la covient coper jusc’a l’os, a l’incisoire subtil legierement;	And if the tortuousness is withered and hardened like stone, and needs to be removed with iron, then it should be cut carefully and gently up to the bone.
et mettre cusenson et estude en la cure.	and apply a poultice and bandage in the treatment.
Ci encomence li livres des dislocations	Here begins the book of dislocations
Dislocations est issue d’aucune jointe de son leu, por coi il ne se puet muevre, et est li membres mal figurez, et sent li malaides grant dolor et grant lesion.	Dislocation occurs when a joint moves out of its place, which prevents it from moving, and the limb is misaligned, causing the patient great pain and injury.
Quant dislocation vient a aucun, si le covient maintenant ramener sens targier.	When dislocation occurs in someone, one should immediately bring it back into alignment without delay.
Car s’on tarde, si enfle li leus, et par aventure si le remet on a poines au leu;	For if one delays, the area will swell, and perhaps it will be reset in place with pain.
por ceu ne covient mie c’on le mueve a l’oure k’il est enflez:	Therefore, it is not good to move it when it is swollen:
maintes fois fait venir spame et autres dolors;	many times it brings on spasms and other pains;
toutevoie, quant ce avenra, si fai sainier lou malaide, puis le laisse, tant que li apostemes chas soit apaisiez;	nevertheless, when this happens, let the patient bleed, then leave him until the abscess is drained.
puis arose le membre d’aigue chaude et d’oile, puis le ramoinne legierement, et cure chescun membre si com li cure venra en son leu.	then warm the limb with hot water and oil, then reset it gently, and dress each wound as it comes to the surface.
Et j’ai ordenez les chapistres des dislocations des lou chief jusc’a piez.	And I have ordered the chapters on dislocation from the head to the feet.
des mandibules	of the mandibles
Poc avient que les mandibules soient desaluees andous, et li dislocations d’ambedous est selonc II manieres:	There are two ways that dislocations can occur: either the jaw is dislocated and both mandibles are affected, or just one mandible is affected.
ou elles sont un poc ostees de lor leus, et mollifies un poc;	or they are slightly displaced from their joints and softened a little.
ou elles sont desaluees entierement, et pendent vers lou pis, et cort li salive de la bouche qu’il ne la puet tenir, ne ne puet clore sa bouche, et envoloupe sa langue avec la parole.	or they are completely displaced and hang down towards the feet, and saliva drips from their mouth which they cannot hold closed, nor can they close their lips around their tongue to speak.
Quant li dislocations est petite, si revient par li em plusors disposicions.	When the dislocation is small, it returns by itself in various ways.
Et s’elle est entiere et acomplie, si covient que tu la ramoinne hastanment, et ne targier mie;	And if the dislocation is complete and finished, then you must reset it quickly and not delay.
et en tel maniere que li ministres teigne le chief dou malaide, et boute li mires som pochet de l’une de ses mains en la racine de la dislocation de la mandibule dedens la bouche, se li dislocations est de II pars;	And in such a way that the assistant grabs the head of the patient and pushes his fingers of one hand into the root of the mandible's joint within the mouth if it is a two-part dislocation.
et li autre doi des mains soient defuer, por mettre igal;	and the other two fingers of the hand be forced, to make them even;
et comande au malaide qu’il les amollisse, ses mandibules, et les mueve de toutes pars.	and instruct the patient to soften his jaws, and move them from all sides.
Et li mires la mete igal, tant qu’elle reveigne en son leu.	And he holds the mirror steady, until it returns to its place.
Et se li ramener est griés, meismement se ce sont les II mandibules ensamble, si les arose d’aigue chaude et d’oile, tant que les ramoinnes legierement;	And if they are stuck together, especially if both jaws are stuck, then treat them with hot water and oil, until you can move them slightly;
ne ne targier mie dou ramener, si com nos avons dit.	do not stop trying to reset it, as we have said.
Et quant elles sont ramenees igalment, et li bouche dou malaide clot bien sens mollifiier, si met sus drapelz moilliez en cerote fait d’oile roset et de cire, puis le lie legierement de molz liiens;	And when they are reset evenly, and the mouth of the patient is closed well without softening, then place wet pieces of cloth in rosin ointment made from rose oil and wax, and then bind it lightly with soft bands;
et dorme li malaides sus son dos, et ses chiés soit estans entre II cussins, si qu’il ne lou mueve ne a destre ne a senestre, ne ne s’efforce mie de maixier, mais preigne legiere viande, tant que les dolors soient ostees, et soient noees les mandibules;	and let the patient sleep on his back, and let his head be between two pillows, so that he does not move it to the right or left, nor try to speak, but take light food, until the pains are relieved, and his jaws are bound;
et puis menjuce ce qu’il vuet legierement, et ne se travaille mie d’ovrir la bouche au mengier et au boivre, tant que li mandibule soit bien noee et sanee.	and then eat what he wants lightly, and do not worry about opening his mouth to eat and drink, as long as the jaw is well-bound and healed.
Et se les .ij. mandibules ne pueent estre remises a point a une houre, et ne sont mie converties a lor leus, si en vient fievres et sode acostumees, et par aventure solution de ventre, et par aventure vomist cole pure.	And if the two mandibles cannot be put back into place within an hour, and are not converted to their place, then fever and usual sodden come, and sometimes stomach problems, and sometimes vomiting of clear fluid.
Et quant tu verras ceu, adonc saiches que c’est perdicions;	And when you see this, then you know that it is a sign of death.
et maintes fois muert cil cui il avient, en VIIII jors.	and many times, the person dies within seven days.
de la forcelle	of the fork
Li forcele ne puet desaluer dou costeit dedens la continuation de li et dou pis, et est desaluee aucune fois au defuer, et bien le sent on.	The shoulder joint cannot be dislocated from within the chest or armpit; it is sometimes dislocated by force, and one feels it strongly.
Et li restauration si est que li malaides gise sovin sor son dos, et estende ses bras;	And the restoration is that the patient lies on his back and extends his arms;
et puis presse le leu forment a ta palme, et elle revenra;	and then press the area firmly with your palm, and it will return to its place;
puis met sus l’emplaustre et lou bendeil, et l’estraint;	then put on the ointment and bandage, and tie it tightly;
et li chiez qui est devers lou coute ne puet desaluer;	and the jaw that is towards the ear cannot be dislocated;
se poc non, et se il desalue aucune fois, si le ramoinne a son leu, si com nos avons dit;	if not, and if it dislocates even once, then reset it to its place, as we have said;
puis met sus l’emplaustre et le bendeil, et l’estraint, et coumande au malaide qu’il se repose tant qu’il soit sanez;	then put on the ointment and bandage, and tie it tightly, and instruct the patient to rest until he is healed;
et ensi meisme est ramenez li chiés de l’espale, quant il est desevrez de son leu.	and so it is with the head of the shoulder when it is dislocated from its place.
de la dislocation de l’espaule	of the dislocation of the shoulder
Saiches que li espaule n’est desaluee fuer que selonc III manieres:	You should know that the shoulder can be dislocated in three ways:
de coi l’une est qu’ele desalue a la partie de l’assele au desoz;	one is when it dislocates at the part of the acromion process below;
et li seconde est a la partie dou pis;	and the second is at the part of the scapula;
et par aventure desalue a la partie desus, et ceu avient poc;	and sometimes it dislocates at the part above, and that doesn't happen often.
et ne desalue mie derrier por l’espaule, et ne desalue mie dedens por les ners;	It doesn't dislocate behind from the shoulder, and not within from the nerves;and it never dislocates in front or to the sides.
et plusors fois desalue desoz vers l’assele, meismement a ces qui ont poc de char, car a ces saut ele fuer hastanment;	And sometimes it dislocates below towards the acromion process, especially in those who have little flesh, because in them it is very easy to dislocate.and it often dislocates to the side of the acromion process, but not directly behind it.
a ces qui ont assez char, saut ele a poines, et rentre a poines.	In those who have plenty of flesh, it only dislocates to the sides and returns to the sides.It never goes directly behind or directly in front.
Et par aventure avient a aucuns homes percussion ou casseure, et enfle li espaule d’un aposteme chaut, et cuide qu’elle est desaluee par ceu.	And by chance it happens to some men that they get a concussion or fracture, and the shoulder swells from a hot abscess, and they think it is dislocated because of that.
Il covient donques que tu l’esprueves, tant que tu en soies certains;	You must therefore test it until you are certain of it;
et adonques encomence la cure.	and then begin the treatment.
Et est conue li dislocations quant il est aval vers l’assele, et met difference entre l’espaule malade et la saine, et tu troveras entre lor diversiteit manifeste;	And you will know that there is a dislocation when it is lower towards the armpit, and there is a difference between the sick shoulder and the healthy one, and you will find a manifest difference between them;
et troveras au chief de l’espaule une fosse, et desoz l’assele au tochier le chief de l’espaule, ausi com se ce soit uns oes;	and you will find in the head of the shoulder a pit, and under the armpit at the top of the shoulder, as if it were an egg;
et ne puet li malaides ramener sa main a son neis, ne movoir de nulz movemens;	and the patient cannot bring his hand to his nose, nor move in any way;
et ausi, s’elle est desaluee en haut, si n’est mie occultee, car tu le trueves manifestement au tochier;	and also, if it is dislocated upwards, it is not hidden, for you will find it clearly at the top;
et ceste maniere de dislocation n’est mie fors a ramener, quant elle est novele, ou se li enfes est malaides.	and this type of dislocation can only be reset when it is new, or if the child is sick.
Et li maniere est que li ministres lieve la main dou malaide en haut, puis met tes peuchas desoz l’assele, et lieve la jointure a force en haut au leu;	And the way to do it is for the assistant to lift the hand of the patient up, then place your fingers under the socket, and forcefully lift the joint up into place.
et li ministres lieve la main, et l’estende en haut, pues le mette desoz;	and the assistant lifts the hand and extends it upward, then brings it back down;
si venra hastanment.	it will quickly come back into place.
Et s’elle ne vient si com nos avons dit em mains jors aprés, si covient ke li malaides soit baigniez en aigue chaude;	And if it does not come back as we have said after several days, then the patient should be bathed in hot water;
et li amenistre arosement mollifiant et assouajant, si com decoction de altee et de fenugrec et de mellilote en aigue, et soit amenistree;	and the assistant should apply softening and soothing poultices, such as a decoction of alder and fenugreek and milfoil in water, and let it be applied;
puis soit sovinez li malaides sus son dos, et mette on desoz l’assele un sto de lainne igal, ne trop mol ne trop dur, puis mette li mires son talon sus le sto, et lieve le chief de l’espaule vertuousement, et traie la main dou malaide;	then the patient should be laid on his back, and a layer of equally soft but not too soft or too hard woolen cloth placed under the socket, then the assistant places their heel on the cloth and lifts the head of the shoulder gently but firmly, and pulls the hand of the patient;
et uns autres ministres teigne lou chief dou malaide, si qu’il ne se mueve aval;	and another minister dyes the head of the patient so that it does not move downward;
celle espaule revient tout maintenant, et se tu vues si le ramoinne selonc ceste maniere:	this shoulder will return immediately, and if you see that it is reset according to this manner:
et est que tu faices estre present I home qui soit plus grans que li malaides;	and you should have a man present who is larger than the patient;
et soit drois devers lou costeit, et boute s’espaule desoz l’assele dou malaide, et lieve l’assele en haut, si que li malaides pende en l’ar;	and stand straight towards the shoulder, and press the shoulder underneath the armpit of the patient, and lift the armpit upwards so that the patient hangs in the air;
et uns autres ministres traie la main dou malaide aval devers lou ventre.	and another minister pulls the hand of the patient downward towards the belly.
Et se li malaides est trop legiers, si pent avec lui aucune chose pesant, et li dislocation revient maintenant.	If the dislocation is too slight, one can weigh it down with something heavy, and it will return immediately.
Et le ramoinne on ausi en autre maniere:	And it is reset in another manner:
et est c’on fiche I lonc tison en terre, dont li chiés soit ausi reons com I pistal, et ne soit ne trop gros ne trop graile;	and one should stick a long thin stick into the ground so that its top is as high as the shoulder, and not too thick or too thin;
puis soit mis desoz lou malaide, mais k’il ait drapelz souef sus, et li malaides soit estans dou lonc dou fust;	then it should be placed underneath the patient, but with a soft cloth over it, and the patient should be upright against the stick;
puis soit estendue sa main aval d’autre part forment, et li jointure revenra en son leu hastanment;	then extend his hand downward on the other side, and the joint will return to its place gradually.
et s’elle ne vuet revenir por toutes ces choses que nos avons dit, si fai ceste cure:	and if it does not want to return despite all that we have said, then do this treatment:
pren I tison de II bras de grant et IIII dois de large, qui ait le chief reont por mues entrer em parfont desoz l’assele, selonc ceste forme:	take a log of wood two feet in length and four fingers in width, which has been split on one side so that it can be inserted deeply under the shoulder, according to this shape:
puis lie sus le chief dou fust drapelz souez, que li fust ne blece lou malaide, puis le met desoz l’assele dou malaide;	then bind it with cloth below so that the log does not hurt the patient, then place it under the shoulder of the patient;
et estende som bras sus le fust dou lonc, et lie l’ajutoire sus le fust, et lou bras au chief de la main, puis met le bras sus I eschillon d’une eschiele dou large, et soit estendue li mains aval, et soit laissiez li cors pendans d’autre part:	and extend his arm above the log, and bind the shoulder to the log, and the arm to the head of the hand, then place the arm on a wooden block two fingers in width, and let the hand hang down, and let the body dangle on the other side;
li jointure reva ens maintenant.	the joint will heal now.
Et quant elle est ens, en quel maniere que ce soit, si covient que tu mettes desoz l’assele une spere de laine igal, puis met l’emplaustre aparilliet de poudre dou molin, avec encens et aubun d’uef, sus toute l’espaule et entor, puis l’estrain desoz l’assele avenanment, et torne le liien sus l’emplaustre, et embraice la main a son col, et soit li mains demorans ensi.	And when it is in place, however it may be, you should place under the joint a round pillow of wool, then apply the plaster prepared from flour with incense and egg white over the entire shoulder and around it; then tighten it under the joint gradually, and tie the string over the plaster, and embrace the hand to his neck, and let the hand remain thus.
Et covient qu’il menjuce poc, tant que li membres soit confortez, car il sanera plus tost;	And one must eat little, until the member is healed, for it will heal faster that way;
et puis menjuce plus aprés V jors ou VII, et le mueve;	and then eat more after a few days, and move it;
et s’il est fermeis et il n’est mollifiez, si est sanez.	and if it is stiff and not柔軟, then it is healed.
Et se li jointure est fuer de leu por moistor que i est venue, ou por autre cause, si covient que tu i aministres cauteres a III pertus, si com il est mis devant ou chapistre des cauteres.	And if the joint has moved out of place due to moisture or any other cause, you should administer cautery at three places, as described in the chapter on cautery.
Et se tu fais tout ceu, et il deslie aprés VII jors, et li jointure ne se tient, et ne puet lever som bras amont, adonc saiches que li nerf au chief de l’espaule sont copeit ou estendut ou amollis;	And if you do all this, and it dislocates after seven days, and the joint does not hold, and he cannot lift his arm upwards, then know that the nerve at the head of the shoulder is cut or stretched or softened;
et saiches que li jointure n’iert jamais fichie en son leu.	and know that the joint will never be fixed in its place.
Li dislocation qui est devers lou pis, et les mameles, ou derrier, si est faite par impulsion, et estendement de mains, et i aministre on autre lieure;	Dislocations which are towards the foot, and the breasts, or behind, are made by pushing, and stretching with hands, and one administers another remedy;
et cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	and treat until it is healed.
Et se aprés la sanation vient grietez au membre, et tardemens em movement, si use li malaides bain maintes fois, tant que celle grietez soit alegie, et reviegne a sa premiere nature.	And if after healing the limb becomes swollen and tender to the touch, and with movement, then the patient should use the bath many times until the swelling goes down and the limb returns to its original state.
de la dislocation dou coute	on the dislocation of the shoulder
Saiches que li jointure dou coute est desaluee a poinnes, et a poinnes revient;	Know that the joint of the neck is dislocated by the nails, and by the nails it returns.
et s’est desaluee de toutes pars, et meismement devant et derrier, et li dislocations n’est mie reponue, car on la voit bien et sent bien;	and it is dislocated throughout, especially in front and behind, and the dislocation is not reduced, for one can see and feel it;
et desalue selonc chescune figure.	and dislocate according to each figure.
Et quant tu joins le coute malaide avec lou sain, si le pues veoir apertement.	And when you join the sick neck with the healthy one, then you can see it clearly.
Car li jointure est chevee, et ne puet ploier lou bras, ne touchier son espaule a tout.	Because the joint is crooked and cannot bend the arm or touch its shoulder at all.
Et covient que tu le ramoinnes ainsois que apostemes chaus i viegne, car se apostemes chaus i venoit, si seroit grief li ramener;	And you should reset it as soon as the abscess forms, for if an abscess forms, then it will be harmful to reset it;
et par aventure ne puet estre ramenez dou tout en tout, meismement quant ele est au derrier;	and indeed it cannot be reset at all, especially when it is at the back;
si vaut pis que les autres dislocations, et est de plus grant dolor, et par aventure i vient li mors.	it is worse than other dislocations and is more painful, and often death ensues.
Et li restauration si est, quant elle est telz c’on la puet ramener, que tu li estendes sa main a tes II mains;	And the restoration, when it can be reset, is to extend your left hand with your right hand;
et ses bras soit espandus, et les mains dou mire selonc le coute entor, desor et desoz, et boute la jointure a ses peuchas ensamble, ou a la racine de sa palme, tant qu’ele reviegne a son leu.	and the arms should be spread out, and the hands held according to the nape of the neck, from behind and underneath, and the joint pressed at its root, or the root of the palm, until it returns to its place.
Et se li dislocations est au devant, si revient quant il double sa main a sa main, et fier de la racine de la palme lou coute qui est desaluez.	And if the dislocation is at the front, it will return when he bends his hand to his hand, and he stretches from the root of the palm the joint which is dislocated.
Et s’il ne vuet revenir au leu, si aministre fort extension;	And if it does not want to return to its place, then apply strong extension;
et est que dui ministre estendent le bras, et le teignent dui ministre, si qu’il ne se mueve a l’estension;	and it is that two ministers extend the arm, and are stretched by two ministers, so that it does not move during extension;
