puis torne le bras de chescune part, puis que tu as envoloupeit un drapeil double lonc et large;	then turn the arm from each side, after you have wrapped a long, wide cloth around it;
et quant li mires a jointe la jointure a sa main, si l’oigne d’aucun oile por amolir la jointure, puis boute la jointure forment, tant qu’ele reviegne;	and when the minister has joined the joint of his hand, he should smear some oil to loosen the joint, then tightly bind the joint so that it heals;
et quant elle est au leu, si met sus emplaustre sec avec aubun d’uef, et l’estrain forment, et pent le bras au col dou malaide, et le laisse aucuns jors, puis le deslie.	and when it is in place, put on a dry poultice with egg white, and tightly bind it, and keep the arm still at the neck of the patient for some days, then loosen it.
Et se li jointure est ferme en son leu, si deslie lou liien, et le laisse;	And if the joint is firm in its place, loosen the binding and leave it;
et se tu vois que li jointure n’estrigne bien, si rencomence l’emplaustre et lou lien, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant qu’il soit fermement mis;	and if you see that the joint is not fitting well, then restart the poultice and the binding, and leave it in this way for some days until it is firmly in place;
puis le deslie.	then loosen it.
Et se il sent grieteit aprés le ramenement de la jointe, et elle se muet, si le baigne et frote bellement, et presse tant qu’il soit assouagiez;	And if there is great pain after the joint is reset and it moves, then bathe and rub it well, and press until the pain subsides.
ou tu met sus la jointure une naige de mouton grasse, puis la laisse I jor et une nuit, puis l’oste, et lou fai entrer ou bain;	Or you can put a fat sheep's knuckle on the joint, then leave it for a day and night, then remove it and let him enter the bath;
et quant il sue, se li frote la jointure tempreement, puis remet la naige sus, et puis entre ou bain;	and when he sweats, gently rub the joint, then put the knuckle back on, then enter the bath again;
et ensi fai II fois ou III, tant qu’il soit sanez;	and so do this twice or thrice until he is healed;
et se tu vues, si met sus fien de vaiche moiste chaufeit avec burre, et l’estrain sus;	and if you see that you put warm moist cow's dung with butter on it and press it onto the joint;
si revenra a sa disposition.	it will return to its natural state.
li dislocation de la main	dislocations of the hand
Li jointure de la main desalue, et li revenue est legiere, plus que les autres jointures.	The joints of the hand heal more easily and quickly than other joints.
Toutevoie, il la covient ramener au leu hastanment, en l’oure meisme qu’ele est desaluee, ainsois que li leus soit enflez, ou qu’il i viegne aposteme chaut.	Nevertheless, it must be reset to its place gently, at the same time as when it was dislocated, otherwise the joint will become swollen or a hot abscess will form.
Et li ramenemens si est que tu mettes la main malaide sus une tauble, et estende li ministres la main, et li mires la mette igal, ensi que il mette sa paume sus l’aparance de la jointure, et la boute tant qu’elle reviegne.	And for the dislocation, if you put the patient's hand on a table, and extend the minister's hand, and look at it to make it even, so that he puts his palm on the appearance of the joint, and bends it until it comes back.
Toutevoie, il covient que vos regardez s’il est bien a leu;	However, you should check if it is in the right place;
adonc mette li malaides lou dos de sa main sus une tauble a l’estension et au ramenement.	then put the patient's back of his hand on a table, extending and bending it.
Et se li dislocations est au dos de la main, si mette li malaides son dos de sa main sus la tauble, et li mires mette sa main sus cele apparance de la jointure.	If the dislocation is in the back of the hand, then the patient should lie on his back with his hand flat on a table, and the surgeon should place his hand over the appearance of the joint.
S’elle revient maintenant, c’est bien.	If it comes back now, that's good.
Se ce non, si l’estrain d’emplaustres apaisans apostemes chaus, et lou laisse ensi sens rencomencier.	If not, then strain with soothing poultices, and let it be without re-encombing.
Et s’il ne le puet soffrir, et tu ne la pues mettre au leu aprés aucuns jors, si demore li jointure torte;	And if he cannot bear it, and you cannot put it in place after several days, then the joint remains crooked;
et ne nuist niant au malaide fuer que tant que li mains est amoillie, et ne puet estraindre aucune chose a tout:	and it does not harm the patient unless that as long as his hand is swollen, and he cannot strain anything at all;
adonc saiches que li nerf sont copez, ou li artere;	then you will know that the nerves are cut, or the arteries;
si n’i a autre engien fuer que d’estraindre par cautere delez le cas, et par aventure n’i vaut autre chose.	if there is nothing else to do except to constrict by fire next to the wound, and by chance nothing else works.
Et quant li mains est au leu, si met sus l’emplaustre que nos avons dit, puis l’estrain et le laisse .v. jors, puis le deslie et laisse ensi.	And when the hand is in place, then apply the plaster that we have mentioned, then hold it and leave it for .v. days, then loosen it and leave it like that.
Et s’il ne la puet bien movoir, et il i a aucune grieteit, si la moille d’aigue chaude, et le frote tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if he cannot move it well, and there is any swelling, then moisten it with warm water, and rub it until it heals.
de la dislocation des dois de la main	of the dislocation of the fingers of the hand
Aucune fois sont desaluez li doi de la main a chescune part, aucune fois au dos de la palme ou au ventre;	Sometimes it dislocates the knuckles of the hand on either side, sometimes on the back of the palm or the palm;
adonques estent le doi, et boute la dislocation a tes pouchés tant qu’il reviegne, puis sostien lou chief dou doi, et le pent vers la partie ou il est desjoins;	then you must pull on the fingers, and put back in place with your thumbs as far as it will go, then hold the head of the finger, and push towards the part that is dislocated;
et le laisse II jors, et puis le met igal celui jor;	and leave for two days, and then reset it straight that day;
et de nut le lie, si com nos avons dit, et lou deslie de jor, et lou fai movoir, et le relie la nut;	and bandage it as we have said, and loosen it during the day, and move it, and relive it at night;
et fai ce sovent, tant qu’il soit estroit, et tout ausi fai, se il est desaluez au ventre de la main, et fai si com tu as fait ci devant, tant qu’il soit sanez;	and do this often until it is healed, and do the same if it dislocates in the palm of the hand, and do as you have done before, until it is healed;
et tout ausi fai, quant il est desaluez d’autre part.	and do the same when it is dislocated from another direction.
dou desaluement de l’eschinee dou dos	from the dislocation of the sciatic nerve from the back
Quant l’eschinee dou dos ou dou col est desaluee, ou il en i a plusors desaluees, si n’i a point de cure, car li mors haste le malaide.	When the sciatic nerve in the back or neck is dislocated, there is no cure, for death hastens the ailment.
Et li signes si est que li egestions saut fuer sens volunteit, ne ne la puet tenir, et maintes fois sont mollifiez aucun membre, ou les II cuixes ou li dui bras ou I.	And the signs are that the bowels move without voluntary effort, and he cannot hold it in, and many times a limb is relaxed, or both thighs or two arms or one.
Et maintes fois se muet li eschinee a IIII pars;	And often the skin splits in four parts;
celle qui se muet au derrier si est apelee «gilbositez»:	that which splits at the back is called "dislocation":
li cure si est que tu rewarde se li gilbositez est venue d’enfance:	the treatment, if the dislocation occurs in children, is to:
si n’i ait point de cure ne de sanation dou tot.	if there is no healing, then it will never heal.
Et celle que vient de cheoir ou de percussions ou de semblans choses, dirent li ancien manieres de cures par grans paroles, ou il n’a mie en toutes grant profit;	And that which comes from falling or blows or similar things, the ancient methods of treatment are given in great detail, but they do not always bring great benefit;
mais je l’ai abregiet selonc mon entention, et ai formez estrumens en diverses manieres.	but I have abbreviated them according to my understanding and created instruments in diverse ways.
Je dis que en la gilbositeit que vient au pis devant, nen a engien ne santeit;	I say that there is no healing or health in the dislocation that comes from the toe facing forward;
et ausi cele que vient droitement en II costez, et ne puet on curer fuers que celi proprement qui vient au dos, si com je dis;	and also those who come straight to both sides, and no one can cure except for those who properly come from the back, as I said;
et est que li malaides soit estendus sus sa faice en I leu igal, et ait de l’estrain desoz lui, qu’il ne se blece;	and it is that the patient be stretched out on his face in one place equally, and has a restraint underneath him, so that he does not bend;
puis fiche I tison au chief en terre forment, et I autre as piez, et lie un liien pardesoz les asseles dou malaide, et I autre as hainches, et as genous, et as chevilles;	then insert the brand into the ground at the head, and another under the feet, and tie a string under the armpits of the patient, and another at the hips, and knees, and ankles;
et dui ministre saichent les liiens, li uns au chief et li autres as piez, parmi les II tisons;	and two assistants handle the strings, one at the head and the other at the feet, between the brands;
et soient bien fermez, li tison si com nos avons dit, et li mires mette ses paumes sus l’espinee forment, tant qu’ele reviegne.	and they are well secured, the brand as we have said, and the healer places his palms on the spine, until it is straightened out.
Et s’elle ne revient par ceste cure, si pren une tauble de III bras de lonc, et chevé desoz la paroit, et li malaides soit en costé, et boute le chief de la tauble desoz la paroit, puis met le mileu de la tauble sus l’espinee;	And if it does not return by this treatment, take a table three yards long, and bend it under the wall, and the patient is on his side, and place the head of the table under the wall, then put the middle of the table on the spine;
et mette li mires ses piez sus l’autre chief de la tauble, et presse bien, tant qu’il reviegne au leu;	and put his feet on the other end of the table, and press hard until it goes back into place.
et se tu vues, si le fai au tornet qui torne a la main.	and if you see that it turns towards the hand.
Et est que tu fiches II tisons au chief dou malaide d’un bras de grant, et devers les piez II autres, et ait entre chescun tison, desoure et desoz, une paume d’espaice de lonc;	And you should put two fires on the head of the sick person's arm, and two more on their feet, with a palm-width of space in between each fire, both above and below.
et ait en chescun tison I pertus, ou li tornet corre, et soient li tison fermement en terre, si qu’il ne se muevent;	And in each fire there should be a hole where the joint turns, and the fires should be firmly planted in the ground so that they don't move.
et entre chescuns II tisons ait I tison tornant, sor coi li liien tornent, et ait en II tornans II petis tisons d’une paume de lonc, por torner le tornet;	And between each pair of fires there should be a turning fire, above which the joint turns, and there should be two small fires on top of the turning fire, about a palm-width long, to turn the joint.
et puis lie lou lien qui est parmi les asseles au tornet devers le chief, et l’autre liien devers les piez a l’autre tornet, et chescuns des ministres torne son tornet a tout le liien, et li maistres mette l’espinee igal si com nos avons dit.	Then tie the string that is between the fires to the joint at the head, and the other string to the joint at the foot, and each of the assistants turns their joint all along the string, and the master puts the spine in evenly as we have said.
Et quant elle est igalz, si met sus emplaustre desiccatif avec abun d’uef, et puis les estoupes, et puis l’estele d’une tablete de III dois de lonc, que porpreigne lou leu de la gilbositeit et la partie de l’espondile sainne, puis le lie d’un liien, si com nos avons dit, et use li malaides de norrissement subtil, tant qu’il soit sanez;	And when it is even, then apply a desiccant poultice with an egg-yolk, and then the towels, and then the carpet of a tablet three inches long, which purples the area of the hernia and the healthy part of the spine, then bind it with a bandage, as we have said, and use the subtle remedy for fainting until he is healed.
et s’aucune chose vient en la fin de la santez, si covient aministrer medicines amollissans et asouajans, avec l’estele que nos avons dit ci devant;	and if nothing comes of it in the end, then soft and soothing remedies must be administered with the carpet we mentioned earlier.
et aucune fois i aministre on une piece de plonc, et aucune fois vient li apparance en la derriere spondile dou dos, et cuide on que ce soit dislocations;	sometimes a lump appears at the back of the spine in the lumbar region, and people think it is a dislocation.
et c’est li os qui apert, por coi on n’i doit mie avoir presumption:	and it is the bone that has appeared, so one should not be presumptuous about it:
par aventure feroit venir la mort.	for it might bring death.
des dislocations de la hainche	of dislocations of the hip
Saiches que as jointures de la hainche et as jointures de l’espaule ne vient fuers que dislocacions soulement, ne n’i vient mie si com as autres jointures;	Know that the joints of the hip and the joints of the shoulder do not become dislocated except through dislocation alone, nor do they become so like other joints.
et li jointure de la hainche est desaluee selonc IIII parties:	and the joint of the hip is dislocated according to four parts:
dedens et defuer ,et devant et derrier;	inside and outside, and forward and backward;
et plus dedens c’aillors, et poc desalue devant et derrier.	and more within chalks, and slightly dislocated in front and behind.
Et li conoissance de sa dislocations dedens si est que quant on joint la jambe malaide avec la sainne, si est plus longe, et apert plus li malaides genous que li sains, et ne puet li malaides doubler son genoil au feu;	And the knowledge of its dislocation within is that when one joins the diseased leg with the healthy one, it is longer, and the diseased knee appears larger than the healthy one, and the diseased person cannot bend their knee to the fire.
et est li leus qui est delez enflez d’aposteme chaut, por ceu que li chiés de la cuixe vient lai.	and is the place that is swollen with hot abscess due to the head of the thigh coming there.
Et li signe de celui cui il vient au defuer, si est que cist accident sont contraire a ces devant.	And the sign of him to whom it comes from disuse, is that these accidents are contrary to those before.
Et li signes de celui cui avient au devant, si est qu’il estent bien sa jambe selonc l’acomplissement;	And the signs of those who have it in front are that they are well-built according to their height;
toutevoie, ne double mie le genoil sens dolor, et s’on le vuet faire aler, si ne puet avant, et retient son urine, et enfle li angre, et quant il vait, si passe sus le talon.	Nevertheless, they cannot bend their knee without pain, and if one tries to make them walk, they cannot, and they retain their urine, and the anus swells, and when they go to the toilet, they pass it over the heel.And if the disease is in the back:
Et li signes de celui cui il avient derrier, si est qu’il ne puet espandre son genoil, ne doubler, et est celle jambe plus torte de l’autre, et li angre est mollifié, et est li chiés de la cuixe au leu desoz les costes.	And the signs of him who has it behind, are that he cannot bend or double his knee, and that leg is more crooked than the other, and the veins are softened, and the head of the thigh is at the place below the ribs.
Li ramenemens de ceste semblance de dislocation si est que tu rewarde se li dislocations est anciainne, et elle demore selonc sa disposition, si n’i a nule cure;	The understanding of this kind of dislocation is that you examine whether the dislocation is old and it persists according to its nature, then there is no treatment for it.
et n’i covient mie qu’il ait presumption.	and he must not have any presumptuousness.
Et en celi dont li dislocation est fresche, et c’est des IIII manieres de dislocation, si te haste que tu tornes la jointe, et l’esten dedens et defuer, et la muef a destre et senestre;	And for those with a fresh dislocation, there are four types of dislocations; you should quickly turn the joint, stretch it inwards and outwards, and move it to the right and left.
par aventure si revenra, et n’a mestier d’autre cure.	It may return on its own without needing any other treatment.
Et s’il ne revient en ceste maniere, si covient que tu apareilles I ministre fort, et esten la jambe fort a II mains, ou a I liien que soit liiez sus lou genoil;	And if it does not return in this way, you must use a strong remedy and stretch the leg firmly with two hands, or with one hand tied to the knee;
et uns autres ministres estende sa main desus en teil maniere qu’il boute ses mains desoz ses asseles, puis l’estrigne d’un souef liien sus la cuixe;	and someone else stretches his hand above in such a way that he pushes his hands under his armpits, then pulls with a strong cord on his thigh;
et uns autres tigne lou chief dou liien;	and someone else pulls on the head with a cord;
et estendent amont et aval tuit a une fois, tant que li malaide soit levez de terre a une fois, et demoure pendans.	and they stretch him upwards and downwards all at once until the patient is lifted off the ground once, and then he hangs limp.
Ceste maniere d’estension si est commune as .iiij. semblances, et se li dislocation est revenue, si com nos avons dit, c’est bien.	This method of stretching is common to all four appearances, and if the dislocation has returned, as we have said, it is good.
Se ceu non, si covient mettre cure a sa semblance.	If not, then you must take care of its appearance.
Quant li dislocations est au pardedens, si covient que tu sovines le malaide sus son costeit sain, puis met le liien sus la racine de la cuixe, et le leu qui est desoz l’angre, puis estent le liien en haut devers l’angre, et devers la forcele;	When the dislocation is in the hip, you must lead the patient up his healthy side, then place the ligature at the root of the thigh, and the place below the groin, then let the ligature ascend towards the groin, and towards the armpit.
puis preigne uns autres ministres ses bras, et embraice le gros leu de la cuixe malaide, et l’estende au defuer forment:	Then have another assistant grab his arms, and embrace the large part of the ill thigh, and stretch it forcefully in a proper manner.
si revenra a son leu maintenant;	And if it doesn't return to its place immediately;
et ceste maniere de dislocation est plus legiere des autres.	and this kind of dislocation is easier than others.Et s’il ne retourne, tu peesche l’esgarnir et le raser: car
Et se tu ne la pues serrer en ceste maniere que nos avons dit, si covient que tu lies les II piés dou malaide ensamble d’un fort liien souef sus les II talons, et sus les II genous, et soit li jambe malaide estendue II dois plus que li autres;	And if you cannot tie it in the manner we have described, then you must bind the sick man's two feet together with a strong silk thread below the two heels, and above the two knees, with the sick leg stretched out two fingers more than the other;
puis soit pendus sus le chief d’un fust, et soit en sus de terre II bras de lonc;	then let him be hung from the top of a pole, and let him be above the ground by two arms' length;
puis comande a I ministre qu’il embraice le chief de la cuixe, et soit uns autres ministres pendans avec le malaide, qui embraice forment la cuixe, car li jointure revient maintenant hastanment.	then instruct the minister to embrace the head of the thigh, and let another minister hanging with the patient embrace the thigh firmly, for the joint will return quickly.
Et quant li dislocations est au defuer, si gise li malaides, si com nos avons dit en celui qui a gilbositeit, et estraigne I liien sus la jambe malaide proprement, et sus le peis ausi;	And when the dislocation is healed, then let the patient lie down as we have said in that which has gout, and tightly bind the leg of the affected limb, and also above it on the thigh;
puis met II tisons, I au chief et I autre as piez, puis fiche I tison entre les cuixes au malaide emmi la forme;	then put two firebrands, one at the head and another at the foot, then insert the firebrand between the thighs of the patient in the groin;
et ait plantei de drapelz moistes entor, qu’il ne blece lou malaide, puis estende chescuns ministre devers lui, et li mires mette igal a sa main la dislocation.	and have moist bandages placed around him so that he does not blink, then each minister should stretch out towards him, and the patient should hold the area of the dislocation with his hand.
S’elle revient, c’est boin.	If it returns, that is good.
Se ce non, met sus .ie. table, et le presse ensi com nos avons dit en la gilbositeit, et gise li malaides sus le sain costeit.	If not, put him on the table and press him as we have said in the gilet [a garment with straps that could be used to restrain a patient], and lay the patient on his healthy side.
Et quant li dislocations est devant, si covient estendre la jambe malaide hastanment, et selonc ce que j’ai dit;	And when the dislocation is forward, then it is necessary to stretch the affected leg gently, and according to what I have said;
et mette li mires sa paine d’estre sus l’angre malaide, puis presse a l’autre main, et l’estent aval devers lou genoil.	and place his weight on the sore joint, then press with the other hand, and stretch it down towards the knee.
Et se li dislocations est au defuer, si ne covient pas estendre le malaide aval, ne lever sus la terre, ains covient qu’il soit ausi com se li hainche estoit desaluee au defuer, si com nos avons dit dou couchement sus les II hainches;	And if the dislocation is outward, then the affected person should not stretch downward or lift himself up from the ground, but he should be as if his hip were dislocated outward, just as we have said about lying on one's side on both hips;
et soit sus sa faice, et li lien estendut si com nos avons dit ci devant, et doit om presser sus la jointure a la table;	and lie on his face, and the limb be stretched as we have said before, and one should press upon the joint while he is on the table;
et sera a point quant li malaides estendra ses jambes, et elles seront igalz;	and it will be easily done when the affected person extends his legs, and they will become even;
adonques ajoste les cuixes, et met l’emplaustre, et l’estrain d’un bendeil, si que li hainche ne se mueve;	then adjust the thighs, and apply the ointment, and bind it with a bandage so that the hip does not move;
et se repose III jors ou IIII, puis le deslie, et met l’emplaustre sus;	and rest for three or four days, then loosen it, and apply the ointment.
et se tu vois qu’elles soient igalz, si l’estrain, si com devant, et le laisse III jors;	And if you see that they are even, then strain them as before, and leave them for three days;
puis le deslie, et lou fai aler belement, tant que li membres soit confortez.	then loosen it, and let it walk comfortably until the limb is healed.
de la dislocation dou genoil	dislocation of the knee
Li genous est desaluez selonc III manieres:	The knee is dislocated in three ways:
c’est a savoir, dedens et defuer, et derrier;	that is to say, inside and outside, and behind;
et ne desalue point devant.	and it does not dislocate in front.
Et li signes si est que tu comande au malaide qu’il plie sa jambe a sa cuixe, et s’ele ne s’aert a sa cuixe, saiches qu’il est desaluez;	And the sign is that you command the patient to bend his leg at the thigh, and if it does not straighten at the thigh, then you know it is dislocated;
et li restauration de toutes si est que tu faices seoir le malaide droit, et estende sa jambe s’il puet, et li met ton dos sus sa faice, et met son piet sus tes piez;	and the restoration of all of them is that you make the patient sit upright and extend his leg if he can, and put your back on his face, and put his foot on your feet;
puis pren son genoil a tes paumes, et retrai entre tes dois, puis plie les II costez dou genoil forment;	then take his knee in your palms, and pull it between your fingers, then bend both sides of the knee smoothly.
et uns autres ministres estende son piet, tant que li genous reviegne a son leu, et li signes est qu’il aert bien sa jambe a sa cuixe legierement;	and another assistant stretches his foot so that the knee returns to its place, and the sign is that he straightens his leg slightly;
et met l’emplastre sus, et fai aerdre la jambe a la cuixe, et les loie ensamble fort III jors ou IIII, puis le deslie;	and apply the plaster, and straighten the leg at the thigh, and bind them together tightly for three or four days, then loosen it.
et ne se travaille mie li malaides d’aler, tant que li membres soit confortez.	and do not make the patient move until the limb is healed.
Et se li membres n’est a point, si aministre estendement fort, si com nos avons dit en la cure de la hainche, tant qu’il soit sanez	And if the member is not at all, then administer very strong extension, as we have said in the treatment of the hip, until it is healed.
de la dislocation dou talon	of dislocation of the heel
Li talons est aucune fois esmeus, et aucune fois desaluez plenement, et dedens et defuer.	Heels are sometimes crushed, and sometimes fully dislocated, both internally and externally.
Et li signes si est que li cheville est enflee, et tent avant a la partie ou elle est desaluee:	And the signs are that the ankle is swollen, and feels tender in the affected part;
li ramenemens si est legier, et le doit on estendre legierement a ses mains quant il est esmeus soulement.	the range of motion should be slight, and one should gently straighten it with their hands when it is dislocated.Et li cheville qui est desaluée, si convient mettre sur une poutre, ou un trescot, et le pied de la cuisse au bas pendent;
Et quant il est desaluez dou tot, si covient que tu faices seoir le malaide droit, et le tigne I ministres fors par la jambe, desus la cheville;	And when it is fully healed, you should make the patient stand upright, and have one assistant hold him firmly by the leg, above the ankle;Et les II autres ministre par la cuisse, desus li genous; si doit il tenir droit et fort I jors entiers, quant il ne se traint mie soulement;
puis trai le piet a toi a ta main destre, et puis a la senestre II fois, puis l’estent en haut, et boute bellement lou piet en haut;	then draw up your foot to your right hand, then to your left hand twice, then stretch it upwards and pull the foot up firmly;
et fai ce II fois, si com nos avons dit, em boutant et en traiant lou piet;	and do this twice as we have said, by pushing and pulling the foot;
s’elle revient, c’est bien;	if it works, that's good;
se ce non, si rencomence l’ovraige, car il revient;	if not, then start the operation again, for it will work;
et s’il ne puet revenir ensi, si fai gesir lou malaide sor son dos sus terre, et fiche I passeil fermement en terre entre ses cuixes, et lie drapelz entor, qu’il ne blece lou malaide;	and if it still doesn't work, then have the patient lie on his back on the ground, and push the passel firmly into the ground between his thighs, and wind cloth around him, so that he does not move the sick person;
puis teigne li ministres la cuixe, et uns autres ministres estende lou piet a ses mains ou a I liien, k’il lie sus le col dou piet;	then the ministers hold his thigh, and another minister stretches the foot to his hands or to his knees, so that he binds it onto the neck of the foot;
puis estende chescuns ministres igalment, et li passelz soit adés entre les cuixes dou malaide por retenir le malaide quant on l’estent;	then each minister stretches equally, and the passels are then between the sick person's thighs to restrain him when he is stretched;
puis mette li mires igal la dislocation a ses mains, et uns autres ministres teigne la jambe sainne au desoz, et li dislocation revenra hastanment.	then have the patient hold the dislocation steady with his hands, and another assistant hold the healthy leg from below, and the dislocation will return to its place gradually.
Et quant elle iert a point, si met l’emplastre et estoupes sus, et l’estrain forment, et lie lou piet a la jambe, et warde les ners qui sont sus la cheville derrier, que li liiens ne soit trop estrois;	And when it is in place, then apply the plaster and padding on top, and stretch it firmly, and bind the foot to the leg, and be careful of the nerves that are on the ankle at the back, that the ligatures are not too tight.
puis le laisse II jors ou III, et se li liiens amolist, si l’estrain;	Then leave it for two or three days, and if the bandages loosen, then tighten them;
puis le deslie au tier jor ou au quart, et deffent a aler lou malaide par IIII jors;	then release it on the third or fourth day, and the patient should walk slowly for four days;
et s’il va devant cel termine, ce n’est mie seurtez qu’il ne desalue encor.	and if he goes before that time, it is not safe that he will not relapse.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si covient que tu l’apaises, si com nos avons dit autre part, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if a deep abscess occurs, you must calm it down as we have said elsewhere, until it is healed.
des dois	you must
Quant li doi sont desaluez, si les covient bellement estendre sens travail, et c’est legiere chose.	When the arms are dislocated, they should be stretched gently without force, and this is a minor matter.
Et se li dislocations est en aucun nout dou dos dou piet, si covient que tu faices seoir le malaide sus I leu plain ou sus .ie. table tot droit, et met ton piet sus ce qui apert de ces jointures, puis presse a ton piet forment, tant qu’il reviegne;	And if the dislocation is in the back of the foot, then you should have the patient sit upright on a flat surface or a table, and put your foot on what is visible from the joints, then press your foot firmly, until it returns to place;
et quant il est igalz, et il n’i apert nient, si met desoz la plante dou piet une table a II chiés, puis l’estrain forment, et le laisse III jors, puis le deslie;	and when it is even, and there is no opening, then place a board with two legs under the sole of the foot, then stretch it forcefully, and leave it for three days, then release it.
et le fai reposer, tant qu’il soit sanez.	and let him rest until he is healed.
de plaie et de dislocation ensamble	of wounds and dislocations together
Quant plaie vient avec la dislocation, et on la vuet restorer, maintes fois avient que li malaides muert:	When there is an injury with the dislocation and one wishes to restore it, many times the patient dies.
si ne soies mie presumptuous en la cure, se tu n’es saiges en l’art et tu ne l’as useit longement, et se tu n’es pitous et misericors et tardis, ne mie hardis;	if you are not confident in the treatment, unless you are wise in the craft and have practiced it for a long time, and if you are not patient and merciful and slow to anger;
et use au comencement de choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et laisse le malaide en la main Deu, se tu n’i vois esperance de santeit;	and use at the beginning of things soothing hot poultices, and let the patient remain in God's hand if you see no hope of healing;
et quant tu i vois esperance, si ramoinne maintenant le membre au leu, ainsois que li apostemes chaus i viegne;	and when you see hope, then reset the member to its place, so that the hot poultices may work.
et quant li membres est a leu, si aministre choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et cure la plaie, si com il covient, d’oignemens desiccatis;	and when the limb is exposed, then administer hot poultices to soothe the abscess and treat the wound, as appropriate, with drying ointments;
et se avec la dislocation a brisure, et os menus desevrez, si les oste, et fai ce que nos avons dit en maladies simples;	and if there is a fracture with the dislocation, and small bones are displaced, then set the bones and follow the instructions given in simple diseases;
et te garde d’entrer en voie de paour, selonc ce que j’ai dit, car ce te vaut mues selonc ton Creator, et por la saveteit de t’arme et de ton cors.	and beware of going down the path of fear, according to what I have said, for it will bring you closer to your Creator, and for the sake of your soul and your body.
